Lha Lama Yeshi Od, the Ngari King invited the Indian Pandita [Dharmapāla], his disciple [Sādhupāla], [guṇapāla] and [prajсāpāla] from whom Gyalwa Sherab of Zhang Zhung received ordination, who then passed the lineage to his disciples Paljor and Jangchub Senge. Thus this lineage came to be known as the Upper Vinaya lineage.
སྟོན-པའི-གཏག-རབས-བདུན	The Seven Successors of the Buddha.\n1){འོད་སྲུང་།} [Kasyapa] 2){ཀུན་དགའ་བོ།} [ānanda]\n3){ཤ་ནའི་གོས་ཅན།} [ṡāṇavāsin]\n4){ཉེར་སྦས།} [Upagupta]\n5){དྷི་དྷི་ཀ} [Dhitika]\n6){ནག་པོ།} [Kṛṣṇa]\n7){ལེགས་མཐོང་ཆེན་མོ།}[Mahasudarsana].
སྟོན-པའི-མཛད-ཆེནབཞི	The four great festivals of Buddha [ṡākyamuni].\n1){ལྷ་ཡུལ་ནས་བབ་པའི་དུས་ཆེན།} His descent from the [tuṣita] god realm\n2){ཆོས་འཁོར་དུས་ཆེན།} turning of the wheel of doctrine\n3){ཆོ་འཕྲུལ་དུས་ཆེན།} His day of victory through miracles\n4){སངས་རྒྱས་པའི་དུས་ཆེན།} His attainment of complete enlightenment.
སྟོབས-ཀྱི-ཕ-རོལ-ཏུ-ཕྱིན-པ-བཅུ	[Daṡa balapāramitā]/ The ten perfections of powers.\n1){བསམ་པའི་སྟོབས།}[āṡaya bala]/ the power of intention\n2){ལྷག་པའི་བསམ་པའི་སྟོབས།}[adhyāṡaya bala]/ the power of resolute intention\n3){གཟུངས་ཀྱི་སྟོབས།}[dhāraṇī bala]/ the power of retention\n4){ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན་གྱི་སྟོབས།}[samādhi bala]/ the power of concentration\n5){ཡང་དག་པར་འབྱོར་བའི་སྟོབས།} [saṁyak prayoga bala]/ the power of perfect application\n6){དབང་གི་སྟོབས།} the power of authority\n7){སྤོབས་པའི་སྟོབས།} [pratibhana bala]/ the power of confidence\n8){སྨོན་ལམ་གྱི་སྟོབས།} [praṇidhāna bala]/ the power of prayers\n9){བྱམས་པ་ཆེན་པོ་དང་སྙིང་རྗེ་ཆེན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [mahāmaitrī mahākaruṇā bala]/ the power of great love and compassion\n10){དེ་བཞིན་གཤེགས་པ་ཐམས་ཅད་ཀྱི་བྱིས་རླབས་པའི་སྟོབས།}[sarva tathāgata adhiṣṭhāna bala]/the power of the blessings of all the Buddhas.
སྟོབས-ལྔ	The five powers; the five forces.\n1. The five powers within the thirty-seven limbs of enlightenment.\n1){དད་པོའི་སྟོབས།}[ṡraddha bala]/ the power of faith\n2){བརྩོན་འགྲུས་ཀྱི་སྟོབས།}[virya bala]/ the power of enthusiastic perseverance\n3){དྲན་པོའི་སྟོབས།}[smṛti bala]/ the power of mindfulness\n4){ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན་གྱི་སྟོབས།}[samādhi bala]/ the power of concentration\n5){ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱི་སྟོབས།}[prajсa bala]/ the power of wisdom.\n2. The five forces according to the seven-point mind training\n1){དཀར་པོ་ས་བོན་གྱི་སྟོབས།} [ṡuklabīja bala]/ the power of the white seed\n2){འཕེན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [āṡaya bala]/ the power of intention\n3){སུན་འབྱིན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [dūsaṇa bala]/ the power of repulsion\n4){གོམས་པའི་སྟོབས།} [abhyāsa bala]/ the power of familiarity\n5){སྨོན་ལམ་གྱི་སྟོབས།}[praṇidhāna bala]/ the power of prayers.
སྟོབས-བཅུ	The ten powers (see- {དེ་བཞིན་གཤེགས་པའི་སྟོབས་བཅུ} or {བྱང་ཆུབ་སེམས་པའི་སྟོབས་བཅུ}).
སྟོབས-དྲུག	The six powers; the six forces. The six powers that are aids to the attainment of the nine stages of mental fixation (see- {སེམས་གནས་དགུ}) in the training of mental quiescence meditation.\n1){ཐོས་པའི་ཨོསྟོབས།}[ṡrūta bala]/ the power of hearing\n2){བསམ་པའི་སྟོབས།}[] asaya bala]/ the power of contemplation\n3){དྲན་པའི་སྟོབས།}[smṛti bala]/ the power of mindfulness\n4){ཤེརས་བཞིན་གྱི་སྟོབས།}[saṁprajānya bala]/ the power of alertness\n5){བརྩོན་འགྲུས་ཀྱི་སྟོབས།}[virya bala]/ the power of enthusiastic perseverance\n6){གོམས་པའི་སྟོབས།}[abhyasa bala]/ the power of familiarity.
བརྟག-པ-རྣམ-པ-བརྒྱད	The eight sciences of examination.\n1){ས་གཞི་བརྟགས་པ།} the examination of earth\n2){རིན་པོ་ཆེ་བརྟག་པ།} the examination of jewels\n3){ལྗོན་ཤིང་བརྟག་པ།} the examination of trees\n4){གོས་བརྟག་པ།} the examination of cloth\n5){བུད་མེད་བརྟག་པ།} the examination of women\n6){རྟ་བརྟག་པ།} the examination of\nhorses 7){གླང་པོ་ཆེཨེ་བརྟག་པ།} the the examination of elephants\n8){སྐྱེས་བུ་བརྟག་པ།} the examination of men.
བརྟན-མ-བཅུ-གཉིད	The Twelve Dharma Protectors; the twelve sister-protectors of Tibet who have promised to protect the Buddha Dharma, belonging to the class of mother tantra.\n1){རྡོ་རྗེ་ཀུན་གྲགས་མ།} Dorje Kundakma\n2){རྡོ་རྗེ་གཡབ་མ་སྐྱོང་།} Dorje Yamakyong\n3){རྡོ་རྗེ་ཀུན་བཟང་མ།} Dorje Kunzangma\n4){རྡོ་རྗེ་གེགས་ཀྱི་གཙོ།} Dorje Gegkyi-Tzo\n5){རྡོ་རྗེ་སྤྱན་གཅིག་མ།} Dorje Chen Chigma\n6){རྡོ་རྗེ་དཔལ་གྱི་ཡུམ།} Dorje Pelgyi Yum\n7){རྡོ་རྗེ་དྲག་མོ་རྒྱལ།} Dorje Dragmo Gyai\n8){རྡོ་རྗེ་ཀླུ་མོ་དཀར་མོ།} Dorje Lumo Karmo\n9){རྡོ་རྗེ་བོད་ཁམས་སྐྱོང་།} Dorje Bodkham Kyong\n10) {རྡོ་རྗེ་སྨན་གཅིག་མ།} Dorje Men Chigma\n11) {རྡོ་རྗེ་གཡར་མོ་སེལ།} Dorje Yarmo Sil\n12) {རྡོ་རྗེ་གཡུ་སྒྲོན་མ།} Dorje Yudron Ma.
བརྟུལ-ཞུགས	[Vrata]/ Ascetic practices. A term used to denote acts of penance involving religious practices; often associated with torturing one's body and exposing it to physical hardship for the attainment of spiritual goals. For a true Buddhist, these extreme practices are forbidden, however in tantric practice they are sometimes deemed necessary.
བརྟེན-པ-རྣམ-ཤེས-ཀྱི-ཁམས-དྲུག	The six consciousnesses that rely upon sensory powers (see-{ཁམས་བཅོ་བརྒྱད}).
བརྟེན-པ-གཞིའི-ས	The ground of basic reliance. According to the Nyingma teachings this is the second spiritual ground attained during the first yogic stage. Since all realizations at this stage becomes the basis or foundation for achieving the path of\npreparation and others, it is knows as the ground of basic reliance.
བརྟེན-པའི-ཁྱད-པར-འགྲོ-བའི-ས	The ground of reliance for exalted progression. According to the Nyingma teachings this refers to the sixth ground attained at the level of the path of seeing, whereupon a Bodhisattva, in reliance upon directly seeing the meaning clear light, progresses higher and higher in achieving the twelve thousand spiritual qualities. Therefore, the sixth ground is known as the ground of reliance for exalted progression.
བསྟན-འགྱུར	The Tangyur; the commentarial canon. The collection of i Tibetan translations of early Indian commentaries to Buddha's teachings which runs into 225 volumes with slight variations between different editions.
བསྟན-བཅོས	[ṡastra]/Treatises; commentanal works; commentarial texts.
བསྟན-བཅོས-ལྟར-སྣང-དྲུག	The six types of imperfect commentanal works; the six classes of imperfect commentarial works.\n1){དོན་མེད་པའི་བསྟན་བཅོས།} the meaningless commentary\n2){སྡོན་ལོག་པའི་བསྟན་བཅོས།} the misleading commentary\n3){ངན་གཡོའི་བསྟན་བཅོས།} the deceptive commentary\n4){བརྩེ་བྲལ་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས།} the uncompassionate commentary\n5){ཐོས་པ་ལྷུར་ལེན་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས།} that which stresses study\n6){རྩོད་པ་ལྷུར་ལེན་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས།} that which stresses debate.
བསྟན-བཅོས-ཡམག-དག-གསུམ	The three types of perfect commentarial works; the three classes of perfect commentaries.\n1){དོན་དང་ལྡན་པའི་བསྟན་བཅོས།} the meaningful commentary\n2){སྡུག་བསྔལ་སྤོང་བའི་བསྟན་བཅོས།}\nthat which dispells suffenngs\n3){སྒྲུབ་པ་ལྷུར་ལེན་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས།} that which stresses practice.
བསྟན-པ	[ṡāsana]/ Teaching; doctrine. Teachings spoken by Buddha himself, or recorded into writing by later disciples in the form of commentaries. Technically, Buddha's teachings can be subsumed under two categories: the transmission of oral and recorded teachings (see- {ལུང་གི་བསྟན་པ}) and the transmission of insights (see- {རྟོགས་པའི་བསྟན་པ}).
བསྟན-པ-ལྔ-དར	The Early Spread; the early period of Buddhism. The introduction of Buddhism during the Tibetan King Lha Tho-Tho-Ri Nyan-Tsen, and its steady spread until the irreligious King Lang Darma who destroyed it in the 10th century. This period of propagation of Buddhism in Tibet is known as the period of the early spread.
བསྟན-པ-ཕྱི-དར	The Later Spread; the later period of Buddhism. The revival of Buddhism in the 12th century starting from the eastern and western part of Tibet after a setback during the reign of King Lang Darma is known as the period of the later spread in the history of Tibetan Budhism.
བསྟན-བསྲུང་	The protectors of the doctrine; the Buddhist protectors.
བསྟོད-ཆེན-བཞི	The four great praises; the four eulogies authorized by Je Tsong Khapa.\n1){སྟོན་པ་ལ་བསྟོད་པ་རྟེན་འབྲེལ་བསྟོད་པ།} Praise of Dependent Origination, in praise of Buddha [ṡākyamuni]\n2){བྱམས་བསྟོད་གཉེན་གཤིན་མ།} The Rapproachment, in praise of Maitreya\n3){འཇམ་དབྱངས་ལ་བསྟོད་པ་བསྟོད་སྤྲོད་སྤྲིན་རྒྱ་མཚོ།}\nThe praise of Ocean of Clouds, in praise of [maсjuṡri]\n4. {རྣམ་རྒྱལ་མ་ལ་བསྟོད་པ་ས་གསུམ་འགྲོ་བའི་རེ་བསྐོང་།} Fulfilling the Wishes of Beings in the Three Realms, in praise of Vijayani.
བསྟོད-ཚོགས	The eulogies. The collection of writings of the Buddha, Bodhisattvas, masters and scholars in praise of any being or object of veneration.
ཐ-སྙད	[Vyavahāra]/ Name; terms; jargon; convention.
ཐ-སྙད-མགན-པོ	1. A glib person, only interested in words or literal conventions.\n2. One who was the first to give names to things, a name abbot.
ཐ-སྙད-བདེན-པ	[Vyavahārasatya]/ The conventional truth. A phenomenon that is real only to an ordinary consciousness, i.e. to a consciousness other than the meditative equipoise of an exalted being ([ārya]).
ཐ-སྙད-ལྔ-ལྔན-གྱི-མི	A person possessing five features. According to the Vinaya\ntradition these are:\n1){མི་ཡིན་པ།} being a person\n2){སྨྲ་ཤེས་པ།} being able to speak\n3){དོན་གོ་བ།} being able to understand the meaning of a language\n4){ཤེས་པ་རང་བཞིན་དུ་གནས་པ།} being in possession of a sound mind\n5){མ་ནིང་སོགས་མིན་པ།} being neither an eunuch nor a hermaphrodite.
ཐ-སྙད-གསུམ	The three features of a person.\n1){མི་ཡིན་པ།} being a person\n2){ཤེས་པ་རང་བཞིན་དུ་གནས་པ།} having sound mind\n3){འདོད་ཁམས་པའི་ས་པ་ཡིན་པ།} living in the desire realm.
ཐ-དང-བཞི	[Catvāri bhedāḥ]/ The four types of differences; the four separate existences.\n1){རང་ལྔོག་ཐ་དད་པ།} separate self-reversed identity\n2){ངོ་བོ་ཐ་དད་པ།} separate nature\n3){རིགས་ཐ་དད་པ།} separate family or class\n4){རྫས་ཐ་དད་པ།} separate substantial entity.
ཐ-མའི-ཆ-མཐུན-ལྔ་	The five fetters with respect to the last realm (also called,\n{ཐ་མའི་ཆ་མཐུན་གྱི་ཀུན་སྦྱོར་ལྔ་།}); the five fetters that bind one in the desire realm.\n[1-3]{མཐོང་སྤང་ཀུན་སྦྱོར་གསུམ།} the three constant letters to be abandoned on the path of seeing (see- {མཐོང་སྤང་ཀུན་སྦྱོར་གསུམ}).\n4){འདོད་པ་ལ་འདུན་པ།}[kāmacchanda]/ admiration for sensual objects\n5){གནོད་སེམས།} [vyāpāda]/ malicious thought.
ཐ-མལ-གྱི-འཆི-བ	The ordinary death; natural death.
ཐ-མལ-སྣང-ཞེན	Compulsive attraction to ordinary appearances. The idea of oneself as an ordinary person which must be abandoned through generating divine pride in the practice of deity yoga in order to produce divine vision and pride.
ཐབས-ཀྱི-དཀྱིལ-འཁོར	[Upāya maṇḍala]/ The method [maṇḍala]. The [maṇḍala]s representing paths:\n1){རྡུལ་མཚོན་གྱི་དཀྱིལ་འཁོར།} sand powdered [maṇḍala]\n2){རས་བྲིས་ཀྱི་དཀྱིལ་འཁོར།} [maṇḍala] painted on cloths\n3){ཚོམ་བུའི་དཀྱིལ་འཁོར།} heaped up [maṇḍala] (this could be just a heap of sand, grains, stones or metal erected for the purpose of representing a [maṇḍala]).
ཐབས-ཀྱི-ཐེག-པ	[Upāya yāna]/ The method vehicle. The tantric path is known as the method vehicle due its four special features (see- {གསང་སྔགས་ཀྱི་ཁྱད་ཆོས་བཞི}) that makes it superior in comparison to the perfection vehicle.
ཐབས-མཁས-བཅུ-གཉིད	The twelve skillful means of a Bodhisattva.\n1){སེམས་ཅན་ཐམས་ཅད་ལ་སྙིང་རྗེ་དང་ལྔན་པ།} he is compassionate towards all beings\n2){རང་བཞིན་ཇི་ལྟ་བ་བཞིན་མཁྱེན་པ།} he knows their nature as it is\n3){བླ་མེད་བྱང་ཆུབ་མངོན་དུ་བྱེད་འདོད་པ།} he aspires to attain supreme enlightenment\n4){འཁོར་བ་མི་གཏོང་བ།} he does not release himself from cyclic existence\n5){ཉོན་མོངས་ཅན་མ་ཡིན་པས་འཁོར་བར་འཁོར་བ།} he is able to take repeated rebirths in cyclic existence because he is not under the sway of delusions\n6){འཚང་རྒྱ་འདོད་པས་བརྩོན་འགྲུས་འབར་བ།} he strives hard for the attainment of Buddhahood\n7){དགེ་བའི་རྩ་བ་ཆུང་རྣམས་ཚད་མེད་པར་སྒྱུར་བར་བྱེད་པ།} he transforms minor roots of virtue into immeasurable virtue\n8){དཀའ་ཚེགས་ཆུང་ངུས་དགེ་རྩ་ཆེན་པོ་འགྲུབ་པར་བྱེད་པ།} he accumulates enormous virtue with little effort\n9){བསྟན་པ་ལ་འགྲན་པ་རྣམས་ཀྱི་ཁོང་ཁྲོ་འཇོམས་པར་བྱེད་པ།} he pacifies anger in those wishing to harm Buddha's doctrine\n10) {བར་མར་གནས་པ་རྣམས་བསྟན་པ་ལ་འཛུད་པར་བྱེད་པ།} he turns the minds of those indifferent to the doctrine\n11) {ཞུགས་པ་རྣམས་སྨིན་པར་བྱེད་པ།} he matures the minds of those\nengaged in the teachings\n12) {སྨིན་པ་རྣམས་གྲོལ་བར་བྱེད་པ།} he liberates those who are matured.
ཐབས-མཁས-པའི-ཉེ-བའི-གཞི-ཤེས	The knowledge of the basis near to the resultant mother due to skill in means.
ཐབས-མཁས-སྦྱོར-བ-བཅུ	The ten trainings in skillful means. The special qualities of a Bodhisattva on the three pure grounds—the eighth, ninth and tenth.\n1){བདུད་བཞི་ལས་རྒྱལ་བའི་སྦྱོར་བ།} victonous from the four demons (see- {བདུད་བཞི})\n2){དོམ་དམ་པར་མི་གནས་ཤིང་ཐ་སྙད་དུ་གནས་པའི་སྦྱོར་བ།} abides in relative state and not in ultimate\n3){གཞན་དོན་སྔོན་གྱི་སྨོན་ལམ་གྱིས་འཕེན་པར་བྱེད་པའི་སྦྱོར་བ།} projects the fulfilment of others' goals through the power of past prayers\n4){ཐུན་མོང་མ་ཡིན་པའི་སྦྱོར་བ།} uncommon trainings\n5){ཆོས་ཐམས་ཅད་ལ་བདེན་པར་རང་བཞིན་མེད་པའི་སྦྱོར་བ།} apprehension of the lack of truly existent or the inherent nature of all phenomena\n6){བདེན་པར་མི་དམིགས་པའི་སྦྱོར་བ།} lack of grasping at true existence\n7){མཚན་མ་མེད་པའི་སྦྱོར་བ།} grasping at signs of true existence\n8){སྨོན་པ་མེད་པའི་སྦྱོར་བ།} lack of truly existent aspiration\n9){ཕྱིན་ཅི་ལོག་བཞི་ལས་གྲོལ་བའི་རྟགས་ཀྱི་སྦྱོར་བ།} has four irreversible signs\n10) {རྟོགས་པ་ཚད་མེད་པའི་སྦྱོར་བ།} has immeasurable insight into realizations.
ཐབས-མ-ཡིན-པའི-རིང-བའི-གཞི-ཤེས	The knowledge of the basis distant from the resultant mother due to lack of skill in means.
ཐབས-ཤེས-ཟུང-སྦྲེལ	The union of method and wisdom. The union of the mind of enlightenment and emptiness as method and wisdom respectively.
ཐམས-ཅད-ཡོན-པར-སྨྲ-བའི-སྔེ	[Mūlasarvāstivāda] School. One of the eighteen Hinayana schools. They assert all phenomena as included in the five categories (see- {གཞི་ལྔ}), recite [sūtra]s in Sanskrit, their abbots are necessarily those belonging to the king's lineage, their multi-patched yellow upper shawl bears a wheel or lotus symbol, their [bikṣus] bear surnames with bhadra or Hridhya, they assert the three times as substantially existent, and they propound that through meditation on the selflessness of person and the accumulation of merits for three countless aeons an individual gains full enlightenment. There are seven sub-schools of this tradition (see- {གཞི་ཐམས་ཅད་ཡོད་པར་སྨྲ་བའི་སྡེ་པ་བདུན}).
ཐར-པ	[Mokṣa]/ [nirvāṇa]; state of liberation. Freedom from the sufferings of cyclic existence through overcoming the obscurations to liberation ({ཉོན་སྒྲིབ}). A state of peace, and the primary goals of the [ṡrāvakas] and Pratyeka buddhas.
ཐལ-འགྱུར-ཁྱབ-པ-སྒོ-བརྒྱད	The eight types of logical pervasion.\n1){རྗེས་ཁྱབ་རྣལ་མ།} correct subsequent pervasion (see- {རྗེས་ཁྱབ་རྣལ་མ})\n2){རྗེས་ཁྱབ་ཕྱིན་ཅི་ལོག} wrong subsequent pervasion (see- {རྗེས་ཁྱབ་ཕྱིན་ཅི་ལོག})\n3){ཐུར་ཁྱབ་རྣལ་མ།} correct downwards pervasion (see- {ཐུར་ཁྱབ་རྣལ་མ})\n4){ཐུར་ཁྱབ་ཕྱིན་ཅི་ལོག} wrong downward pervasion (see- {ཐུར་ཁྱབ་ཕྱིན་ཅི་ལོག})\n5){ལྡོག་ཁྱབ་རྣལ་མ།} correct counter pervasion (see- {ལྡོག་ཁྱབ་རྣལ་མ})\n6){ལྡོག་ཁྱབ་ཕཡན་ཅི་ལོག} wrong counter pervasion (see- {ལྡོག་ཁྱབ་ཕྱིན་ཅི་ལོག})\n7){འགལ་ཁྱབ་རྣལ་མ།} correct contrary pervasion (see- {ཁྱབ་རྣལ་མ})\n8){འགལ་ཁྱབ་ཕྱིན་ཅི་ལོག} wrong contrary pervasion (see- {ཁྱབ་ཕྱིན་ཅི་ལོག}).
ཐལ-འགྱུར-བ	[prāsaṅgika] School; the consequentialists. A school of Madhyamika philosophy regarded as the highest of all Buddhist schools of philosophy representing Buddha [ṡākyamuni]'s ultimate view of reality. This school asserts not only the lack of true existence of all phenomena but also their lack of inherent or natural existence and establishes dependent origination and emptiness as mutually inclusive. [nāgārjuna] followed by [buddhapālita] and [candrakīrti] are considered the proponents of this school.
ཐིག-ལེ	[Bindu]/ [ṡukra]/ Drop; essential drop, the seed for generating great bliss in the tantric practice of the male and female regerative fluid.
ཐིག-ལེ-དཀར-དམར	The white and red drops; the white seminal drops and red seminal drops of the father and mother respectively.
ཐུགས-ཀྱིས-བྱིན-གྱིས-བརླབས-པའི-བཀའ-གསུམ	The three kinds of Buddha's teachings resulting from his\nmental blessing. Teachings through:\n1){བསམ་གཏན་གྱི་བྱིན་གྱིས་བརླབ་པའི་བཀའ།} the blessings of concentration\n2){སྙིང་རྗེའི་བྱིན་གྱིས་བརླབས་པའི་བཀའ།} the blessings of compassion\n3){ཆོས་ཉིད་ཀྱིས་བྱིན་གྱིས་བརླབས་པའི་བཀའ།} the blessings of reality.
ཐུགས-དཀྱིལ	[Citta maṇḍala]/ The Mind Mandala. The divine [maṇḍala] visualized and retained in concentration meditation.
ཐུགས-ལྔ་	The five types of minds of a Buddha. According to the Nyingma tradition these are: 1){མི་རྟོག་ཆེན་པོའི་ཐུགས།} great non-conceptual mind\n2){མཉམ་པ་ཆེན་པོའི་ཐུགས།} the great balanced mind\n3){འགྲོ་བ་གྲོལ་བའི་ཐུགས།} the mind for liberating sentient beings\n4){མི་ཕྱེད་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཐུགས།} the indestructible adamantine mind\n5){མངོན་བྱང་གི་ཐུགས།} the totally enlightened mind.
ཐུགས-ལྗགས-སྤྱན-གསུཨེམ	The three—heart, tongue and eye balls. Some of the highly realized masters leave their heart, tongue and eye balls untouched by fire at their cremation as a source of inspiration and devotion, symbolizing their blessings of body, speech and mind as relics for their followers.
ཐུགས-བདེན-པའི-བྱིན-གྱིས-བརླབས-པའི-བཀའ	The words of truth blessed by Buddha's mind. A type of teaching blessed by Buddha which can be heard from trees, sky, rays of lights, music, etc.
ཐུན-དྲུག-བླ-མའི-རྣལ-འབྱོར	The six-session guru yoga. The practice of the generation and completion stage yogas, technically to be done in six sessions of a day—dawn, morning, afternoon, evening, early night and late night. In the Gelug tradition, it is often recognized as a text of daily commitment after having received initiation into the highest class of tantra.
ཐུན-མིན-ལོངས-སྐུའི-མཎཌལ	The uncommon [sambhogakāya maṇḍala]. A practice of [maṇḍala] offering made to one's spiritual master visualizing him or her as being a Sambhogakaya Buddha residing within a fully adorned Buddha field surrounded by an infinite number of goddesses.
ཐུན-མོང-གི-བཀའ-བབས-བཞི	The four common transmissions.\n1){ཕྱག་ཆེན་གྱི་བཀའ་བབས།} the transmission of [mahāmudra]\n2){ཕ་རྒྱུད་ཀྱི་བཀའ་བབས།} the transmission of father tantra 3){མ་རྒྱུད་ཀྱི་བཀའ་བབས།} the transmission of mother tantra\n4){འོད་གསལ་གྱི་བཀའ་བབས།} the transmission of clear light.
ཐུན-མོང-གི-དངོ-གྲུབ-བརྒྱད	[Aṣṭa sādhārana siddhayaḥ]/ The eight common powerful attainments; the eight common feats; the eight siddhis common to both Buddhist and Hindu traditions. According to Buddhist tantra, these are believed to be the external signs of maturing the completion stage practices.\n1){རིལ་བུའི་དངོས་གྲུབ།} siddhi of pills 2){མིག་སྨན་གྱི་དངོས་གྲུབ།} siddhi of eye lotion 3){ས་འོག་གི་དངོས་གྲུབ།} siddhi of travelling underground\n4){རལ་གྲིའི་དངོས་གྲུབ།} siddhi of the sword\n5){ནམ་མཁར་འཕུར་པའི་དངོས་གྲུབ།} siddhi of flying-in-the-sky\n6){མི་སྣང་བའི་དངོས་གྲུབ།} siddhi of invisibility\n7){འཆི་བ་མེད་པའི་དངོས་གྲུབ།} siddhi of immortality\n8){ནད་འཇོམས་པར་བྱེད་པའི་དངོས་གྲུབ།} siddhi of healing sickness.
ཐུན-མོང-གི-ཐེག-པ-གསུམ	The three common vehicles. According to the Nyingma tradition these are:\n1){ཉམ་ཐོས་ཀྱི་ཤེག་པ།} the Hearer's vehicle 2){རང་རྒྱལ་གྱི་ཐེག་པ།} Solitary Realizer's vehicle\n3){བྱང་སེམས་ཀྱི་ཐེག་པ།} the Bodhisattva's vehicle.
ཐུན-མོང-སྤྲུལ-སྐུའི-མཎཌལ	The common [nirmāṇakāya maṇḍala]. A practice of [maṇḍala] offering in which one visualizes all the excellent riches of gods and human beings, roots of virtues and resources in the form of the [maṇḍala] articles and are offered to one's own spiritual master visualizing him or her as being a [nirmāṇakāya] Buddha.
ཐུན-མོང-བའི-དབང-ཕྱུག-གི-ཡོན-ཏན-བརྒྱད	also/ {དབང་ཕྱུག་བརྒྱད།}\nThe eight common features of glory; the eight qualities or siddhis common to worldly feats.\n1){གཟུགས་ཕྲ་བའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} subtle physical form\n2){གཟུགས་རགས་པའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} gross physical form\n3){ཡང་བའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} weighing little\n4){ཁྱབ་པའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} pervasive\n5){ཡང་དག་པར་ཐོབ་པའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} perfect attainments\n6){རབ་ཏུ་གལས་བའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} perfect luminosity\n7){བརྟན་པའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} ever-firm\n8){འདོད་རྒུ་འབྱུང་བའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} fulfillment of all wishes.
ཐུན-མོང-བའི-སྲུང-འཁོར	The common protection wheel. The meditation and visualization of a protection wheel common to all the four classes of tantra.
ཐུན-མོང-མ-ཡོན-པའི-བཀའ-བབས-བཞི	The four exclusive transmissions.\n1){གཏུམ་མོའི་བཀའ་བབས།} the transmission of psychic heat\n2){སྒྱུ་ལུས་ཀྱི་བཀའ་བབས།} the transmission of the illusory body\n3){འོད་གསལ་གྱི་བཀའ་བབས།} the transmission of clear light\n4){ཕོ་བ་དང་བར་དོའི་བཀའ་བབས།} the transmission of consciousness transference and the intermediate state yoga.
ཐུན-མོང-མ-ཡོན-པའི-དབང-ཕྱུག-གི-ཡོན-ཏན-བརྒྱད	The eight uncommon features of glory; the eight qualities or siddhis uncommon to Tathagatas.\n1){སྐྱའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of body\n2){གསུང་གི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of speech\n3){ཐུགས་ཀྱི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of mind\n4){འཕྲུལ་ལས་གྱི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of virtuous energy.\n5){རྫུ་འཕྲུལ་གྱི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of miracles\n6){ཀུན་ཏུ་འགྲོ་བའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of universal appearance\n7){གནས་ཀྱི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of abode\n8){ཅི་འདོད་ཀྱི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of wish-fulfillment.
ཐུན-མོང-མ-ཡིན-པའི-རྣམ-མཁྱེན-གྱི-རྣམ-པ-སུམ-ཅུ-རྩ-དགུ-རྣམ-མཁྱེན-གྱི-ཐུན-མོང-མ-ཡིན-པའི-རྣམ-པ-སུམ-ཅུ-རྩ-དགུ	The thirty-nine qualities exclusive to the Omniscient Mind.\n[1-10]{སྟོབས་བཅུ།} [dasa balāni]/ the ten powers (see- {དེ་བཞིན་གཤེགས་པའི་སྟོབས་བཅུ})\n[11-14] {མི་འཇིགས་པ་བཞི།} [catvāri vaiṡāradyāh]/the four fearlessnesses (see-\n{མི་འཇིགསྤ་བཞི})\n[15-18] {སོ་སོར་ཡང་དག་པར་རིག་པ་བཞི།} [catvа_ri pratides'anīyāḥ]the four specific perfect understandings (see- {སོ་སོར་ཡང་དག་རིག་པ་བཞི})\n[19-36] {ཆོས་མ་འདྲིས་པ་བཅོ་བརྒྱད།}[aṣṭādaṡāveṇika dharmāḥ]/ the eighteen unshared qualities of a Buddha (see- {མ་འདྲེས་པ་བཅོ་བརྒྱད})\n[37-39] {རྣམ་མཁྱེན་ཉིད་ཀྱི་རྣམ་པ་གསུམ།} the three exclusive qualities of the Omniscient Mind itself:\n1){དེ་བཞིན་ཉིད་ཀྱི་རྣམ་པ།} the aspect of suchness\n2){རང་བྱུང་གི་རྣམ་པ།} the aspect of spontaneity\n3){སངས་རྒྱས་ཉིད་ཀྱི་རྣམ་པ།} the aspect of the fully enlightened being himself.
ཐུན-མཚམས	Intervals between meditation sessions; post-meditational periods.
ཐུན-བཞིའི-རྣལ-འབྱོར	The four session yoga. The meditation practiced in the four sessions of a day:\n1){ཐོ་རངས།} early dawn\n2){སྔ་དྲོ།} morning [З] {ཉིན་གུང་།} day time (afternoon)\n4){སྲོད།} dusk.
ཐུར-ཁྱབ	Downward pervasion. The pervasion that whatever is that predicate is the reason in a logical syllogism.
ཐུར-ཁྱབ-རྣལ-མ	Correct downward pervasion. The pervasion that whatever is the predicate is the reason in a logical syllogism. Synonymous with downward pervasion (see- {ཐུར་ཁྱབ})
ཐུར-ཁྱབ-ཕྱིན-ཅོ-ལོག	Wrong downward pervasion. The pervasion in a logical syllogism that whatever is the predicate is not the reason.
ཐུར-སེལ-གྱི-རླུང་	The downward moving wind; One of the five principal energy-winds (see- {རྩ་བའི་རླུང་ཨཱིང}) that control the lower sphincter muscles, holding and discharging faeces, urine, semen and menstrual blood.
ཐེ-ཚོམ-གསུམ	[Tri viciktsā]/ The three types of doubt.\n1){དོན་འགྱུར་གྱི་ཐེ་ཚོམ།} doubt inclining towards fact/ factual doubt\n2){དོན་མི་འགྱུར་གྱི་ཐེ་ཚོམ།} doubt inclining away from fact/ non-factual doubt\n3){ཆ་མཉམ་པའི་ཐེ་ཚོམ།} evently balanced doubt.
ཐེག-ཆེན	[Mahāyāna]/ The Greater Vehicle. The Bodhisattva vehicle leading to full enlightenment and is superior in seven ways (see {ཆེན་པོ་བདུན}) from the lower vehicles of the Hearers and Solitary Realizers. It has two types:\n1){ཕར་ཕྱིན་ཐེག་པ།} the perfection vehicle\n2){སྔགས་ཀྱི་ཐེག་པ།} the secret mantrayana vehicle.
ཐེག-ཆེན-གྱི-སྒྲུབ-པ-སྒོམ-ལམ	[Mahāyāna pratipatti bhāvanā mārga]/ The [mahāyāna] path of meditation of achievement. The uncontaminated [mahāyāna] path of meditation which is a cause for the attainment of the realizations of the first to the tenth level ofthe Bodhisattva's path.
ཐེག-ཆེན-སྒོམ-ལམ-གྱི-བྱེད-པ	[Mahāyāna bhavanā mārga karaṇa]/ The function of the\n[mahāyāna] path of meditation; the benefits derived through meditation on the [mahāyāna] path of meditation.
ཐེག-ཆེན-སྒྲུབ-པ-བཅུ-གསུམ	The thirteen achievements of [mahāyāna]; the thirteen trainings of the [mahāyāna] path:\n[1-4] {ངེས་འབྱེད་ཆ་མཐུན་བཞི།} the four levels of the path of preparation (see- {ངེས་འབྱེད་ཆ་མཐུན་བཞི})\n5){མཐོང་ལམ།} path of seeing\n6){སྒོམ་ལམ།} path of meditation\n7){གཉེན་པོའི་སྒྲུབ་པ།} achievement through antidotes\n8){སྤོང་པའི་སྒྲུབ་པ།} achievement through elimination\n9){དེ་དག་ཡོངས་སུ་གཏུགད་པའི་སྒྲུབ་པ།} achievement through forsaking discrimination between antidotes and abandonments\n10) {ཤེས་རབ་སྙིང་བརྩེའི་སྒྲུབ་པ།} achievement through the unity of wisdom and compassion\n11) {སློབ་མ་ཐུན་མོང་མ་ཡིན་པའི་སྒྲུབ་པ།} achievement for uncommon practitioners\n12) {གཞན་དོན་གོ་རིམ་དུ་བྱེད་པའི་སྒྲུབ་པ།} achievement through persistently working for the welfare of others\n13) {ཡེ་ཤེས་རྩོལ་བ་མི་མངའ་བའི་སྒྲུབ་པ།} achievement through effortless wisdom.
ཐེག-ཆེན-སྒྲུབ-པ-རང-དབང-དུ-འཇུག-པའི-རྒྱུ-སྤྱན-ལྔ་	The five eyes (see- {སྤན་ལྔ}) that are the cause for engaging independently in the [mahāyāna] path of achievements.
ཐེག-ཆེན-སྒྲུབ-པའི-ཆེད-དུ-བྱ-བ-གསུམ	The three aims of [mahāyāna] achievements.\n1){སེམས་དཔའ་ཆེན་པོ།} [mahāsattva]/ greatness of thought\n2){སྤོང་བ་ཆེན་པོ།} [mahāprahāṇa]/greatness of elimination\n3){རྟོགས་པ་ཆེན་པོ།} [adlṅgamamahattva]/greatness of insights.
ཐེག-ཆེན-སྒྲུབ-པའི-དམིག-པ-བཅུ-གཅིག	The eleven objects of observation of the [mahāyāna] achievements.\n1){དགེ་བ།} [kuṡala]/ wholesome phenomena\n2){མི་དགེ་བ།} [akuṡala]/ unwholesome phenomena\n3){ལུང་མ་བསྟན།} [avyākṛta]/ unspecified phenomena\n4){འཇིག་རྟེན་པ།} [lokika]/worldly phenomena\n5){འཇིག་རྟེན་ལས་འདས་པ།} [lokottara]/transworldly phenomena\n6){ཟག་བཅས།} [sāsrava]/ contaminated phenomena\n7){ཟག་མེད།} [anāsrava]/ uncontaminated phenomena\n8){འདུས་བྱས།} [saṁskṛta]/ conditioned phenomena\n9){འདུས་མ་བྱས།} [asaṁskṛta]/ unconditioned phenomena\n10) {ཐུན་མོང་བ།} [sādhāraṇa]/ common qualitites\n11) {ཐུན་མོང་མ་ཡིན་པ།} [asādhāraṇa]/ uncommon qualities.
ཐེག-ཆེན-འཕགས-པ	[Mahāyāna ārya]/ A [mahāyānist] Noble Being; a [mahāyāna ārya] A practitioner of the greater vehicle on or above the path of seeing who has gained direct insight into emptiness.
ཐེག-ཆེན-མོས-པ-སྒོམ-ལམ	[[mahāyāna]dhimukti bhavana marga]/ [mahāyāna] path of meditation of belief. The [mahāyāna] path of meditation that is believed to be the source of fulfilling the purpose of self, others and both.
ཐེག-ཆེན-གསོ-སྦྱོང་	The [mahāyāna] precepts or vows. An ordination of the [mahāyāna] tradition normally accepted for twenty hours during special occasions in the presence of a master or an image of the Buddha, taken by both lay and ordained Buddhists. This entails generating the mind of enlightenment and pledging to follow the footsteps of Buddhas and Bodhisattvas of the past in accordance with the ritual text of this ordination. On top of not eating meat, there are eight precepts to be observed (see- {བསྙེན་གནས་ཡན་ལག་བཞི}) conjoined with the motive of enlightenment.
ཐེག-མཆོག-འཁོར-ལོ-བཞི	The four wheels of the supreme vehicle; the four essential factors for a Mahayanist practitioner.\n1){མཐུན་པར་གྱུར་བའི་ཡུལ་ན་གནས་པ།} living in a conducive place\n2){སྐྱེ་བོ་དམ་པ་ལ་བརྟེན་པ།} relying upon a holy person\n3){སྨོན་ལམ་བཏབ་པ།} making prayers\n4){བསོད་ནམས་བསགས་པ།} accumulating merits.
ཐེག-པ-ཆེན-པའི-དགེ-བའི-བཤེས-གཉེན-གྱི-མཚན-ཉིད-བཅུ	[Daṡa mahāyāna kalyāṇamitra guṇāḥ]/ The ten qualities of a [mahāyāna] spiritual master.\n1){ལྷག་པ་ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་ཀྱི་བསློབ་པས་དུལ་བ།} in his higher training of discipline he is humble\n2){ལྷག་པ་ཏིང་ངེ་འཇིན་གྱི་བསླབ་པས་ཞི་བ།} his higher training of concentration he is peaceful\n3){ལྷག་པ་ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱི་བསླབ་པས་ཉེ་བར་ཞི་བ།} in his higher training of wisdom he has pacified his ego\n4){ལུང་གི་ཡོན་ཏན་གྱིས་ཕྱུག་པ།} he is rich in lineages and oral teachings\n5){སྟོང་པ་ཉིད་རྟོགས་པ།} has realized emptiness\n6){སློབ་མ་ལས་ཡོན་ཏན་ལྷག་པ།} he has higher qualities than his disciples\n7){སྨྲ་མཁས་པ།} he is skillful in teaching\n8){བརྩེ་བ་དང་ལྡན་པ།} he is compassionate\n9){བརྩོན་འགྲུས་དང་ལྔན་པ།} he is hard working\n10) {འཁོར་བ་ལ་སྐྱོ་ངལ་བསྐྱེད་དུ་བཅུག་པ།} he inspires aversion of cyclic existence.
ཐེག-པ-གཉིས	The two vehicles.\n[1)]\n1){ཐེག་ཆེན།} [[mahāyāna]]/ the greater vehicle\n2){ཐེག་དམན།} Hinayana/ the smaller vehicle.\n[2)]\n1. {རྒྱུ་ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པའི་ཐེག་པ།} the causal perfection vehicle\n2. {འབྲས་བུ་གསང་སྔགས་ཀྱི་ཐེག་པ།} the resultant mantra vehicle.
ཐེག-པ-རིན-པ-དགུ	The nine vehicles; the nine paths (see- {རྙིང་མའི་ཐེག་པ་རིམ་པ་དགུ}).
ཐེག-པ-གསུམ	[triyāna]/ The three vehicles; the three causal vehicles.\n1. {སྙན་ཐོས་ཀྱི་ཐེག་པ།} [ṡrāvaka yāna]/ Hearer's vehicle\n2. {རང་རྒྱལ་གྱི་ཐེག་པ།} [pratyekabuddha yāna]/ Solitary Realizer's vehicle\n3. {ཐེག་ཆེན་གྱི་ཐེག་པ།} [mahāyāna]/ Greater vehicle.
ཐེག-དམན	[hīnayāna]/ Lower vehicle; the lesser vehicle. Path followed by [ṡrāvakas] and Pratekya Buddhas which leads to the attainment of liberation from cyclic existence.
ཐེག-དམན-དགྲ-བཅོམ-པ-གཉིས	[dvi hīnayāna arhat]/ The two Arhats of the lower vehicle.\n1. {ཉན་ཐོས་ཀྱི་མི་སློབ་པ།} Arhat of the Hearer vehicle\n2. {རང་སངས་རྒྱས་ཀྱི་མི་སློབ་པ།} Arhat of the Solitary realizer's vehicle.
ཐེག-དམན-ས-བརྒྱད	[aṣṭa hīnayāna bhūmayaḥ]/ The eight spiritual grounds of the lower vehicle.\n1. {དཀར་པོ་རྣམ་པར་མཐོན་པའི་ས།} [ṡukla vidarṡanā bhūmi]/ the ground of seeing virtuous dharma\n2. {རིགས་ཀྱི་ས།} [gotra bhūmi]/ the ground the family\n3. {བརྒྱད་པའི་ས།} [aṣṭamaka bhūmi]/ the eighth ground\n4. {མཐོང་པའི་ས།} [darṡana bhūmi]/ the ground of seeing\n5. {བསྲབས་པའི་ས།} [tanū bhūmi]/ the ground of subtleness\n6. {འདོད་ཆགས་དང་བྲལ་བའི་ས།} [vigata rāga bhūmi]/ the ground free of attachment\n7. {བྱས་པ་སྲུགས་པའི་ས།} [kṛtāvi bhūmi]/ the ground of protecting deeds\n8. {བྱས་པ་རྟོགས་པའི་ས།} [kṛtāvi samaya bhūmi]/ the ground of realizing deeds.
ཐེར-ཟུག-གི-དངོས-པོ	The unchangeable phenomenon; the permanent existents.
ཤོག-མ-དང-ཐ-མ-མེད-པའི-སྟོང-པ-ཉིད	[anavarāgraṡūnyatā]/ The emptiness of that which is without beginning or end. One of the sixteen types of emptinesses (see {སྟོང་ཉིད་བཅུ་དྲུག}), the emptiness of the beginninglessness and endlessness of cyclic existence.
ཐོགས-མེད	[ārya Asaṇga]. The brother of Vasubandhu and the founder of the [cittamātrin] school of thought. He was the pioneer of the lineage of extensive deeds (rgya-chen spyod-rgyud) and is famous for bringing the Five Wort ofMaitreya (see {བྱམས་ཆོས་སྡེ་ལྔ}) from Tusita heaven. His works include the Five Treatises of Asanga (see {ས་སྡེ་ལྔ}) and the Two Compendiums (see {སྡོམ་རྣམ་གཉིས}).
ཐོགས-རེག-ཅད-གྱི-དངོས-པོ	Tangible objects; obstructive things.
ཐོས-བསམ-སྒོམ-གསུམ	[ṡruta cintā bhāvanā]/ The threefold practice of study, contemplation and meditation.
མཐའ-ཁོབ-ཀྱི-མི	A human from a remote place. To be born as a barbarian or among men dwelling in a country far from the place of the eight conducive factors (see {དལ་བ་བརྒྱད}) preventing the practice of religion.
མཐའ-གཉིས	The two extremes. A.\n1. {རྟག་མཐའ།} [nityānta]/ extreme of eternalism\n2. {ཆད་མཐའ།} [ucchedānta]/ extreme of nihilism.\nB.\n1. {སྲིད་པ་འཁོར་བའི་མཐའ།} extreme of cyclic existence— [saṁsara]\n2. {ཞི་བ་མྱང་འདས་ཀྱི་མཐའ།} extreme of peace— [nirvāṇa]\nС.\n1. {ཡོད་མཐའ།} [astyanta]/ extreme of existence\n2. {མེད་མཐའ།} [ananta]/ extreme of non-existence.\nD.\n1. {བཟང་མཐའ།} extreme of good\n2. {ངན་མཐའ} extreme of evil.
མཐའ-བཞི	A. The four extreme beliefs in the inherent existence:\n1. {བདག་ལས་སྐྱེ་བ།} [ātmaja]/ production from self\n2. {གཞན་ལས་སྐྱེ་བ} [paraja]/ production from others\n3. {གཉིས་ཀ་ལས་སྐྱེ་བ།} [ubhayaja]/ production from both\n4. {རྒྱུ་མེད་ལས་སྐྱེ་བ།} [akāraṇaja]/ production without causes.\nB. The four ends:\n1. {སྐྱེས་མཐའ་འཆི་བ།} death as the end of birth\n2. {འདུས་མཐའ་བྲལ་བ།} separation as the end of meeting\n3. {བསགས་མཐའ་འཛད་པ།} exhaustion as the end of accumulation\n4. {མཐོ་མཐའ་སླུཨུུང་བ།} downfall as the end of an elevated position.\nС. The four extremes:\n1. {ཡོད་མཐའ།} extreme of existence\n2. {མེད་མཐའ།} extreme of non-existence\n3. {གཉིས་ཀའི་མཐའ།} extreme of being both\n4. {གཉིས་མིན་གྱི་མཐའ།} extreme of being neither.
མཐའ-ལས-འདས-པ-སྟོང-པ-ཉིད	[atyanta ṡūnyatā]/ That emptiness of that which is beyond extremes. One of the sixteen types of emptinesses (see {སྟོང་པ་ཉིད་བཅུ་དྲུག}), the emptiness of reality free of the two extremes—the extreme of existence and non-existence.
མཐར-གྱིས-གནས-པའི-སྙོམས-འཇུག-དགུ	The nine meditative absorptions existing in series.\n1-4. {བསམ་གཏན་གྱི་སྙོམས་འཇུག་བཞི།} [catvāri dhyāna samāpattayaḥ]/ the four types of meditative absorptions of the form realm (see {བསམ་གཏན་གྱི་སྙོམས་ཇུག་བཞི}) 5-8. {གཟུགས་མེད་ཀྱི་སྙོམས་འཇུག་བཞི།} [catvāri arūpa samāpattayaḥ]/ the four types of meditative absorptions within the formless realms (see {གཟུགས་མེད་སྙོམས་འཇུག་བཞི})\n9. {འགོག་པའི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} [nirodha samāpatti]/ the meditative absorption of cessation.
མཐར-གྱིས-སྦྱོར-བ	[anupūrva prayoga]/ The Serial Training. A Bodhisattva's wisdom which through serial meditation upon the 173 aspects of the three wisdoms (the basis, path and resultant wisdom) gains firm understanding of these aspects.
མཐར-གྱས-སྦྱོར-བ-མཚོན-བྱེད-ཀྱི-ཆོས-བཅུ-གསུམ	[tridaṡa anupūrva prayoga lakṣanāni]/ The thirteen topi charactesed by serial training. 1-6. {ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ་དྲུ་གི་མཐར་གྱིས་སྦྱོར་བ།}\nThe serial training of the six perfections (see {ཕར་ཕྱིན་དྲག})\n7-12. {རྗེས་སུ་དྲན་པ་དྲུག་གི་མཐར་གྱིས་སྦྱོར་བ།} the serial training of the six recollections (see {རྗེས་སུ་དྲན་པ་དྲུག})\n13. {ངོ་བོ་ཉིད་མེད་རྟོགས་པའི་སྦྱོར་བ།} the serial training understanding the lack of true entity.
མཐར-མངོན-པར-རྫོགས-པ-སངས-རྒྱས-ཚུལ	The way in which Buddha finally attained Perfect Enlightenment. After accumulating merits for three countless aeons, he attained complete enlightenment in the celestial abode known as [akaniṣṭa], the Heaven Beneath None, in the name of Buddha Indraketudhvaja (dbang-po-tog) and displayed his attainment of enlightenment at Bodhgaya. This is the view of the Descent into Lanka [sūtra] (lankavatara).
མཐར-ལྟ	The extreme view. An extreme view of nihilism that takes the self from the view of the transitory collection (see {ལྗིགས་ལྟ}) as its object and apprehends it as being permanent or non-capable of connecting to subsequent rebirth. The function of such a view hinders the realization of the middle way path.
མཐར-ཐུག-གི-སྒྱུ-ལུས	The ultimate elusory body. The attainment of the state of union of a no-more learner, i.e. the sambhogakaya being of a Buddha by means of severing the karma and delusion through the force of the spontaneously born wisdom of the clear light mind ('od-gsal lhan-cig skyes-pa'i ye-shes).
མཤར-ཐུག-གི-འབྲས-བུའི-ཁྱད-ཆོས-གསུམ	The three qualities of the ultimate result or fruit.\n1. {ངོ་བོ་ཀ་ནས་དག་པ་རིག་སྟོང་དབྱེར་མེད།} the inseparability of intuitive awareness and emptiness as the primordial nature\n2. {རང་བཞིན་ལྷུན་གྱིས་གྲུབ་པ་གལས་སྟོང་དབྱེར་མེད།} the inseparability of clarity and emptiness as the spontaneous reality\n3.{ ཐུགས་རྗེ་ཀུན་ལ་ཁྱབ་པ་སྣང་སྟོང་དབྱེར་མེད།} the inseparability of appearance and emptiness as the all pervading compassion.
མཐུན-རྐྱེན-ལྔ་	The five favourable conditions. The five-fold conditions required of someone wishing to accept ordination as a monk or nun.\n1. {ཡུལ་མཆོག་གསུམ་དང་མཁན་སློབ་བཞུགས་པ་དང་།}\nthe presence of the Three Jewels, abbot and masters as the object of receiving ordination and not forsaking vows already received 2. {ཚིག་སྔ་མ་སྔོན་དུ་སོང་བ།} having already made a personal request 3. {རྟགས་སྐྲ་དང་ཁ་སྤུ་བྲེགས་ཤིང་ཡོ་བྱད་ཚང་བ།} possession of all the necessary articles required of an ordained person, and having a shaved head and beard as the signs 4. {བསམ་པ་རྒྱུ་དུས་ཀྱི་ཀུན་སློང་དང་ལྡན་ཞིང་ངེས་འབྱུང་གི་བསམ་པས་ཟིན་པ།}\none's mind being conjoined with the thought of renunciation, as the motivation.\n5. {ཆོ་ག་སྦྱོར་དངོས་མཇུག་གསུམ་ཚང་བ།} conducting the rituals in its entirety from the preliminary to the conclusion.
མཐོ-རིས-ཀྱི-ཡོན-ཏན-བདུན	[sapta svargaguṇ_aḥ]/ The seven qualities of higher rebirth.\n1. {རིགས་བཟང་བ།} [kulaguṇa]/ better family-lineage\n2. {གཟུགས་མཛེས་པ།} [rūpaguṇa]/ attractive physical features\n3. {ཚེ་རིང་བ།} [cirāyuroguṇa]/ long life\n4. {ནད་མེད་པ།} [arogaguṇa]/ good health\n5. {སྐལ་བ་བཟང་བ།} [saubhāgyaguṇa]/ good fortune\n6. {ནོར་ཕྱུག་པ།} wealthy\n7. {ཤེས་རབ་ཆེ་བ།} [prajсaguṇa]/ good wisdom.
མཐོང-ཆོས-བདེར-གནས-ཀྱི-ལམ-ལྔ་	The five paths bestowing peace in this life.\n1. {ནམ་མཁའ་མཐའ་ཡས་ཀྱི་དངོས་གཞིའི་སྙིམས་འཇུག} the actual meditative absorption of infinite space\n2. {རྣམ་ཤེས་མཐའ་ཡས་ཀྱི་དངོས་གཞིའི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} the meditative absorption of infinite consciousness\n3. {ཅི་ཡང་མེད་ཀྱི་དངོས་གཞིའི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} the actual meditative absorption of nothingness\n4. {སྲི་རྩེའི་དངོས་གཞིའི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} the actual meditative absorption of the peak of existence\n5. {འགོག་པའི་རྣམ་ཐར།} the actual meditative absorption of emancipation in cessation.
མཐོང-ཐོབ-པ	[dṛṣṭi prāpta]/ One who has attained the correct view; a devotee by reason.
མཐོང-སྤང-ཀུན-སྦྱོར-གསུམ	The three constant fetters to be abandoned on the path of seeing.\n1. {འཇིག་ལྟ་ཀུན་བཏགས།} satkaya dr.s.t.i/ intellectual view of the transitory collection\n2. {ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་དང་བརྟུལ་ཞུགས་མཆོག་འཛིན།} [ṡīlavrataparamārṡa]/ holding bad ethics and discipline to be superior\n3. {ཐེ་ཚེམ་ཉོན་མོངས་ཅན།} [kliṣṭavicikitsā]/ deluded doubt.
མཐོང-སྤང-འཇུག-པ-གཟུང-རྟོག-དགུ	The nine conceptions of grasping at the objects of\nengagement to be abandoned on the path of seeing. Grasping 1. {ཐེག་ཆེན་གྱི་ལམ་འབྲས་སྤྱི་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the general [mahāyāna] paths and fruits 2. {ཐེག་ཆེན་ལམ་གྱི་ངོ་བོ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the nature of the [mahāyāna] paths\n3. {ཐེག་ཆེན་ལམ་གྱི་མི་མཐུན་ཕྱོགས་སེལ་བའི་ནུས་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the power to\neliminate negative forces from the [mahāyāna] paths\n4. {གཞན་དོན་བྱེད་པ་པོའི་ནུས་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the power of the persons who work for the welfare of others\n5. {གཞན་དོན་བྱ་བའི་འབྲས་བུ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the results of benefiting others\n6. {ཐེག་ཆེན་གྱི་རིགས་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the [mahāyāna] lineage\n7. {ཐེག་ཆེན་ལམ་གྱི་ཡུལ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the objects of the [mahāyāna] paths\n8. {ལམ་གྱི་འབྲས་བུ་རང་དོན་ལ་དམིགས་པ།}\nthe personal benefit which is the result of the paths\n9. {གཞན་དོན་བྱ་བའི་ལས་ལ་དམིགས་ནས་བདེན་གྲུབ་ཏུ་ཞེན་པ།} activities for benefiting others. The mode of grasping is conceiving those practices as being truly existent objects to be cultivated.
མཐོང-སྤང-བཏགས-འཛིན-རྟོག-པ-དགུ	The nine conceptions of grasping at the imputed objects to be eliminated on the path of seeing. The grasping at:\n1. {འབྲས་བུ་དོན་དུ་གཉེར་བྱ་མི་ཐོབ་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} fruits wnich are\nimpossible to attain\n2. {ལམ་ལ་ཕྱིན་ཅི་ལོག་ཏུ་ཞེན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} wrong apprehension of the paths\n3. {དགག་སྒྲུབ་བདེན་པར་འཛིན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} truly existent negative and positive\nphenomena\n4. {ཆོས་ལྡན་མི་ལྡན་བདེན་པར་འཛིན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} truly existent phenomena with or without qualities\n5. {གནས་ལུགས་ཀྱི་དོན་བདེན་པར་འཛིན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} truly existent conceptions of the mode of reality\n6. {ཐེག་ཆེན་གྱི་ལམ་དང་འགལ་བ་དམན་པའི་རིགས་ཉམས་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the\ndegenerated lineage of the lower vehicle which contradicts the [mahāyāna] lineage\n7. {འབྲས་བུ་ཁྱད་པར་ཅན་ལ་དོན་གཉེར་མེད་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} persons not interested in the superior fruits\n8. {རྣམ་མཁྱེན་གྱི་རྒྱུ་ཤེར་ཕྱིན་གྱི་ཉམས་ལེན་མེད་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།}\npersons lacking the practice of the perfection of wisdom that is a cause for producing omniscience\n9.{ འགལ་རྐྱེན་བདུད་ལ་སོགས་པས་ཟིན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་ནས་བདེན་གྲུབ་ཏུ་ཞིན་པ།} those\nbeing seized by demons which are obstacles to one's practice. The mode of grasping is conceiving the person imputed by these nine practices as being truly existent.
མཐོང-སྤང-སྡོག-པ-གཟུང-རྟོག-དགུ	The nine conceptions of grasping at the objects of elimination to be abandoned on the path of seeing. The grasping at:\n1.{ ཉན་རང་གི་ལམ་འབྲས་རྟོགས་པ་དམན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the lesser path; results and insights of the Hearer's vehicle\n2. {བདག་རྐྱེན་ཡོངས་འཛིན་དམན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the lesser spiritual master who is the fundamental cause\n3. {གཞན་དོན་སྒྲུབ་པའི་ཐབས་དམན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the lesser means of fulfilling other's purpose\n4. {རང་དོན་སྒྲུབ་པའི་ཐབས་དམན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the lesser means of fulfilling one's own purpose\n5. {རང་གཞན་གཉིས་ཀའི་དོན་སྒྲུབ་པའི་ཐབས་དམན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the lesser means of fulfilling the purposes of both\n6. {སྤང་བྱ་དམན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the lesser objects of elimination\n7. {རྟགས་པ་དམན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} the lesser insights or realizations\n8. {ལམ་ཁྱད་པར་ཅན་མ་ཐོབ་པས་ཉམས་པ་ལ་དམགས་པ།} the degeneration caused by the failure to attain superior paths\n9. {འབྲས་བུ་ཁྱད་པར་ཅན་མ་ཐོབ་པས་ཉམ་པ་ལ་མིགས་ནས་བདེན་གྲུབ་ཏུ་ཞེན་པ།} the degeneration caused by the failure to attain superior fruits. The mode of grasping is conceiving those as being the truly existent objects of elimination.
མཐོང-སྤང-རྗས-ཛིན-རྟོག-པ-དགུ	The nine conceptions of grasping at the substantial objects to\nbe abandoned on the path of seeing Grasping at:\n1. {བླང་དོར་ལ་ཞེན་པ།} those to be cultivated and abandoned\n2. {དེའི་ཀུན་སློང་ལ་ཞེན་པ།} their motivation\n3. {དེའི་ཉེས་དམིགས་ལ་ཞེན་པ།} their faults\n4. {དེ་དག་བདེན་པར་ཞེན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} their truly existent nature\n5. {དེ་དག་བདེན་མེད་དུ་ཞེན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་} {པ}! their lack of truly existent nature\n6. {བཏགས་པ་ཙམ་དུ་ཞེན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} their mere imputation\n7. {མི་མཐུན་ཕྱོགས་ལ་ཞེན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} their opposite aspects\n8. {གཉེན་པོ་ལ་ཞེན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་པ།} their antidotes\n9. {འབྲས་བུ་རྣམ་མཁྱེན་ལས་མས་པ་ལ་ཞེན་པ་ལ་དམིགས་ནས་བདེན་གྲུབ་ཏུ་ཞེན་བ།}\nthe degeneration from the resultant omniscient mind. The mode of grasping is by conceiving the persons engaged in those practices as being truly existent practitioners.
མཐོང-བའི-ས	[darṡana bhūmi]/ The stage of seeing. One of the seven stages of a Hearer (see {ཉན་ཐོས་ཀྱི་ས་བདུན}), the realization within the mental continuum of a person abiding on the level of fruit of the stream-winner, where the selflessness of person is cognized directly for the first time via a transworldly path.
མཐོང-ལམ	[bhāvana mārga]/ The path of seeing. The third of the five paths to enlightenment, where a practioner cognizes reality directly for the first time.
མཐོང-ལམ-གྱི-བཟོད-པ-བརྒྱད	[aṣṭa bhāvanā mārga dharmakṣāntayaḥ]/ The eight moments of forbearance of the path of seeing. These are the eight moments of wisdom of the path of seeing known as the uninterrupted paths (bar-chad med-lam, see mthong-lam shes-bzod skad-cig bcu-drug—the eight forbearances and subsequent forbearances connected to the four noble truths).
མཐོང-ལམ-གྱི-ཤེས-པ-བརྒྱད	The eight moments of cognition of the path of seeing. These are the eight moments of wisdom of the path of seeing known as the path of thorough liberation (rnam-grol-lam, see mothong-lam shes-bzod skad-cig-ma bcu-drug—the eight cognitions and subsequent cognitions connected to the four noble truths).
མཐོང-ལམ-རྩོ-སྦྱོར-གྱི-སྤང-བྱ-རྟོག-པ-བཞི	The four conceptions to be abndoned on the peak training of the path of seeing. 1-2. {གཟུང་རྟོག་གཉེས།} two conceptual graspings at the object (see {གཟུང་རྟོག་གཉིས}) 3-4. {འཛིན་རྟོག་གཉིས}1 two conceptual graspings at the subject (see {འཛིན་རྟོག་གཉིས}).
མཐོང-ལམ-ཤེས-བཟོད-བསྐད-ཅིག-བཅུ-དྲུག	[ṣoḍaṡa darṡanamārgakṣāḥ]/ The sixteen moments of cognition and forbearance of the path of seeing.\n1. {སྡུག་བསྔལ་ཆོས་བཟོད།} [duḥkhe dharmakṣānti]/ forbearance with the reality of suffering\n2. {སྡུག་བསྔལ་ཆོས་ཤེས།} [duḥkhe dharmajсānam]/ cognition of the reality of suffering\n3. {སྡུ་ག་བསྔལ་རྗེས་བཟོད།} [duḥkhe 'nvayakṣānti]/ subsequent forbearance with suffering\n4. {སྡུག་བསྔལ་རྗེས་ཤེས།} [duḥkhe 'nyayajсānam]/ subsequent cognition of suffering\n5. {ཀུན་འབྱང་ཆོས་བཟོད།} [samudaye dharmakṣānti]/ forbearance with the reality of the origin of suffering\n6. {ཀུན་འབྱུང་ཆོས་ཤས།} [samudaye dharmajсānam]/ cognition of the reality of the origin of suffering\n7. {ཀུན་འབྱུང་རྗེས་བཟོད།} [samudaye 'nyayakṣānti]/ subsequent forbearance with the origin of suffering\n8. {ཀུན་འབྱུང་རྗེས་ཤས།} [samudaye 'nvayajсānam]/ subsequent cognition of the origin of suffering\n9. {འགོག་པ་ཆོས་བཟོད།} [nirodhe dharmakṣānti]/ forbearance with reality of the cessation of suffering\n10. {འགོག་པ་ཆོས་ཤེས།} [nirodhe dharmajсānam]/ cognition of the reality of the cessation of suffering\n11. {འགོག་པ་རྗེས་བཟོད།} [nirodhe 'nyayaakṣānti]/ subsequent forbearance with the cessation of suffering\n12. {འགོག་པ་རྗེས་ཤེས།} [nirodhe anvayajсānam]/ subsequent cognition of the cessation suffering\n13. {ལམ་ཆོས་བཟོད།} [mārge dharmakṣānti]/ forbearance with the reality of the path\n14. {ལམ་ཆོས་ཤེས།} [mārge dharmajсānam]/ cognition of the reality of the path\n15. {ལམ་རྗེས་བཟོད།} [mārge 'nyayakṣānam]/ subsequent forbearance with the path\n16. {ལམ་རྗེས་ཤེས།} [mārge 'nvayajсānam]/ subsequent cognition of the path. dA na shI la/[dānaṡīla]/ An Indian pandit of the eighth century born in Kashmir. He was invited to Tibet during the reign of King Trisong Deutsan and made considerable contributions in the translation of Buddhist texts into Tibetan.
དག-བ-གཉིས-ལྡན	The state free from the two delusions, obstructions to liberation and omniscience; Buddhahood.
དག-པ-བཞི	[catvāri pariṡuddhāḥ]/ The four punties; the four total purities of a Tathagata.\nA.\n1. {ལུས་དག་པ།} pure body\n2. {དམིགས་པ་དག་པ།} pure objectives\n3. {སེམས་དག་པ།} pure mind\n4. {ཡེ་ཤེས་དག་པ།} pure primordial wisdom.\nB.\n1. {གནས་དག་པ།} pure abode\n2. {ལུས་དག་པ།} pure body\n3. {ལོངས་སྦྱོད་དག་པ།} pure resources\n4. {ཡེ་ཤེས་དག་པ།} pure wisdom.
དག-པ-ས-གསུམ	The three pure stages of Bodhisattva; the last three grounds of a Bodhisattva—the eigth, ninth and tenth, where he or she is totally free of pride.
དག-བའི-སྒྱུ-ལུས	[pariṡuddha māyakāya]/ The pure illusory body. One of the practices carried out in the completion stage practice of tantra. Meditating upon the illusory nature of the entire residence and resident [maṇḍala].
དག-རྫོགས-སྨིན-གསུམ	The three principles of purification, completion and ripening. A feature explained in the Nyingma tantra where each step of the generation stage practice is qualified by these three basic principles.
དང-པོ-ཐུགས-བསྐྱེད-ཚུལ	The way in which Buddha first generated the Bodhimind. A. According to the Hinayana tradition, Buddha [ṡākyamuni] first generated the mind of enlightenment in the presence of Buddha [ṡakya Mahāmuni] (sha-kya thub-chen). B. According to [mahāyāna] tradition, he first generated the Bodhimind while yoked to a chariot"in the hell realm; this follows the tradition of the [sūtra] called Repaying the Kindness.
དང-པོ-སྦྱོར-བའི-ཏིང-ངེ-འཛིན	The concentration of first union. One of the three concentrations of the generation stage practice. It is the first because the concentration of the principal male and female deities which become the origin or source of emanating all other deities of the [maṇḍala], take over the other two concentrations in series, and the unity of method and wisdom is inseparably maintained by this practice.
དད-པ-རྣམ-གསུམ	The three types of faith.\n1. {ཡིད་ཆེས་པའི་དད་པ།} convinced faith\n2. {དང་བའི་དད་པ།} pure faith\n3. {མངོན་འདོད་ཀྱི་དད་པ།} longing faith.
དད-པ-བཞི	The four types of faith.\n1. {ཡིད་ཆེས་པའི་དད་པ།} convinced faith\n2. {དང་བའི་དད་པ།} pure faith\n3. {མངོན་འདོད་ཀྱི་དད་པ།} longing faith.\n4. {ཕྱིར་མི་ལྡོག་པའི་དད་པ།} the irreversible faith.
དད-པའི-སྟོབས	[ṡraddha bala]/ The power of faith. One of the five powers of the thirty-seven auxiliaries to enlightenment (see {བྱང་ཕྱོགས་སོ་བདུན}); an overwhelming faith in the three jewels free of any obstacles that oppose faith.
དད-བའི-ནོར	[ṡraddhā dhanam]/ The wealth of faith. One of the seven possessions of the noble ones (see {འཕགས་པའི་ནོར་བདུན}); the convinced faith in the law of causality which helps turning one's mind towards the dharma; analogous to a precious wheel.
དད-པའི-དབང-པོ	[ṡraddhendriya]/ Faculty of faith. One of the five faculties of the thirty-seven auxiliaries to enlightenment (see {བྱང་ཕྱོགས་སོ་བདུན}); an overwhelming conviction in the four noble truths.
དད-པའི-ས	[ṡraddhā bhūmi]/ The ground of faith. The stage of a spiritual path where a practitioner is predominantly skillful in the practice of faith, efforts, mindfulness, concentration and wisdom.
དམ-པ-དྲུག-ལྡན	The six-fold supreme ways. The six fundamental ways of accomplishing the six perfections (see {ཕར་ཕྱིན་དྲུག}). These are:\n1. {རྟེན་དམ་པ་བྱང་ཆུབ་ཀྱི་སེམས་དང་ལྡན་པ།} maintaining the mind of enlightenment as the fundamental basis\n2. {དངོས་པོ་དམ་པ་སྦྱིན་སོགས་ཕྱོགས་རེ་བ་མ་ཡོན་པར་གཞི་ཐམས་ཅད་ལ་འཇུག་པ།} engaging in all six perfections in an unbiased manner as the fundamental approach\n3. {ཆེད་དུ་བྱ་བ་དམ་པ་སེམས་ཅན་ཐམས་ཅད་ཀྱི་དོན་དུ་སྦྱོད་པ།} working for the welfare of all sentient beings as the fundamental beneficiary of one's practices\n4. {ཐབས་དམ་པ་འཁོར་གསུམ་རྣམ་པར་མི་རྟོག་པའི་ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱིས་ཟིན་པ།} conjoining all one's practices with the thought of purity of the three factors (see {འཁོར་གསུམ་ཡོངས་སུ་དག་པའི་འཇུག་སྒྲུབ}) through skillful wisdom as the fundamental means\n5. {ཡོངས་སུ་བསྔོ་བ་དམ་པ་བླ་མེད་བྱང་ཆུབ་ཏུ་བསྔོ་བ།} dedicating all one's virtues to the attainment of the sublime state of enlightenment as the fundamental dedication\n6. {རྣམ་དག་དམ་པ་སྒྲིབ་གཉིས་ཀྱི་དངོས་གཉེན་དུ་སྤྱོད་པ།} applying antidotal forces against the two types of delusions (see {སྒྲིབ་པ་གཉིས}) as the fundamental purification.
དམ-པ-རིགས-བརྒྱ	The hundred supreme divinities. The one hundred deities according to Guhyasamaja meditation, visualized as the Victorious one's {རྒྱལ་བའི་ཕུང་པོ་ལྔ་བ་དེ་གཤེགས་ལྔ།} five aggregates as the five Tathagatas; {ཁམས་བཞི་ཡུམ་བཞི།} four elements as the four consorts; {སྐྱེ་མཆེད་དྲུག་སེམས་དཔའ་དྲུག} six sources of perception as the six Bodhisattvas; {ཡུལ་ལྔ་རྡོ་རྗེ་མ་ལྔ་།} five objects of perception as the five Vajra Dakinis. Each of these twenty is further visualized into a class of five deities each making a cycle of one hundred deities in all.
དམ-ཚིག-གི-རྫས-ཤ-ལྔ་	[paсca samaya maṁsāḥ]/ The five fleshes of commitment.\n1. {མིའི་ཤ} [manuṣya māṁsa]/ human flesh\n2. {གླང་པོ་ཆེའི་ཤ} [hasti māṁsa]/ elephant flesh\n3. {བ་གླང་གི་ཤ} [go māṁsa]/ ox flesh\n4. {ཁྱིའི་ཤ} [kukkura māṁsa]/ dog flesh\n5. {རྟའི་ཤ} [aṡva māṁsa]/ horse flesh.
དམ-ཚིག-སེམས-དཔའ	[samayasattva]/ The commitment being. Generating oneself in the form of a deity according to the generation stage practice of tantra.
དམ-ཚིག-གསུམ-བཀོད	The threefold commitment beings. A. A type of Buddha [ṡākyamuni] images known as Dam-tshig sum-bkod, three samayas or pledges related to a Buddha's body, speech and mind (see {དམ་ཚིག་སེམས་དཔ།་ཡེ་ཤེས་སེམས་དཔའ་ཨནད་ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན་སེམས་དཔའ}). B. The three commitments to be observed:\n1. {ཁྲིལ་མི་ཉལ་བ།} not sleeping on an elevated bed\n2. {ཆང་མི་འཐུང་བ།} not taking intoxicants\n3. {ཕྱག་རྒྱ་འདྲ་བ་མི་ཟ་བ།} not consuming edible things made in the shape of the various implements of deities such as lotus, vajra, etc.
དར-དཔྱངས	[paṭṭāṅka]/ Silk ribbons; tassels of silk threads that hang over the ears from a tantric ritual head-dress.
དལ-བ-བརྒྱད	The eight leisures; the eight freedoms.\nA. Four freedoms from the four fetters within human existence:\n1. {ལོག་ལྟ་ཅན་མ་ཡིན་པ།} not holding wrong views\n2. {ཀླ་ཀློར་སྐྱེ་བ་མིན་པ།} not born in a barbaric land\n3. {རྒྱལ་བའི་བཀའ་མེད་པའི་ཡུལ་དུ་སྐྱེ་བ་མིན་པ།} not born in a place where Buddha has not appeared\n4.{ གླེན་ལྷུགས་ཅན་མ་ཡིན་པ།} not born as a mute or fool.\nB. Four freedoms from the four fetters of non-human existence:\n1. {དམྱུལ་བར་སྐྱེ་བ་མིན་པ།} not being a hell being\n2. {ཡི་དྭགས་སུ་སྐྱེ་བ་མིན་པ།} not being a hungry ghost\n3. {དུད་འགྲོར་སྐྱེ་བ་མིན་པ།} not being an animal\n4. {ལྷ་ཚེ་རིང་པོར་སྐྱེ་བ་མིན་པ།} not being a long living god.
དལ-འབྱོར-གྱི-རྟེན	A fully endowed human rebirth. A human life which is characterized by the eight leisures (see {དལ་བ་བརྒྱད}) and the ten endowments (see {སྦྱོར་བ་བཅུ}) thus making it suitable for practising Dharma.
དུག-གསུམ	The three poisons; the three poisonous delusions.\n1. {འདོད་ཆགས།} [rāga]/ desire-attachment\n2. {ཞེ་སྡང་།} [krodha]/ hatred-anger\n3. {གཏི་མུག} [moha]/ closed mindedness.
དུར-ཁྲོད-ཀྱི-ཆས-བརྒྱད	The eight adornments of an ascetic who dwells in a cemetery; the eight costumes of a cemetery Yogi.\n1. {མི་མགོའི་དབུ་རྒྱན།} he is crowned with human skulls\n2. {མི་མགོའི་དོ་ཤལ།} he wears a rosary of human heads carved in crystal\n3. { གླང་ཆེན་གྱི་པགས་པའི་སྟོད་གཡོག} he wears an elephant skin as an upper garment\n4. {ཞིང་ལྤགས་ཀྱི་གཡང་གཞི།} he uses the skin of a human being who has committed heinous non-virtues as his skin\n5. {ཞག་གི་སོར་རིས།} his forehead bears three greased lines horizontally and vertically\n6. {སྟག་སྤགས་ཀྱི་ཤམ་ཐབས།} he wears a tiger skin as his lower garment\n7.{ ཁྲག་གི་ཐིག་ལེ།} he uses blood for the tilaka between his eyes\n8. {ཐལ་ཆེན་གྱི་ཚོམ་བུ།} his body is covered with ashes.
དུར-ཁྲོད-ཆེན-པོ-བརྒྱད	[aṣṭa mahā ṡmaṡāna]/ The eight great cemeteries.\n1. {ཤར་དུ་གཏུ་དྲུག} The Fiery One to the east\n2. {བྱང་དུ་ཚང་ཚིང་འཁྲིགས་པ།} The Wilderness to the north\n3. {ནུབ་ཏུ་རྡོ་རྗེ་འབར་བ།} The Vajra Fire to the west\n4. {ལྷོར་ཀེང་རུས་ཅན།} The Skeleton Bound to the south\n5. {དབང་ལྡན་དུ་དྲག་ཏུ་རྒོད་པ།} The Terrific Laugh to the north-east\n6. {མེར་བཀྲ་ཤིས་ཆལ།} The Auspicious Garden to the south-east\n7. {བདེན་བྲལ་དུ་མུན་པ་དྲག་པོ།} The Gloomy One to the south-west\n8. {རླུང་དུ་ཀི་ལི་ཀི་ལིའི་སྒྲ་སྒྲོག་པ།} The One Pronouncing Ki-li Ki-li to the north-west.
དུར-ཁྲོད-པ	[smṡānika]/ He who dwells in a cemetery; an ascetic dwelling in a cemetery. There are three types of such practitioners: the initial practitioner dwells in the remains of the former charnel ground, the intermediate in the temporary charnel ground and the advanced in the permanent charnel ground.
དུས-ཀྱི-འཁོར-ལོ	[kālacakra]/ A tantric deity belonging to the highest class of tantra. When referred to it as a tantra, it can be understood as having three levels. 1. the outer [kālacakra] comprising the universe 2. the inner [kālacakra] comprising the system of energy channels, winds and drops of the inhabitants of the universe 3. the alternative [kālacakra] comprising the residence and resident [kālacakra] [maṇḍala] and meditation on the energy-channel, winds and essential drops.
དུས-ཁྲིམས-ཡན-ལག-བརྒྱད	The eight precepts of a specific period (see {བསྙེན་གནས་ནན་ལག་བརྒྱད}).
དུས-ཆེན-བཞི	The four great festivals; the four holy occasions in Buddha's life.\n1. {དང་པོའི་ཡར་ངོ་ལ་ཆོ་འཕྲུལ་དུས་ཆེན།} the period when Buddha performed miracles from the 1st through 15th of the first Tibetan month\n2. {བཞི་པའི་བཙ་ལྔར་མངོན་པར་རྫོགས་པར་སངས་རྒྱས་པའི་དུས་ཆེན།} the day when Buddha attained full enlightenment on the 15th of the fourth Tibetan month.\n3. {དྲུག་པའི་བཞི་ལ་ཆོས་འཁོར་བསྐོར་བསྡོར་པའི་འདུས་ཆེན།} the day which Buddha turned the wheel of dotrine on the 4th of the sixth Tibetan month.\n4. {དགུ་པའི་ཉེར་གཉིས་ལ་ལྷ་བབས་དུས་ཆེན།} the day which Buddha descended from Tusita heaven on the 22nd of the ninth Tibetan month.
དུས-ཆེན-གསུམ-འཛོམས	The combination of three festivals. The 15th of the 4th Tibetan month celebrated as Buddha's entering into the womb of his mother for conception; complete enlightenment; and passing away into [parinirvāṇa].
དུས-མཐིད-ཅིག-མ	The single instant of the end of time. According to Abhidharmkosa this is the period of time equivalent to one fraction of the sixty parts of a normal person's finger snap.
དུས-གཞན-ལ-དགོངས-པ	[kālāntarabhiprāya]/ Determining another time. Interpretive [sūtra] taught with reference to another time, e.g. the [sūtra] in which the Buddha taught, 'If you recite Sukhavati prayers you will immediately be born there', where the intention of the Buddha was that through proper practice of the precepts of the Buddha of the Blissful Realm, one may be born there in the future.
དེ-ཁོ-ན-ཉིད-བཞི	The four types of thatnesses; the four thatnesses of the Action tantra.\n1. {བདག་གི་དེ་ཁོ་ན་ཉོད།} thatness of self\n2. {སྔགས་ཀྱི་དེ་ཁོ་ན་ཉེད།} thatness of mantra\n3. {ལྷའི་དེ་ཁོ་ན་ཉིད།} thatness of the deity\n4. {བསམ་གཏན་བྱི་དེ་ཁོ་ན་ཉིད།} fatness of concentration.
དེ-ཉིད-བཅུ	[daṡatattva]/ The ten suchnesses (see {ནང་གི་དེ་ཉིད་བཅུ་} and {ཕྱིའི་དེ་ཉིད་བཅུ}@{}).
དེ-ལྟར-བྱུང-བའི-སྡེ	[Itivṛttika]/ Legendary teachings. One of the twelve scriptural categories of Buddha's teachings reaching its audience through legends.
དེ-མ-ཐག-རྐྱེན	[samanantara pratyaya]/ Immediate condition. One of the four conditions (see {རྐྱེན་བཞི}) which produce a cognition; that perception just preceding the actual understanding of an object.
དེ-ཙམ-ལྔ་	[paсca tanmātrāṇi]/ The five mere existents. According to the Sanikhya school of Hindu philosophy all phenomena are included into six categories.\n1. {གཟུགས།} [rūpa]/ form\n2. {སྒྲ།} [ṡabda]/ sound\n3. {དྲི།} [gaṅdha]/ smell\n4. {རོ།} [rasa]/ taste\n5. {རེག་བྱ།} spars'a/ object of touch.
དེ-བཞིན-ཉིད-གསུམ	The three suchnesses. According to The Compendium of Precepts ([abhidharma-samuccaya]), there is no difference in the suchness of all phenomena, however, due to the difference in their basis of existence there can be three suchnesses which are:\n1. {དགེ་བའི་དེ་བཞིན་ཉིད།} suchness of virtues\n2. {མི་དགེ་བའི་དེ་བཞིན་ཉིད།} suchness of non-virtues\n3. {ལུང་མ་བསྟན་གྱི་དེ་བཞིན་ཉིད།} suchness of the unspecified phenomena.
དེ-བཞིན-གཤེགས-པ-བཞི	The four Tathagatas.\n1. {རྒྱལ་བ་རིན་ཆེན་མང་།} Jinaratnabahulya\n2. {གཟུགས་མཛེས་དམ་པ།} [Jinasarūpottama]\n3. {སྐུ་འབྱམས་ཀླས།} [Jinaru_pa-paryānta]\n4. {འཇིགས་བཐམས་ཅད་དང་བྲལ་བ།} [Jinasarkāyavimuktasena].
དེ-བཞིན-གཤེགས-པའི-སྟོབས-བཅུ	[daṡa tathāgata balāni]/ The ten powers of a Buddha.\n1. {གནས་དང་གནས་མིན་མཁྱེན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [sthānāsthāna jсāna balam]/ power of knowing right from wrong\n2. {ལས་ཀྱི་རྣམ་པར་སྨིན་པ་མཁྱེན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [karma vipāka jсana balam]/ power of knowing the consequences of actions\n3. {མོས་པ་སྣ་ཚོགས་མཁྱེན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [nānādhimukti jсāna balam]/ power of knowing various mental inclinations\n4. {ཁམས་སྣ་ཚོགས་མཁྱེན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [nānā dhātu jсāna balam]/ power of knowing various mental faculties\n5. {དབང་པོ་སྣ་ཚོགས་མཁྱེན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [indriya varāvara jсāna balam]/ power of knowing various degrees of intelligence\n6. {ཐམས་ཅད་དུ་འགྲོ་བའི་ལམ་མཁྱེན་པའི་སྟོབ།} [sarvatra gāmam pratipaj jсāna balam]/ power of knowing the paths to all goals\n7. {ཀུན་ནས་ཉོན་མོངས་པ་དང་རྣམ་པར་བྱང་བ་མཁྱེན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [saṁkleṡa vyavadāna vyutthāna jсāna balam]/ power of knowing the ever-afflicted and purified phenomena\n8. {སྔོན་གྱི་གནས་རྗེས་སུ་དྲན་པ་མཁྱེན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [pūrva nivāsānusmṛti jсāna balam]/ power of knowing past lives\n9. {འཆི་འཕོ་བ་དང་སྐྱེ་བ་མཁྱེན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [cyutyutpatti jсana balam]/ power of knowing death and birth\n10. {ཟག་པ་ཟད་པ་མཁྱེན་པའི་སྟོབས།} [āṡrava kṣaya jсāna balam]/ power of knowing the exhaustion of contaminations.
དོན-གྱི-འོད-གསལ	The meaning clear light. The transformation of the basic clear light mind into its final form through meditation; a completion stage practice of tantra
དོན-གྲུབ-ཀྱི-དམ-ཚིག-གཉིས	The two pledges concerning the Buddha Amoghasiddhi.\n1. {སྡོམ་པ་གསུམ་གྱི་བཅས་པ་མཐའ་དག་བསྲུང་བའི་དམ་ཚིག} safeguarding all precepts of the three vows\n2. {མཆོད་པའི་དམ་ཚིག} pledges concerning the practices of offering and worship.
དོན-གཉིས	Two purposes; two goals.\n1. {རང་དོན།} the purpose of self\n2. {གཞན་དོན།} the purpose of others.
དོན-དམ-གཉིས	The two types of ultimate truths.\nA.\n1. {རྣམ་གྲངས་པའི་དོན་དམ།} the nominal ultimate truth\n2. {རྣམ་བྲངས་མ་ཡིན་པའི་དོན་དམ།} the real ultimate truth.\nB.\n1. {མཐུན་པའི་དོན་དམ།} the approximate ultimate truth\n2. {དོན་དམ་དངོས།} the actual ultimate truth.
དོན-དམ-གསུམ	The three types of ultimate truth.\n1. {དོན་དོན་དམ་པ།} [arthaparamārtha]/ ultimate meaning\n2. {ཐོབ་པ་དོན་དམ་པ།} [prāptaparamārtha]/ ultimate accomplishment\n3. {སྒྲུབ་པ་དོན་དམ་པ།} [siddhaparamārtha]/ ultimate practice.
དོན-དམ-བདེན-པ	[paramārtha satya]/ Ultimate truth. Generally referring to emptiness as opposed to the conventional phenomena.
དོན-དམ-པ-སྟོང-པ-ཉིད	[paramārtha ṡūnyatā]/ The emptiness of that which is ultimate. One of the sixteen types of emptinesses; the emptiness of [nirvāṇa].
དོན-དམ-པའི-སྐྱབས	[paramārtha ṡaraṇam]/ The ultimate object of refuge, i.e. the Buddha [ṡākyamuni].
དོན-དམ-པའི-མཚན-ཉིད-ལྔ་	The five characteristics of the ultimate truth; emptiness.\n1. {བརྗོད་དུ་མེད་པ།} inexpressible\n2. {གཉིས་སུ་མེད་པ།} non-dual\n3. {རྟོག་གེའི་ཡུལ་མིན་པ།} not being an object of logicians\n4. {རོ་གཅིག་པ།} single-taste\n5. {མཚན་ཉིད་མེད་པ།} signiessness.
དོན-དམ-པའི-སྲུང-འཁོར	The ultimate protection wheel; meditation on the protection wheel by means of the primordial wisdom.
དོན-བདུན-ཅུ	[arthasaptati]/ The Seventy Topics. The seventy divisions of the eight realizations or topics (see {དངོས་པོ་བརྒྱད}).\n1-10. {རྣམ་མཁྱེན་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བཅུ།} the ten topics that characterize the omniscient mind (see {རྣམ་མཁྱེན་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བཅུ})\n11-21. {ལམ་ཤེས་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བཅུ་གཅིག} the eleven topics that characterize the knowledge of the paths (see {ལམ་ཤེས་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་དགུ}) 22-30. {གཞེ་ཤེས་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་དག} the nine topics that characterize the knowledge of the basis (see {གཞི་ཤེས་མཏཧསོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་དགུ})\n31-41. {རྣམ་རྫོགས་སྦྱོར་བ་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བཅུ་གཅིག} the eleven topics that characterize the training of the complete aspects (see {རྣམ་རྫོགས་སྦྱོར་བ་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བཅུ་གཅིག})\n42-49. {རྩེ་མོའི་སྦྱོར་བ་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བརྒྱད།} the eight topics that characterize the peak training (see {རྩེ་མོའི་སྦྱོར་བ་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བརྒྱད})\n50-62. {མཐར་གྱིས་སྦྱོར་བ་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བཅུ་གསུམ།} the thirteen topics that characterize the serial training (see {མཐར་གྱིས་སྦྱོར་བ་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བཅུ་གསུམ})\n63-66. {སྐད་ཅིག་མའི་སྦྱོར་བ་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བཞི།} the four topics that characterize the momentary training (see {སྐད་ཅིག་མའི་སྦྱོར་བ་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བཞི})\n67-70. {འབྲས་བུ་ཆོས་སྐུ་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བཞི།} the four topics that characterize the resultant truth body (see {འབྲས་བུ་ཆོས་སྐུ་མཚོན་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བཞི}).
དོན-སྦྱི	Meaning generality; generic image. The image of an object in thought or idea, e.g. the vase as it would appear in the imagination.
དེན-བྱེད-ནུས-པ	[arthakriyāṡakti]/ A functioning thing; effective phenomena. The class of phenomena that has the ability or power to effect changes. Synonymous to impermanence.
དོན-གཞན-ལ-དགོངས-པ	[arthāntarābhiprāya]/ Determining another meaning; intending another meaning. Interpretive [sūtra] indicating another meaning, e.g. the [sūtra], 'all phenomena lack inherent existence', to those who accept inherent existence as their basic philosophy.
དོན-གཟུངས	Meaning retention; retaining the meaning. Spiritual power of retaining the meaning of teachings that are received from the Buddhas and Bodhisattvas, e.g. the practice of the Bodhisat-tva levels and the ten perfections. This may also mean the power to retain the specific or general meaning of all that exists.
དོར-བ-མེད-པ-སྟོ-ང-པ-ཉིད	[anavakāra ṡūnyatā] The emptiness of that which is not to be abandoned. One of the sixteen types of emptinesses (see {སྟོང་པ་ཉིད་བཅུ་དྲུག}); the lack of inherent existence of the reality of all phenomena which is neither to be abandoned nor discarded.
དྭགས-པོ-བཀའ-བརྒྱུད	Dakpo Kagyud Tradition. The Kagyud tradition that comes from Marpa, Milarepa and Dagpo Lhaje (Gampopa); because this tradition flourished extensively during Dagpo Lhaje (1079-1153), the sun-like disciple of Milarepa, it is known as Dagpo Kagyud. A sub-school of Kagyud's mainstream.
དྲང-སྲོང་	[ṛṣi]/ A Sage (Rishi); Lit. 'the righteous one'. Ancient vedic masters and practitioners; [mahārṣi] is used as an epithet for Buddha.
དྲན-པ-བཅུ	[daṡa smṛtiayaḥ]/ The ten mindfulnesses (see {རྗེས་སུ་དྲན་པ་བཅུ}).
དྲན-པ-ཉེ-བར-བཞག-པ-བཞི	[catvāri smṛtyūpasthānāḥ]/ The four close mindfulnesses; the four close contemplations. The four objects of mindfulness for mental quiescence meditation.\n1. {ལུས་དྲན་པ་ཉེ་བར་བཞག་པ།}\n[kāya smṛtyūpasthāna]/ close contemplation of body\n2. {ཚོར་བ་དྲན་པ་ཉེ་བར་བཞག་བ།} [vedanā smṛtyūpasthāna]/ close contemplation of feelings\n3. {སེམས་དྲན་བཉེ་བར་བཞག་པ།} [citta smṛtyūpasthāna]/ close contemplation of mind\n4. {ཆོས་དྲན་པ་ཉེ་བར་བཞག་པ།} [dharma smṛtyūpasthāna]/ close contemplation of Dharma.
དྲན-པ-ཉི-བར-བཞག-པ-གསུམ	The three mindfulnesses of a Buddha.\n1. {གདུལ་བྱ་གུས་པས་ཉན་པ་ལ་ཆགས་པ་མེད་པ།} he has no attachment towards those who listen respectfully\n2. {གུས་པས་མི་ཉན་བ་ལ་སྡང་བ་མེད་པ།} he has no hatred towards those who do not listen respectfully\n3. {འདྲེས་མར་འཇུག་པ་ལ་གཉིས་ཀ་མིན་པ།} he has neither attachment nor hatred to those who listen him with mixed feeling.
དྲི-བཅས-རྣམ-བརྫུན	The False Aspect ([cittamātrin]) School. A sub-school of the Mind Oniy school which asserts that the Buddha's primordial awareness is conjoined with the stains of dualistic appearence.
དྲི-དྲུག	[ṣaḍ gandhāḥ]/ The six types of smells; the six odours.\n1. {དྲི་ཞིམ་པ།} [sugandha]/ sweet smell\n2. {དྲི་ང་བ།} [durgandha]/ bad smell\n3. {དྲི་མཉམ་པ།} [samagaridha]/ indifferent smell\n4. {ལྷན་སྐྱེས་ཀྱི་དྲི།} [sahaja gandha]/ natural smell\n5. {སྦྱར་བྱུང་གི་དྲི།} [samyojaka gandha]/ artificial smell 6. {གྲུར་བ་ལས་བྱུང་བའི་དྲི།} converted smell.
དྲི-མ-དྲུག	A. The six waste products of the body.\n1. {དྲི་ཆིན།} excrement\n2. {དྲེ་ཆུ།} urine\n3. {མིག་སྐྱག} eye mucus\n4. {རྣ་སྤབས།} ear wax\n5. {མཆིལ་མ།} saliva\n6. {སྣོབས།} snot.\nB. The six wrong attitudes to be discarded while listening to a teaching.\n1. {ང་རྒྱལ།} pride\n2. {མ་དད་པ།} lack of faith\n3.{ དོན་གཉེར་མེད་པ།} lack of interest\n4. {རྣམ་པར་གཡོང་བ།} distraction\n5. {རྨུགས་པ།} mental sloth\n6. {རྒོད་པ།} despair.
དྲིམ-མེད-པ	[vimala bhūmi]/ The Stainless Ground. The second of the ten Bodhisattva grounds (see {ས་བཅུ}) during which there is special practice of the perfection of moral discipline and self-control.
དྲི-མགསུམ	The three waste products. The three waste products of our body,\n1. {ཁ་ཟས་སྐ་བའི་སྙིགས་མ་བཤང་བ།} faeces as the waste product of gross food\n2. {སླ་བའི་སྙིགས་མ་གཅིན།} urine as the waste product of liquids\n3. {དྲོད་ཀྱི་སྙིགས་མ་རྔུལ་ནག} sweat as the waste product of the body's warmth.
དྲི-མེད-རྣམ-བརྫུན	The True Aspect ([cittamātrin]) School. A sub-school of the [cittamātrin]s who assert that the primordial awareness of the Buddha is free from the stains of dualistic appearance.
དྲི-ཟ	[gandharva]/ The smell eaters. The intermediate beings, categorized as belonging to the class of hungry ghosts, who sustain on the smoke of burnt offerings.
དྲིན-ཅན-གྱི-ལོ-པཎ-གསུམ	The three kind master-translators. The three great translators of the eighth century in Tibet during the reign of King Trisong Deutsan:\n1. Jinamitra\n2. [dhanaṡīla]\n3. Zhang Yeshede.
དྲུག-པ-ཚེས-བཞི	The 6th of the 4th Tibetan month. The celebration of Buddha's turning of the wheel of doctrine of the four noble truths at [vārāṇasi]. One of the important Buddhist festivals.
དྲུག-སྡེ	[ṣaḍ vargika]/ The six close disciples of Buddha [ṡākyamuni],\nwho were punished by Buddha [ṡākyamuni] for their breach of disciplines.\n1. {དགའ་བོ།} Nanda\n2. {ཉེ་དགའ་བོ།} Upananda\n3. {འགྲོ་མབྱོགས།} [aṡvaka]\n4. {ནབས་སོ།} Punarvasu\n5. {འདུན་པ།} Chanda\n6. {འཆར་ཀ།} [udāyi].
དྲེགས-པ-བཅོ-ལྔ་	The fifteen types of arrogance.\n1. {ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་ཀྱིས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of observing moral discipline\n2. {ཐོས་པས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of being learned\n3. {སྤོས་པས་དྲེགསཔ།} arrogance of being proud\n4. {རྙེད་པས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of finding wealth\n5. {བཀུར་སྟིས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of being respected by others\n6. {རིག་གནས་མཁས་པས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of being a scholar in the sciences of learning\n7. {དབེན་གནས་ཀྱིས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of being a hermit\n8. {སྦྱངས་པའི་ཡོན་ཏན་གྱིས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of the knowledge and trainings received\n9. {ཡོ་བྱད་ཉུང་བས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of owning only a few material possessions\n10. {གཟུགས་བཟང་བས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of possessing excellent physical features\n11. {ལོངས་སྦྱོད་ཀྱིས་དྲེགསཔ།} arrogance of being rich\n12. {དབང་ཆེ་བས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of being powerful\n13. {འཁོར་གཡོག་བཟང་བས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of having an excellent circle of followers and servants\n14. {བསམ་གཏན་མངོནཤེས་ཀྱིས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of possessing meditative concentrations and extra-sensory perceptions\n15. {ལྷ་ཀླུ་སོགས་ཀྱིས་བསྟོད་པས་དྲེགས་པ།} arrogance of being praised by gods and nagas.
གདགས-གཞི	A basis of imputation, e.g. the five psycho-physical aggregates which are the basis for imputing 'person', 'I' or 'self.
གདན-གསུམ-གྱི-དཀྱིལ-འཁོར	The [maṇḍala] of threefold seats. The meditation of visualizing one's own physical aggregates, sensory faculties and sources of perceptions as a divine [maṇḍala] of threefold seats in their entirety.\n1. {ཕུང་ཁམས་གཤེགས་པ་གཤེགས་མའི་གདན།} visualizing one's aggregates and sensory faculties as the seat for the male and female Tathagathas\n2. {སྐྱེ་མཆེད་སེམས་དཔའ་སེམས་མའི་གདན།} visualizing one's sources of perceptions as the seat for the male and female Bodhisattvas\n3. {ཡན་ལག་ཁྲོ་བོ་ཁྲོ་མོའི་གདན།} visualizing one's limbs as the seat for the male and female wrathful deities.
གདམས-ངག	[upadeṡa]/ Instruction. The essential spiritual communication—oral, written or intuitive, given by a guru to his disciple.
དལ-བ-ཆོས-ཉིད-ཀྱི-ས	The exalted ground of reality. According to the Nyingma teachings this refers to the ninth ground attained at the fifth level of yoga when a trainee transcends all apprehensions of the activity and appearance of reality through his experience of the inseparability of the objective ultimate meahing clear light mind and the subjective divine body appearances.
གདུང-རྒྱུད	Blood lineage; a hereditary hierarch. The patriarchal or matriarchal lineage holder of an exalted being, e.g. the heirs of the [ṡākya] tradition.
གདོད-མའི-སངས-རྒྱས	[ādibuddha]/ The primordial Buddha. The primordial Buddha, Samantabhadra. However, the basic primordial Buddha is recognized as the [tathāgata] essence within the mental continuum of all sentient beings.
གདོན-གསུམ	The three evil forces.\n1. {སྟེང་གདོན་གཟའ་དང་རྒྱུ་སྐར།} the planet of the upper world\n2. {བར་གདོན་བཙན་དང་རྒྱལ་པོ།} the mountain-gods of the intermediate world\n3. {འོག་གདོན་ཀླུ་དང་ས་བདག} the nagas and earth-lords of the subterranean world.
བདག-རྐྱེན	The fundamental condition. Something which is the main producer of a result but does not actually transform it into its substantial continuity, e.g. the eye sense power that generates eye consciousness.
བདག-བསྐྱེད	[sādhana]/ Self-generation. A tantric practice of generating oneself into a deity and carrying out incantations of mantras and then dissolving into the sphere of emptiness at the conclusion, etc., according to a ritual-text ([sādhana]).
བདག-གི-དེ-ཁོ-ན-ཉིད	The suchness of self. One of the four suchnesses in action tantra meditation. In this meditation, also known as the pure reality deity of the right view, a trainee visualizes a deity within the understanding of one's mind being empty and clear and free of any elaboration and total pacification of all conventional appearances. Hence, his experience qualifies six features (see {བདེ་གཤེགས་སྙིང་པོའི་ཆོས་དྲུག}).
བདག-གི-གཞི	The self-basis. In performance tantra it is the practice of self-generation in the form of a deity.
བདག-གཅིག-འབྲེལ	Relationship of identical nature, e.g. the relationship between a functional thing and an impermanent thing.
བདག-འཇུག	Self-empowerment; self-initiation. The practice of receiving initiation directly from the deity in the [maṇḍala] without a tantric preceptor; a lama before giving initiation to others receives self-initiation from the wisdom-beings and meditates himself being inseparable from the deity.
བདག-ཏུ-རྨོངས-པའི-མ-རིག-པ	The ignorance of self-nescience. This refers to the ignorance that is the root of cyclic existence. The lack of knowledge of reality through which one sees one's aggregates as permanent, blissful, being the self, being solid and being the person contradicting the real nature of phenomenal status.
བདག-ལྟ-གཉིས	The two types of view of self. The two wrong views of self to be refuted through logical reasoning.\n1. {ཆོས་ཀྱི་བདག་ཏུ་ལྷ་བ།} [dharma ātmagrāha]/ the view of a self of person\n2. {གང་ཟག་གི་བདག་ཏུ་ལྟ་བ།} [puruṣātmagrāha]/ the view of self of phenomena.
བདག-ལྟ-ཉ-ཤུ	The twenty views of self; the twenty wrong views of self.\n1. {གཟུགས་བདག་ཏུ་ལྷ་བ།} the view of form as self\n2. {གཟུགས་ལ་བདག་དང་ལྡན་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as possessing form\n3. {གཟུགས་ལ་བདག་ཡོད་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as abiding in form\n4. {བདག་ལ་གཟུགས་ཡོད་པར་ལྟབ།} the view of form as abiding in self\n5. {ཚོར་བ་བདག་ཏུ་ལྷ་བ།} the view of feeling as self\n6. {བདག་ཚོར་བ་དང་ལྡན་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as possessing feeling\n7. {ཚོར་བ་ལ་བདག་ཡོད་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as abiding in feeling\n8. {བདག་ལ་ཚོར་བ་ཡོད་བར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of feeling as abiding in self\n9. {འདུ་ཤེས་བདག་ཏུ་ལྟ་བ།} the view of perception as self\n10. {བདག་འདུཤེས་དང་ལྡན་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as possessing perception\n11. {འདུཤེས་ལ་བདག་ཡོད་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as abiding in perception\n12. {བདག་ལ་འདུ་ཤེས་ཡོད་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of perception as abiding in self\n13. {འདུ་བྱེད་བདག་ཏུ་ལྟ་བ།} the view of compositional factors as self\n14. {བདག་འདུ་བྱེད་དང་ལྡན་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as possessing compositional factors\n15. {འད་བྱེད་ལ་བདག་ཡོད་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as abiding in compositional factors\n16. {བདག་ལ་འདུ་བྱེད་ཡོད་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of compositional factors as abiding in self\n17. {རྣམ་ཤེས་བདག་ཏུ་ལྟ་བ།} the view of consciousness as self\n18. {བདག་རྣམ་ཤེས་དང་ལྡན་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as possessing consciousness\n19. {རྣམ་ཤེས་ལ་བདག་ཡོད་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as abiding in consciousness\n20. {བདག་ལ་རྣམ་ཤེས་ཡོད་པར་ལྟ་བ།} the view of consciousness as abiding in self.
བདག-ལྟ-ཉེར-ལྔ་	The twenty-five views of self; the wrong views of self (see 1 -20, bdag-lta nyi-shu, above) plus:\n21. {བདག་གཟུགས་ལས་གཞན་དུ་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as other than form\n22. {བདག་ཚོར་བ་ལས་གཞན་དུ་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as other than feeling\n23. {བདག་འདུ་ཤེས་ལས་གཞན་དུ་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as other than perception\n24. {བདག་འདུ་བྱེད་ལས་གཞན་དུ་ལྟ་བ།} the view of self as other than compositional factors\n25. {བདག་རྣམ་ཤེས་ལས་གཞན་དུ་ལྷ་བ།} the view of self as other than consciousness.
བདག-པོའི-འབྲས-བུ	[adhipatiphala]/ Environmental results. One's own experience of environment which is a result of one's previous actions in association with the community or surrounding in which one resides, e.g. the local fields which will not yield crops.
བདག-བྱིན-གྱིས-བརླབ-པའི-རིམ-པ	The stage of blessing oneself. The ritual and rite of purifying one's impure body and faculties, thereby blessing these into three vajras—vajra body, speech and mind.
བདག-འབྲས	[adhipatiphala]/ The environmental result (see {བདག་པོའི་འབྲས་བུ}).
བདག-མེད	[nairātmya]/ Selflessness. The view of selflessness or the lack of an identity of independently existing phenomenon. There are two types:\n1. {གང་ཟག་གི་བདག་མེད།} [puruṣa nairātmya]/ the elflessness of person\n2. {ཆོས་ཀྱི་བདག་མེད།} [dharma nairātmya]/ the selflessness of phenomena.
བདག-མེད-མ	[nairātmyā]/ She the Non-ego ([anātma]). The consort of Hevajra. Marpa's consort is also knwon by this name because of his spiritual association with the deity [hayagrīva]
བདག-མེད-ཕྲ-རགས	The gross and subtle selflessnesses. The lack of an independent and self-suficient person and the lack of the inherent existence of a person.
བདག-འཛིན-གཉིས	Two types of graspings at the self; the conceptual misapprehension of a truly existent self of either a person or a phenomenon.\n1. {བདག་འཛིན་ཀུན་བཏགས།} intellectual grasping at the self\n2. {བདག་འཛིན་ལྷན་སྐྱེས།} innate grasping at the self.
བདུད-ཀྱི-མདའ-ལྔ་	The five evil arrows; the five evil influences.\n1. {ཆགས་པར་བྱེད་པའི་མདའ།} that causing desirious attachment\n2. {རྨོངས་བྱེད་ཀྱི་མདའ།} that causing ignorance\n3. {ང་རྒྱལ་གྱི་མདའ།} that causing pride\n4. {འཐབ་བྱེད་ཀྱི་མདའ།} that causing conflict\n5. {གཡེང་བྱེད་ཀྱི་མདའ།} that causing distraction.
བདུད-དགའ-རབ-དབང-ཕྱུག-གི-མེ-ཏོག-གི-མདའ-ལྔ་	The five flower-arrows of the Lord of Desire; the five evil influences of lust.\n1. {དྲེགས་པར་བྱེད་པའི་མདའ།} that causing arrogance\n2. {རྨོངས་པར་བྱེད་པའི་མདའ།} that causing ignorance\n3. {ཀུན་} {ཏུ་རྨོངས་པར་བྱེད་པའི་མདའ།} that causing strong ignorance\n4. {བརྒྱལ་བར་བྱེད་པའི་མདའ།} that causing one to faint\n5. {སེམས་མེད་པར་བྱེད་པའི} {མདའ།} that causing unconsciousness.
བདུད-རྩི-ལྔ	[paсcamṛtāni]/ The five nectars; the five substances for preparing an inner offering in tantric practices.\n1. {དྲ་ཆེན།} excrement\n2. {དྲི་ཆུ།} urine\n3. {རཀྟ།} blood 4.{ མཾས།} flesh\n5. {རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཟིལ་པ།} white and red regenerative substances.
བདུད-བཞི	[catvāri mārāḥ]/ The four devils; the four evil forces.\n1. {ཕུང་པོའི་བདུད།} [skandhamāra]/ the evil of the aggregates\n2. {ཉོན་མོངས་པའི་བདུད།} [kleṡamara]/ the evil of afflictions\n3. {འཆི་བདག་གི་བདུད།} [mrṭyupatimāra]/ the evil of death\n4. {ལྷའི་བུ་ཡི་བདུད།} [devaputramāra]/ the evil of the son of god (lust).
བདུད-བཞི-ཕྲ-མོ	[catvāri sūkṣma mārāḥ]/ The four subtle evils; the four subtle hinderances.\n1. {ཕུང་པོའི་བདུད་ཕྲ་མོ།} [skandha sūkṣma māra]/the subtle evil of the aggregates, i.e. the aggregates caused by the latency of ignorance and uncontaminated actions\n2. {ཉོན་མོངས་པའི་བདོད་ཕྲ་མོ།} [kleṡa sūkṣma mara]/ the subtle evil of affliction, i.e. the latency of ignorance\n3. {འཆི་བདག་གི་བདུད་ཕྲ་མོ།} [mṛtyupati sūkṣma māra]/ the subtle evil of death; i.e. inconceiveable death\n4. {ལྷའི་བུ་ཡི་བདུད་ཕྲ་མ།} [devaputra kleṡa sūkṣma māra]/ the subtle evil of lust, i.e. those evils other than the first three.
བདུད-བཞི-རགས-པ	[catvāri sthūla mārāḥ]/ The four gross evils; the four gross hinderances.\n1. {ཕུང་བོའི་བདུད་རགས་པ།} [skandha sthūla māra]/ the gross evil of the aggregates, i.e. the contaminated aggregates\n2. {ཉོན་མོངས་པའི་བདུད་རགས་པ།} [kleṡa sthūla mara]/ the gross evil of afflictions, i.e. the six root delusions (see {རཏཟ་ཉོན་དྲུག}) and the twenty secondary delusions (see {ཉེ་ཉོན་ཉི་ཤུ})\n3. {འཆི་བདག་གི་བདུད་རགསཔ།} [mṛtyupati sthūla māra]/ the gross evil of death, i.e. natural death through severance of the life force\n4. {ལྷའི་བུ་ཡི་བདུད་རགས་པ།} [devaputra sthūla māra]/ the gross evil of lust, i.e. the evil of Kamadeva.
བདུན-རྣམ-དག	The seven pure practices.\n1. {བཤགས་པ།} confession\n2. {རྗེས་སུ་ཡི་རང།} rejoicing\n3. {དོན་དམ་པའི་བྱང་ཆུབ་ཀྱི་སེམས་བསྐྱེད་པ།} generating the ultimate mind of enlightenment\n4. {སྐྱབས་འགྲོ} taking refuge\n5. {སྨོན་སེམས་བསྐྱེད་པ།} generating the aspiring mind of enlightenment\n6. {འཇུག་སེམས་བསྐྱེད་པ།} generating the engaging mind of enlightenment\n7. {བསྔོ་བ།} dedication.
བདེ-སྐྱོང-འཁོར-ལོ	[sukhapāla cakra]/ The wheel of sustaining bliss. The channel wheel located at the region of the secret organ which has thirty-two petals spreading out from the central channel like the ribs of an umbrella spreading downwards.
བདེ-འགྲོ	[sugati]/ Fortunate beings; happy migrators. Beings in the fortunate realm — humans, gods and demi-gods.
བདེ-ཚེན-འཁོར-ལོ	[mahāsukha cakra]/ The wheel of great bliss. The channel wheel located at the level of the third eye which has thirty-two petals spreading out from the central energy channel like the ribs of an umbrella spreading downwards.
བདེ-ཆེན-ཕྱག-རྒྱ-ཆེན-མོ	[mahāṁudrā]/ The [mahāmudrā] of great bliss. The [mahāmudrā] meditation according to the Kagyud tradition known as the [mahāmudrā] of the path of liberation (grol-lam phyag-rgya chen-mo)—the union of emptiness and the unchanging great bliss.
བདེ-ཆེན-ཞིང་	[sukhāvatī]/ The [sukhāvatī] Buddha field. The abode of Buddha Amitabha called the Buddha field of great bliss in the western direction.
བདེ-སྟོང-དབྱེར-མེད	The inseparability of bliss and void; the unity of great bliss, the method, and emptiness, the wisdom aspect. Also the Guru [pūja] rite and meditation in the Gelug tradition.
བདེ-གཤེགས-མཆེད-བརྒྱད	The eight Medicine Buddhas (see {སྨན་བླ་བདེ་གཤེགས་བརྒྱད}).
བདེ-གཤེགས-སྙིང-པོའི-ཆོས-དྲུག	The six features of the [tathāgata] essence.\n1. {གཟུང་འཛིན་ལ་སོགས་པའི་རྟོག་པ་མེད་པ།} being free from grasping at subjective or objective phenomena\n2. {རྣམ་པར་མི་རྟོག་པའི་སྣང་བ་མེད་པ།} being free of a non-conceptual appearances\n3. {རྡུལ་ཕྲ་རབ་ཀྱི་གཟུགས་མེད་པ།} being free of body of subtle particles\n4. {མཚན་མའི་གཡོ་བ་མེད་པ།} being free of disturbances from imaginative signs\n5. {དེ་རྣམས་ཀྱིས་སྟོང་པའི་མེད་དགག་ལས་འདས་པའི་རང་བཞིན་འོད་གསལ་བ།} being naturally clear because their emptiness transcends non-affirming negatives\n6. {རང་གི་ངོ་བོ་སོ་སོ་རང་གིས་རག་པའི་མཚན་ཉི་ཅན།} experiencing the self-nature by intuitive awareness.
བདེན-པ-གཉིས	The two truths; the two divisions of truth.\n1. {ཀུན་རྫོབ་བདེན་པ།} [saṁvrti satya]/ the conventional truth\n2. {དོན་དམ་བདེན་པ།} [paramārtha satya]/ the ultimate truth.
