སྤྱི-མཐུན-གྱི-ལས	Collective karma; common karma, e.g. karma of a society or locality.
སྤྱི-གཙོ-བོ	[prakṛti]/ The Fundamental Nature; the Universal Principle. The fundamental principle as asserted by the [saṁkhyā] school_of Hindu philosophy, which is permanent, pervasive over all animate and inanimate objects, is the creator of all activities and is an undifferentiable unit.
སྤྱི-མཚན	[sāmānya lakṣaṇa]/ Generally characterized phenomena. Phenomena that are ultimately unable to perform a function, e.g. space.
སྤྱི-བཞི	The four types of generality.\n1. {ཚོགས་སྤྱི།} [saṁgraha sāmānya]/ collective generality\n2. {རིགས་སྦྱི།} [gotra sāmānya]/ categorical generality\n3. {དོན་སྤྱི།} [artha sāmānya]/ meaning generality\n4. {སྒྲ་སྤྱི།} [ṡabda sāmānya]/ sound generality.
སྤྱོད-རྒྱུད	[cārya Tantra]; Performance Tantra. The second of the four classes of tantras, stressing the importance of a balanced approach in both the external rites and internal mental activity.
སྤྱོད-རྒྱུད-ཀྱི-དམ-ཚིག-བཅུ-བཞི	The fourteen commitments related to performance tantra.\n1-10. {མི་དགེ་བ་བཅུ་སྤོང་བ།} The abandonment of the ten non-virtues (see {མི་བ་བཅུ}),\n11. {དམ་པའི་ཆོས་མི་གཏོང་བ།} not to abandon the sublime Dharma\n12. { བྱང་ཆུབ་ཀྱི་སེམས་མི་གཏོང་བ།} not giving up the mind of enlightenment\n13. {སེར་སྣས་མི་གཏོང་བ།} not abandoning practicing giving due to miserliness\n14. {སེམས་ཅན་ལ་གནོད་མི་བྱེད་པ།} not harming other sentient beings.
སྤྱོད-རྒྱུད-ཀྱི-དབང-དྲུག	[ṣaḍ cārya tantra abhiṣekhāḥ]/ The six initiations of performance tantra.\n1. {མེ་ཏོག་ཕྲེང་དབང་།} initiation of flower garland\n2. {ཆུའི་དབང་།} water initiation\n3. {ཅོད་པཎ་གྱི་དབང་།} crown initiation\n4. {རྡོ་རྗེའི་དབང་།} vajra initiation\n5. {དྲིལ་བུའི་དབང་།} bell initiation\n6. {མིང་གི་དབང་།} name initiation.
སྤྱོད-རྒྱད-རིགས-གསུམ	[tri cārya tantra gotrāḥ]/ The three families of performance tantra.\nA.\n1. {དེ་བཞིན་གཤེགས་པའི་རིགས།} the [tathāgata] family\n2. {པད་མའི་རིགས།} the lotus family\n3. {རྡོ་རྗེའི་རིགས།} the vajra family.\nB.\nThat of {སྐུ་སུང་ཐུགས་ཀྱི་རིགས།} Buddha's body, speech and mind.
སྤྱོད-འཇུག	A Guide to the Bodhisattva's Way of Life ([bodhisattvacāryāvatāra]).\nA fundamental text of [mahāyāna] composed by [ācārya ṡāntideva] during the eighth century, in which a Bodhisattva's conduct is explained.
སྤྱོད-པ-རྣམ-བཞི	The four activities.\nA.\n1. {འགྲོ་བ།} going\n2. {འཆག་པ།} walking\n3. {ཉལ་བ།} sleeping\n4. {འདུག་པ།} waking.\nB.\n1. {ཀུན་བཟང་སྤྱོད་པ།} all-good behaviour\n2. {གསང་བའི་སྤྱོད་པ།} secret behaviour\n3. {འདུ་འཛིའི་སྤྱོད་པ།} behaviour in a crowd\n4. {ཕྱག་ཆེན་གྱི་སྤྱོད་པ།} the [mahāmudrā] behaviour.
སྤྱོད-པའི-སྒོ-བཞི	The doors of activity in performance tantra.\n1. {འཇུག་པའི་སྦྱོད་པ།} activity of entering into practice\n2. {སྦྱོར་བའི་སྤྱོད་པ།} activity of application\n3. {སྒྲུབ་པའི་སྦྱོད་པ།} activity of the actual stage of practice\n4. {གྲུབ་པའི་སྤྱོད་པ།} activity of accomplishment.
སྤྲིན-ལྟ-བུའི-སེམས-བསྐྱེད	[meghopamacittotpāda]/ Cloud-like Bodhicitta. The mind of enlightenment associated with skillful means within the continuum of a [nirmāṇakāya] Buddha.
སྤྲུལ-སྐུ-གསུམ	The three emanation bodies of a Buddha.\n1. {བཟོ་བོ་སྤྲུལ་སྐུ།} [ṡilpa nirmāṇakāya]/ artisan emanation\n2. {སྐྱེ་བ་སྤྲུལ་སྐུ།} [janma nirmāṇakāya]/ miscellaneous emanation\n3. {མཆོག་གི་སྤྲུལ་སྐུ།} [uttama nirmaṇakāya]/ supreme emanation.
སྤྲུལ-པའི-འཁོར-ལོ	[nirmāṇacakra]/ The wheel of emanation; the channel-wheel located at the navel.
སྤྲུལ-པའི-མུ-སྟེགས-པ	A non-Buddhist by emanation. Buddhas and Bodhisattvas who have chosen to emanate as teachers of non-Buddhist philosophy in order to lead those beings not yet ripened to progress on the higher states of realizations.
སྤྲུལ-ལམ-གསུམ	The three paths of manifestation; the three paths of emanation (see {རྣམ་ཐར་བརྒྱད}A.).
སྤྲོས-པའི-མཐའ-བརྒྱད	The eight extremes; the eight extreme views.\n1. {སྐྱེ་མཐའ།} production\n2. {འགག་མཐའ།} cessation\n3. {རྟག་མཐའ།} eternalism\n4. {ཆད་མཐའ།} nihilism\n5. {འགྲོ་མཐའ།} going\n6. {འོང་མཐའ།} coming \n7. {གཅིག་ཡིན་པའི་མཐའ།} one\n8. {ཐ་དད་པའི་མཐའ།} different.
སྤྲོས-བྲལ-བརྒྱད	The lack of eight extremes. The extremes to be abandoned while establishing the view of [prāsangika Mādhyamika]. Lack of inherently existent birth and so on (see {སྤྲོས་པའི་མཐའ་བརྒྱད}).
ཕ-རྒྱུད	[pitṛ tantra]/ Father Tantra. The highest class of tantra in which the primary focus is the development of an illusory body, e.g. [guhyasamāja] tantra.
ཕ-ཆོས	The father Dharma; also called the teachings of the father of the Kadam tradition, compiled by the father of the Kadampa tradition, Dromtonpa. This collection of teachings includes his questions to [atiṡa] and the tatter's replies on many essential doctrinal points, and a short biography of [atiṡa] and the guru lineage of the Kadampa's sixteen drops (thig-le bcu drug) transmission.
ཕ-ཆོས-བུ-ཆོས	The father and son dharma (see {ཕ་ཆོས}and {བུ་ཆོས}) of the Kadampa tradition.
ཕ-རོལ-ཏུ-ཕྱིན-པ-བཅུ	[daṡa pāramitā]/ The ten perfections.\n1-6. The six perfections (see {ཕར་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ་དྲུག}).\n7. {ཐབས་ཀྱི་ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ།} [upāya pāramitā]/ perfection of means\n8. {སྨོན་ལམ་གྱི་ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ།} [praṇidhāna pāramitā]/ perfection of aspirational prayers\n9. {སྟོབས་ཀྱི་ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ།} [bala pāramitā]/ perfection of power\n10. {ཡེ་ཤེས་ཀྱི་ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ།} jсāna pāramitā]/ perfection of primordial wisdom.
ཕ-རོལ-ཏུ-ཕྱིན-པ-དྲུག	[ṣaḍ pāramitāḥ]/ The six perfections.\n1. {སྦྱིན་པའི་ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ།} [dāna pāramita]/ perfection of giving\n2. {ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་ཀྱི་ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ།} [ṡīla pāramitā]/ perfection of morality\n3. {བཟོད་པའི་ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ།} [kṣānti pāramitā]/ perfection of patience\n4. {བརྩོན་འགྲུས་ཀྱི་ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ།} [virya pāramitā]/ perfection of effort\n5. {བསམ་གཏན་གྱི་ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ།} [dhyāna pāramitā]/ perfection of concentration\n6. {ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱི་ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པ།} [prajсa pāramitā]/ perfection of wisdom.
ཕ-རོལ-ཏུ-ཕྱིན-པའི-མི-མཐུན-ཕྱོགས-དྲུག	[ṣaḍ pāramitā pratipakṣāḥ]/ The six opponents to the six perfections.\n1. {སེར་སྣ།} [matsava]/ miserliness\n2. {ཚུལ་འཆལ།} [duḥṡīla]/ corrupt morality\n3. {ཞེ་སྡང་།} [krodha]/ hatred\n4. {ལེ་ལོ།} [alasa]/ laziness\n5. {རྣམ་གཡེང་།} [vikṣapana]/ mental wandering\n6. {ཤེས་རབ་འཆལ་བ།} [duḥprajсā]/ corrupt wisdom.
ཕག-ལས-ཐོབ-པའི-མཛོད-གསུམ	The three treasures obtained from the father; the three constituents obtained from father.\n1. {ཁུ་བ།} regenerative fluid\n2. {རྐང་།} marrow\n3.{ རུས་པ།} bone.
ཕག-གྲུ-བཀའ-བརྒྱུད	The Phagdru Kagyud Order. One of the divisions of the Kagyud order of Tibetan Buddhism founded by Phagmo Drupa (1110-1170), the chief disciple of Gampopa. He\nmastered the art of writing and painting without being taught. His eight disciples founded the eight sub-sects of the Kagyud.
ཕན-ཚུན-ཐ-དད	Mutually exclusive things.
ཕན-ཚུན-སྤང-འགལ	Mutually exclusive contradictions; mutually exclusive dichotomy, e.g. permanence and impermanence, or hot and cold.
ཕམ-པ-བརྒྱད	[aṣṭa parājikā dharmāḥ]/ The eight moral defeats; the eight root\ntransgressions of a fully ordained nun, [bhikṣunī].\n1-4. the four moral defeats (see {ཕམ་པ་བཞི}) of a [bhikṣu]\n5. {སྐྱེས་པ་ལ་ཆགས་སེམས་ཀྱིས་ལུས་འཁྱུད་ཅིང་རེག་པ།} touching and embracing a man with lust\n6. {སྐྱེས་པ་ལ་ཆགས་སེམས་ཀྱིས་ལུས་གན་རྐྱལ་དུ་བཀན་པ།} throwing a man down overwhelmed with lust\n7. {ཟླ་མོར་ཕམ་པ་བྱུང་བ་ཤེས་བཞིན་དུ་འཆབ་པ།} knowingly concealing moral defeat of a fellow nun\n8. {དགེ་སློང་འགའ་ཞིག་དགེ་འདུན་གྱི་གནས་ནས་ཕྱུང་བ་ལ་སླར་ཡང་འགྱོད་པའི་སེམས་ཀྱིས་བཟོད་པར་གསོལ་བ་དེ་ཉིད་ལུས་ངག་གི་སྒོ་ནས་ཟློག་པར་བྱེད་པ།} ignoring the\nforgiveness sought by [bhikṣu]s through physical and verbal\ngestures for their expulsion from the monastery.
ཕམ-པ-འཆབ-བཅས	The concealed moral defeats. Concealment of any of the four root transgressions by an ordalned monk.
ཕམ-པ-བཞི	[catvāri parājikā dharmāḥ]/ The four moral defeats; the four root transgressions of a monk, the committing of any would lead to loosing the status of a being a monk.\n1. {མི་བསད་པ།} [manusyabadha]/ killing a human\n2. {མ་བྱིན་པར་ལེན་པ།} adattādana/ taking what is not given\n3. {མི་ཚངས་པར་སྦྱོད་པ།} [abrahmacārya]/ indulging in sexual misconduct\n4. {མི་ཆོས་བླ་མའི་བརྫུན་སྨྲ་བ།} [uttaramanuṣya dharma pralāpa]/ lying about one's attainment of suprahuman dharmas.
ཕར-ཕྱིན-ཐེག-པ	[pāramitā yāna]/ The Perfection Vehicle. The Bodhisattva vehicle as taught in the [sūtra]s known as the causal vehicle (rgyu'i-iheg-pa) in contrast to the mantrayaria vehicle known as the resultant vehicle.
ཕར-ཕྱིན-དྲུག-ལ-འཇུག-པའི-འཇུག-སྒྲུབ	[ṣaḍ pāramitā vṛttiprasthāna pratipatti]/ Achievement through engagement in the six perfections; the Bodhisattva paths encompassing the practice of the six perfections.
ཕལ-ཆེན-པའི-སྡེ-པ	[mahāsaṁgikā]/ [mahāsaṁgikā] school. One of the four principal schools of the Hinayana tradition whose direct teacher is [kāṡyapa] (see {དགེ་འདུན་ཕལ་པོ་ཆེའི་སྡེ་པཻང}).
ཕུགས-ནོར-བཅུ	The ten innermost jewels of the Kadampa tradition (see {བཀའ་གདམས་ཕུགས་ནོར་བཅུ}).
ཕུང-པོ-ལྔ	[paсca skandhāḥ]/ The five aggregates.\n1. {གཟུགས་ཀྱི་ཕུང་པོ།} [rūpa skandha]/ aggregate of form\n2. {ཚོར་བའི་ཕིང་པོ།} [vedanā skandha]/ aggregate of feeling\n3. {འདུ་ཤེས་ཀྱི་ཕུང་པོ།} [saṁjсā skandha]/ aggregate of perception\n4. {འདུ་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཕུང་པོ།} [saṁskara skandha]/ aggregate of compositional factors\n5. {རྣམ་པར་ཤེཨེས་པའི་ཕུང་པོ།} [vijсāna skandha]/ aggregate of consciousness.
ཕུང-པོ-དྲུག	[ṣaḍ skandhāḥ]/ The six aggregates 1-5. The five aggregates (see {ཕུང་པོ་ལྔ})\n6. {ཡེ་ཤེས་ཀྱི་ཕུང་པོ།} [jсāna skandha]/ the aggregate of primordial wisdom.
ཕུང-པོ-གསུམ-པ	The Tnree Heaps. A.{ ཕུང་པོ་གསུམ་པོའི་མདོ། ལྟུང་བཤགས།} The [sūtra] of confession: 1. {སྡིག་པ་བཤགས་པ།} the practice of confessing non-virtues\n2. {རྗེས་སུ་ཡི་རང་བ།} the practice of rejoicing\n3. {དགེ་བསྔོ་བ།} the practice of dedication.\nB.\n1. {སྡིག་པ་བཤགས་པ།} confessing non-virtues\n2. {རྗེས་སུ་ཡི་རང་བ།} rejoicing at the virtues\n3. {ཆོས་འཁོར་བསྐོར་བ།} turning the wheel of doctrine.
ཕུན-ཚོགས-ལྔ་	The five excellences.\nA.\n1. {ཆོས་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ།} [dharma saṁpanna]/ excellent Dharma\n2. {དུས་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ།} [kāla saṁpanna]/ excellent period\n3. {སྟོན་པ་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ།} [ṡāstra saṁpanna]/ excellent teacher\n4. {གནས་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ།} [sthāna saṁpanna]/ excellent abode\n5. {འཁོར་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ།} [pariṣad saṁpanna]/ excellent retinue.\nB.\n1. {སྐུ་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ།} [kāya saṁpanna]/ perfect body with the major and minor marks\n2. {སྤངས་རྟོགས་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ།} [prahāṇa pratīta saṁpanna]/ perfect abandonments and accomplishments\n3. {འཁོར་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ} [pariṣada saṁpanna]/ perfect retinue\n4. {ཞིང་ཕུན་སིམ་ཚོགས་པ།} [kṣetra saṁpanna]/ perfect field created from the wisdom of self-awareness\n5. {སྤྲུལ་པ་ཕུན་སིམ་ཚོགས་པ།} [nirmāṅa saṁpanna]/ perfect emanation of wisdom and body.
ཕུན-ཆོགས-སྡེ-བཞི	The four excellences.\nA. {འཇིག་རྟེན་པའི་ཕུན་ཚོགས་སྡེ་བཞི} The four worldly excellences:\n1. {ཆོས།} Dharma\n2. {ནོར།} wealth\n3. {འདོད་པ།} wishes\n4. {ཐར་པ།} liberation.\nB. {འཛིག་རྟེན་ལས་འདས་པའི་ཕུན་ཚོགས་སྡེ་བཞི།} The four transworidiy excellences:\n1. {སངས་རྒྱས་ཀྱི་ཚོས་དར་བ།} flourishing of the Buddha Dharma\n2. {ནོར་ལོངས་སྤྱོད་དང་ལྡན་པ།} possessing riches and wealth\n3. {འདོད་ཡོན་ལྔ་ལ་སྤོད་པ།} enjoying the five sensual objects (see {འདོད་ཡོན་ལྔ})\n4. {ཆོས་ལ་བརྟེན་ནས་ཐར་པ་མྱང་འདས་ཀྱི་གོ་འཕང་འཐོབ་པ།} attalnment of the state of liberation following Dharma practices.
ཕུན-ཚོགས-གསུམ-ལྡན	The triple excellences; the three primary requirements for a person going to receive monk vows.\n1. {གང་ལ་སྡོམ་པ་བླང་པའི་ཡུལ་མཁན་སློབ།} the presence of an abbot and assistant abbots from whom the vows are to be received\n2. {གང་གིས་སྡོམ་འབོག་པར་བྱེད་པའི་ཆ་ག} the full-fledged ritual ceremony through which the vows are to be received\n3. {གང་བསླབ་པར་བྱ་བའི་གནས་ལ་ཚུལ་བཞིན་དུ་བསླབ་པར་འདོད་པའི་བསམ་པ།} the perfect motivation to receive the vows.
ཕུན-སུམ-ཚོགས-པ-གསུམ	A. The three excellences.\n1. {རྒྱུ་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ།} excellent cause\n2. {འབྲས་བུ་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ།} excellent fruit\n3. {ཕན་འདོགས་བ་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ།} excellent benefit\nB. The three perfect accomplishments.\n1. {རང་དོན་ཕུན་ཚོགས།} accomplishment of one's goals\n2. {གཞན་དོན་ཕུན་ཚོགས།} accomplishment of others' goals\n3. {དོན་གཉིས་སྒྲུ་པའི་ཐབས་ཕུན་ཚོགས།} accomplishment of the means for achieving both goals.
ཕོ-གཅོད	The Male Ritual of Cutting-Off. The transmission of the cutting-off ritual (gcod), of severing the ego, directly handed down from Phadampa Sangye to Yarlung Lama [ṣonam] and his disciples.
ཕོ-རྩླ-སྣ-དགུ	The nine skills of a man; nine dexterities of manhood.\nA. {ལུས་ངག་ཡིད་གསུམ་གྱི་རྩལ་གསུམ་རེ་སྟེ་དགུ} The three each of body speech and mind.\nB. According to another tradition these are:\n1. {གཏམ།} oratorship\n2. {ཡི་གེ} writing\n3. {རྩིས།} calculation\n4. {མདའ།} archery\n5.{ རྡོ།} weight lifting\n6. {མཆོངས།} jumping\n7. {བང་།} running\n8. {རྒྱལ།} swimming\n9. {སྦེ།} stick-games.
ཕྱ-ལེ-བ	[ṡāta]/ Eveniy shaped. The perfect and refined shape of a thing.
ཕྱ-ལེ-བ-མ-ཡིན-པ	[viṡata]/ Unevenly shaped. The imperfect and unrefined shape of a thing.
ཕྱག-རྒྱ	[mudrā]/\nA. Hand gestures ([mudrā])\nB. Official or non-official seal.
ཕྱག-རྒྱ-ཆེན-པོ	[mahāmudrā]; the Great Seal. The greal seal of emptiness; an exalted meditation on the nature of mind, particularly associated with the Kagyud order of Tibetan Buddhism.
ཕྱག-རྒྱ-མ	The consort. Wife of an accomplished Lama
ཕྱག-རྒྱ-དྲུག	A. The six symbolic ornaments. Costumes associated with tantric deities and yoginis, made of bones representing the six perfections.\n1. {ནོར་བུ།} jewels\n2. {ལག་གདུབ།} bracelets\n3. {རྣ་ཆ།} ear rings\n4. {སྐ་རག} belt\n5. {འཁོར་ལོ།} wheel\n6. {ཐལ་བ།} funerary ashes. B. The six sacred articles obtained from heaven during the reign of the Tibetan King, Lha Tho-Tho-Ri Nyan-Tsen. 1. {མདོ་སྡེ་སྤང་སྐོང་ཕུག་རྒྱ།} the [sūtra] {སྤང་སྐོང་ཕྱག་རྒྱ}\n2. {མདོ་སྡེ་ཟ་མ} {ཏོག} the [sūtra] {ཟ་མ་ཏོག}\n3. {གསེར་གྱི་མཆོད་རྟེན།} a golden stupa\n4. {གཡུའི་མཆོད་རྟེན།} a turquoise stupa\n5. {མུ་དྲའི་ཕྱག་རྒྱ།} a [mudrā] of woven pearl-net\n6. {ཙིཏྟམཎིའི་སྐོས་ཕོར།} wish-fulfilling pot.
ཕྱག-རྒྱ-བཞི	The four seals; the four principles of meditation according to the yoga tantra tradition.\n1. {ལས་ཀྱི་ཕྱག་རྒྱ།} [karma mudrā]/ seal of activity\n2. {དམ་ཆིག་ཕུག་རྒྱ།} [samaya mudrā]/ seal of pledge\n3. {ཆོས་ཀྱི་ཕྱག་རྒྱ།} [dharma mudrā]/ seal of doctrine\n4. {སྟོང་པའི་ཕུག་རྒྱ།} [ṡūnyatā mudrā]/ seal of emptiness or great seal.
ཕྱག-རྒྱའི-ལྷ	The [mudrā] deity. One of the six kinds of deities within action tantra, involving visualizing implements such as a vajra, wheel etc., at the heart and sealing it with the commitment related to the concerned deity.
ཕྱག-ཆེན-གའི-མ	The Amulet Box traditon of [mahāmudrā]. The [mahāmudrā] transmission of the realization of the clear light mind, through meditation on the inseparability of bliss and emptiness, being likened to the two clasped sides of an amulet box.
ཕྱག-ཆེན-རྣླ-འབྱོར-བཞི	The four [mahāmudra] yogas.\n1. {རྩེ་གཙིག་མའི་རྣལ་འབྱོར།} the yoga of single-pointed concentration on the nature of mind\n2. {སྤྲོས་བྲལ་གྱི་རྣལ་འབྱོར།} the yoga of realizing the mind as being free from\nconceptual elaboration\n3. {རོ་གཅིག་གི་རྣལ་འབྱོར།} the yoga of realizing the sameness of the appearance and mind\n4. {སྒོམ་མེད་ཀྱི་རྣལ་འབྱོར།} the yoga of no more meditation.
ཕྱག-ཆེན-རྣལ-འབྱོར-བཞི	[sahaja mahāmudra prayoga]/ The [mahāmudrā] of simultaneous arisal and merging. A [mahāmudrā] linage of practice taught by Gampopa for practitioners of the initial level in order that they gradually realize the beginningless, inseparable nature of the mind and finally attain the Truth Body of a Buddha
ཕྱག-ན-རྡོ-རྗེ	[vajrapāṇi]; the Vajra Holder. A Bodhisattva who embodies the might and power of all the Buddhas.
ཕག-མཚན	[mudrā]/\nA. Emblems, implements and hand gestures of a deity.\nB. Signs and marks.
ཕྱི-སྒེག-བཞི	The four outer offering goddesses inside the [maṇḍala].\n1. {སྒེག་མ།} goddess with pleasing gesture\n2. {ཕྲེང་བ་མ།} goddess holding garland\n3.{ གླུ་མ།} goddess of song\n4. {གར་མ།} goddess of dance.
ཕྱི-རྒོལ	The defender, the opponent. The respondent in a debate who defends his or her position.
ཕྱི-རྒྱུད-སྡེ-གསུམ	The three outer tantras. According to the Nyingma tradition the Kriya (action) tantra was taught by Buddha [ṡākyamuni] himself and the Upayoga (performance) tantra and Yoga (union) tantra were taught by Buddha Vairocana.
ཕྱི-རྒྱུད	The entrance from outside; the process of initiation of the disciples entering from outside the curtain of the [maṇḍala]. This involves having made requests to the master, placing the disciple at the eastern gate of the [maṇḍala], bestowal of the common and uncommon vows and enquiring about their Buddha family and aspiration, generating the all-encompassing yogic mind and binding the disciples to the oath of secrecy.
ཕྱི-སྟོང-པ-ཉེད	[bahirdhā ṡūnyatā]/ The emptiness of external objects. One of the sixteen emptinesses (see {སྟོང་པ་ཉིད་བཅུ་དྲུག}); the lack of inherent existence of non-sentient phenomena, such as the four external elements, object of perception, etc.
ཕྱི-དོན	External phenomena. The assertion that form, i.e. the five objects of sensory consciousness, and the cognizing sensory consciousness are not substantially the same, but exist separately and have a special causal relationship. This is an assertion of the two lower schools of Buddhist tenets, as well as of the [prāsangika mādhyamika] school.
ཕྱི-དོན-བེམ-པོ	External matteṛ For instance rocks and eartḥ
ཕྱི-ནང-སྟོང-པ-ཉེད	[adhyānta bahirdhā ṡūnyatā]/ The emptiness of external and internal objects. One of the sixteen types of emptinesses (see {སྟོང་པ་ཉིད་བཅུ་དྲུག}); the lack of inherent existence of objects pervaded by consciousness, such as the six faculties, six consciousnesses and the internal organs.
ཕྱི-ཕན-པའི-དབང-བཅུ	The ten beneficial outer initiations. The initiations that are the gateway to entering the mahayoga tantra teachings in the Nyingma tradition.\n1. {སྙིང་པོ་ལྔའི་དབང་།} The initiations of the five essences (see {སྙིང་པོ་ལྔ})\n2. {དབུ་རྒྱན་གྱི་དབང་།} initiation of the head-dress\n3. {བུམ་པའི་དབང་།} vase initiation\n4. {ཅོད་པན་གྱི་དབང་།} crown initiation\n5. {ཕྲེང་བའི་དབང་།} garland initiation\n6. {གོ་ཆའི་དབང་།} armour initiation\n7. {རྒྱལ་མཚན་གྱི་དབང་།} initiation of the victory banner\n8. {གདུགས་ཀྱི་དབང་།} initiation of the umbrella\n9. {ཕྱག་རྒྱའི་དབང་།} initiation of the [mudrā]\n10. {བཟའ་བཏུང་གི་དབང་།} initiation of food and drinks.
ཕྱི-རོལ-པ	An outsider; a non-Buddhist. Those who belong to a faith other than Buddhism.
ཕྱིན-ཅི-ལོག-བཞི	The four misapprehensions; the four wrong thoughts.\n1. {མི་གཙང་བ་ལ་གཙང་བར་འཛིན་པ།} to apprehend what is impure as pure\n2. {བདག་མེད་པ་ལ་བདག་ཏུ་འཛིན་པ།} to apprehend what is selfless as\nhaving a self\n3. {སྡུག་བསྔལ་བ་ལ་བདེ་བར་འཛིན་པ།} to apprehend what is miserable as happiness\n4. {མེ་རྟག་པ་ལ་རྟག་པར་འཛིན་པ།} to apprehend what is impermanent as permanent.
ཕྱིན-དྲུག-གི-ཁྱད-ཆོས-བཞི	The four qualities of the six perfections (see {ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པདྲག}).\n1. {ཕར་ཕྱིན་རང་རང་གི་མི་མཐུན་པའི་ཕྱོགས་དང་བྲལ་བ།} non-association with their respective opponents (see {ཕ་རོལ་ཏུ་ཕྱིན་པའི་མི་མཐུན་ཕྱོགས་དྲུག})\n2. {གྲོགས་འཁོར་སུམ་མི་རྟོག་པའི་ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱིས་ཟིན་པ།} conjoined with the wisdom of the purity of the three circles (see {འཁོར་གསུམ}) as their favourable condition\n3. {བྱེད་ལས་གཞན་གྱི་འདོད་དོན་རྫོགས་པར་བྱེད་པ།} fulfilling others' wishes as their function\n4. {འབྲས་བུང་ཆུང་ཆུབ་གསུམ་སྨིན་པར་བྱེད་པ།} ripening of the fruits as their results.
ཕྱིའི-དཀར-པོ-གསུམ	The three external white substances.\n1. {འོ་མ།} [kṣira]/ milk\n2. {ཞོ།} [dadhi]/ curd\n3. {མར།} [ghṛta]/ butter.
ཕྱིའི-དཀྱིལ-འཁོར-བཞི	The four external [maṇḍala]s.\n1. {རྡུལ་ཚོན་གྱི་དཀྱིལ་འཁོར།} coloured powder [maṇḍala]\n2. {རས་བྲིས་དཀྱིལ་འཁོར།} [maṇḍala]s painted on cloth\n3. {བསམ་གཏན་གྱི་དཀྱིལ་འཁོར།} concentration [maṇḍala]\n4. {ལུས་དཀྱིལ།} body [maṇḍala].
ཕྱིའི-སྐྱེ-མཆེད-དྲུག	The six outer sources of perception (see {ཡུལ་དྲུག}).
ཕྱིའི-ཁམས-དྲུག	[ṣaḍ bahirdhā dhātavaḥ]/ The six outer sensory spheres (see {ཁམས་བཅོ་བརྒྱད}, A).
ཕྱིའི-རྟིན-འབྲེལ	The outer dependent arising; the working of the nature; the phenomena of nature.
ཕྱིའི-དེ-ཉིད-བཅུ	The ten external qualities of a Vajracarya.\n1. {དཀྱིལ་འཁོར་འབྲི་བ་ལ་མཁས་པ།} skilled in the art of drawing [maṇḍala]s and meditating upon them\n2. {དང་པོ་སྦྱོར་བ་སོགས་ཀྱི་ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན་ལ་མཁས་པ།} skilled in performing the preliminary practices such as maintaining concentration\n3. {ལྷ་ལ་རྒྱས་འདེབས་པའི་ཕུག་རྒྱ་ལ་མཁས་པ།} skilled in performing mudras or hand gestures\n4. {སྟངས་སྟབས་ལ་མཁས་པ།} skilled in positioning the body\n5. {འདུག་སྟངས་སོགས་ལ་མཁས་པ།} skilled in maintaining various sitting positions\n6. {བཟླས་བརྫོད་ལ་མཁས་པ།} skilled in mantra recitation\n7. {སྦྱིན་སྲེག་ལ་མཁས་པ།} skilled in performing fire-rituals\n8. {མཆོད་པའི་ཆོ་ག་སོགས་ལ་མཁས་པ།} skilled in performing offering rituals\n9. {ལས་ལ་སྦྱོར་བ་ལ་མཁས་པ།} skilled in performing practical ritual arts\n10. {གཤེགས་གསོལ་དང་སླར་བསྡུ་བའི་ལས་ལ་མཁས་པ།} skilled in bidding farewell to the deities and withdrawing them into the heart, etc.
ཕྱིའི-ཕྱག-རྒྱ	[bahīrdhā mudrā]/ External [mudrā]; external seal; a tantric consort; a gesture.
ཕྱིའི-ཡོངས-འཛིན	External tutor. The living Guru other than oneself.\n{ཕྱིར་བཅོས།}\n[pratikriyā]/ Restoration of vows. Restoration of transgressed vows through a confession ceremony.
ཕྱིར-མི-འོང-བཅུ	Ten never-returners.\n1. {ཕྱིར་མི་འོང་ཞུགས་པ།} the enterer into never-returner\n2. {བར་དོར་འདའ་བ།} the never-returner who attains liberation in the intermediate state\n3. {སྐྱེས་ནས་འདའ་བ།} the never-returner who attains liberation as soon as he is born\n4. {འཕར་བ་གསུམ།} the three never-returners of the leap-over\n5. {མཐོང་ཆོས་ཞི་བ།} the never-returner who attains liberation in the same life-time\n6. {ལུས་མངོན་བྱེད།} the never-returner who attains liberation with the cessation of his body.
ཕྱིར-མི-འོང-པའི-དགེ-འདུན-ལྔ་	The five irreversible aspirants to virtue. The Bodhisattvas on the peak, forbearance, and supramundane levels of the path of preparation and the path of seeing and meditation.
ཕྱིར-འོང་	Once-returner.
ཕྱོགས-སྐྱོང-བརྒྱད	[aṣṭa digpālāḥ]/ The eight directional protectors.\n1. {ཤར་དུ་དབང་པོ།} Indra to the east\n2.{ལྷོ་རུ་གཤིན་རྗེ།} Yarna to the south\n3. {ནུབ་ཏུ་ཆུ་བདག} [varuṇa] to the west\n4. {བྱང་དུ་གནོན་སྦྱིན།} [yakṣa] to the north\n5. {ཤར་ལྷོར་མེ་ལྷ།} [agnideva] to the south-east\n6. {ལྷོ་ནུབ་ཏུ་བདེན་བྲལ།} to the south-west\n7. {ནུབ་བྱང་དུ་རླུང་ལྷ།} [vāyudeva] to the north-west\n8. {བྱང་ཤར་དུ་དབང་ལྡན།} [Indra] to the north-east.
ཕྱོགས-སྐོང-བཅུ	[daṡa digpālāḥ]/ The ten directional protectors.\n1. {དབང་པོ།} [Indra]\n2.{གཤིན་རྗེ།} [yama] 3. {ཆུ་བདག} [varuṇa]\n4. {གནོད་སྦྱིན།} [yakṣa]\n5. {མེ་ལྷ།} [agnideva]\n6. {སྲིན་པོ།} [rakṣasa]\n7. {རླུང་ལྷ།} [vāyudeva]\n8. {འབྱུང་པོ།} [bhūta]\n9. {ཚངས་པ།} [brahma]\n10.{སའི་ལྷ་མོ།} [vanadevi].
ཕྱོཨོགས-སྐྱོང-བཅོ-ལྔ་	[paсcadaṣa digpālāh]/ The fifteen directional protectors.\nA. (see {ཕྱོགས་སྐྱོང་བཅུ} 1-10.)\n11. {ཉེ་དབང་།} [upendra]\n12. {ཚོགས་བདག} [gaṇapati]\n13. {ཉི་མ།} [sūrya]\n14.{ ཟླ}.{བ།} Candra\n15.{ ཐགས་བཟང་།} [avirala].\nB. According to [guhyasamāja] tantra, these are:\n1. {ཤར་དུ་རྡོ་རྗེ་མཚོན་ཚ་སེར་པོ།} Yellow Vajra Weapon to the east\n2. {གཡས་སུ་སྒྱུ་མ་རྡོ་རྗེ་ནག་པོ།} Black Vajra Illusion to his right\n3. {མེར་རྡོ་རྗེ་མེ་དམར་པོ།} Red Vajra Fire to the south-east\n4. {ལྷོར་རྡོ་རྗེ་དུས་ནག་པོ།} Black Vajra Time to the south\n5. {ལྷོ་ནུབ་ཏུ}"{རྡོ་རྗེ་གཏུན་ཤིང་།} Black Vajra Club to the south-west\n6. { ནུབ་ཏུ་རྡོ་རྗེ་ཀླུ་དཀར་པོ།} White Vajra Naga to the west\n7.{ ནུབ་བྱང་དུ་རྡོ་རྗེ་རླུང་ལྗང་ཁུ།} Green Vajra Wind to the north-west\n8. {བྱང་དུ་རྡོ་རྗེ་འཇིགས་བྱེད་སོར་པོ།} Yellow Vajra Terrifier to the north\n9. {གཡས་སུ་རྡོ་རྗེ་སྣ་རིང་དཀར་པོ།} White Vajra [ganeṡ] to his right side\n10.{ བྱང་ཤར་དུ་རྡོ་རྗེ་ཁྲོ་བོ་དཀར་པོ།} White Vajra Wrath to the north-east\n11. {དབང་ལྡན་དང་ཉེ་དབང་གི་བར་དུ་རྡོ་རྗེ་འཁྲིལ་བ་དམར་པོ།} Red Vajra Sun between north-east and east\n12. {རྡོ་རྗེ་འོད་དཀར་པོ།} White Vajra Moon\n13. {མི་སྨྲ་རྡོ་རྗེ་སེར་པོ།} Yellow Vajra Silent (Brahma)\n14. {ཆུ་ལྷ་དང་བདེན་བྲལ་གྱི་བར་དུ་ཐགས་བཟང་རིས་ནག་པོ།} Black Tak Zangri between west and south-west\n15. {ས་ཡི་ལྷ་མོ་སེར་མོ།} Yellow Goddess of the Earth.
ཕྱོགས-བཅུ	The ten directions.\n1-4. {ཕྱོགས་བཞི།} the four cardinal directions\n5.8. {མཚམས་བརྒྱད།} the four sub-directions\n9. {སྙིང་།} zenith\n10. {འོག} nadir.
ཕོགས-ཆོས	[pakṣa dharma]/ The first logical mark. The first condition to be fulfilled in a logical syllogism, i.e. the existence or presence of a logical mark in the subject of the syllogism.\n{ཕྲ་རྒྱས།}\n[anuṡaya]/ Delusion; affliction. That which is subtle and multiplying. Delusions are subtle because they are difficult to see, and they are multiplying because of their auxilary mental factors or objects of grasping.
ཕྲ-རྒྱས-ཀྱི-ཐེ-ཚོམ	The delusive doubt; the deluded doubt.
ཕྲ-རྒྱས-དགུ-བཅུ-རྩ-བརྒྱད	The ninety-eight delusions. The ninety-eight delusions of the three realms—eighty-eight delusions to be abandoned on the path of seeing, and ten delusions to be abandoned on the path of meditation.
ཕྲ-རྒྱས-བརྒྱ-དང-ཉེར-བརྒྱད	The hundred and twenty-eight delusions. The one hundred and twenty-eight delusions of the three realms, one hundred and twelve delusions to be abandoned on the path of seeing, and sixteen delusions to be abandoned on the path of meditation.
ཕྲ-རྒྱས-བཅུ	The ten delusions (see {མི་དགེ་བ་བཅུ}).
ཕྲ-རྒས-དྲུག	The six delusions (see {རྩ་ཉོན་དྲུག}).
ཕྲ-རྒྱས-རྟོག-པའི-རྣལ-འབྱོར	The yoga of subtle conceptions. The subtle conceptual yoga. A generation stage practice in the highest yoga tantra in which the objects of meditation are subtle.
ཕྲེང-བ	[mālā]/ A rosary. Common religious article used for counting prayers, mantras, etc., usually strung with 108 beads. Also means a garland; a row, e.g. of votive lamps.
འཕགས-པ	[ārya]/ A Noble Being. An exalted being; a superior. One who has attained the third path, the path of seeing, on which a person becomes a real [saṇgha] refuge.
འཕགས-པ-ཀླུ-སྒྲུབ	[ārya] [nāgārjuna]The pioneer of the Madhyamika philosophy after Buddha [ṡākyamuni], who elucidated the subtlest profound view of emptiness.
འཕགས-པ-ཉེ-བར-འཁོར	[ārya Upa li]. A close disciple of Buddha [ṡākyamuni], and a\nbarber by caste and profession, who was renowned for his mastery of the Vinaya teachings. After Buddha [ṡākyamuni]'s passing away, he was responsible for reciting the Vinaya teachings at the first Buddhist council.
འཕགས-པ-འོད-སྲུང-ཆེན-པོ	[ārya Mahākās'yapa]. A close disciple of Buddha [ṡākyamuni] belonging to the Brahmin caste, he was the first patriach or successor of the Buddha and was responsible for reciting the Abhidharma teachings at the first Buddhist council.
འཕགས-པའི-བདེན-པ-བཞི	[catvāri ārya satyāni]/ The four noble truths.\n1. {སྡུག་བསྔལ་བདེན་པ།} [duḥkha satya]/ the truth of suffering\n2. {ཀུན་འབྱུང་བདེན་པ།} [samudaya satya]/ the truth of the origin of suffering\n3. {འགོག་པའི་བདེན་པ།} [nirodha satya]/ the truth of cessation\n4. {ལམ་གྱི་བདེན་པ།} [mārga satya]/ the truth of the path.
འཕགས-པའི-ནོར-བདུན	[sapta ārya dhanāni]/ The seven riches of the Noble Beings; the Seven Jewels of the [ārya]s.\n1. {དད་པ།} [ṡraddha]/ faith\n2. {ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས།} [ṡīla]/ moral discipline\n3. {ཐོས་པ།} [ṡruta]/ hearing\n4. {གཏོང་བ།} [tyāga]/ generosity\n5. {ངོ་ཚ་ཤེས་པ།} [hrī]/ a sense of shame\n6. {ཁྲིལ་ཡོད་པ།} [apatrāpya]/ a dread of blame\n7. {ཤེས་རབ།} [prajсa]/ wisdom.
འཕགས-པའི-རིགས-བཞི	The four types of [ārya]s; the four types of ascetics.\n1. {ཆོས་གོས་ངན་ངོན་ཙམ་གྱིས་ཆོག་ཤེས་པ།} one who is content with poor clothing\n2. {བསོད་སྙོམས་ངན་ངོན་ཙམ་གྱིས་ཆོག་ཤེས་པ།} one who is contented with meagre alms\n3. {གནས་མལ་ངན་ངོན་ཙམ་གྱིས་ཆོག་ཤེས་པ།} one who is content with a poor dwelling\n4. {སྤོང་བ་སྒོམ་པ་ལ་དགའ་བ།} one who takes joy in ascetic practices.
འཕགས-པའི-གསང-བ-གསུམ	The three secret ways of the [ārya]s.\n1. {སྣོད་ཐམས་ཅད་གཞལ་ཡས་ཁང་དང་བཅུད་ཐམས་ཅད་ལྷའི་རྣམ་རོལ་དུ་ལྷ་བ།} viewing the environment as the divine abode and all sentient beings as divine manifestations\n2. {སྒྲ་ཐམས་ཅད་གཟུངས་སྔགས་དང་གདམས་ངག་ཏུ་འཁྱེར་བ།} taking all sounds as being mantras or teachings of the Buddha\n3.{ཆོས་ཐམས་ཅད་གདོད་མ་ནས་སྟོང་པར་ལྷ་བ།} viewing all phenomena as being empty of true existence from beginningless time.
འཕགས-པ-ལྷ	[āryadeva]. A direct disciple of [nāgārjuna] who defeated the famous Tirthika teacher [aṡvaghoṣa], a highly regarded scholar, in an open debate. Author of the Four Hundred Stanzas.
འཕགས-ལམ-ཡན-ལག-བརྒྱུད	[āryaṣṭāṅga mārga]/ The eight-fold Noble Path.\n1. {ཡང་དག་པའི་ལྟ་བ།} [saṁyakdṛṣṭi]/ right view\n2. {ཡང་དག་པའི་རྟོག་པ།} [sam`yaksaṁkalpa]/ right thought\n3. {ཡང་དག་པའི་ངག} [saṁyagvāk]/ right speech\n4. {ཡང་དག་པའི་རྩོལ་བ།} [saṁyag vyāyama]/ right effort\n5. {ཡང་དག་པའི་འཚོ་བ།} [saṁyagājīva]/ right livelihood\n6. {ཡང་དག་པའི་དྲན་པ།} [saṁyaksmṛti]/ right mindfulness\n7. {ཡང་དག་པའི་ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན།} [saṁyaksamādhi]/ right concentration\n8. {ཡང་དག་པའི་ལས་ཀྱི་མཐའ།} [saṁyakkarmānta]/ right action.
འཕངས-པའི-ཡན-ལག	The projected results; the four propelled fruits within the twelve links of interdependent origination—name and form, sources, contact, and feeling.
འཕེན-བྱེད-ཀྱི-ཡན-ལག	Projecting causes; the three causes within the twelve links of interdependent origination which implant the causes for ripening karmas to be reborn in cyclic existence ([saṁsāra])— ignorance, karmic formation and consciousness.
འཕེལ-གདུང་	Multiplied relics. Relics like mustard seeds, off-white in colour, found in the cremated ashes of holy lamas; they are placed inside statues, stupas, or amulet boxes as articles of protection and devotion.
འཕོ-བ	[saṁkrānti]/ Consciousness transference.\nA type of exalted purification practice in which one's or other's consciousness is transfered to a pure land; one of the six yogas of Naropa (see {ན་རོ་ཆོས་དྲུག}).
འཕོ-བ-གྲོང-འཇུག	The consciousness transference of entering a corpse (see {གྲོང་འཇུག}),\n{འཕྲལ་གྱི་འཕྲུལ་རྒྱུ།}\nCauses for temporary deception.
འཕྲིན-ལས	Virtuous activity; Buddha's grace. Synonymous with the virtue, merits or positive energy received through the blessings of the Buddha and his teachings.
འཕྲིན-ལས-ལྔ་	The five types of virtuous activities. The five activities of a Buddha:\n1. {ཞི་བའི་ལས།} activity of peace\n2. {རྒྱས་པའི་ལས།} activity of increase\n3. {དབང་གི་ལས།} activity of power\n4. {དྲག་པོའི་ལས།} activity of wrath\n5. {ལྷུན་གྱིས་གྲུབ་པའི་ལས།} the spontaneous activity.
འཕྲིན-ལས-བཞི	The four types of virtuous activity (see {ཕྲིན་ལས་ལྔ} 1-4).
བ-དན	[patāka]/ Flags; prayer flags.
བ-བྱུང-ལྔ་	The five products of a cow; fresh substances produced from a cow, collected before they drop to the ground.\n1. {ཆུ།} urine\n2. {སྕི་བ།} dung\n3.{ འོ་མ།} milk\n4.{ མར།} butter\n5.{ ཞོ།} curd.
བ-བྱུང-རིལ-བུ	Pills made out of cow products (see {བ་བྱུང་ལྔ་།}).\n{བག་ཆགས།}\n[vāsanā]/ Latencies; instincts; karmic imprints.
བག-ཆགས-ཀྱི-ལུས	[vāsana kāya]/ The instinct body; the body of a dream state mainiy impelled by the instincts left upon one's mind.
བག-ཆག-བཞི	The four types of instincts.\n1. {མངོན་བརྗོད་ཀྱི་བག་ཆགས།} instinct of intuition\n2. {བདག་ལྟའི་བག་ཆགས།} instinct of the view of grasping at self\n3. {སྲིད་པའི་ཡན་ལག་གི་བག་ཆགས} instinct of samsaric experiences\n4. {རིགས་མཐུན་པའི་བག་ཆགས།} instinct of similar factors.
བག-ཆགས-གསུམ	The three types of instincts. That of body, speech and mind.\n{བག་མེད་པ།}\nLack of conscientiousness; recklessness; negligence. An attitude of not guarding one's actions.
བག-ལ-ཉལ-བ-བདུན	[ṡapta anuṡayāh]/ The seven subconscious minds. The different subconscious experiences activated in conjunction with one's own experiences.\n1. {འདོད་པའི་འདོད་ཆགས་ཀྱི་བག་ཉལ།} subconscious attachment to the desire realm\n2. {ཁོང་ཁྲོའི་བག་ཉལ།} subconscious anger\n3. {སྲིད་པའི་འདོད་ཆགས་ཀྱི་བག་ཉལ།} subconscious attachment within [saṁsāra]\n4. {ང་རྒྱལ་གྱི་བག་ཉལ།} subconscious pride\n5. {མ་རིག་པའི་བག་ཉལ།} subconscious ignorance\n6. {ལྟ་བའི་བག་ཉལ།} subconscious view\n7.{ ཐེ་ཚོམ་གྱི་བག་ཉལ།} subconscious doubt.
བང-མཛོད-བུའི-སེམས-བསྐྱེད	Treasure-like Bodhicitta. The mind of enlightenment possessed by Bodhisattvas on the three pure stages—the eighth, ninth and tenth, surpassing the two accumulations of merits and insights.
བམ-པོ	Volume. Generally a standard number of three hundred verses forming the sub-divisions of a text; a device to ensure accurate translation and classification of a manuscript; but it may vary from text to text.
བར-བསྐལ	[antarakalpa]/ The intermediate aeon. The period of time taken for each of the four intermediate aeons (see {བར་བསྐལ་བཞི།}) to begin and end in themselves.
བར-བསྐལ-བཞི	The four intermediate aeons.\n1. {ཆགས་པའི་བསྐལ་བ།} aeon of formation\n2. {གནས་པའི་བསྐལ་བ།} aeon of endurance\n3. {འཇིག་པའི་བསྐལ་བ།} aeon of destruction\n4. {སྟོང་པའི་བསྐལ་བ།} aeon of vacuity.
བར-བསྐལ-ཉི-ཤུ	The twenty intermediate aeons; consisting of:\n1. {མིའི་ཚེ་ལོ་དཔག་མེད་ནས་ཚེ་ལོ་བརྒྱད་ཁྲིའི་བར་བྲི་བ་ནས་ཚེལ་བཅུའི་བར་བྲི་བ་དེ་བར་བསྐལ་པ་གཅིག} one mn of decline) during wnicn the infinite human lifespan decreases to 80,000 to 10 years.\n2. {དེ་ནས་ཡང་ཚེ་ལོ་བརྒྱད་ཁྲིའི་བར་དུ་ཡར་འཕེལ་ཞིང་མར་ལོ་བཅུའི་བར་དུ་བྲི་བའི་བསྐལ་པ་བཅོ་བརྒྱད།} eighteen aeons of increase and decrease, during which the lifespan of human beings goes from 10 to 80,000 and back to\n10.3. {ཡང་ཚེ་ལོ་བཅུ་པ་ནས་བརྒྱད་ཁྲིའི་བར་ཡར་འཕྲེལ་བའི་བསྐལ་པ་གཅིག} one\naeon of increase, during which the human life span increases from 10 to 80,000 years.
བར-ཆད-མེད-པའི-ཏིང-ངེ-འཛིན	[ānantarya samādhi]/ The uninterrupted concentration. The moment of capturing a meditative concentration that realizes emptiness directly.
བར-ཆད-མེད-པའི-རྩེ-སྦྱོར	[ānantaryamūrdhaprayoga]/ Uninterrupted peak training. The final moment of the Bodhisattva path that results in the\nimmediate attainment of Buddhahood. Synonymous with the wisdom of the last moment within the mental continuum of a Bodhisattva.
བར-ཆད-མེད-ལམ	[ānantarya mārga]/ Uninterrupted path. A path of single-pointed concentration that overcomes its respective object of abandonment, e.g. the first instant of the path of seeing.
བར-ཆད-བཞི	The four interruptions. The four interruptions in the course of maintaining meditative concentration:\n1. {རོ་མྱང་ཅན།} obsession of taste\n2. {ང་རྒྱལ་ཤས་ཆེ་བ།} strong pride\n3. {མ་རིག་པ་ཤས་ཆེ་བ།} strong ignorance\n4. {ལྟ་བ་ཤས་ཆེ་བ།} strong view.
བར-དོ	[antarābhava]/ Intermediate state. The state of existence between death and rebirth, during which the consciousness takes a mental body projected by the previous karmic tendencies.
བར-དོ-དྲུག	Six classes of intermediate states.\n1. {སྐྱེ་བའི་བར་དོ།} intermediate state of birth\n2. {རྨི་ལམ་གྱི་བར་དོ།} intermediate state of dreams\n3. {བསམ་གཏན་གྱི་བར་དོ།} intermediate state of concentration\n4. {འཆི་ཁའི་བར་དོ།} intermediate state of near-death\n5. {ཆོས་ཉིད་བར་དོ།} intermediate state of reality\n6. {སྲིད་པའི་བར་དོ།} intermediate state of becoming.
བར-མ-རབ-བྱུང་	The probationary novice. One who has received layman's ordination but has not yet received novice vows.
བས-མཐའ	[prānta]/ Wilderness retreat. A retreat place completely set apart from the town life.
བུ-ག-སྒོ-དགུ	The nine orifices or gates of exit for consciousness to exit from the human body (see {རྣམ་ཤེས་འཕོ་བའི་བུ་ག་དགུ}).
བུ-དགོན	A branch monastery. A subsidiary centre of learning founded by a later disciple of a master affiliated to the monastic centre, which is called the 'mother monastery' (ma-dgon).
བུ-ཆོས	The son dharma. The collection of teachings of [atiṡa] and Drom Tonpa as received and compiled by their spiritual son, Ngog Legpe Sherab comprising many anecdotes in the life of Dromtonpa, and the entrustment of the Kadampa's doctrine to Dromtonpa during the last days of [atiṡa]'s life. This collection is also known as the Kadampa's miraculous text (sprul-pa'i glegs-bam).
བུ-སྟོན-རིན-ཆེན-གྲུབ	The great scholar Buton (1290-1364). Born in central Tibet, he became famous for his scholarship of all sciences of learning. He compiled all the treatises translated from Sanskrit into Tibetan in a systematic order of index, and has also left more than two dozen volumes of collected wntings. Je Tsong Khapa also became his disciple and received many tantric teachings from him. His lineage is known as the Buton lineage (bu-lugs).
བུ-རམ-ཤིང-པ	[Ikṣvāku]/ The sugarcane descendant. An epithet for Buddha [ṡākyamuni] whose ancestral lineage is traced to a child born of an egg that was dropped from semen which had dripped onto a sugarcane leaf.
བུད-རྙེད-ཐོབ-གསུམ	The expulsion, finding and attainment. The Kadampa principles of;\n1. {མི་གྲལ་ནས་བུད།} expulsion from the ranks of worldly people\n2. {ཁྱི་གྲལ་བསྙེགས།} finding the ranks of dogs\n3.{ ལྷ་གྲལ་ཐོབ།} attaining the rank of a god.
བུམ-པ-བསྐྱེད-པ	The generation of the vase. A tantric practice of generating the ritual vase as a deity by connecting vajra threads (multicoloured thread) from the vase to the heart of the master. First the vase to the heart of the master visualizes the deities, then they are offered blessed scented water from a conch, then are immersed in the nature of bliss and void and transformed as inseparable from the scented water contained in the vase etc., following a ritual text and tradition.
བུམ-པ-སྟ-གོན	The preparatory vase ritual. A part of the preparatory rite for an initiation. The commitment beings (see {དམ་ཚིག་སེམས་དཔའ}) are generated in the vase and the wisdom beings (see {ཡེ་ཤེས་སེམས་དཔའ}) are immersed into it, and then the initiation is bestowed following a rite and tradition of a lineage.
བུམ-དབང་	The Vase Initiation. A tantric empowerment (see {བུམ་དབང་བཅུ་གཅིག}) meant for ripening a disciples's mental continuum and allowing the practice of the generation stage paths aimed at gaining Buddhahood.
བུཨུུམ-དབང-བཅུ-གཅིག	The eleven vase initiations.\n1. {བུམ་དབང་།} water initition\n2. {ཅོད་པན་གྱི་དབང་།} crown initiation\n3. {རྡོ་རྗེའི་དབང་།} vajra initiation\n4. {དྲིལ་བུའི་དབང་།} bell initiation\n5. {མིང་གི་དབང་སྟེ་སློབ་མའི་དབང་ལྔ་།} name initiation\n6. {རྡོ་རྗེ་སློབ་དཔོན་གྱི་དབང་།} [vajra-cārya] initiation\n7. {སྔགས་ཀྱི་དབང་།} mantra initiation\n8. {ལུང་བསྟན་དང་དབུགས་དབྱུང་གི་དབང་།} prophecy and relief granting initiation\n9. {རྡོ་རྗེའི་བརྟུལ་ཞུགས་ཀྱི་དབང་།} vajra practice initiation\n10. {སྤྱོད་པའི་བརྟུལ་ཞུགས་ཀྱི་དབང་།} ascetic practice initiation\n11. {རྗེས་སྣང་གི་དབང་།} permission initiation.
བུའི-འོད-གསལ	[putraprabhāsvara]/ The son clear light. The clear light mind recognized through the power of meditation while on the trainee's path arising during the dissolution of winds within the central channel through the force of meditation; the son clear light is the experience of various levels of clear light mind gained on the path towards total perfection. This has two types:\n1. {དབེན་པའི་འོད་གསལ།} the clear light of isolation\n2. {མི་དབེན་པའི་འོད་གསལ།} the clear light of non-isolation.
བེ-ཅོན	[daṇḍa]/ Club with an ornamental human, vajra, or human head at its top; generally depicted as an implement in the hands of Asuras.
བེམ-པོ	Matter. Any existent thing that is neither form nor consciousness, e.g. a person. There are two types of matter.\n1.{ཕྱི་དོན་བེན་པོ།} external matter, e.g. a clay pot\n2. {ནང་དན་བེན་པོ།} internal matter, e.g. sense organs.
བྱ-དཀའ-རྣམ-གསུམ	Three difficult aspects of practice.\n1. {ཆེད་དུ་བྱ་དཀའ་བ།} fulfilling the goals\n2. {སྦྱོད་པ་བྱ་དཀའ་བ།} executing the conduct\n3. {ལས་བྱ་དཀའ་བ།} pursuing the practice.
བྱ-ཁྱུང་	[garuḍa]; celestial eagle. A bird in Buddhist and Hindu mythology which is half man and half eagle symbolizing anger or wrath.
བྱ-ཁྲུས	A purification ceremony conducted by a lama in which he sprinkles blessed water on one's head and gives water to sip.
བྱ-རྒོང-ཕུང-པོ-རི	[gṛdhrakūta]/. Vulture Peak. The holy place near Rajgiri where Buddha [ṡākyamuni] turned the second wheel of doctrine, e.g. the Perfection of Wisdom [sūtra]s.
བྱ-རྒྱུད	[kriyātantra]/ Action tantra. The first of the four classes of tantra, stressing the importance of purifying external\nactivities.
བྱ-རྒྱུད-ཀྱི-དངོས-གྲུབ-གསུམ	The three types of siddhis of action ([kriyā]) tantra. The power\nof gaining proficiency in caryatantra practices\n1. {རབ་རིག་འཛིན་དང་མངོན་ཤེས་དང་ནསྟན་བཅོས་ཀུན་ཤེས་པ་སོགས་དང་།}\nthe siddhi of knowledge of all sciences of learning as the supreme result\n2.{ འབྲིང་མི་སྣང་བ་དང་བཅུད་ལེན་དང་རྐང་མགྱོགས་སོགས་དང་།} the siddhi of disappearance, extracting the essence/ art of elixir and swift footedness as the middling result\n3. {ཐ་མ་གཞན་དབང་དུ་འདུ་བ་དང་བསད་བསྐྲད་སོགས་སམ་རྫས་ལུས་ལོངས་སྤྱོད་གསུམ་སོགས་དབང་དུ་འདུ་བ།} the siddhi of capturing, killing and expelling others or gaining control over matter, body and resources as the modest result.
བྱ-རྒྱུད-ཀྱི-དེ-ཁོ-ན-ཉིད-བཞི	The four suchnesses according to action tantra. The four primary applications of the action tantra practices (see {དེ་ཁོ་ན་ཉིད་བཞི}).
བྱ-རྒྱུད-ཀྱི-དབང-གསུམ	The three initiations according to action tantra\n1. {མེ་ཏོག་ཕྲེང་བའི་དབང་།} the flower garland initiation\n2. {ཆུ་དབང།} water initiation\n3. {ཅོད་པཎ་གྱི་དབང་།} crown initiation.
བྱ-རྒྱུད-ཀྱི-བསམ-གཏན-གསུམ	The three types of concentration according to the action tantra The three suchnesses of concentration.\n1. {མེར་གནས་ཀྱི་དེ་ཉིད} suchness of abiding in fire\n2. {སྒྲར་གནས་ཀྱི་དེ་ཉིད།} suchness of abiding in sound\n3. {སྒྲ་མཐའི་དེ་ཉིད།} suchness of abiding in the finality of sound.
བྱ-རྒྱུད-ཀྱི-ལྷ-དྲུག	The six deities of the action tantra.\n1. {སྟོང་པའི་ལྷ།} [ṡūnyatā deva]/ emptiness deity\n2. {ཡི་གེའི་ལྷ།} [akṣara deva]/ letter deity\n3.{སྒྲའི་ལྷ} [ṡabda deva]/sound deity\n4. {གཟུགས་ཀྱི་ལྷ།} [rūpādeva]/ form deity\n5. {ཕྱག་རྒྱའི་ལྷ།} [mudrā deva]/ seal deity\n6. {མཚན་མའི་ལྷ།} [lalcṣaṇa deva]/ symbol deity.
བྱ-རྒྱུད-སྤྱིའི-དམ-ཚིག-བཅུ-བཞི	The fourteen commitments of action tantra in general.\n1-3. {དཀོན་མཆོག་གསུམ་ལ་དད་པ།} maintaining faith in the Three Jewels\n4. {སྔགས་ལ་དད་པ།} faith in mantra\n5. {ཐེག་ཆེན་ལ་མོས་པ} possessing aspiration in the greater vehicle teachings\n6. {བླ་མ་དང་ཆོས་གྲོགས་ལ་གུས་པ།} being respectful to spiritual masters and friends\n7. {འདས་མ་འདས་ཀྱི་ལྷ་གཞན་ལ་མི་སྡང་བ།} having no hatred towards other deities of the past and future 8. {ཉ་སྟོང་དུས་བཞིའི་མཆོད་པ་མི་གཅོག་པ།} not failing in carrying out one's commitments during the four days of a month, i.e., the eighth, fifteenth, twenty-fifth and thirtieth\n9. {ཀླ་ཀློ་དང་མུ་སྟེགས་པའི་གཞུང་གཞན་ལ་མི་མཆོད་པ།} not worshipping other barbarian and non-buddhist doctrines or philosophies\n10. {གློ་བུར་ལྷགས་པའི་མགྲོན་ལ་ཟས་སྐོམ་སོགས་མཆོད་པ།} offering of feast to strangers\n11. {སེམས་ཅན་ལ་} {བྱམས་པ་མ་ག་ཏང་བ།} not giving up one's love and affection towards sentient beings\n12. {བསོད་ནམས་ཀྱི་ཚོགས་གོང་དུ་སྤེལ་བ།} accumulating the collection of merits\n13. {བཟླས་བརྗོད་ལ་རྩོན་པ།} devotion to incantation of mantras\n14. {དམ་ཚིག་གཞན་རྣམས་ཀྱང་བསྲུང་བ།} observing other commitments.
བྱ-རྒྱུད-རིགས-དྲུག	The six families of action tantra.\n1. {དེ་བཞིན་གཤེགས་པའི་རིགས།} the Tathagata family\n2. {པདྨའི་རིགས།} the Padma family\n3. {རྡོ་རྗེའི་རིགས།} the Vajra family, known as the three transworldly families\n4. {ནོར་བུའི་རིགས།} the Ratna family\n5. {ལྔས་རྩེན་གྱི་རིགས།} the Spirit (lngas-rtsen) family\n6. {འཇིག་རྟེན་ཕལ་པའི་རིགས།} the common family, known as the three worldly families.
བྱ-རྒྱུད-རིགས-གསུམ	The three families of action tantra (see {བྱ་རྒྱུད་རིགས་དྲུག}, 1-3).
བྱ-རྫོགས-སྐད-ཅིག-མ	The time between the beginning and end of an activity. The span of time whrch is l/60th of a finger-snap.
བྱང-ཆུབ-ཀྱི-སེམས	Bodhicitta/ Mind of enlightenment. Altruistic mind of enlightenment to attain Buddhahood for the sake of other sentient beings; a Bodhisattva's way of life.
བྱང-ཆུབ-ཡན-ལག-བདུན	[sapta bodhyaṅgāni]/ The seven limbs of enlightenment; the seven auxiliaries to enlightenment which are in an equilibrim state of concentration and wisdom.\n1. {དྲན་པ།} [smṛti]/ mindfulness\n2. {ཤེས་རབ།} [prajсa]/ wisdom\n3. {བརྩོན་འགྲུས།} [virya]/ effort\n4. {དགའ་བ།} [priti]/joy\n5. {ཤིན་སྦྱངས།} [praṡrabdhi]/ suppleness\n6. {ཏེང་ངེ་འཛིན།} [samādhi]/ concentration\n7. {བཏང་སྙོམས།} [upeksa]/equanimity.
བྱང-ཆུབ-ཤིང་	[bodhivṛkṣa]/ Bodhi tree. The pipal tree under which Buddha [ṡākyamuni] attained complete eniightenment at Bodhgaya.
བྱང-ཆུབ-སེམས-དཔའ	Bodhisattva. Practitioner of the greater vehicle teachings who has resolved to attain Buddhahood for the sake of ail sentient beings; also called the son of the Victorious Ones, more strictly, one who has at least attained the first path of the greater vehicle.
བྱང-ཆུབ-སེམས-དཔའི-སྟོབས-བཅུ	[daṡa bodhisattvabalāni]/ The ten powers of a Bodhisattva\n1. {བསམ་པའི་སྟོབས།} [āṡaya balam]/ power of intention\n2. {ལྷག་པའི་བསམ་པའི་སྟོབས།} [adhyāṡaya balam]/ power of resolute intention\n3. {སྦྱོར་བའི་སྟོབས།} [prayoga balam]/ power of application\n4. {ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱི་སྟོབས།} [praj~na balam]/ power of wisdom\n5. {སྨོན་ལམ་གྱི་སྟོབས།} [praṇidhāna balam]/ power of prayer\n6. {ཐེག་པའི་སྟོབས།} [yāna balam]/ power of vehicle\n7. {སྤྱོད་པའི་སྟོབས།} [caryā balam]/ power of conduct\n8. {སྤྲུལ་པའི་སྟོབས།} [vikurvaṇa balam]/ power of emancipation\n9. {བྱང་ཆུབ་ཀྱི་སྟོབས།} [bodhi balam]/ power of eniightenment\n10. {ཆོས་ཀྱི་འཁོར་ལོ་བསྐོར་བའི་སྟོབས།} [dharmacakra pravartana balam]/ power of turning the wheel of doctrine.
བྱང-ཆུབ-སེམས-དཔའ-དང-ཐུན-མོང-བའི-རྣམ-པ-སོ-བཞི	The thirty-four qualities common to Bodhrsattvas; the thirty-four aspects of the omniscient mind (see {རྣམ་མཁྱེན་གྱི་ར་ནམ་པ་སུམ་ཅུ་སོ་བཞི}).
བྱང-ཆུབ-སེམས-དཔའི-དབང-བཅུ	The ten aspects of a Bodhisattva's control.\n1. {ཚེ་ལ་དབང་བ།} control over life\n2. {སེམས་ལ་དབང་བ།} control over mind\n3. {ཡོ་བྱད་ལ་དབང་བ།} control over materials\n4. {ལས་ལ་དབང་བ།} control over action\n5. {སྐྱེ་བ་ལ་དབང་བ།} control over birth\n6. {ཆོས་ལ་དབང་བ།} control over doctrine\n7. {སྨོན་ལམ་ལ་དབངབ།} control over prayers\n8. {རྫུ་འཕྲུལ་ལ་དབང་བ།} control over miracles\n9. {མོས་པ་ལ་དབང་བ།} control over different faculties\n10. {ཡེ་ཤེས་ལ་དབང་བ།} control over wisdom.
བྱང-ཆུབ-སེམས-དཔའི-ས-བཅུ	[daṡa bodhisattva bhūmayaḥ]/ The ten Bodhisattva grounds; the ten levels of Bodhisattvas (see {ས་བཅུ}).
བྱང-ཆུབ-སེམས-དཔའི-སེམས-ཅན-གྱི-དོན-བྱ-ཚུལ-བཅུ-གཉིས	Twelve ways in which a Bodhisattva fulfils the purposes of sentient beings; the Bodhisattva's twelve means of working for the welfare of others.\n1. {བྱ་བ་བྱེད་པ།} performance in action\n2. {སྡུག་བསྔལ་གྱིས་གཟིར་བའི་དོན་བྱེད་པ།} helping those who are suffering\n3. {ཐབས་ལ་རྨོངས་པའི་དོན་བྱེད་པ།} helping those ignorant of means\n4. {ཕན་འདོགས་པའི་དོན་བྱེད་པ།} helping those in need of help\n5. {འཇིགས་པས་ཉེན་པའི་དོན་བྱེད་པ།} helping those oppressed by fear\n6. {མྱ་ངན་གྱིས་གཟིར་བའི་དོན་བྱད་པ།} helping those overcome by suffering\n7. {ཡོ་བྱད་ཀྱི་ཕོངས་པའི་དོན་བྱེད་པ།} helping those lacking resources\n8. {གནས་འཆའ་བར་བྱེད་པའི་དོན་བྱེད་པ།} helping the homeless\n9 {བློ་མཐུན་པར་འདོད་པའི་དོན་བྱེད་པ།} helping those seeking to live in harmony\n10. {ཡང་དག་པར་ཞུགས་པའི་དོན་བྱེད་པ།} helping those wishing to enter the teaching\n11. {ལོག་པར་ཞུགས་པའི་དོན་བྱེད་པ།} helping those holding wrong views\n12. {རྫུ་འཕྲུལ་གྱི་སྒོ་ནས་དོན་བྱེད་པ}1 helping through miraculous deeds.
བྱང-ཕྱོགས-སོ-བདུན	The thirty-seven limbs of enlightenment; the thirty-seven auxiliaries to enlightenment.\n1-4. {དྲན་པ་ཉེ་བར་བཞག་པ་བཞི།} four close contemplations (see {དྲན་པ་ཉེ་བར་བཞག་པ་བཞི})\n5-8. {ཡང་དག་པར་སྤོང་བ་བཞི།} four perfect abandonments (see {ཡང་དག་སྤོང་བ་བཞི})\n9-12. {རྫུ་འཕྲུལ་གྱི་རྐང་པ་བཞི།} four limbs of miracles (see {རྫུ་འཕྲལ་གྱི་རྐང་པ་བཞི})\n13-17. {དབང་པོ་ལྔ་།} five powers (see {དབང་པོ་ལྔ})\n18-22.{སྟོབས་ལྔ་།} five forces (see {སྟོབས་ལྔ་།})\n23-29. {བྱང་ཆུབ་ཕྱོགས་ཀྱི་ཆོས་བདུན།} seven limbs of enlightenment (see {བྱང་ཆུབ་ཡན་ལག་བཞི})\n30-37. {འཕགས་ལམ་ཡན་ལག་བརྒྱད།} eight noble paths (see {འཕགས་པའི་ལམ་ཡན་ལག་བརྒྱད}).
བྱང-སེམས-ཀྱི-སྡོམ-པ	[bodhisattva saṁvara]/ Bodhisattva vows; Bodhisattva precepts. The vows taken with the aim of helping others to attain the state of Buddhahood.
བྱང-སེམས-འཕགས-པ	[ārya Bodhisattva]; superior Bodhisattva. A Bodhisattva who has attained the third of the five paths—the path of seeing.
བྱམས-ཆོས-སྡེ-ལྔ་	The Five Works of Maitreya\n1. {མདོ་སྡེ་རྒྱན།} Ornament of [mahāyāna] Discourses ([mahāyāna sūtrālaṁkāra])\n2. {མངོན་རྟོགས་རྒྱན}1 Ornament of Clear Realization ([abhisamayālaṁkāra])\n3. {དབུས་མཐའ་རྣམ་འབྱེད།} Clear Distinction Between the Middle Way and Extremes ([madhyāntavibhaṅga])\n4. {ཆོས་དབྱིངས་རྣམ་འབྱེད།} Clear Distinction Between Phenomena\nand their Reality ([dharma dharmatāvibhaṅga])\n5. {རྒྱུད་བླ་མ།} The Sublime Continuum ([uttaratantra]).
བྱམས-པ	[maitreya]/. A. Love; the wish for all sentient beings to be happy. B. Buddha Maitreya. Also called Maitreyanath, the future Buddha who will appear after the total disappearance of Buddha [ṡākyamuni]'s teaching, presently believed to be residing in the Tusita God Realm. C. Bodhisattva Maitreya The author of the Five Works of Maitreya (see {བྱམས་ཆོས་སྡེ་ལྔ}).
བྱིན-གྱིས-བརླབས-བའི-བཀའ	Blessed words of the Buddha; the teaching given through the force of Buddha's blessings although not spoken by him. There can be the blessings of body, speech and mind, e.g. the Heart [sūtra] is a discourse of the Buddha blessed by his mind.
བྱིན-རླབས-བཞི	The four types of blessings.\n1. {བདེན་པའི་བྱིན་རླབས།} blessing of the truth\n2. {གཏོང་བའི་བྱིན་རླབས།} blessing of giving\n3. {ཉེ་བར་ཞི་བའི་བྱིན་རླབས།} blessing of ultimate peace\n4. {ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱི་བྱིན་རླབས།} blessing of wisdom.
བྱིས-པ-ལྟར-འཇུག-པའི-དབང-བདུན	The seven initiations of entering (the [maṇḍala]) like a child.\n1. {ཆའི་དབང་།} water initiation\n2. {ཅོད་པཎ་གྱི་དབང་།} crown initiation\n3. {དར་དཔྱངས་ཀྱི་དབང་།} ribbon initiation\n4. {རྡོར་དྲིལ་གྱི་དབང་།} vajra and bell initiation\n5. {རྡོ་རྗེ་བརྟུལ་ཞུགས་ཀྱི་དབང་།} vajra practice initiation\n6. {མིང་གེ་དབང་།} name initiation\n7. {རྗེས་སྣངག་དབང་།} permission initiation.
བྱེ-བྲག-བ	[vaiṡeṣika]/ The Particularists. Proponents of non-Buddhist tenets following the sage Kanand, who asserted that all objects of knowledge are included in six categories (see {བྱེ་བྲག་པའི་ཚེག་དོན་དྲུག}); they also assert that ablution, initiations, fasts, and offerings of fire rituals are perfect paths to liberation; accordingly, when the self is in isolation free from desire, hatred, anger or pleasure, liberation is attained.
བྱེ-བྲག-པའི-ཚེག-དོན-དྲུག	The six principles of the Paticularists.\n1. {རྫས།} [dravya]/ substance\n2. {ཡོན་ཏན།} [guṇa]/ quality\n3. {ལས།} [karma]\n4. {སྤྱི།} [sāmānya]/ enerality\n5. {བྱེ་བྲག} [viṡeṣa]/ particularity\n6. {འདུ་བ།} [saṁgraha]/ composition.
བྱེ-བྲག-སྨྲ-བ	[vaibhāṣika]. A lower school of Buddhist philosophy that asserts the division of all phenomena into the following five I categories, and assert three times as substantially existent.\n1. {འདུ་མ་བྱས་རྟག་པའི་གཞི།} non-composite phenomena as permanent\n2. {སྣང་བ་སེམས་ཀྱི་གཞི།} appearances as form (objects of perception)\n3. {གཙོང་བོ་སེམས་ཀྱི་གཞི།} primary mind\n4. {འཁོར་སེམས་བྱུང་གི་གཞ།} secondary minds\n5. {ལྡན་པ་མ་ཡིན་པའི་འདུ་བྱེད་ཀྱི་གཞི།} non-associated compositional factors.
བྱེ-བྲག-སྨྲ-བའི-སྡེ-པ-བཅོ-བརྒྱད	[aṣṭadaṡa vaibhāṣika nikāyāḥ]/ The eighteen schools of [vaibhāṣika] The eighteen schools of Hearers (see {ཉན་ཐོས་སྡེ་པ་བཅོ་བརྒྱད}).
བྱེ-བྲག-སྨྲ-པའི-སྡེ-པ-པ	The four principal schools of [vaibhāṣika]. The four mains schools of Hearers (see {ཉན་ཐོས་རཏཟ་བའི་སྡེ་པ་བཞི}).
བྱེ-བྲག-བཤད-མཚོ-ཆེན-མོ	[mahāvibhāṣa]/ The Great Ocean of Commentary (mahavibhasa). One of the principal texts of the [vaibhāṣika] school of philosophy said to have been composed collectively by five hundred Arhats lead by Upali, after the passing away of Buddha [ṡākyamuni]. It belongs to the Abhidharma class of teachings.
བྱེད-རྒྱུ	[kāraṇahetu]/ Active phenomena; active cause. A phenomenon is said to be an active cause of another when it is both substantially distinct from that phenomenon and does not obstruct its arisal. There are two types of active causes:\n1. {བྱེད་རྒྱུ་ནུས་ལྡན།} effective active cause, e.g. food for body\n2.{ བྱེད་རྒྱུ་ནུས་མེད།} ineffective active cause, e.g. permanent phenomena.
བྱེད-རྒྱུ-ཉི-ཤུ	Twenty types of active causes.\n1. {གནས་པའི་ཨེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of endurance\n2. {བརྟན་པའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause-of stablization\n3. {འབྲལ་བའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of separation\n4. {གསལ་བའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of clarity\n5. {ཡིད་ཆེས་པའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of conviction\n6. {བསྒྱུར་བའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of transformation\n7. {ཡིད་ཆེས་པར་བྱེད་པའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of prompting conviction\n8. {འཐོབ་པའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of achievement\n9. {ཐ་སྙད་པའི་པབྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of convention\n10. {ལྟོས་པའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of reliance\n11. {འཕེན་པའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of projection\n12. {མངོན་པར་འགྲུབ་པའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of establishment\n13. {ཡོངས་སུ་འཛིན་པའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of perfection\n14. {ཆུང་བར་བྱེད་པའི་བྱིད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of diminishment\n15. {སོ་སོར་ངེས་པའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of specific understanding\n16.{ ལྷན་ཅིག་བྱེད་པའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of co-operation\n17. {མི་མཐུན་པའི་དྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of discord\n18. {མི་མཐུན་པ་མ་ཡིན་པའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ}! active cause of harmony\n19. {འབྱུང་བའི་བྱེད་རྒྱུ།} active cause of elements\n20. {བྱེད་རྒྱ།} active cause itself.
བྲམ-ཟེ	Brahmin. One of the four castes of Indian society who are traditionally occupied with religious duties.
བྲམ-ཟེའི-རིག-བྱེད-བཞི	Four Vedas of Brahmins.\n1. {ངེས་བརྗོད།} Rig Veda\n2. {མཆོད་སྦྱིན།} Yajur Veda 3.{སྙན་ཚིག} Sama Veda 4. {སྲིད་སྲུང་།} Atharva Veda
བྲམ-ཟེའི-ལས-དྲུག	Six tasks of a Brahmin; six trainings of a Brahmin.\n1. {ཀློག་པ།} reading\n2.{ ཀློག་ཏུ་འཇུག་པ།} training others to read\n3. {མཆོད་སྦྱིན།} making sacrificial offerings\n4. {མཆོད་སྦྱིད་བྱེད་དུ་འཇུག་པ།} encouraging others to perform sacrificial offerings\n5. {སྦྱིན་པ།} giving alms\n6. {ལེན་པ།} accepting offerings.\n{བྲལ་བའི་འབྲས་བུ།}\n[visaṁyoga phalam]/ Fruit of cessation, e.g. the noble truth of cessation of suffering.
བླ-ན-མེད-པ-དྲུག	[ṣaḍ anuttarayāṇi]/ Six unsurpassables.\n1. {མཐོང་བ་བླ་ན་མེད་པ།} [darṡanānuttaryam]/ unsurpassable seeing\n2. {ཐོས་པ་བླ་ན་མེད་པ།} [ṡravaṇanūttaryam]/ unsurpassable hearing\n3. {རྙེད་པ་བླ་ན་མེད་པ།} [lābhānuttaryam]/ unsurpassable finding\n4. {བསླབ་པ་བླ་ན་མད་པ།} [ṡikṣānuttaryam]/ unsurpassable precepts\n5. {རིམ་གྲོ་བླ་ན་མེད་པ།} [paricaryānuttaryam]/ unsurpassable honour\n6. {རྗེས་སུ་དྲན་པ་བླ་ན་མེད་པ།} [anusmṛty anuttaryam]/ unsurpassable recollection.
བླ-བྲང་	Lama estate. An estate owned by a high lama
བླ-བྲེ	Canopy. A brocade and silk hanging above a high lama's throne.
བླ-མ	Lama. A. Spiritual master; qualified religious teacher. Lit. 'high one' (guru) or 'weighty one', meaning one who possesses great knowledge and spiritual accomplishments.
བླ-མ-དཀོན-མཆོག	A. The entire group of objects of refuge.\nB. A humble and sincere person.\nC. Not good, not bad.
བླ-མ-ཁྱད-ཆོས-སུམ-ལྡན	Three qualities of a Guru.\n1. {ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་རྣམ་པར་དག་པས་སྒོ་གསུམ་གྱི་སྤྱོད་པ་གཙང་པ།} tne conduct of his body, speech and mind are pure due to his strict morality\n2. {ཤེས་རབ་རྣམ་པར་དག་པས་བཤད་པའི་དོན་ལ་མཁས་པ།} ne is wise in giving\nteaching due to his pure wisdom\n3. {བསམ་པ་རྣམ་པར་དག་པས་གཞན་ལ་ཕན་འདོགས་པ།} he benefits others due to his pure altruistic thoughts.
བླ-མ-རྒྱུད-བ	A tantric monk. A monk either from the upper or lower tantric college of the Gelug order.
བླ-མ-མ-ཎི	A Buddhist minstrel. A professional bard who moves freely, tell stories and sings poems of Buddhist ethics, karma, life stories and epics to people.
བླ-མའི-རྣལ-འབྱོར	Guruyoga. The practice of guru devotion; the meditation and services to please one's guru in order to increase one's power to reach one's goal of ultimate enlightenment.
བླ-མེད-ཀྱི-དབང-བཞི	The four initiations of the highest tantra (see {དབང་བཞི}).
བླ-མེད-རྒྱུད-གསུམ	The three highest yoga tantras (anuttarayoga tantra).\n1. {ཕ་རྒྱུད།} father tantra, e. g Guhyasamaja\n2. {མ་རྒྱུད།} mother tantra, e.g. Cakrasanivara\n3. {གཉིས་མེད་ཀྱི་རྒྱུད།} non-dual tantra, e.g. [kālacakra].
བླངས-འདས-སོ-དྲུག	The thirty-six precepts of observance and abandonment of a novice monk (see {དགེ་ཚུལ་གྱི་བླངས་འདས་སོ་དྲུག}).
བླ	Buddhi/1. Mind; perception\n2. Wisdom.
བློ-གྲོས	Wisdom; intelligence; sagacity; prudence; knowledge.
བློ-ངན-གསུམ	The three evil wisdoms.\n1. {མ་རྟོགས་པ།} not-knowing\n{ལོག་པར་རྟོག་པ།} knowing wrong\n3. {ཐེ་ཚོམ།} doubt.
བློ-སྡོག-རྣམ-བཞི	The four principles of thought transformation; the four basic mind trainings.\n1. {དལ་འབྱོར་རྙེད་དཀའ་བསམ་པ།} realizing the preciousness of a human rebirth\n2. {འཆི་བ་མི་རྟག་བསམ་པ།} realizing the impermanence of this life\n3. {འཁོར་བའི་ཉེས་དམིགས་བསམ་པ།} realizing the faults of cyclic existence ([saṁsāra])\n4. {ལས་རྒྱུ་འབྲས་བསམ་པ།} realizing that pleasure and suffering result from good and bad actions respectively.
བློ-སྦྱོང-ཐུན-བརྒྱད-མ	Eight sessions of mind training. Kadampa's mind training precepts transmitted by Dromtonpa.\n1. {ཟས་ལ་བརྟོན་པའི་བློ་སྦྱོང་།} mind training in reliance on eating\n2. {དབུགས་ལ་བརྟེན་པའི་བློ་སྦྱོང་།} mind training in reliance on breath\n3. {ལུས་གངྒཱའི་བྱེ་མ་སྙེད་དུ་སྤྲུལ་པ་ལ་བརྟེན་པའི་བློ་སྦྱོང་།} mind training through visualizing one's body as being as numerous as the grains of sand in the river Ganges\n4. {ཤ་ཁྲག་ལ་བརྟེན་པའི་བློ་སྦྱོང་།} mind training in reliance on flesh and blood\n5. {གཏོར་མ་ལ་བརྟེན་པའི་བློ་སྦྱོང་།} mind training in reliance on ritual cake offerings\n6. {འབྱུང་བ་ལ་བརྟེན་པའི་བློ་སྦྱོང་།} mind training in reliance on the elements\n7. {ལུས་ཡིད་བཞིན་ནོར་བུར་སྤྲུལ་ཏེ་བློ་སྦྱོང་།} mind training through transforming one's body into a wish-fulfilling jewel\n8. {འཆི་བ་མན་ངག་བློ་སྦྱོང་} mind training in reliance on the instructions for death.
བློ-སྦྱོང-དོན-བདུན-མ	The seven point mind training. The Kadampa's mind training precepts: {སྔོན་འགྲོ་རྟེན་གྱི་ཆོས་སེམས་པ།} the preliminary practice\n2. {དངོས་གཞི་བྱང་ཆུབ་ཀྱི་སེམས་སྦྱོང་བ།} generating the mind of enlightenment\n3.{ རྐྱེན་ངན་བྱང་ཆུབ་ཀྱི་ལམ་དུ་བསྒྱུར་བ།} transforming misfortunes into paths to eniightenment\n4. {ཚེ་གཅིག་གི་ཉམས་ལེན་དྲེལ་ནས་བསྟན་པ།} synthesizing the practices of this life\n5. {བློ་འབྱོངས་པའི་ཚད།} the yardstick of mind training\n6.{ བློ་སྦྱོང་གི་དམ་ཚིག} the commitments of mind training\n7.{ བློ་སྦྱོང་གི་བསློབ་བྱ།} the precepts of mind training.
བློ-སྦྱོང-ཞེན-པ-བཞི-བྲལ	The mind training, 'Parting Away from the Four Clingings' common to the Sakya tradition.\n1. {ཚེ་འདི་ལ་ཞེན་ན་ཆོས་པ་མིན།} if you have attachment to this life, you are not a religious practitioner\n2. {འཁོར་བ་ལ་ཞེན་ན་ངེས་འབྱུང་མིན།} if you are attached to cyclic existence, you have no renunciation\n3. {རང་དོན་ལ་ཞེན་ན་བྱང་སེམས་མིན།} if you are attached to your own welfare, you do not have the mind of enlightenment\n4 {འཛིན་པ་བྱུང་ན་ལྟ་བ་མིན།} if you have grasping, you do not have the correct view.
བློ-རིག-བདུན	Seven awarenesses; seven ways of knowing.\n1. {མངོན་སུམ།} [pratyakṣa]/ direct perception\n2. {རྗེས་དཔག} [anumāna]/ inferential perception\n3. {བཅད་ཤེས།} [paricchinna jсāna]/ subsequent cognition\n4. {ཡིད་དཔྱོད།} [manaḥparīkṣā]/ presumption\n5. {སྣང་ལ་མ་ངེས།} [darṡanāniyata]/ inattentive perception\n6. {ཐེ་ཚོམ།} [vicikitsā]/ indecisive mind/ doubt\n7. {ལོག་ཤེས།} [mithyājсāna]/ distorted awareness.
བློ-རིག-བཞི	The four classes of awareness. The classification of mind according to the way it cognizes its respective object of perception.\n1. {སྣང་ལ་མ་ངེས་པ་དང་ཡིད་དཔྱོད་གཉིས་པོ་མ་རྟོགས་པའི་བློ།} non-discerning mind, e.g. the presumptions and inattentive mind\n2. {རྟོག་བཅས་རྟོག་མེད་ཀྱི་ལོགཤེས་གཉིས་པོ་ལོག་པར་རྟོག་པའི་བློ།} distorted mind, e.g. the conceptual and non-conceptual misconceptions\n3.{ བློ་རྩེ་གཉིས་སུ་འཇུག་པ་ཐེ་ཚོམ་གྱི་བློ།} doubt, e.g. wavering minds\n4. {མངོན་རྗེས་ཀྱི་ཚད་མ་གཉིས་པོ་རྟོགས་པའི་བློ།} fcrning mind, e.g. valid direct perception and inferential minds.
བློ-ལ-གཉིས-སུ-དབྱེ-བ	Ways of dividing mind into two.\nA. {རྟོག་པ་དང་རྟོག་མེད་གཉིས་སུ་དབྱེ་བ།} Conceptual and non-conceptual minds.\nB. {ཚད་མ་ཚད་མིན་གཉིས་སུ་དབྱེ་བ།} Valid and invalid cognitions.\nC. {འཁྲུལ་བ་དང་མ་འཁྲུལ་བའི་ཤེས་པ་གཉིས་སུ་དབྱེ་བ།} Mistaken and unmistaken minds.\nD. {རྟོགས་པ་དང་མ་རྟོགས་པ་གཉིས་སུ་དབྱེ་བ།} Realized and unrealized minds.
བློའི-གཞན-སེལ	Mental exclusion of other. An affirming negadve which is a mere projection of thought, e.g. the appearance of not not a vase, i.e. the generic image of a vase.
བློས-བྱས-སྟོང-པ-ཉེད	Intellectually formulated emptiness. Wrongly conceived emptiness.
དབང་	[abhiṣekha]/ Initiation; empowerment. A tantric ceremony in which a lama empowers his disciples to engage in higher practices of tantra through ripening their mental continuum.
དབང-གི-དངོས-གཞིའི-ཆོ-ག	The actual-initiation rite. A part of the initiation programm entailing the erection of the [maṇḍala] and performing the accomplishment rite (sgrub-mchod), the self-initiation and bestowing initiation to others.
དབང-གི-མཐའ-རྟེན	The concluding rite of initiation. Offering of the thanks giving [maṇḍala], agreeing to abide by the commitments, offering the three gates of activities for the master's service, and dedicating virtues.
དབང-གི-སྦྱོར-བ	The preparatory rite of initiation. This includes the ground ritual seeking permission for its use, preparatory rites of accomplishment by constructing the [maṇḍala] be that a powdered sand or painted [maṇḍala], and the actual accomplishment rite for a couple of days.
དབང-མངོན-ལྔ་	The five sensory direct perceptions. That of eyes, ears, nose, tongue and body senses.
དབང-བཅུ	[daṡa vaṡitāḥ]/ The ten powers. The ten powers or^Bodhisattvas having transcended the rank of being an ordinary person, i.e.\ncontrol over the ten types of harms which a common person is likely to experience.\n1. {ཚེ་ལ་དབང་བ།} control of life-span\n2. {སེམས་ལ་དབང་བ།} control of mind\n3. {ཡོ་བྱད་ལ་དབང་བ།} control of resources\n4. {ལས་ལ་དབང་བ།} control of activities\n5. {སྐྱེ་བ་ལ་དབང་བ།} control of rebirth\n6. {མོས་པ་ལ་དབང་བ།} control of aspiration or wishes\n7. {སྨོན་ལམ་ལ་དབང་བ།} control of prayers\n8. {རྫུ་འཕྲུལ་ལ་དབང་བ།} control of miracles\n9. {ཆོས་ལ་དབང་བ།} control of dharma\n10. {ཡེ་ཤེས་ལ་དབང་བ།} control of wisdom.
དབང-བཅུ-གཅིག	The eleven initiations; the eleven initiations that are gateways to entering yoga tantra.\n1-5. {སློབ་མའི་དབང་ལྔ་།} the five initiations of a disciple (see {རིག་པའི་དབང་ལྔ}).\n6-11. {སློབ་དཔོན་གྱི་དབང་དྲུག} the six initiations of the master (see {སློབ་དཔོན་གྱི་དབང་དྲུག}).
དབང-པོ-དགུ	[navendriyāṇi]/ The nine powerful faculties. The nine faculties possessed by an [ārya]\n1-5. {རྣམ་བྱང་གི་དབང་པོ་སྔ་།} the five pure powers or purified mental faculties (see {དབང་པོ་ཨཱིང} B). 6. {ཚོར་བ་བདེ་བ།} pleasant feeling 7. {ཡིད་བདེ་བ།} unpleasant feeling\n8. {བཏང་སྙོམས།} equanimity\n9. {ཡིད་དབང་།} faculty of consciousness.
དབང-པོ-ལྔ་	[paсcendriyāṇi]/The five faculties; the live powers. A. {དབང་པོ་གཟུགས་ཅན་པ་ལྔ་།} The five physical sense faculties (see {ཁམས་བཅོ་བརྒྱད}, 7-12). B. {རྣམ་བྱང་གི་དབང་པོ་ལྔ་།} The five purified mental faculties: 1. {དད་པའི་དབང་པོ།} [ṡraddhendriyam]/ power of faith\n2. {བརྩོན་འགྲུས་ཀྱི་དབང་པོ།} [vīryendriyam]/ power of effort\n3. {དྲན་པའི་དབང་པོ།} [smṛtindriyam]/ power of mindfulness\n4. {ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན་གྱི་དབང་པོ།} [samādhīndriyam]/ power of concentration\n5. {ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱི་དབང་པོ།} [prajсendriyam]/ power of wisdom.\nC. {སོ་སྐྱེའི་རྒྱུད་ཀྱིས་བསྡུས་པའི་ཚོར་བ་སྔ་།} The five ever-afflictive faculties; the five feelings of an ordinary person.\n1-2 {ལུས་ཀྱི་ཚོར་བ་བདེ་སྡུག་གཉིས།} comfortable and uncomfortable feeling of the body\n3-4. {ཡིད་ཀྱི་ཚོར་བ་ཡིད་བདེ་དང་ཡིད་མི་བདེ་གཉིས།} the pleasant and unpleasant feeling of the mind\n5. {ཚོར་བ་བཏང་སྙོམས།} the indifferent feeling.
དབང-པོ-བཅུ-གཅིག	[Ekadaṡendriyāṇi]/ Eleven faculties.\n1-5. {དབང་པོ་ལྔ་།} the five sense powers (see {དབང་པོ་དྲུག} 1-5)\n6. {ཁ།} mouth\n7. {ལག་པ།} hands 8.{ རྐང་པ།} feet 9.{ རྐུབ།} anus 10. {གསང་གནས།} secret organs\n11. {ཡིད་དབང་།} faculty of mind.
དབང-པོ-ཉེར-གཉིས	The twenty-two faculties; the twenty-two powers.\n1-7. {རྟེན་གྱི་དབང་པོ་བདུན།} The seven faculties of reliance (see {རྟེན་གྱི་དབང་པོ་བདུན}).\n8-9. {རྟེན་ཅན་གྱི་དབང་པོ་གཉིས།} The two faculties of basis or sex (see {རྟེན་ཅན་གྱི་དབང་པོ་གཉིས}).\n10-14. {ཚོར་བའི་དབང་པོ་ལྔ་།} The five faculties of feeling (see {ཚོར་བ་ལྔ}).\n15-19. {རྣམ་བྱང་གི་དབང་པོ་ལྔ་།} the five purified faculties (see {དབང་པོ་ལྔ}B).\n20-22. {ཟག་མེད་ཀྱི་དབང་པོ་གསུམ།} the three uncontaminated faculties (see {ཟག་མེད་ཀྱི་དབང་པོ་གསུམ}).
དབང-པོ-དྲུག	[ṣaḍ indriyāṇi]/ Six cognitive powers; six faculties; also called the six internal sources of perception (nang-gi skyed-mched drug).\n1. {མིག་གི་དབང་པོ།} [cakṣurindriyam]/ eye sense power\n2. {རྣ་བའི་དབང་པོ།} [ṡrotrendriyam]/ ear sense faculties\n3. {སྣའི་དབང་པོ།} [ghraṇendriyam]/ nose sense faculties\n4. {ལྕེའི་དབང་པོ།} [jihvendriyam]/ tongue sense power\n5. {ལུས་ཀྱི་དབང་པོ།} kāyendriyam]/ body sense power\n6. {ཡིད་ཀྱི་དབང་པོ།} [mana indriyam]/ mental sense power.\n{དབང་པོ་གཟུགས་ཅན་པ་ལྔ་།}\nThe five physical faculties (see {ཁམས་བཅོ་བརྒྱད} B. 1-5).
དབང-པོ-གསུམ	The three faculties. A. The three pure powers gained on the paths of seeing, meditation and no-more learning, respectively (see 6-8 of {རྣམ་བྱང་གི་དབང་པོ་བརྒྱད།་ཟག་མེད་ཀྱི་དབང་པོ་གསུམ}).\nB. The three types of persons according to their level of intelligence:\n1. {དབང་པོ་ཐ་མ།} poor intellect\n2. {དབང་པོ་འབྲིང་།} moderate intellect\n3. {དབང་པོ་རབ།} sharp intellect
དབང-ཕྱུག	[īṡvara]/ A. Mahadeva ([ṡiva]).\nB. Glory and power.\nC. Excellence.\nD. Powerful attainments ([siddhi]).
དབང-ཕྱུག-བརྒྱད	A. The eight sovereign qualities (see {ཐུན་མོང་མ་ཡིན་པའི་དབང་ཕྱུག་གི་ཡོན་ཏན་བརྒྱད}).\nB. The eight powerful attainments; the eight worldly feats (see {ཐུན་མོང་བའི་དབང་ཕྱུག་གི་ཡོན་ཏན་བརྒྱད}).
དབང-ཕྱུག-བཅུ	The ten sovereign qualities of a Bodhisattva; the ten powers (see {བདང་བཅུ}).
དབང-ཕྱུག-པ	[īṡvara]/ The followers of [īṡvara]. A school of Hindu philosophy which asserts that the world and its inhabitants are created by the projected thought (blo-yi gyo-ba) of Isvara (Siva), who they believe to be permanent, omniscient and never changing.
དབང-པབཞི	The four-fold initiations. The four-fold initiations of the\nhighest yoga tantra.\n1. {བུམ་དབང་} the vase initiation\n2. {གསང་དབང་།} the secret initiation\n3. {ཤེས་རབ་ཡེ་ཤེས་ཀྱི་དབང་།} the primordial-wisdom initiation\n4. {ཚིག་དབང་།} the word initiation.
དབང-བཞི-པ	The fourth initiation. The verbal initiation of words by which a tantric master introduces his disciple to the union of the pure body (illusory body) and mind (clear light) of a Buddha.
དབང-ལུང-ཁྲིད-གསུམ	The threefold lineages—initiations, transmissions and explanations.
དབུ-སྡེ-གཉིས	The two holy assemblies; the two spiritual communities.\n1. {གོས་དཀར་ལྕང་ལོ་ཅན་གྱི་ལྔེ་།} tantric yogis and yoginis who wear a white lower garment\n2. {རབ་བྱུང་ངུར་སྨྲིག་གི་སྡེ།} monks and nuns who wear red robes.
དབུ-མ-ཐལ-འགྱུར-བ	[prāsaṅgika mādhyamika] school. The highest school of Madhyamika philosophy which asserts that phenomena do not exist by their own nature, inherently, not even on the conventional level.
དབུ-མ-པ	[mādhyamika] school. The middle-view school, who assert emptiness as being free of two extremes—the extreme of existence and extreme of non-existence.
དབུ-མ-རང-རྒྱུད-པ	[svātantrika mādhyamika] school. A sub-school of [mādhyamika] philosophy which asserts that all phenomena exist by their own nature, inherently, but do not have true existence.
དབུ-མ-རིགས-ཚོགས-ལྔ་	The five middle way treatises. The five famous treatises of [ācārya Nāgārjuna]\n1. {དབུ་མ་རྩ་བ་ཤེས་རབ།} [prajсāmūla]/ The Fundamental Wisdom of the Middle Way\n2. {རྩོད་ཟློག} [vigrahavyāvartanī]/ Refutation of Arguments\n3. {སྟོང་ཉིད་བདུན་ཅུ།} [ṡūnyatāsaptati]/ Seventy Stanzas on Emptiness\n4. {རིགས་པ་དྲུག་ཅུ།} [yuktiṣaṣṭikā]/ Sixty Stanzas of Reasoning\n5. {ཞིབ་མོ་རྣམ་འཐག} [vaidalyasūtra]/ Fine Investigation and Discernment.
དབུ-མ-རིག-ཚོགས-དྲུག	The six middle way treatises (see {དབུ་མ་རིགས་ཚོགས་ལྔ་།} 1-5)\n6. {རིན་ཆེན་ཕྲེང་བ།} [ratnāvali]/ The Jewel Garland.
དབུ-མ-གཞན-སྟོང་	The alternative emptiness; the other emptiness (see {གཞན་སྟོང}). The view asserted by Kunkhyen Dolpo-pa, a prophet of Jo-nang school of tibetan Buddhist philosophy (see {གཞན་སྟོང}).
དབེན-པ-གསུམ	The three isolations.\nA. {མདོ་སྔགས་ཐུན་མོང་བའི་དབང་དུ།} The three isolations common to both [sūtra] and tantra traditions.\n1. {ལུས་འདུ་འཛིས་དབེན་པ།} body free of association in busy life\n2. {སེམས་མི་དགེ་བའི་རྣམ་རྟོག་གིས་དབེན་པ།} mind fee of non-virtuous conceptualizations\n3. {སྒོ་གསུམ་ཐ་མལ་གྱི་སྣང་ཞེན་གྱིས་དབེན་པ།} the three gates of activities free of ordinary vision and clinging.\nB. {གསང་སྔགས་རྫོགས་རིམ་གྱི་རྣལ་འབྱོར་ལ།} According to the Vajrayana's completion stage yoga of triple isolation (see {དབེན་གསུམ་རྡོ་རྗེའི་རྣལ་འབྱོར}).
དབེན-གསུམ-རྡོ-རྗེའི-རྣལ-འབྱོར	Vajrayoga of triple isolation. A meditation practice similiar to the completion stage yoga in highest tantra.\n1. {ངག་དབེན།} isolation of speech\n2. {ལུས་དབེན།} isolation of body\n3. {སེམས་དབེན།} isolation of mind.
དབྱངས-ཀྱི-ཡན-ལག-དྲུག-བཅུ	The sixty features of a melodic voice; the sixty mellifulous speech.\n1. {མཉན་པ།} flexible\n2. {འཇམ་པ།} soft\n3. {ཡིད་དུ་འོང་བ།} attractive\n4. {ཡིད་ལ་ཐད་པ།}delightful\n5. {དག་པ།} pure\n6. {དྲི་མ་མེད་པ།} faultless\n7. {གསལ་བ།} clear\n8.{ སྣང་ཞིང་འཇེབས་པ།} pleasantly soothing\n9. {མཉན་པར་འོས་པ།} worthy of hearing\n10. {མི་ཚུགས་པ།} not harmful\n11. {སྙན་པ།} beautiful\n12. {དུལ་བ།} subdued\n13. {མི་རྩུབ་པ།} not coarse\n14. {མི་བརླང་པ།} not rought\n15. {རབ་ཏུ་དུལ་བ།} completely subdued\n16. {རྣར་སྙན་པ།} beautiful to hear\n17. {ལུས་སུམ་པར་བྱེད་པ།} refreshing for body\n18. {སེམས་སིམ་པར་བྱེད་པ།} refreshing for mind\n19. {རྙིང་དགའ་བར་བྱེད་པ།} pleasing the heart\n20. {དགའ་བ་དང་བདེ་བ་བསྐྱེད་པ།} generating pleasure and happiness\n21. {ཡོངས་སུ་གདུང་བ་མེད་པ།} completely without sadness\n22. {ཀུན་ཏུ་ཤེས་པར་བྱེད་པ།} being the object of universal knowledge\n23. {རྣམ་པར་རིག་པར་བྱེད་བ།} being the object of thorough understanding\n24. {རྣམ་པར་གསལ་བ།} completely clear\n25. {དགའ་བར་བྱེད་པ།} producing pleasure\n26. {མངོན་པར་དགའ་བར་བྱེད་པ།} producing manifest pleasure\n27.{ ཀུན་ཏུ་ཤེས་པར་བྱེད་པ།} producing universal knowledge\n28. {རྣམ་པར་རིག་པར་བྱེད་པ།} producing thorough understanding\n29. {རིགས་པ།} logical\n30. {འབྲེལ་བ།} relevant\n31. {ཚིག་ཟློས་པའི་སྐྱོན་མེད་པ།} free of repetition\n32. {སེང་གེའི་སྒྲའི་ཤུགས།} possessing the strength of a lion's roar\n33.{ གླང་པོ་ཆེའི་སྒྲ་སྐད།} producing the sound of an elephant\n34. {འབྲུག་གི་སྒྲད་སྐད།} producing the sound of a cloud (thunder)\n35. {ཀླུའི་སྒྲ་སྐད།} producing the sound of a Naga (serpent-spirit)\n36. {དྲི་ཟའི་གླུ་དབྱངས།} producing the sound of Gandharva (a celestial musician)\n37. {ཀ་ལ་པིང་ཀའི་གླུ་དབྱངས།} producing the melody of a spanow\n38. {ཚངས་པའི་སྒྲ་དབྱངས།} producing the melody of Brahma\n39. {ཤང་ཤང་ཏེའི་སྒྲ་དབྱངས་བསྒྲགས་པ།} producing the sound of a [jīvaсjīvaka] bird\n40. {ལྷའི་དཔང་པོའི་དབྱངས་ལྟར་སྙན་པ།} pleasant as the melodies of the lord of gods\n41. {རྔ་ཡི་སྒྲ།} producing the sound of a dundubhi drum\n42. {མ་ཁེངས་པ།} free of arrogance\n43. {མི་དམའ་པ།} not degraded\n44. {སྒྲ་ཐམས་ཅད་ཀྱི་རྗེས་སུ་ཞུགས་པ།} harmonious to all sounds\n45. {ཚིག་ཟུར་ཆག་པ་མེད་པ།} free of corrupted words\n46. {མ་ཚང་བ་མེད་པ།} not incomplete\n47. {མ་ཤུམ་པ།} not crying\n48. {མ་ཞན་པ།} not depressed\n49. {རབ་ཏུ་དགའ་བ།} extremely joyous\n50. {ཁྱབ་པ།} pervasive\n51. {ཆུབ་པ།} perfected\n52. {རྒྱུན་ཆགས་པ།} flowing\n53. {འགྲེལ་བ།} elegantly connected\n54. {སྒྲ་ཐམས་ཅད་རྫོགས་པར་བྱེད་པ།} making all sounds complete\n55. {དབང་པོ་ཐམས་ཅད་ཚིམ་པར་བྱེད་པ།} satisfying all senses\n56. {མ་སྨད་པ} non-abusive\n57. {མི་འགྱུར་བ།} unchanging\n58. {མ་བརྟགས་པ།} unwavering\n59. {འཁོར་ཀུད་ཏུ་གྲགས་པ།} popular in all circles\n60. {རྣམ་པ་ཐམས་ཅད་ཀྱི་མཆོག་དང་ལྡན་པ།} possessing the best of all components.
དབྱངས-ཀྱིས-བསྙད-པའི-སྡེ	Verse-form teachings. One of the twelve scriptural categories (see {གསུང་རབ་ཡན་ལག་བཅུ་གཉིས}); verses which Buddha uttered during the beginning or conclusion of a discourse.
དབྱངས-ཅན-མ	[sarasvatīdevī]. Goddess of eloquence. A goddess of both the Hindu and Buddhist pantheons, worshipped as the perfection of eloquence and regarded as the embodiment of mellifluent clarity of sound and speech.
དབྱར-སྔ-མ	Early summer retreat. Observance of a summer or rainy season retreat by the monastic communities from the sixteenth of the sixth month of the Tibetan calendar until the thirtieth of the eighth month. The tradition followed by the monastic community in general.
དབྱར-གནས	[vārṣika]/ Summer retreat. One of the three basic observances for monks as prescribed by Buddha [ṡākyamuni]; rainy season retreat during which time they do not go beyond the marked bounds of the monasteries and observe rules and regulations in addition to their regular routine.
དབྱར-ཕྱི-མ	Later summer retreat. Observance of a summer retreat by the monastic communities from the sixteenth day of the seventh month of the Tibetan calendar until thirtieth of the eighth month. This tradition is followed by both the upper and lower tantric colleges of Lhasa.
དབྱིག-གཉེན	[vasubandhu]/ Regarded as a renowned Buddhist scholar of the 5th century, the younger brother of [ārya Asaṅga] and the author of [abhidharmakoṡṭika] and the eight treatises of Vasubandhu (see {པྲ་ཀ་ར་ན་སྡེ་བརྒྱད}).
དབྱིབས-སྔགས-ཆོས-གསུམ	The threefold practices; the three generation stage yogas or practices:\n1. {བསྐྱེད་པ་དབྱིབས་ཀྱི་རྣལ་འབྱོར།} the yoga of generating into the shape and form of a deity\n2. {བཟླས་པ་སྔགས་ཀྱི་རྣལ་འབྱོར།} the yoga of reciting mantras of the deity\n3. {འོད་གསལ་འཇུག་ལྡང་ཆོས་ཀྱི་རྣལ་འབྱོར།} the yoga of dissolution and arisal within the clear light experience.
དབྱིབས-གཟུགས-བརྒྱད	Eight types of shape and form.\n1. {རིང་བ།} long\n2. {ཐུང་བ།} short\n3. {མཐོ་བ།} high\n4. {དམའ་བ།} low\n5.{ལྷམ་པ།} square\n6. {ཟླུམ་པོ།} round\n7.{ ཕྱ་ལེ་བ།} even\n8. {ཕྱ་ལེ་བ་མ་ཡིན་པ།} uneven.
དབྱེར-མེད-ཆོས-སྐུ	Inseparable truth body. The inseparability of the emanation body, enjoyment body and the natural truth body of a Buddha.
དབྱེར-མེད-རྡོ-རྗེའི-གསུང་	The inseparable vajra teachings. One of the five kinds of teachings of a Buddha (see {བསུང་ཨིང}) according to the Nyingma tradition. This refers to the non-duality of sound and emptiness of all speeches and teachings of a Buddha being totally free of the two extremes.
འབའ-རོམ-བཀའ-བརྒྱུད	Bamrom Kagyu tradition. One of the eight lineages of Kagyu tradition of Tibetan Buddhism founded by Gampopa's disciple, Bamrom Darma Wangchuk who is believed to have been the incarnation of Tulzug Choepa Nagpopa.
འབུར-པོ-ལྔ་	Five protruberances. That state of foetal development in the womb of a mother when the signs of five parts of body become obvious.\n1-2. {དཔུས་མོ་གཉིས།} signs of two legs\n3-4. {དཔུང་པ་གཉིས།} signs of two arms\n5. {མགོ།} the head.
འབྱུང-འགྱུར-གྱི-རེག-བྱ-བདུན	Seven tangible objects arising from the elements; seven objects of touch that are transformations of the four elements.\n1.{འཇམ་པ།} smoothness\n2. {རྩུབ་པ།} roughness\n3. {ཡང་བ།} lightness\n4. {ལྕི་བ།} heaviness\n5. {གྲང་བ།} coldness\n6. {བཀྲེས་པ།} hunger\n7. {སྐོམ་པ།} thirst.
འབྱུར-འགྱུར-གྱི-རེག-བྱ-ཉེར-གཉིས	Twenty-two tangible objects arising from the elements.\n1-7. (see {འབྱུང་འགྱུར་གྱི་རེག་བྱ་བདུན})\n8. {མཉེན་པ།} pliancy\n9. {ལྷོད་པ།} loseness\n10. {ལྷོད་པ་མ་ཡིན་པ།} tauntness\n11. {ཚིམ་པ།} contentment\n12. {ཉམ་ཆེ་བ།} strong\n13. {ཉམ་ཆུང་བ།} weak\n14. {བརྒྱལ་བ།} fainting/ swooning\n15. {གཡའ་བ།} itching\n16. {བགྲེད་པ།} slipperiness\n17. {ན་བ} illness\n18. {རྒ་བ།} aging\n19. {འཆི་བ།} death\n20. {ངལ་བ།} fatigue\n21. {ངལ་གསོ་བ།} rest\n22.{ སྤུངས་ཆེ་བ།} weighty.
འབྱུང-བ-བཞི	The four elements.\n1. {ས།} earth\n2. {ཆུ།} water\n3. {མ།} fire\n4. {རླུང་།} wind. When it is five add {ནམ་མཁའ།} space; and when six add {རྣམ་ཤེས།} consciousness.
འབྱོར-བ-བཅུ	Ten endowments; ten condusive factors for a person to practise dharma\n1. {མི་ཡིན་པ།} being a human\n2. {ཡུལ་དབུས་སུ་སྐྱེས་པ།} being born in a Buddhist land\n3. {དབང་པོ་ཚང་བ།} having sound senses\n4. {ལས་མཐའ་མ་ལོག་པ།} being free from extreme actions\n5. {ཆོས་ལ་དད་པ།} having faith in the Dharma\n6. {སངས་རྒྱས་བྱོན་པ།} Buddha's having appeared\n7. {དམ་ཆོས་གསུངས་པ།} Buddha's having taught the Dharma\n8. {བསྟན་པ་གནས་པ།} the flourishing of his teachings\n9. {དེའི་རྗེས་སུ་འཇུག་པ་བཞུགས་པ།} there being people following his teachings\n10. {གཞན་ལ་རྟག་ཏུ་བརྩེ་བ་སྙིང་རྗེ་དང་ལྡན་པ།} having compassionate feelings towards others.
འབྲས-སྐྱབས	[phala ṡaraṇa]/The resultant refuge. The fully enlightened state of Buddha in one's own continuum, i.e. that fully enlightened refuge developed within oneself.
འབྲས-ཆོས-ལྔ་	The five resultant phenomena; the five qualities of Buddhahood. Those of the body, speech, mind, qualities, and enlightened activities of a Buddha.
འབྲས-ཆོས-ཉེར-ལྔ་	The twenty-five resultant phenomena; the five each with respect to the body, speech, mind, qualities and enlightened activities of a Buddha according to the explanation given in the Nyingma tantras.
འབྲས-རྟགས-ཡང-དག	Correct reason of effect. A correct reason which is the effect of the predicate in a logical syllogism.
འབྲས-རྟགས-ཡང-དག-གི-དབྱེ-བ-ལྔ་	Five divisions of correct reason of result.\n1. {རྒྱུ་དངོས་གྲུབ་ཀྱི་རྟགས།} that establishing the direct cause\n2. {རྒྱུ་སྔོན་སོང་གི་རྟགས།} that establishing the preceding cause\n3. {རྒྱུ་སྤྱི་སྒྲུབ་ཀྱི་རྟགས།} that establishing the general cause\n4. {རྒྱུ་ཁྱད་པར་སྒྲུབ་ཀྱི་རྟགས།} that establishing the particular cause\n5. {རྒྱུ་ཆོས་རྗེས་དཔོག་གི་རྟགས།} establishing the quality of a cause.
འབྲས-དུས-ཀྱི-འོད-གསལ	The resultant clear light. The perfect realization of the final reality of the basic primordial clear light existent within oneself as introduced by a qualified meditation master, and the ability to maintain this experience day and night.
འབྲས-བུ-ལྔ་	[paсca phalāni]/ Five types of results; five types of fruits.\n1. {རྒྱུ་མཐུན་གྱི་འབྲས་བུ།} [niṣyanda phalam]/ results that accord with the cause\n2. {བདག་པོའི་འབྲས་བུ།} [adhipati phalam]/ environmental cause\n3. {སྐྱེས་བུའི་བྱེད་པའི་འབྲས་བུ} [puruṣa kāra phalam]/ results caused by persons\n4. {རྣམ་པར་སྨིན་པའི་} {འབྲས་བུ།} [vipāka phalam]/ ripened results\n5. {བྲལ་པའི་འབྲས་བུ།} [visaṁyoga phalam]/ cessational results.
འབྲས-བུ-ཆོས-སྐུ-མཚོན-བྱེད-ཀྱི-ཆོས-བཞི	Four features characterizing the resultant Truth Body of a Buddha.\n1. {ངོ་བོ་ཉིད་སྐུ}[svabhāvakāya]/ the nature truth body\n2. {ཡེ་ཤེས་ཆོས་སྐུ} [jсānadharmakāya]/ the wisdom truth body\n3. {ལོངས་སྐུ} [saṁbhogakāya]/ the complete enjoyment body\n4. {སྤྲུལ་སླུ} [nirmāṇakāya]/ the emanation body
འབྲས-བུ-ཐུཨོད-རྒལ	He who attains the fruit by leaps.
འབྲས-བུ-རིམ-གྱིས-པ	He who attains the fruit successively.
འབྲས-བུའི-ཐེག-པ-དྲུག	The five resultant vehicles; the five tantric vehicles or paths.\n1-4. The four classes of tantra (see {རྒྱུད་སྡེ་བཞི})\n5. {ཨ་ནུ་ཡོ་ག} anuyoga vehicle\n6. {ཨ་ཏི་ཡོ་ག} atiyoga vehicle.
འབྲས-བུའི-འོད-གསལ	The resultant clear light. The dharmakaya itself.
འབྲས-གཟུགས-བཅུ-གཅིག	Eleven resultant forms.\n1-5. {དབང་པོ་གཟུགས་ཅན་པ་ལྔ་།} five physical sense faculties (see {དབང་པོ་དྲུག} 1-5)\n6-10. {གཟུང་དོན་ལྔ་།} five objects of perception (see {ཡུལ་དྲུག})\n11. {ཆོས་ཀྱི་སྐྱེ་མཆེད་པའི་གཟུགས།} abstract forms that are sources for mental consciousness.
འབྲས-ཡུམ-ལ-ཉེ-བའི-གཞི-ཤེས	[phalabhūtamāturāsannībhuta vastujсāna]/ Basic wisdom close to the resultant mother. The knowledge of the basis near to omniscient wisdom; synonymous with the knowledge of the basis (gzhi-shes) within the mental continuum of a [mahāyāna ārya] that is conjoined with exalted means and wisdom, characterized as an antidote towards grasping at true existence.
འབྲས-ཡུམ-ལ-རིང-བའི-གཞི-ཤེས	[phalabhūtamāturadūrībhūta vastujсana]/ Basic wisdom distant from the resultant mother; knowledge of the basis distant from omniscient wisdom; synonymous with the knowledge of the basis within the mental continuum of a [hīnayāna ārya], that lacks great compassion and is bound by grasping at true existence.
འབྲི-གུང-བཀའ-པབརྒྱུད	Drikung Kagyud. One of the prominent linaeges of the Kagyud order of Tibetan Buddhism, founded by the master KyobaJigtenGonpo (1143-1217).
འབྲུག-པ-བཀའ-བརྒྱུད	Drugpa Kagyud. One of the prominent lineages of the Kagyu order of Tibetan Buddhism, founded by Yogi Lingrepa Pema Dorje and Choeje Tsangpa Gyalre.
འབྲེལ-བ-གཉིས	Two types of relationship. Relationship between any\nphenomena can come under these two forms.\n1. {བདག་གཅིག་འབྲེལ།} relationship of identical nature\n2. {དེ་བྱུང་འབྲེལ།} cause and result relationship.
འབྲོག-དགོན-པ	[kāntāra]/ Hermitage. Monastery or seat of learning for monks situated at least 500 armspans away from a town; a hermitage is situated further away then this according to the Vinaya rules.
སྦས-དོན	Hidden meaning; implicit meaning, e.g. the teachings of\nemptiness presented in the text, Ornament of Clear Realization.
