That of:\n1. {འདུན་པའི་རྫུ་འཕྲུལ་གྱི་རྐང་པ།} [chanda ṛddhipāda]/ aspiration\n2. {བརྩོན་འགྲུས་ཀྱི་རྫུ་འཕྲུལ་གྱི་རྐང་པ།} [virya ṛddhipāda]/ effort\n3. {བསམ་པའི་རྫུ་འཕྲུལ་གྱི་རྐང་པ།} [citta ṛddhipāda]/ thought\n4. {དཔྱོད་པའི་རྫུ་འཕྲུལ་གྱི་རྐང་པ།} [mīmaṃsā ṛddhipāda] analysis.
རྫུ-འཕྲུལ-ལྔ་	Five types of miracles.\n1. {སྒོམ་བྱུང་གི་རྫ་འཕྲུལ།} miracles acquired through meditation\n2. {སྐྱེས་ཐོབ་ཀྱི་རྫུ་འཕྲུལ།} miracles acquired by birth\n3. {སྔགས་ལས་ཐོབ་པའི་རྫུ་འཕྲུལ།} miracles acquired through tantric practices\n4. {སྨན་ལས་བྱུང་བའི་རྫུ་འཕྲུལ།} miracles acquired through medicinal pills\n5. {ལས་ལས་བྱུང་བའི་རྫུ་འཕྲུལ།} miracles acquired through karmic forces.
རྫུན-བཞི	Four types of lying; four types of lying about monk's precepts.\n1. {ཕམ་པའི་སྡེར་གཏོགས་ཀྱི་རྫུན།} lying classed as a defeat\n2. {ལྷག་མའི་སྡེར་གཏོགས་ཀྱི་རྫུན།} lying classed as a remainder\n3. {མ་ངེས་པའི་སྡེར་གཏོགས་ཀྱི་རྫུན།} lying classed as an indefinite case\n4. {ཉེས་བྱས་ཀྱི་སྡེར་གཏོགས་ཀྱི་རྫུན།} lying classed as a fault.
རྫིགས-ལྡན-གྱི-དུས	The Perfected Aeon (see {བསྐལ་པ་རྫོགས་ལྡན}).
རྫོགས-པ-ཆེན-པོ	Great perfection. A term exclusive to Nyingma doctrine and meditation. The spontaneous and natural perfection of fully enlightened qualities possessed by the three [kāyas] within the reality of mind, i.e. the primodially empty nature [dharmakāya]; the naturally luminous [sambhogakāya]; and all-pervasive compassion [nirmāṇakāya], which is otherwise the ultimate reality of all phenomena.
རྫོགས-པ-ཆེན-པོ-སྙིང-ཏིག	Heart's core great perfection. The transmission of great perfection originally received by King Trisong Deutsan from [ācārya vimalamitra] During the later period of propagation of Buddhism (see {བསྟན་པ་ཕྱི་དར}) in Tibet. This transmission was widely disseminated by the great master Kunkhyen Longchen Rabjampa (see {ཀུན་མཁྱེན་ཀློང་ཆེན་རབ་འབྱམས}).
རྫོགས-པ-སྤྱི-ཆིབས-ཀྱི-ས	The ground of riding the uhiversal {རྫོགས་ཆེན་}. According to the Nyingma tradition, this refers to the tenth Bodhisattva ground attained on the fifth stage of yoga, where a person has completely and perfectly integrated all experiences and appearances on the path to liberation into the sphere of lack of production of all projections of the Rupakaya.
རྫོགས-རིམ	[saṃpanna krama]/ Completion stage. An anuttarayoga tantra practice of meditation in which a practioner trains or is able to activate the innate primordial wisdom through experiencing the four-fold joys (see {དགའ་བ་བཞི}) and the mind of clear light through experiencing the four-fold empties (see {སྟོང་བཞི}) respectively upon this vajra (deity) body.
རྫོགས-རིམ-རྣལ-འབྱོར-བཞི	The four completion stage yogas; the four completion stage yogas of the [yamāntaka tantra].\n1. {སྔགས་ཀྱི་རྣལ་འབྱོར།} yoga of mantra\n2. {དམ་ཚིག་གི་རྣལ་འབྱོར།} yoga of samaya\n3. {དབྱིབས་ཀྱི་རྣལ་འབྱོར།} yoga of shape\n4. {ཡེ་ཤེས་ཀྱི་རྣལ་འབྱོར།} yoga of primordial wisdom.
རྫོགས-རིམ-རིམ-ལྔ་	Five levels of the completion stage.\n1. {ལུས་དབེན།} isolation of body\n2. {ངག་དབེན} isolation of speech\n3. {སེམས་དབེན།} isolation of mind\n4. {འིད་གསལ།} clear light mind\n5. {སྒྱུ་ལུས།} illusory body. In some cases, the first two are listed as one and the state of union ([yuganaddha]) is added to the list to make five. See the five profound paths ([zab-lam rim-lnga]).
རྫོགས-རིམ-རིམ-པ-དྲུག	Six levels of the completion stage, (see {རྫོག་རིམ་རིམ་ལྔ} 1-5, above)\n6. {ཟུང་འཇུག} the state of union ([yuganaddha]).
རྫོགས-བྱེད-ཀྱི-ལས	Completing karma. Karma that primarily determines the specific details of environmental and physical attributes, personality, etc., of a being irrespective of the level of rebirth, e.g. a dtfg enjoying comforts of living in a palace though just an animal.
རྫོགས-སྨིན-སྦྱངས-གསུམ	Accomplishment, maturation and purification.\n{རྫུས་སྐྱེས།}\n[upapāduka]/ Miraculous birth. One of the four types of birth (see {སྐྱེ་གནས་བཞི}), e.g. the birth of Guru Padmasambhava.
ཝ-སྐྱེས	Fox; exemplifies cowardice and deceit in a person
ཝ-ཁ	Gutter.
ཝ-ཁུང་	Guttur or wolf's lair.
ཝ-བད	Rhinoceros.
ཝ-ར-སྐད-ཅན	Donkey; ass.
ཝཱ-རཱ-ཎ-སཱི	[vārāṇasi]. One of the four principal holy places of Buddhist\npilgrimage, where Buddha [ṡākyamuni] turned the first wheel of doctrine concerning the four noble truths to the the five ascetics (see {འཁོར་ཨཱིང་སྡེ་བཟང་པོ}).
ཝ-རཱུ-ཎ	Name of a [nāga]; a water-deity.
ཝ-ལམ-ཅན	Cemetery.
ཝང-གང་	Joyful state of mind; laughing expression.
ཝ-ལེ-ཝ-ལེ	Clear mental comprehension of words and meanings.
ཝར-ཏུ	Vartu. An ancient script used by Tonmi Sambhota as a model for headless Tibetan script (U-med).
ཝེར-མ	Warrior god; god of weapon.
ཝོ-རྒྱལ	{འོ་རྒྱལ།}\nTiredness; fatigue.
ཞ-ལུ-དགོན-བ	Zhalu monastery. A monastery in the vicinity of Zhigatse established during the 11th century, which flourished as a principal centre of study and training of Zhalu philosophy during the time of Buton Rinchen Drup. It is believed that this monastery had many Sanskrit texts.
ཞང-ཞུང་	Zhang-Zhung is believed to be the cradle of ancient Tibetan culture, and according to some the place of origin of the Bon religion. Some historical texts like the Blue Annals identify Zhang-zhung with Guge, now the Tsa-dha district in the Ngari region of western Tibet.
ཞབས-ཏོག-རྣམ-གསུམ	The threefold services; the three ways to honour and please\none's root guru.\n1. {རབ་སྒྲུབ་པའི་མཆོད་པ།} offering of practice as the supreme\n2. {འབྲིང་ལུས་ངག་གི་ཞབས་ཏོག} physical and vocal service as the middling\n3. {ཐ་མ་ཟང་ཟིང་གི་འབུལ་བ།} material offering as the modest.
ཞལ-ཏ-བ	[vārika]/ Monk steward. Monk official in charge of economic affairs; especially one chosen during the three months rainy season retreat.
ཞལ-ནས-གསུངས-པའི-བཀའ	Spoken teaching of Buddha. Teachings that Buddha actually spoke from his mouth directly; verbal teachings of Buddha.
ཞལ-གདམས	Instruction; advice of a respected person.
ཞལ-ཟས	[bhojya]/ Food; food offerings.
ཞི-གནས	[ṡamatha]/ Mental quiescence meditation; calm abiding meditation. A single-pointed meditative concentration developed through the techniques of settling the mind; a practice common to both Buddhists and non-Buddhists.
ཞི-གནས-ཀྱི-སྟོབས-དྲུག	The six powers of calm abiding meditation (see {སྟོབས་དྲུག}).
ཞི-གནས-ཀྱི-དམིགས-པ-བཞི	Four objects of mental quiescence meditation.\n1. {ཁྱབ་པའི་དམིགས་པ།} pervasive object\n2. {སྤྱད་པ་རྣམ་སྦྱོང་གི་དམིགས་པ།} objects for overcoming objects of obsession\n3. {མཁས་པའི་} {དམིགས་པ།} object of the wise practitioner\n4. {ཉོན་མོངས་རྣམ་སྦྱོང་གི་དམིགས་པ།} object for purification of delusions.
ཞི-གནས-ཀྱི-ཚོགས	The conditions for calm abiding meditation; the necessities for practicing calm abiding meditation.\n1. {མཐུན་པའི་ཡུལ་ན་གནས་པ།} living in a harmonious place\n2. {འདོད་པ་ཆུང་བ།} having few desires\n3. {ཆོག་ཤེས་པ།} having contentment\n4. {བྱ་བ་མང་པོ་ཡོངས་སུ་སྤངས་པ།} having few activities of involvement\n5. {ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་རྣམ་པར་དག་པ།} having pure morality\n6. {འདོད་པ་ལ་སོགས་པའི་རྣམ་པར་རྟོག་པ་ཡོངས་སུ་སྤངས་པ།}\nhaving freedom from gross delusions such as attachment.
ཞི-གནས-ཀྱི-ཡིད-བྱེད-བཞི	The four attentions of calm abiding meditation (see {ཡིད་བྱེད་བཞི}).
ཞི-གནས-ཀྱི-གསོ-སྦྱོང	Restoration and purification ritual through mental quiescence meditation. A gathering of monks for purification of negativities entailing meditation on close mindfulness or contemplation.
ཞི-གནས-སྐབས-ཀྱི-ཉེས-པ-ལྔ་	The five faults of calm abiding meditation (see {ཉེས་པ་ལྔ}).
ཞི-བ-འཚོ	[ṡāntarakṣita]/ [ācārya ṡāntarakṣita]. A highly learned master-scholar from Bengal who visited Tibet during the time of King Tnsong Deutsan. He assisted Guru Padmasambhava in the building of Samye monastery and was responsible for founding the monastic community for the first time in Tibet.
ཞི-བྱེད	The Pacifier. This is a Buddhist religious tradition founded by Phadampa Sangye at the beginning of the 12th century, and propagated the practice of gcod (cutting-off) ritual in Tibet.
ཞི-ལྷག-ཟུང-འབྲེལ	[ṡamatha vipaṡyana yuganaddha]/ Union of mental quiescence and penetrative insight meditation.
ཞིང-དཉ-སྦྱོར-བ	[kṣetrapāla]/ Field protectors. Protectors of the land and fields; a kind of local deity often associated with charnel grounds. Also those male and female guardians who reside in the heavens.
ཞིང-བཅུ-ཚང-བའི-དགྲ-གེགས	The ten heinous hindrances (see {བསྒྲལ་བའི་ཞིང་བཅུ}). These identify someone as an enemy of the Buddha Dharma to be expelled according to tantra
ཞིང-དག-སྦྱོར-བ	[kṣetraṡuddhi prayoga]/ Pure land training. A Bodhisattva practice by which one can transform all roots of virtue into means for establishing a Buddha field, with its inhabitants, where he will gain the state of full enlightenment; this path arises on the three pure Bodhisattva grounds, i.e. the eigth, ninth and tenth.
ཞུགས-གནས-གྱད	Eight noble persons; enterers and abiders in the four state of an ascetics—Stream-winner, Once returner, Never returner and Arhatship.\n1. {རྒྱུན་ཞུགས་ཞུགས་པ།} enterer into the fruit of a stream-winner\n2. {རྒྱུན་ཞུགས་འབྲས་གནས།} abider in the fruit of a stream-winner\n3. {ཕྱིར་འོང་ཞུགས་པ།} enterer into the fruit of a once-returner\n4. {ཕྱིར་འོང་འབྲས་གནས།} abider in the fruit of a once-returner\n5. {ཕྱིར་མི་འོང་ཞུགས་པ།} enterer into the fruit of a never-returner\n6. {ཕྱིར་མི་འོང་འབྲས་གནས།} abider in the fruit of a never-returner\n7. {དགྲ་བཅོམ་ཞུགས་པ།} enterer\ninto the fruit of a Foe-destroyer\n8. {དགྲ་བཅོམ་འབྲས་གནས།} abider in the fruit of a Foe-destroyer.
ཞུགས-གནས-ཐིམ-གསུམ	Entering, abiding and dissolution. The three-fold tantric practice of causing the energy winds to enter, abide and dissolve into the central channel through meditation.
ཞེན-པ-བཞི-བྲལ	The mind training, "Parting Away from Four Clingings" (see {བློ་སྦྱོང་ཞེན་པ་བཞི་བྲལ}).
ཞེན-ཡུལ	Object of attachment. Synonymous with the apprehended object of conception ({རྟོག་པའི་ཞེན་ཡུལ}).
གཞན-གྱི-དངོས-པོ-སྟོང-པ-ཉིད	[parabhāva ṡūnyatā]/ Emptiness of others. One of the sixteen types of emptinesses; the lack of inherent existence of transwordly phenomena as opposed to worldly exi stents.
གཞན-འགྱུར-བཞི	Four changeable mental factors.\n1. {གཉིད།} [niddham]/ sleep\n2. {འགྱོད་པ།} [kaukṛtyam]/ regret\n3. {རྟོག་པ།} [vitarka]/ gross investigation\n4. {དཔྱོད་པ།} [vicara]/ subtle investigation.
གཞན-སྟོང་	Other emptiness; alternative emptiness. The lack of existence of other conventional phenomena, i.e. dependent and imputed phenomena, etc., upon the thoroughiy established phenomena, i.e. the non-dual wisdom understanding the inseparability of the subjective mind and objective existence. An alternative middle-vtew asserted by Jonangpa school of Tibetan Buddhism.
གཞན-གནོད-གཞི-དང-བཅས-པ-སྤོང-བ	Abandonments of harms to others along with the basis. The\nnature of individual liberation vows; 'others', here refers to\nthe seven non-virtuous activities of body and speech that\ninflicts direct harm on others, and 'bases', here refers to the\ncauses of those non-virtues—the three non-virtues of mind. When a person holding individual liberation vows eliminates these with his or her mind conjoined with a sense of\nrenunciation, it becomes a fully characterized individual\nliberation vow (pratimoksa).
གཞན-པ-མི-མཐུན-ཕྱོགས	Alternative dissimilar factor. That which is a dissimilar factor, yet shows a common basis with the predicate in a logical syllogism.
གཞན-དབང-གཉིས	Two types of dependent phenomena. One of the three categories of phenomena according to the [cittamātrin] school.\n1. {དག་པའི་གཞན་དབང་།} [ṡuddhaparatantra]/ pure dependent phenomena\n2. {མ་དག་པའི་གཞན་དབང་།} [aṡuddhaparatantra]/ impure dependent phenomena.
གཞན-འབྱོར-ལྔ་	Five circumstantial endowments. Of the ten endowments (see {འབྱོར་བ་བཅུ}) the five factors required to be fulfilled in the environment in which one lives:\n1. {སངས་རྒྱས་འཇིག་རྟེན་ན་བྱོན་པ།} Buddha's having come\n2. {དམ་པའི་ཆོས་གསུངས་པ།} His having taught the doctrine\n3. {བསྟན་པ་གནས་པ།} the existence of His doctrine\n4. {དེའི་རྗེས་འཇུག་ཡོད་པ་།} the existence of His followers\n5. {གཞན་ཕྱིར་རྟག་ཏུ་སྙིང་བརྩེ་བ།} being compassionate towards others.
གཞན-ལས-ངེས-ཀྱི-ཚད-མ	Valid cognition ascertainable from other factors, e.g. valid\ncognition within the continuum of a person who has no knowledge of valid cognition.
གཞན-སེལ	[anyāpoha]/ Exclusion of other; negative phenomena. An awareness that understands its own object of perception through negating the existence of its direct opposite, e.g. the generic image of a vase. Synoymous with negative phenomena. There are two types:\n1. {མེད་དགག་གི་གཞན་སེལ།} non-affirming exclusion of other, e.g. emptiness\n2. {མ་ཡིན་དགག་གི་གཞན་སེལ།} affirming exclusion of other, e.g. not being a vase.
གཞལ-བྱ-གཉིས	Two types of knowable objects; two objects of knowledge.\n1. {སྦྱི།} [sāṃanya]/ general phenomena\n2. {བྱེ་བྲག} [viṡeṣa]/ particular phenomena or\n1. {སྦྱི་མཚན།} {བརྫུས་སྐྱེས།} [sāmnānyalakṣaṇa]/generally characterized\n2. {རང་མཚན།} [svalakṣaṇa]/ self-characterized phenomena or\n1. {རྟག་པ།} [nitya]/ permanent\n2. {མི་རྟག་པ།} [anitya]/impermanent.
གཞི-བྱའི-གནས-གསུམ	Three objects of knowledge.\n1. {མངོན་གྱུར།} [pratyakṣa]/ manifest phenomena, e.g. pillar\n2. {ལྐོག་གྱུར།} [parokṣa]/ obscure phenomena, e.g. impermanence\n3. {ཤིན་ཏུ་ལྐོག་གྱུར།} [atiparokṣa]/ extremely obscure phenomena, e.g. very subtle nature of the law of causality.
གཞལ-མེད-ཁང་	[vimāna]/ Inconceiveable mansion; celestial mansion; heaven.
གཞི-བཅུ-བདུན	The seventeen basic precepts. The basic precepts of cultivation for an ordained monk. There is one precept for obtaining the vows not yet obtained; nine precepts for protecting the vows already obtained; and seven precepts for purifying the transgressed vows.
གཞི-ཇི-བཞིན-པ	[yathāsaṃstarika]/ He who sleeps wherever he happens to be. One of the twelve ascetic practice (see {སྦྱངས་པའི་ཡོན་ཏན་བཅུ་གཉིས}); to sleep on a bed of grass or leaves, etc., which are laid out once without being rearranged for comfort's sake.
གཞི-ཐམས-ཅད-ཡོད-པར-སྨྲ-བའི-སྡེ-བདུན	[sapta mūlasarvāstivādāḥ]/ Seven Mulasarvastivadin schools. One of the eighteen schools of the Hinayana tradition. 1. {གཞི་ཐམས་ཅད་ཡོད་པར་སྨྲ་བ།} [mūlasarvāstivāda]\n2. {འིད་སྲུང་བ།} [kāṡyapīyāḥ]\n3. {ས་སྟོན་པ།} [mahīṡāsakāḥ]\n4. {ཚོས་སྲུང་བ།} [dharmaguptāḥ]\n5. {མང་ཐོས་པ།} [bāhuṡrutiyāḥ]\n6. {གོས་དམར་བ།} [tāmraṡātīyāḥ]\n7. {རྣམ་པར་ཕྱེ་སྟེ་སྨྲ་བ།} [vibhajyavādinaḥ]
གཞི-དུས-ཀྱི-འོད-གསལ	The basic clear light mind. The Buddha nature within the mental continuum of sentient beings, i.e. the primordially pure nature of the minds of all beings.
གཞི-དུས-ཀྱི-ཡེ-ཤེས-ལྔ་	The five basic wisdoms for transforming the five delusions into wisdoms.\n1. {གཞི་དུས་ཀྱི་མེ་ལོང་ཡེ་ཤེས།} mirror-like wisdom for self-pacification of hatred-anger\n2. {གཞི་དུས་ཀྱི་མཉམ་ཉིད་ཡེ་ཤེས།} wisdom of equality or sameness for self-pacification of pride\n3. {གཞི་དུས་ཀྱི་སོར་རྟོགས་ཡེ་ཤེས།} wisdom of analysis for self-pacification of desire-attachment\n4. {གཞི་དུས་ཀྱི་བྱ་སྒྲུབ་ཡེ་ཤེས།} wisdom of accomplishment for self-pacificationof jealousy\n5. {གཞི་དུས་ཀྱི་ཆོས་དབྱིངས་ཡེ་ཤེས།} wisdom of reality for self-pacification of closed-mindedness.
གཞི-ཤེས-ཀྱི-རྣམ-པ-ཉེར-བདུན	Twenty-seven aspects of the basic wisdom. 1-12. {བདེན་པ་དང་པོ་གསུམ་རྣམ་པ་བཅུ་གཉིས།} twelve aspects of the first three noble truths (see {བདེན་པ་དང་པོ་གསུམ་གྱི་རྣམ་པ་བཅུ་གཉིས}) 13-27. {ལམ་བདེན་གྱི་རྣམ་པ་བཅོ་ལྔ་།} fifteen aspects of the noble truth of the path (see {ལམ་བདེན་གྱི་རྣམ་པ་བཅོ་ལྔ}).
གཞི-ཤེས-མཚོན-བྱེད-ཀྱི-ཆོས-དགུ	Nine topics that characterize the basic wisdom.\n1. {ཤེས་པས་སྲིད་ལ་མི་གནས་པའི་གཞི་ཤེས།} non-abidance in the extreme of existence through knowledge\n2. {སྙིང་རྗེས་གཞི་ལ་མི་གནས་པའི་གཞི་ཤེས།} non-abidance in the extreme of peace through compassion\n3. {ཐབས་མ་ཡིན་པས་འབྲས་ཡུམ་ལ་རིང་བའི་གཞི་ཤེས།} distant from the mother effect due to lack of skill in means\n4. {ཐབས་མཁས་པས་འབྲས་ཡུམ་ལ་ཉེ་བའི་གཞི་ཤེས།}\nclose to the mother effect due to skill in means\n5. {མི་མཐུན་ཕྱོགས་ཀྱི་གཞི་ཤེས།} basic wisdom classed as a discordant factor\n6. {གཉེན་པོ་ཕྱོགས་ཀྱི་གཞི་ཤེས།} basic wisdom classed as an antidote\n7. {གཞི་ཤེས་ཀྱི་སྦྱོར་བ།} training in basic wisdom\n8. {གཞི་ཤེས་ཀྱི་མཉམ་ཉེད་སྦྱོར་བ།} training in the sameness of basic wisdom\n9. {གཞིཤེས་ཀྱི་མཐོང་ལམ།} path of seeing.
གཞི-གསུམ-ཆོ-ག	The three basic rituals; the three basic ceremonies of monks. The text of rituals concerning:\n1. {གསོ་སྦྱོང་།} bi-monthly restoration and confession ceremony\n2. {དབྱར་གནས།} summer or rainy season retreat for three months beginning from the sixteenth of the sixth Tibetan month\n3. {དགག་དབྱེ།} the ceremony of lifting restrictions after the completion of the three months retreat.
གཞིའི-སྐུ-གསུམ	The three basic kayas.\n1. {ཐ་མལ་བའི་སྐྱེ་བ་གཞིའི་སྤྲུལ་སྐུ} the\nordinary state of birth as the basic [nirmāṇakāya]\n2. {ཐ་མལ་གྱི་འཚི་བ་གཞིའི་ཆོས་སྐུ} the ordinary state of death as the basic [dharmakāya]\n3. {ཐ་མལ་གྱི་བར་དོ་གཞིའི་ལོངས་སྐུ} the ordinary state of intermediate rebirth as the basic [sambhogakāya].
གཞུག-པ-ལྡེམ-པོར-གགོངས-པ	[avatāraṇābhisaṃdhi]/ Interpretative [sūtra] encouraging conversion, e.g. a [sūtra] explaining the existence of the self of a person in order to convert a follower into Buddhist doctrine.
གཞུང-ཆེན-མོ	The great treatises of philosophy studied in the monastic universities or elsewhere.
གཞུང-པོ-ཏི-ལྔ་	The five treatises of Buddhist philosophy.\n1. {ཕར་ཕྱིན།} Perfection of Wisdom\n2. {དབུ་མ།} Middle Way\n3. {ཚད་མ།} Valid Cognition\n4. {འདུལ་བ།} Monastic Discipline\n5. {མཛོད།} Treasure of Knowledge.
གཞོགས-འཕྱས	Chiding; reprimand; upraising in an ironic manner.
གཞོལ-པ-གསུམ-གྱི-བཟླས-པ	The three types of incantation according to action tantra; the three suchnesses of recitation in prahayama meditation.\n1. {གཞི་ལ་གཞོལ་བ།} recitation while concentrating on the object deity\n2. {སེམས་ལ་གཞོལ་བ།} recitation while concentrating on the mind deity\n3. {སྒྲ་ལ་གཞོལ་བ།} recitation while concentrating on the sound deity.
བཞོན-པ-ལྟ-བའི-སེམས-བསྐྱེད	Mount-like bodhicitta. Mind of enlightenment associated with the exalted practice of compassion and resolute intention possessed by a Bodhisattva on the three pure grounds.
ཟ-མ-ཏོག	[karaṇḍa]/ A. Food casket; carried by ascetics as their pot. B. Za-ma-tog [sūtra] concerning [ārya avalokiteṡvara] cycle of teaciiings.
ཟག-བཅས	[sāsrava]/ Contaminated phenomena. Deluded phenomena capable of increasing affliction by their presence, e.g. a human body.
ཟག-བཅས-ཀྱི-ཕུང-པོ-ལྔ་	Five contaminated aggregates (see {ཕུང་པོ་ལྔ}).
ཟག-པ-བཞི	Four types of contaminations (see {ཆུ་བོ་བཞི}).
ཟག-པའི-སྒོ-དྲུག	The six gates of contamination; the six ways in which delusions increase or become stronger.\n1. {ཟག་པའི་བདག་ཉིད།} being a contaminated thing, such as being any of the twenty root or near delusions (see {རྩ་ཉོན་དྲུག} and {ཉེ་ཉཅན་ཉི་ཤུ})\n2. {ཟག་པ་དང་འབྲེལ་བ།} being connected to a contamination, such as the sense faculties that are immediate conditions for producing contaminated mental experiences\n3. {ཟག་པས་བཅིངས་པ།} being bound by contamination, such as the contaminated virtues within the three realms of existence\n4. {ཟག་པའི་རྗེས་སུ་འབྲེལ་བ།} being possessed by contamination, such as the inability to exploit one's body, speech and mind for positive activities\n5. {ཟག་པའི་རྗེས་སུ་མཐུན་པ།} being similar to contamination, such as form, sound etc., that are physical sources of contamination\n6. {ཟག་པའི་རྒྱུ་ལས་བྱུང་བ།} arisen from the contaminated, the results of contamination, such as this human body.
ཟག-མེད-ཀྱི-ཕུང-པོ-ལྔ་	Five uncontaminated aggregates; the five pure ways.\n1. {ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་ཀྱི་ཕུང་པོ།} [ṡīla skandha]/ aggregate of moral disciple\n2. {ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན་གྱི་ཕུང་པོ།} [samādhi skandha]/ aggregate of concentration\n3. {ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱི་ཕུང་པོ།} [prajсā skandha]/ aggregate of wisdom\n4. {རྣམ་པར་གྲོལ་བའི་ཕུང་པོ།} [vimukti skandha]/ aggregate of thorough liberation\n5. {རྣམ་པར་གྲོལ་བའི་ཡེ་ཤེས་མཐོང་བའི་ཕུང་པོ།} [vimukrijсāna skandha]/ aggregate of seeing the wisdom of thorough liberation.
ཟག-མེད-ཀྱི-དབང-པོ-གསུམ	The three uncontaminated powers (see {དབང་པོ་གསུམ}, B). The powers of a person who has attained the truth of the path.
ཟག-མེད-ཀྱི-ལམ-ལྔ་	The five uncontaminated paths (see {ཟག་མེད་ཀྱི་ཕུང་པོ་ལྔ}). These are known as the five uncontaminated paths when the word aggregates are replaced with the word path.
ཟག-མེད-ཡེ-ཤེས-སྡེ-ཚན-ཉེར-གཅིག	Twenty-one groups of uncontaminated wisdom.\n1. {བྱང་ཕྱོགས་སོ་བདུན།} thirty-seven auxiliaries to enlightenment (see {བྱངས་ཕྱོག་སོ་བདུན})\n2. {ཚད་མེད་བཞི།} four immeasurables (see {ཚད་མེད་བཞི})\n3. {རྣམ་ཐར་བརྒྱད།} [aṣṭa vimokṣāḥ]/ eight emancipations (see {རྣམ་ཐར་བརྒྱད})\n4. {མཐར་གྱིས་གནས་པའི་སྙོམས་འཇུག་དགུ} nine absorptions (see {སྙོམས་འཇུག་དགུ})\n5. {ཟད་པར་བཅུ།} ten exhaustions/ ten totally pervasive concentrations (see {ཟད་པ་བཅུ})\n6. {ཟིལ་གྱིས་གནོན་པ་བརྒྱད།} eight outshining factors/ eight surpassing concentrations (see {ཟིལ་གནོན་བརྒྱད})\n7. {ཉོན་མོངས་མེད་པའི་ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན།} concentration free of delusions\n8. {སྨོན་གནས་མཁྱེན་པ།} [praṇidhijсāsamādhi]/ knowledge of one's object of prayers\n9. {མངོན་ཤེས་དྲུག} six extra-sensory perceptions (see {མངོན་པར་ཤེས་པ་དྲུག})\n10. {སོ་སོ་ཡང་དག་རིག་པ་བཞི།} four specific perfect understandings (see {སོ་སོར་ཡང་དག་པ་རིག་པ་བཞི})\n11. {རྣམ་དག་བཞི།} four purities: a) {རྟེན་རྣམ་དག} pure basis b) {དམིགས་པ་རྣམ་དག} pure objects c) {ཐུགས་རྗེ་རྣམ་དག} pure compassion d) {ཡེ་ཤེས་རྣམ་དག} pure primordial wisdom\n12. {དབངབཅུ།} ten sovereign qualities (see {དབང་ཕུག་བཅུ})\n13. {སྟོབས་བཅུ།} [daṡa balāni]/ ten powers (see {དེ་བཞིན་གཤེགས་པའི་སྟོབས་བཅུ})\n14. {མི་འཇིགས་པ་བཞི།} four fearlessnesses (see {མི་འཇིགས་པ་བཞི})\n15. {བསྲུང་བ་མེད་པ་གསུམ།} three unguarded aspects—that of physical, verbal and mental behaviours of a Buddha\n16. {དྲན་པ་ཉེ་བར་གཞག་པ་གསུམ།} three close contemplations (see {དྲན་པ་ཉེ་བར་གཞག་པ་གསུམ})\n17. {བསྙེལ་བ་མི་མངའ་བའི་ཆོས་ཉེད།} non-negligence of the purpose of sefttient beings\n18. {བག་ཆགས་ཡང་དག་བཅོམ་པ།} complete elimination of latencies of three delusions\n19. {ཐུགས་རྗེ་ཆེན་པོ།} [mahākaruṇā]/ great compassion\n20. {སངས་རྒྱས་ཀྱི་ཆོས་མ་འདྲེས་པ་བཅོ་བརྒྱད།} eighteen unshared qualities of a Buddha (see {མ་འདྲེས་པ་བཅོ་བརྒྱད})\n21. {མཁྱེན་པ་གསུམ} three wisdoms (see {མཁྱེན་གསུམ}).
ཟག-མེད-ས-དགུ	[navānāsrava bhūmayaḥ]/ Nine uncontaminated grounds; nine uncontaminated levels of concentration.\n1. {བསམ་གཏན་དང་པོའི་དངོས་གཞི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} actual absorption of the first concentration\n2. {བསམ་གཏན་དང་པོའི་དངོས་གཞི་སྙོམས་འཇུག་ཙམ་པོ་བ།} ordinary absorption of the first concentration\n3. {བསམ་གཏན་དང་པོའི་དངོས་གཞི་སྙོམས་འཇུག་ཁྱད་པར་ཅན།}\nexalted absorption of the first concentration\n4. {བསམ་གཏན་གཉིས་པའི་དངོས་གཞི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} actuai absorption of the second concentration\n5. {བསམ་གཏན་གསུམ་པའི་དངོས་གཞི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} actual absorption of the third concentration\n6. {བསམ་གཏན་བཞི་པའི་དངོས་གཞི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} actual absorption of the fourth concentration\n7. {ནམ་མཁའ་མཐའ་ཡས་དངོས་གཞི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} actual absorption of infinite space\n8. {རྣམ་ཤེས་མཐའ་ཡས་དངོས་གཞི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} actual absorption of the infinite consciousness\n9. {ཅི་ཡང་མེད་ཀྱི་དངོས་གཞི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} actual absorption of nothingness.
ཟང-ཐལ	The unobstructed phenomena; The uninterrupted phenomena\n{ཟངས་མདོག་དཔལ་རི།}\nThe copper coloured glorious mountain. The legendary abode of Guru Padmasambhava.
ཟང-ཟིང་	[āmiṣa]/ A. Material goods. B. Blurred vision; confusion.\n{ཟད་པ་ཤེས་པ།}\n[kṣayajсāna]/ Knowledge of exhaustion. One of the ten types of awarenesses according to the Abhidharma tradition (see {མཛོད་ལས་བཤད་པའི་ཤེས་པ་བཅུ}); knowledge of one's own confidence of having abandoned all objects of elimination.
ཟག-པར-གྱི-སྐྱེ-མཆེད	The total pervasive concentration; the concentration of exhaustion. The power of concentration gained by a person who is able to transform any phenomena into any particular element.
ཟད-པར-གྱི-སྐྱེ-མཆེད-བཅུ	The ten exhaustions; the ten totally pervasive concentrations (see {ཟད་པར་བཅུ}, below).
ཟད-པར-བཅུ	Ten exhaustions; ten totally pervasive concentrations the aim of which is to develop omniscience, by training in perceiving an element such as fire or a color such as blue as totally pervading all phenomena. Totally pervasive concentration with respect to 1 -4. {ས་ཆུ་མེ་རླུང་བཞི་དང།} five elements 5-8. {སྔོ་སེར་དཀར་དམར་བཞི།} four root colours-blue, yellow, white and red\n9. {ནམ་མཁའ་མཐའ་ཡས།} infinite space\n10. {རྣམ་ཤེས་མཐའ་ཡས།} infinite consciousness.
ཟན-གྲིལ	The dough-ball divination. In this system the contents of divination written down on pieces of paper are rolled up in a dough-ball and thrown in front of holy images or paintings of deities of special significance through chanting invocation prayers.
ཟཔ-མ-ལྟ-བརྒྱུད	[gaṃbhīradarṡana tantra]/ Lineage of the profound view; the profound view lineage. Lineage of teaching and practice coming from [maсjuṡrī], [nāgārjuna] and [candrakīrti] which mainiy emphasises the wisdom aspect of the teachings.
ཟབ-མོ-སྟོང-པ-ཉིད	[gaṃbhīra ṡūnyatā]/ Profound emptiness; profound voidness.
ཟབ-མོ-དག-སྣང-གི-བརྒྱུད-པ	Lineage of profound pure perception; lineage of sacred vision. A. The transmission obtained as a result of direct vision and access of one's personal meditational deity. B. A Nyingma lineage derived from accomplished masters, who through their pure perception, have attained a vision of their root guru and meditational deity as the same, and received certain secret teachings that are transmitted only to a limited circle of disciples.
ཟབ-མོའི-ཆོས-ཉིད-རྣམ-པ-བརྒྱད	[aṣṭa gaṃbhira dharmatāḥ]/ Eight profound realities; eight aspects of the profound reality.\n1. {སྐྱེ་བ་ཟབ་མོ།} profound production\n2. {དགག་པ་ཟབ་མོ།} profound stopping\n3. {དེ་ཉིད་ཟབ་མོ།} profound thusness/reality\n4. {ཆོས་ཟབ་མོ།} profound phenomena\n5. {ཤེས་པ་ཟབ་མོ།} profound awareness\n6. {ཉམས} {ལེན་ཟབ་མོ།} profound practice\n7. {གཉིས་སྟོང་ཟབ་མོ།} pro-found non-duality\n8. {ཐབས་མཁས་ཟབ་མོ།} profound skill in means.
ཟབ-ཞི	The profound peace; the clear light mind of a Buddha; the dharmakaya The unfathomable omniscience and the state of [nirvāṇa] or cessation of sufferings within the continuum of a Buddha.
ཟབ-ཞི-སྤྲོས-བྲལ	The profound peace free of the eight extremes (see {སྤྲོས་པའི་མཐའ་བརྒྱད}).
ཟབ-ལམ-རིམ-ལྔ་	The five profound paths; the five stages of tantric paths\naccording to the highest yoga tantra.\n1. {ངག་དབེན།} isolation of speech\n2. {སེམས་དབེན།} isolation of mind\n3. {སྒྱུ་ལུས།} illusory body\n4. {འོད་གསལ།} clear light mind\n5. {ཟུང་འཇུག} the state of unity of the illusory body and clear light mind.
ཟབ-གསལ-གཉིས-མེད-ཀྱི-རྣལ-འབྱོར	The yoga of non-dual profundity and clarity. The yoga of union of emptiness and the primordial mind realizing it.
ཟབ-གསལ-གཉིས-མེད-ཀྱི-ཡེ-ཤེས	The primordial wisdom of non-dual profundity and clarity. The wisdom of a yogi, who experiences a clear vision of the divine [maṇḍala] like the rainbow within the understanding of emptiness.
ཟས-ཀྱི-རྣལ-འབྱོར	The yoga of foods.\n1. {ཁ་ཟས་སྨན་དང་འདྲ་བར་རིག་པར་སྤྱོད་པ།} the practice of relishing food like a medicine for sustenance\n2. {ནང་སྤྱིན་སྲེག་གི་ཚུལ་དུ་ལོངས་སྤྱོད་པ།} the practice of relishing food like offering for the inner fire-ritual.
ཟས-དཀར-གསུམ	The three white foods; yogurt, milk and butter.
ཟས-ཕུད	The first bit of food. The tradition of offering the first portion of a meal to the objects of refuge before one eats.
ཟས-གཙང-མ	[ṡuddhodana]/ King [ṡuddhodana]; the father of Buddha [ṡākyamuni].
ཟས-བཞི	[catvāra-āhārāḥ]/ Four types of food; four nourishments.\n1. kham gyi zas/ [kavalīkārahāra]/ coarse food, for the growth of the sense organs of this body\n2. {རེག་པའི་ཟས།} [sparṡāhāra]/ food of touch, for the growth of consciousness\n3. {སེམས་ཀྱི་ཟས།} [manaḥ saṃcetanāhāra]/ food of mental thought, for projecting rebirth in future lives\n4. {རྣམ་པར་ཤེས་པའི་ཟས།} [vijсānāhāra]/ food for consciousness, for the actualization of the next rebirth.
ཟིན-པའི-སྒྲ	The conjoined sounds. The sound produced by a person through the force of elements such as wind, e.g. sound of clapping hands and flute.
ཟིལ-གྱིས-གནོན-པའི-སྐྱེ-མཆེད-བརྒྱད	[aṣṭabhibhavāyatanāni]/ Eight surpassing concentrations; the power of concentration through which a yogi aims to gain control of the miracles.\n1. {རང་གཟུགས་ཅན་དུ་འདུ་ཤེས་པས་ཕྱི་རོལ་གྱི་གཟུགས་ཆུང་ངུ་ལ་བལྟ་ཞིང་གཟུགས་དེ་དག་ཟིལ་གྱིས་གནོན་པ།} imagining himself having form, he sees small external forms and overcomes them\n2. {རང་གཟུགས་ཅན་དུ་འདུ་ཤེས་པས་ཕྱི་རོལ་གྱི་གཟུགས་ཆེན་པོ་ལ་བལྟ་ཞིངགཟུགས་དེ་དག་དག་ཟིལ་གྱིས་གནོན་པ།} imagining himself having form, he sees large external forms and overcomes them\n3. {རངགཟུགས་མེད་པར་འདུ་ཤེས་པས་ཕྱི་རོལ་གྱི་གཟུགས་ཆུང་ངུ་ལ་བལྟ་ཞིང་གཟུགས་དེ་དག་ཟིལ་གྱིས་གནོན་པ།} imagining himself as lacking form, he sees small external forms and overcomes them\n4. {རང་གཟུགས་མེད་པར་འདུ་ཤེས་པས་ཕྱི་རོལ་གྱི་གཟུགས་ཆེན་པོ་ལ་བལྟ་ཞིང་གཟུགས་དེ་དག་ཟིལ་གྱིས་གནོན་པ།} imagining himself as lacking form, he sees large external forms and overcomes them\n5. {རང་གཟུགས་ཅན་མེད་པར་འདུ་ཤེས་པ་ཁོ་ནས་ཕྱི་རོལ་གྱི་གཟུགས་སྔོན་པོ་ལ་བལྟ་ཞིང་གཟུགས་དེ་དག་ཟིལ་གྱིས་གནོན་པ།} merely imagining himself as lacking form, he sees external blue forms and overcomes them\n6. {རང་གཟུགས་མེད་པར་འདུ་ཤེས་པ་ཁོ་ནས་ཕྱི་རོལ་གྱི་གཟུགས་སེར་པོ་ལ་བལྟ་ཞིང་གཟུགས་དེ་དག་ཟིལ་གྱིས་གནོན་པ།} merely imagining himself as lacking form, he sees external yellow forms and overcomes them\n7. {རང་གཟུགས་མེད་པར་འདུ་ཤེས་པ་ཁོ་ནས་ཕྱི་རོལ་གྱི་གཟུགས་དམར་པོ་ལ་བལྟ་ཞིང་གཟུགས་དེ་དག་ཟིལ་གྱིས་གནོན་པ།} merely imagining himself as lacking form, he sees external red forms and overcomes them\n8. {རང་གཟུགས་མེད་པར་འདུ་ཤེས་པ་ཁོ་ནས་ཕྱི་རོལ་གྱི་གཟུགས་དཀར་པོ་ལ་བསྟ་ཞིང་གཟུགས་དེ་དག་ཟིལ་གྱིས་གནོན་པ།} merely imagining himself as lacking form, he sees external white forms and overcomes them.
ཟུང-འཇུག	[yuganaddha]/ A. Unification; state of union, e.g. the union of calm-abiding and penetrative insight meditation or the union of bhss and void. B. One of the five levels of the completion stage practices in tantr^ the union of emptiness, the wisdom aspect and great compassion, the method aspect or the union of the wisdom of spontaneous great bliss, the method aspect and the emptiness of clear light mind, the wisdom aspect or the ever-supreme emptiness, the object and the unclianging wisdom of great bliss, the object-per(^iver.
ཟུང-འཇུག-ཉེར-གསུམ	Twenty-three types of unification; twenty three states of union.\n1. {འཁོར་འདས་དབྱེར་མེད་ཀྱི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of the inseparability of cyclic existence and the state beyond suffering\n2. {ཀུན་བྱང་གི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of ever-deluded and ever-purified phenomena\n3. {རྣམ་བཅས་རྣམ་མེད་ཀྱི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of that with and without aspects\n4. {གཟུང་འཛིན་གྱི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of object and object-perceiver\n5. {རྟག་ཆད་བླལ་བའི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of mat wnich is free of the extremes of eternalism and nihilism\n6. {སྟོང་ཉིད་རྗེའི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of emptiness and compassion 7 {ཐབས་ཤེས་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of method and wisdom\n8. {ལྷག་བཅས་ལྷག་མེད་ཀྱི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of residual and non-residual cessation\n9. {བདག་མེད་གཉིས་ཀྱི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of two selflessnesses\n10. {སྒྱུ་ལུས་དང་འོད་གསལ་གྱི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of the illusory body and clear light\n11. {རིལ་འཛིན་གྱི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of thorough dissolution\n12. {རྗེས་གཞིག་གི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of gradual dissolution\n13. {བདེན་གཉིས་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of two truths\n14. {མཉམ་གཞག་ག་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of meditative equipoise\n15. {རྗེས་ཐོབ་ཀྱི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of post-meditative equipoise\n16. {སད་གཉིད་ཀྱི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of sleep and the awakened state\n17. {མཉམ་པར་འཇུག་ལྡང་གི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of engagement and arisal from meditative equipoise\n18. {དྲན་པ་མི་དྲན་པའི་ཟུངའཇུག} union of mindfulness and unmindfulness\n19. {བདེ་སྟོང་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of bliss and emptiness\n20. {བྱ་བྱེད་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of action and action-performed\n21. {བསྐྱེད་རྫོགས་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of generation and completion stage\n22. {དག་མ་དག་གི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of a pure and impure state\n23. {གཟུགས་ཅན་གཟུགས་མེད་ཀྱི་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of an embodied and unembodied entity. In the list of twenty-one, nos. 11 and 12 and nos. 14 and 15 are counted as one each the union of thorough and gradual dissolution and the union of a meditative and post-meditative state.
ཟུང-ཇུག-གཉིས	Two types of unification; two states of union (yuganaddha).\n1. {སློབ་པའི་ཟུངའཇུག} state of union of a trainee or learner\n2. {མི་སློབ་པའི་ཟུང་འཇུག} state of union of a non-trainee or a Buddha.
ཟུང-འཇུག-བཞི	The four types of unification; the four states of union.\n1. {སྣང་སྟོང་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of appearance and emptiness\n2. {རིག་སྟོང་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of awareness and emptiness\n3. {བདེ་སྟོང་ཟུངའཇུག} union of bliss and emptiness\n4. {གསལ་སྟོང་ཟུང་འཇུག} union of clear light and emptiness.
ཟུར-ཕུད	[cīraka]/ Top-knot; knotted hair gathered at the crown of the head.
ཟླ-གམ	Monk's overcoat; worn during religious gatherings, especially during winter.
ཟླ-བ-འབྱུང-ངོ-ཅོག-གི-དུས-བཟང-བཞི	Four auspicious days of every month; four special days of a month according to the Tibetan Buddhist tradition.\n1. {ཚེས་བརྒྱད་པར་སངས་རྒྱས་སྨན་བླའི་དུས་བཟང།} eighth is the day of the Medicine Buddha\n2. {ཚེས་བཅུ་པར་མཁའ་འགྲོའི་དུས་བཟང་།} tenth is the day of the [ḍākinī]\n3. {ཚེས་བཅོ་ལྔར་སངས་རྒྱས་ཤཱཀྱ་ཐུབ་པའི་དུས་བཟང་།} fifteenth is the day of Buddha [ṡākyamuni]\n4. {ཚེས་སུམ་ཅུ་པར་སངས་རྒྱས་འོད་དཔག་མེད་ཀྱི་དུས་བཟང་།} thirtieth is the day of Buddha [amitābha].
ཟླ-བ-ཡར-ངོ-མར-ངོ་	Waxing and waning moon.
གཟའ-དགུ	[nava graha]/ Seven planets; seven days of the week.\n1. {ཉི་མ།} [āditya]/ Sun\n2. {ཟླ་བ།} [soma]/ Moon\n3. {མིག་དམར།} [aṇgāraka]/ Mars.\n4. {ལྷག་པ།} [budha]/ Mercury\n5. {ཕུར་བུ།} [bṛhaspatiḥ]/Venus\n6. {པ་སངས།} [ṡukraḥ]/ Jupiter\n7. {སྤེན་པ།} [ṡanaiṡcara]/ Saturn.\n8. {སྒྲ་གཅན།} [rāhu]/ ascending node of the moon\n9. {མཇུག་རིང་།} [ketu]/ descending node of the moon.
གཟིགས-པ-ལྔ་	Five predeterminations of Buddha [ṡākyamuni] before conceiving to be born in this world while he was in the god realm, born as [devaputra] ({དམ་པ་ཏོག་དཀར་པོ}).\n1. {དུས་ལ་གཟིགས་པ།} observation of the time for his appearance\n2. {རུས་ལ་གཟིགས་པ།} observation of the family of his birth\n3. {རིགས་ལ་གཟིགས་པ།} observation of the caste of his lineage\n4. {ཡུམ་ལ་གཟིགས་པ།} observation of the mother to who he would be born\n5. {ཡུལ་ལ་གཟིགས་པ།} observation of the land in which to disseminate his doctrine.
གཟུགས-ཀྱི-སྐྱེ-མཆེད	[pūpāyatanam]/ The source of perception of form; synonymous with forms (gzugs); direct objects of sight—shape and colour.
གཟུགས-ཀྱི-ལྷ	[rūpadeva]/ The form deity. One of the six deities according to action tantra. A visualization meditation of emitting and withdrawing light from the moon [maṇḍala] and the circle of mantras, the transformation of which then give rise to complete feaiures of the concerned deity of one's meditation.
གཟུགས-ཁམས	[rūpadhātu]/ Form realm. Realm in which beings are preoccupied with meditative concentration free of attachment to sensual objects within the desire realm but have attachment to forms.
གཟུགས-ཁམས-ཀྱི-སྒོམ-སྤང-བརྒྱ-དང-བརྒྱད-ཅུ	One hundred and eighty objects of elimination within the form realm to be* abandoned on the path of meditation. The four levels of concentrations—first, second, third and fourth within the form realm each have forty-five objects of elimination (see {གཟུགས་ཁམས་ཀྱི་སྒོམ་སྤང་ལྔ}) when each of the five eliminations are further divided into nine levels of subtlety from within the three basic levels of great, middling and small and each of these levels are further divided into three levels, thus making one hundred and eighty in all.
གཟུགས-ཁམས-ཀྱི-སྒོམ-སྤང-ལྔ	The five objects of elimination within the form realm to be abandoned on the path of meditation.\n1. {མ་རིག་པ།} ignorance\n2. {འདོད་ཆགས།} desire-attachment\n3. {ང་རྒྱལ།} pride\n4. {འཇིག་ལྟ།} view of transitory collection\n5. {མཐར་ལྟ།} the extreme view.
གཟུགས-ཁམས-ཀྱི-གནས-བཞི	The four levels of the form realm; the four states of concentration within the form realm; the four worlds of the form realm – {བསམ་གཏན་དང་པོ།} {གཉིས་པ།} {གསུམ་པ།} {བཞི}' {པ།} first, second, third and fourth concentration realms.
གཟུགས-ཁམས-གནས-རིས-བཅུ-བདུན	Seventeen regions of the form realm. Three states of the first level concentration:\n1. {ཚངས་རིས།} [brahmakāyikāḥ]/ Brahma type\n2. {ཚངས་པ་མདུན་ན་འདོན།} [brahmapurohitāḥ]/ Brahma attendants\n3. {ཚངས་ཚེན།} [mahābrahmāṇaḥ]/ great Brahma. Three states of the second level concentration:\n4. {འོད་ཆུང་།} [parīttābhāḥ]/ little light\n5. {ཚད་མེད་འོད།} [apramāṇābhāḥ]/ limitless light\n6. {འོད་གསལ།} [ābhāsvarāḥ]/ bright light. Three states of the third level concentration:\n7. {དགེ་ཆུང་།} [parīttaṡubhāḥ]/ little virtue\n8. {ཚད་མེད་དགེ} [apramāṇaṡubhāḥ]/ limitiess virtue\n9. {དགེ་རྒྱས།} [ṡubhakṛtṣnāh]/ vast virtue. Eight states of the fourth level concentration:\n10. {སྦྲིན་མེད།} [anabharakāḥ]/ cloudless\n11. {བསོད་ནམས་སྐྱེས།} [puṇyaprasavāḥ]/ born from merit\n12. {འབྲས་བུ་ཆེ་བ།} [bṛhatphalāḥ]/ great fruit\n13. {མི་ཆེ་བ།} [avṛhāḥ]/ not great\n14. {མི་གདུང་བ།} [atapāḥ]/without pain\n15. {གྱ་ནོམ་སྣང་།} [sudṛṡāḥ]/\nexcellent appearance\n16. {ཤིན་ཏུ་མཐོང་།} [ṡudarṡanāḥ]/ great perception\n17. {འོག་མིན།} [akaniṣṭāḥ]/ not low.
གཟུགས-ཅན-གཟུགས-ལ-ལྟ-བའི-རྣམ-ཐར	Emancipation of one possessing form, looking at a form. A concentration of the form realm cultivated by a yogi while considering himself as a being with physical form, in order to eliminate attachment towards external forms.
གཟུགས-ཅན-མ-ཡིན-པའི-མཚངས-ལྡན-འདུ-བྱེད-ཀྱི-ཕུང-པོའི-སྡེ-ཚན-དྲུག	Six classes of non-physical aggregates of concomitant compositional factors.\n1. {སེམས་ཀྱི་ས་མང་།} mental attitude\n2. {དགེ་བའི་ས་མང་།} virtuous attitude\n3. {མི་དགྲེ་བའི་ས་མང་།} non-virtuous attitude\n4. {ཉོན་མོངས་ཆེན་པོའི་ས་མང་།} mental attitude of the major delusions\n5. {ཉོན་མོངས་ཆུང་ངུའི་ས་མང་།} mental attitude of the minor delusions\n6. {མ་ངེས་པའི་ས་མང་།} indefinite mental attitude.
གཟུགས-ཉེར-སྔ་	Twenty-five types of forms.\n1-4. {རྩ་བའི་ཁ་དོག་བཞི།} four root colors (see {རྩ་བའི་ཁ་དོག་བཞི})\n5-12. {ཡན་ལག་གི་ཁ་དོག་བརྒྱད།} eight secondary colours (see {ཡན་ལག་གི་ཁ་དོག་བརྒྱད})\n13. {རིང་བ།} long\n14. {ཐུང་བ།} short\n15. {ལྷམ་པ།} squareness\n16. {ཟླུམ་པོ།} sphencal\n17. {རྡུལ་ཕྲ་མོ།} fine particles\n18. {རྡུལ་རགས་པ།} gross particles\n19. {མཐོ་བ།} high\n20. {དམའ་བ།} low\n21. {ཕྱ་ལེ་བ།} evenness\n22. {ཕྱ་ལེ་བ་མ་ཡིན་པ།} unevenness\n23. {མངོན་པར་སྐབས་ཡོད་པ།} manifest form\n24. {རྣམ་པར་རིག་བྱེད།} revelatory form\n25. {ནམ་མཁའ་དང་ཁ་དོག་གཅིག་པའི་གཟུགས།} color identical with the sky.
གཟུགས-ཕུང-བཅོ-ལྔ་	Fifteen form aggregates.\n1-4. {རྒྱུ་འབྱུང་བ་ཆེན་པོ་བཞི།} four causal elements (see {འབྱུང་བ་བཞི})\n5-15. {འབྲས་གཟུགས་བཅུ་གཅིག།} eleven resultant form aggregates (see {འབྲས་གཟུགས་བཅུ་གཅིག}).
གཟུགས-ཕུང-རིགས-ཀྱི-ཆོས-ལྔ་	Five phenomena on the level of the form aggregate.\n1. {གཟུགས་ཀྱི་ཕུང་པོ།} form aggregate\n2. {གཞི་དུས་ཀྱི་མེ་ལོང་ཡེ་ཤེས།} basic mirror-like wisdom\n3. {སའི་ཁམས།} earth element\n4. {མིག་གི་དབང་པོ།} eye sense power\n5. {རང་རྒྱུད་ཀྱིས་བསྡུས་པའི་གཟུགས།} form within one's mental continuum.
གཟུགས-མེད-ཁམས	[arūpa dhātu]/ Formless realm. The realm in which the beings do not have a gross body but have a pure mental body; they are free of attachment towards sensual objects, but have attachments to the formless realms.
གཟུགས-མེད-ཉེར-འགྲོའི-ཕྱིར-མི-འོང་	Never-returner who attains liberation without effort and migrates to the formless realm.
གཟུགས-མེད-ཉེར-འགྲོའི-ཕྱིར-མི-འོང-སྐྱོས-འདའ-བ	Never-returner who attains liberation as soon as he is born in the formless realm.
གཟུགས-མེད-ཉེར-འགྲོའི-ཕྱིར-མི-འོང-གོང-འཕོ-བ	Never-returner who attains liberation in the highest state (either in [akaniṣṭha] or the Peak of Existence) after migrating to the formless realm.
གཟུགས-མེད-ཉེར-འགྲོའི-ཕྱིར-མི-འོང-འདུ-བྱེད-དང-བཅས-པར-འདའ-བ	Never-returner who attains liberation with great effort and migrates to the formless realm.
གཟུགས-མེད-ཉེར-འགྲོའི-ཕྱིར-མི-འོང-འདུ-བྱེད-མེད-པར-འདའ-བ	Never-returner who atains liberation without effort and migrates to the formless realm.
གཟུགས-མེད-སྙོམས-འཇུག-བཞི	[catasra ārūpyasamāpattayaḥ]/ Four formless absorptions; four types of formless meditative absorptions.\n1. {ནམ་མཁའ་མཐའ་ཡས་སྙོམས་འཇུག} [ākāṡānantyāyatanaṃ]/ absorption of infinite space\n2. {རྣམ་ཤེས་མཐའ་ཡས་སྙོམས་འཇུག} [vijсānānantyāyatanaṃ]/ absorption of infinite consciousness\n3. {ཅི་ཡང་མེད་པའི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} [akiсcanyāyatanaṃ]/ absorption of nothingness\n4. {འདུ་ཤེས་མེད་འདུ་ཤེས་མེད་མིན་གྱི་སྙོམས་འཇུག} [naivasaṃjсānāsaṃjсayatanaṃ]/ absorption of that which is neither with discrimination nor non-discrimination.
གཟུགས-མེད-གཟུགས-ལ-སྟ-བའི-རྣམ-ཐར	Emancipation of one without form looking at a form. A concentration within the form realm cultivated by a yogic while considering himself as a being without form in order to eliminate his attachment to external objects.
གཟུགས-སུ-ཉེར-འགྲོའི-ཕྱིར-མི-འོང་	Never-returner who migrates to the form realm.
གཟུགས-སུ-ཉེར-འགྲོའི-ཕྱིར-མི-འོང-གོང-འཕོ-བ	Never-returner who attains liberation in the highest state ([akaniṣṭha]) after migrating to the form realm.
གཟུགས-སུ-ཉེར-འགྲོའི-ཕྱོར-མི-འོང-སྐྱེས-འདའ-བ	Never-returner who attains liberation as soon as he is born in the form realm.
གཟུགས-སུ-ཉེར-འགྲོའི-ཕྱིར-མི-འོང-བར-འདའ-བ	Never-returner who attains liberation in the intermediate existence of the form realm.
གཟུགས-སུ-ཉེར-འགྲོའི-ཕྱིར-མི-འོང-འདུ-བྱེད-དང-བཅས-པར-འདའ-པ	Never-returner who attains liberation with great effort and migrates to the form realm.
གཟུགས-སུ-ཉེར-འགྲོའི-ཕྱིར-མི-འོང-འདུ-བྱེད-མེད-པར-འདའ-བ	Never-returner who attains liberation without effort and migrates to the form realm.
གཟུང-རྟོག-གཉིས	Two objective graspings; two graspings at objects; two conceptual graspings at objects.\n1. {འཇུག་པ་གཟུང་རྟོག} grasping at engagements that are to be cultivated\n2. {ལྡོག་པ་གཟུང་རྟོག} grasping at elimination that are to be abandoned or\n1. {ཉོན་མོངས་གཟུང་རྟོག} grasping at delusive phenomena\n2. {རྣམ་བྱང་གཟུང་རྟོག} grasping at purified phenomena.
གཟུང-འཛིན-གཉིས-ལྔང་	Non-duality of the object and object-perceiver. The lack of difference between the object and the object-perceiver; a view asserted by the [cittamātrin] school of philosophy.
གཟུང-ཡུལ	[grāhyaviṣaya]/ Referent object. Object as seized by a perception, e.g. vase for a consciousness apprehending vase.
གཟུངས	[dhāraṇī]/ Retention power ([dhāraṇī]). The ability to hold words and meanings of the dharma through the force of exalted mindfulness and wisdom. Also means mantras ({གཟུངས་སྔགས}) through the power of which one summons blessings and the ability to eliminate interfering forces.
གཟུངས-ཀྱི-སྒོ-བཞི	Four types of retention power, four doors of dharani.\n1. {བཟོད་པའི་གཟུངས།} [kṣāntidhāraṇi]/ retention of patience, the ability to endure patiently the emptiness discerned without being terrified by it\n2. {སྔགས་ཀྱི་གཟུང་།} [mantradhāraṇī]/ retention of mantra, the ability to convert any syllable or syllables into a mantra for eradicating infectious diseases and interfering forces\n3. {ཚིག་གི་གཟུངས།} [vākya dhāraṇī]/ retention of word, the ability to retain names, terms or words through the power of memory\n4. {དོན་གྱི་གཟུངས།} [artha dhāraṇī]/ retention of meaning, the ability to retain the specific and general meanings of all phenomena through the power of mindfulness.
བཟའ-བའི-དམ-ཚིག	The commitment related to food. The commitment according to the highest yoga tantra to accept the five fleshes (see {ཤ་ལྔ}) and five nectars (see {བདུད་རྩི་ཨཱིང}) without any preconceptions.
བཟོ-བོ-སྤྲུལ-སྐུ	[ṡilpanirmāṇakāya]/ Artisan emanation. A form of incarnate Buddha's emanation as artisans and master-craftsman in order to tame beings.
བཟོ-རིག-གི-སྒྱུ-རྩལ-སུམ-ཅུ	The thirty skills of arts and craft. A section of the sixty-four arts.\n1. {ཡི་གེ} literacy\n2. {ལག་རྩིས།} calculation by hand\n3. {གྲངས།} mathematics\n4. {རྩིས་ཆེན།} great mathematics\n5. {ཐོར་ཚུགས།} scare crowing\n6. {གོམ་སྟབས།} gestures by feet\n7. {ལྕགས་ཀྱུས་སྒྱུར་ཐབས།} art by iron rods\n8. {རལ་གྲིའི་ཐབས།} sword slinging\n9. {ཞགས་པ་གདབ་པ།} lasso throwing\n10. {མདའ་བོ་ཆེ་འཕེན་པ།} archery\n11. {མདུན་དུ་བསྣུར་བ།} offensive\n12. {ཕྱིར་བསྣུར་བ།} defensive\n13. {བཅད་པ} cutting\n14. {དྲལ་བ།} tearing\n15. {དབྱུག་པ།} stick throwing\n16. {རྒྱང་ནས་འཕོག་པ།} remote targeting\n17. {སྒྲ་གྲག་པར་འཕོག་པ།} blasting\n18. {གནད་དུ་འཕོག་པ།} blowing the target\n19. {མི་ཚོར་བར་འཕོག་པ།} insensitive targeting\n20. {ཚབས་ཆེ་བར་འཕོག་པ།} intense targeting\n21. {མཆོངས་པ།} jumping\n22. {གྱད་ཀྱི་འཛིན་པ།} weight lifting\n23. {བང་།} racing\n24. {རྐྱལ།} swimming\n25. {བརྒལ་བ།} crossing\n26. {གླང་པེ་ཆེའི་གཉར་ཞོན་པ།} elephant riding\n27. {རྟ་ལ་ཞོན་པ།} horse riding\n28. {ཤིང་རྟའི་བཟོ་ཐབས།} chariot making\n29. {མདའ་ཞུའི་བཟོ་ཐབས།} bow and arrow making\n30. {གྱད་སྟོབས།} wrestling.
བཟོད-པ-རྣམ-གསུམ	The three types of patience.\n1. {གནོད་པ་ལ་ཇི་མི་སྙམ་པའི་བཟོད་པ།} patience of not retaliating against someone who harms you\n2. {སྡུག་བསྔལ་དང་ལེན་གྱི་བཟོད་པ།} patience of willingly enduring sufferings\n3. {ཆོས་ལ་ངེས་ཤེས་ཀྱི་བཟོད་པ།} patience of discriminative awareness of the Dharma.
བཟོད-པ-ཕྱིར-མི-ལྡོག-པའི-རྟགས-གཉིས	Two signs of irreversibility on the patience level of the path of preparation.\n1. {གཞན་གྱིས་དཀྲིར་མི་བཏུབ་པ།} he cannot be led astray by others\n2. {ལས་བཅོས་མ་སྟོན་པའི་བདུད་ལ་བདུད་དུ་རྟོགས་པ།} he recoghizes the maras preaching counterfeit paths as true maras.
བཟོད-པའི-རྩེ-སྦྱོར	[kṣāntigata mūrdhaprayoga]/ Peak training of the forbearance level of the path of preparation. A Bodhisattva path where he has gained stability in establishing his realization to progress further.
ཟློས-གར-གྱི-ཡན-ལག-ལྔ་	The five fundamentals of the performing arts; the five limbs of performing arts.\n1. {མདོ་འཛིན་པ།} memorization of texts\n2. {རོལ་མོ།} music\n3. {ཆས་ཞུགས།} costumes\n4. {བཞད་གད།} comedy\n5. {ཟློས་གར།} art of dance and drama.
བཟླས-བརྗིད-ཡན-ལག-བཞི	Four branches of recitation; four types of incantation practice\nand meditation according to [krīya tantra].\n1. {སྒྲའི་གཞི་ལ་གཞོལ་བ།} retitation while concentrating on the sound deity\n2. {སེམས་ཀྱི་གཞི་ལ་གཞོལ་བ།} recitation while concentrating on the mind deity\n3. {གཞན་གྱི་གཞི་ལ་གཞོལ་བ།} recitation while\nconcentrating on another deity\n4. {བདག་གི་གཞི་ལ་གཞོལ་བ།} recitation while concentrating on self-deity.
བཟླས-བརྗོད-ལ-ལྟོས-པའི-བསམ-གཏན	[japāpekṣatadhyāna]/ Concentration dependent on recitation.
བཟླས-བརྗོད-ལ-མི-ལྟོས-པའི-བསམ-གཏན	[japānāpekṣeiadhyāna]/ Concentration independent of recitation.
འོག-མིན	[akaniṣṭha]/ A. The [akaniṣṭha] Buddha field where the [sambhogakāya] form of Buddhas reside, also called the "Richly Adorned Heaven Beneath None". B. Heaven Beneath None; the highest god realm within the form realms of the fourth concentration domain.
འོག-མའི-ཆ-མཐུན-ལྔ་	The five delusions of the lower realms; the five delusions within the desire realm.\n1. {འདོད་ཆགས།} desire-attachment\n2. {ཞེ་སྡང་།} hatred-anger\n3. {འཛིག་ཚོགས་ལ་ལྟ་བ།} view of the transitory collection\n4. {ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་དང་བརྟུལ་ཞུགས་མཆོག་འཇིན།} view of holding wrong moral disciplines and ascetic practices as supreme\n5. {ཐེ་ཚོམ།} doubt.
འོད-དཔག-མེད	[amitābha]/ Buddha Amitabha. The Buddha of the western direction.
འོད-དཔག-མེད-ཀྱི-དམ-ཚིག-གསུམ	Three pledges related to Amitabha Buddha.\n1. {ཕྱི་བྱ་སྤྱོད།} performance and action tantra as the outer practice\n2. {གསང་བ་རྣལ་འབྱོར་དང་བླ་མེད།} yoga and anuttarayoga tantra as the secret practice\n3. {ཐེག་པ་གསུམ་གྱིས་བསྡུས་པའི་དམ་ཚིག} all practices encompassing the doctrine of the three vehicles.
འོད-མའི-ཚལ	[veṇuvana]/ A. Bamboo grove; a park near [rājagṛha] that was offered to Buddha [ṡākyamuni] by King [bimbisāra].
འོད-སྲུང་	[kāṡyapa]/ A. [kāṡyapa] Buddha. The third of the thousand Buddhas and sixth of the Seven Heroid Buddhas (see {སངས་རྒྱས་དཔའ་བོ་བདུན}) B. [mahākāṡyapa]. The first of the seven hierarchs (see {སྟོན་པའི་གཏད་རབས་བདུན}) and one of the ten close disciples of Buddha [ṡākyamuni], famous for his scholarship, and was also responsible for collecting all the Abhi-dharma class of teachings during the First Council.
འོད-གསའ་	[prabhāsvara]/ Clear Light. A. A domain of gods within the second concentration realm. B. Clear light mind; the fundamental state of consciousness which manifests at the time of death. A qualified tantric practitioner employs this subtle mind to realize emptiness. There are two types:\n1. {བུའི་འོད་གསལ།} son clear light (see {བུའི་འོད་གསལ})\n2. {མའི་འོད་གསལ།} mother clear light (see {མའི་འོད་གསལ}).
འོད-གསལ-སྒྱུ-མ	[prabhāsvara māyā]/ The clear light illusory body. One of the types of illusory bodies, the empty-body, like a reflection on a mirror, that is attained as a result of successful meditation on the completion stage of tantra.
འོད-གསལ-སྒྲིབ-མེད	Non-obscured clear light mind. In the Sakya tradition this refers to the Buddha nature present in all sentient beings.
འོད-གསལ-མཚན-ཉིད-པ	Actual clear light. The fully characterized clear light mind.
ཡང-དག-ཀུན-རྫོབ	[saṃyak saṃvṛtti]/ Real conventional truth; perfect conventional truth. The causes and results giving rise to the ten virtues and other wholesome activities as a result of a perfect examination of the outer and inner nature of dependent-arising principles,\n{ཡང་དག་པའི་ངག}\n[saṃyag vāk]/ Right speech. To speak correct and show others means of teaching, debate and writing, aimed at generating correct views.
ཡང-དག-པའི-ཏིག-ངེ-འཛིན	[saṃyak samādhi]/ Right concentration. Establishing meditative concentrations free of the faults of laxity and excitement; an antidote to the hinderences in meditation.
ཡང-དག-པའི-རྟོག-པ	[saṃyak saṃkalpa]/ Right thought. Engaging in the study of scriptures and teachings with proper motivation.
ཡང-དག-པའི-ལྟ-བ	[saṃyag dṛṣṭi]/ Right view. Discerning the meanings of the four noble truths and the two truths through proper analytical and contemplative means.
ཡང-དག-མཐའ	[saṃyag ānta]/ The perfect finality. The sphere of reality or emptiness at the cessation of the pervasive suffering, [nirvāṇa].
ཡང-དག-པའི-དྲན-པ	[saṃyak smṛti]/ Right mindfulness. Retaining the object of clam abiding and penetrative insight through application of balanced approach of meditation techniques.
ཡང-དག-པའི-རྩོལ-བ	[saṃyag vyāyāma]/ Right effort. Application of perseverance in one's practice of eliminating the obscuration to liberation and omniescence.
ཡང-དག-པའི-འཚོ-བ	[saṃyagājīva]/ Right livelihood. Right physical and vocal behaviour free of wrong means such as wheedling behavior, flattery and so forth, to earn one's livelihood.
ཡང-དག-པའི-ལས-ཀྱི-མཐའ	[saṃyak karmānta]/ Right action; right conduct. Maintenance of one's behavior free from negative techniques in contrast with the principles of teachings.
ཡང-དག-པར-བླངས-པ-ལས-གྱུར-པ	Forms arising from pledges, e.g. a vow or an obeisance of vows revealed through physical, verbal and mental activities.
ཡང-དག-སྤོང-བ-བཞི	[catvāri prahāṇāni]/ Four perfect abandonments; four right eliminations. A section of the thirty-seven auxilaries to enlightenment.\n1. {མི་དགེ་བ་སྐྱེས་པ་སྤོང་བ།} abandonment of non-virtues that have not been produced\n2. {མི་དགེ་བ་མ་སྐྱེས་པ་མི་བསྐྱེད་པ།} non-generation of non-virtues that have not yet been produced\n3. {དགེ་བ་མ་སྐྱེས་པ་བསྐྱེད་པ།} increasing virtues that have been produced\n4. {དགེ་བ་སྐྱེས་པ་སྤེལ་བ།} making effort in generating virtues that have not yet been produced.
ཡངས-པ-ཅན	[vaiṡālī]/ A. [vaiṡālī]. The city of [vaiṡālī] in the vicinity of Patna where Buddha [ṡākyamuni] turned the Third Wheel of Doctrine; the doctnne of good distinction between the three divisions of phenomena—imputed, dependent and thoroughly established (reality). B. A chapel in Ganden monastery.
ཡན-ལག-གི-ཁ-དོག-བརྒྱད	Eight secondary colors.\n1. {སྤྲིན་གྱི་ཁ་དོག} cloudy\n2. {དུ་བའི་ཁ་དོག} smoky\n3. {རྡུལ་གྱི་ཁ་དོག} dusty\n4. {ཁུག་རྣའི་ཁ་དོག} misty\n5. {བྲིབ་མའི་ཁ་དོག} shadowy\n6. {ཉི་འོད་ཀྱི་ཁ་དོག} sunny\n7. {སྣང་བའི་ཁ་དོག} brightness\n8. {མུན་པའི་ཁ་དོག} darkness.
ཡན-ལག-གི-རླུང-ལྔ་	Five secondary energy winds. The five energy winds in the body produced through the force of basic elements within the body.\n1. {རྒྱུ་བའི་རླུང་།} [caraṇa vāyu]/ moving wind for the cognitive faculty of vision\n2. {རྣམ་པར་རྒྱུ་བའི་རླུང་།} [vicaraṇa vāyu]/ thoroughly moving wind for the cognitive faculty of hearing\n3. {ཡང་དག་པར་རྒྱུ་བའི་རླུང་།} [samudācaraṇa vāyu]/ perfectly moving wind for the cognitive faculty of smell\n4. {ངེས་པར་རྒྱུ་བའི་རླུང་།} [avicarata vāyu]/ definitely moving wind for the cognitive faculty of touch or contact\n5. {རབ་ཏུ་རྒྱུ་བའི་རླུང་།} [upacāra vāyu]/ strongly moving wind for the cognitive faculty of taste. There is another way of listing these five energy winds from the perspective of their dynamic reaction within the body. {ལུས་ལ་གནས་པའི་འབྱུང་འགྱུར་གྱི་རླུང་ལྔ་།}\n1. {ཀླུའི་རླུང་ས་ཁམས།} the earth element as the naga's wind\n2. {རུས་སྦལ་གྱི་རླུང་རླུང་ཁམས།} the wind element as the tortoise's wind\n3. {རྩངས་པའི་རླུང་མེ་ཁམས།} the fire element as the lizard's wind\n4. {ལྷས་བྱིན་གྱི་རླུང་ཆུ་ཁམས།} the water element as devadatta's wind\n5. {ནོར་རྒྱལ་གྱི་རླུངས་ཁམས།} the earth element as vasuraja's wind.
ཡན-ལག-བརྒྱད-ལྡན-གྱི-ཆུ	The river or water fulfilling eight qualities (see {ཆུ་ཡན་ལག་བརྒྱད་ལྡན}).
ཡན-ལག-ལྔ་	[paсcān'ga]/ The five limbs. Two arms, two legs and head.
ཡན-ལག-ལྔ-ལྡན-གྱི-སྦྱོར-བ	The five preparatory stages. The five preliminary steps of [mahāmudrā] meditation according to the Drigung Kagyud tradition.\n1. {བྱང་ཆུབ་ཀྱི་སེམས་བསྒོམ་པ།} meditation on the mind of enlightenment\n2. {རང་ལུས་ལྷར་བསྒོམ་པ།} meditation on oneself as a deity\n3. {བླ་མ་ལ་མོས་གུས་བསྒོམ་པ།} meditation on faith and devotion to one's spiritual master\n4. {མི་རྟོག་པའི་ལྟ་བ་བསྒོམ་པ།} meditation on the non-conceptual view\n5. {བསྔོ་སྨོན་གྱིས་རྒྱས་འདེབས་པ།} concluding one's practice by dedication.
ཡན-ལག-བདུན-པ	[saptāṇga pūja]/ Seven branch practice; seven limbed practice. The seven priliminaries for carrying out a Dharma practice.\n1. {ཕྱག་འཚལ་བ།} [vandana]/ prostration\n2. {མཚོད་པ་ཕུལ་བ།} [pūjanā]/ offering\n3. {བཤགས་པ་ཕུལ་བ།} [deṡaya]/ confession\n4. {རྗེས་སུ་ཡི་རང་བ།} [anumoda]/ rejoicing\n5. {བསྐུལ་བ།} [saṃcodana]/ requesting\n6. {གསོལ་བ་འདེབས་པ།} [adhyeṣaṇa]/ supplication\n7. {བསྔོ་བ།} [pariṇāmana]/ dedication (see {སྔགས་ཕྱོགས་ཀྱི་ཡན་ལག་བདུན་པ།་ཨནད་རྒྱུན་བཤགས་ཀྱི་ཡན་ལག་བདུན་པ}).
ཡབ	[pitṛ]/ Male deity. Male deity or protector in the tannic system representing the method aspect of practice.
ཡབ-ཀྱི-ཕྱག-རྒྱ-དྲུག	Six ornaments of a male deity.\n1. {དབུ་རྒྱན།} head-dress\n2. {རྣ་རྒྱན།} earrings\n3. {མགུལ་རྒྱན།} necklace\n4. {གདུ་བུ།} bracelets\n5. {མཆོད་ཕྱིར་ཐོགས་པ།} skull cup\n6. {ཐལ་ཆེན་གྱི་ཚོམ་བུ།} daubing of ashes.
ཡར-གྱི-མཚམས-མེད-ཀྱི-ལས	Higher boundless action. Positive action of higher potentiality that leads one to the higher attainments, as opposed to the boundless non-virtue which directly drives one to the hell realm.
ཡས-འདེད	Removing obstacles downwards. Such as in the practice of Vajrasattva meditation; the elimiantion of obstacles of the body through visualizing them being flushed out of one's lower orifices with the downward flow of light and nectar from Vajrasattva at the crown of one's head.
ཡས-བབས-ཀྱི-དགའ-བཞི	The four joys of the descending order. A skill gained through successful meditation on psychic heat by way of melting bodhicitta induced in the wheels of the energy channels,\naccording to the completion stage meditation of the mother tantra in the highest yoga practice. Thus when the bodhicitta melts and descends it produces:\n1. {བྱང་སེམས་སྤྱི་པོ་ལས་བབ་པས་དགའ་བ།} joy from the level of the crown\n2. {མགྲིན་པར་བབ་པས་མཆོག་དགའ།} supreme joy at the level of the throat\n3. {སྙིང་གར་དགའ་བྲལ།} extraordinary joy at the level of the heart\n4. {ལྟེ་བར་ལྷན་ཅིག་སྐྱེས་དགའ།} spontaneous joy at the level of the navel.
ཡས-བབས-མས-བརྟན	The descending and ascending order of joys from the melting of bodhicitta from crown level to the secret organ and vice-versa.
ཡི-གེའི-ལྷ	[akṣara deva]/ Letter deity. One of the six types of deities in performance ([kriyā]) tantra; meditation of the syllables visualized upon a moon cushion generated out of emptiness.
ཡི-དམ	Meditational deity; personal deity; tutelary deity. Buddhas or Bodhisattvas relied upon by a practitioner having special bond or relationship in accordance with the tantric values.
ཡི-དྭགས-གསུམ	Three types of hungry ghosts.\n1. {ཕྱི་སྒྲིབ་ཅན།} those with external obstructions (food)\n2. {ནང་སྒྲིབ་ཅན།} those with internal obstructions (drink)\n3. {ཟས་སྐོམ་གཉིས་ཀའི་སྒྲིབ་པ་ཅན།} those with obstructions to both food and drink.
ཡིག-བརྒྱ	Hundred Syllable mantra. Such as of [vajrasattva], [heruka], [yamāntaka] and others.
ཡིག-ཆ	A. Text book. Treatises on Buddhist philosophy studied in each of the monastic universities that form their basic curriculum of religious study. B. Documents old or new.
ཡིད-མངོན-ལྔ་	The five types of direct mental perception. Those related to:\n1. {གཟུགས་འཛིན་ཡིད་མངོན།} form\n2. {སྒྲ་འཛིན་ཡིད་མངོན།} sound\n3. {དྲི་འཛིན་ཡིད་མངོན།} smell\n4. {རོ་འཛིན་ཡིད་མངོན།} taste\n5. {རེག་འཛིན་ཡིད་མངོན།} objects of touch.
ཡིད-ཆེས-ཀྱི-དད-པ	[pratyayita ṡraddhā]/ Convinced faith; trusting faith. Total faith in the working of karma and the three objects of refuge.
ཡིད-དཔྱོད	[manaḥparīkṣa]/ Presumption; correct belief. A fresh awareness that apprehends the correct object, without depending on experience or correct reasohing as its basis, e.g. the presumption that sound is impermanent merely through hearing the statement, 'sound is changeable'. There are three types of presumptions:\n1. {རྒྱུ་མཚན་མེད་པའི་ཡིད་དཔྱོད།} presumption for no reason\n2. {རྒྱུ་མཚན་ལྟར་སྣང་ལ་བརྟེན་པའི་ཡིད་དཔྱོད།} presumption for an incorrect reason\n3. {རྒྱུ་མཚན་མ་ངེས་པའི་ཡིད་དཔྱོད།} presumption for an indefinite reason.
ཡིད-བྱེད-དྲུག	Six attentions.\n1. {མཚན་ཉིད་སོ་སོར་རིག་པ་ཡིད་བྱེད།} attention\nto individual characteristics\n2. {མོས་པ་ཡིད་བྱེད།} attention arisen from belief\n3. {རབ་ཏུ་དབེན་པ་ཡིད་བྱེད།} attention of complete isolation\n4. {དགའ་བ་བསྡུད་པའི་ཡིད་བྱེད།} attention encompissing joy\n5. {དཔྱོད་པ་ཡིད་བྱེད།} attention to analysis\n6. {སྦྱོར་བ་མཐའི་ཡིད་བྱེད།} attention to the conclusion of activity.
ཡིད-བྱེད-བཞི	Four attentions; the four ways of attending to an object of meditation while practicing concentration meditation.\n1. {བསྒིམས་ཏེ་འཇུག་པ།} painstaking attention\n2. {ཆད་པ་དང་བཅས་ཏེ་འཇུག་པ།} repeated attention\n3. {ཆད་པ་མེད་པར་འཇུག་པ།} uninterrupted attention\n4. {རྩོལ་བ་མེད་པར་འཇུག་པ།} effortless attention.
ཡིད-བཞིན-ནོར-བུ	[cintāmaṇi]/ A. Wish-fulfilling gem. B. Dalai Lama\n3. Human body.\n4. Gems obtained from the ocean.
ཡིད-བཞིན-ནོར-བུ-ལྟ-བུའི-སེམས-བསྐྱེད	[cintāmaṇyupamacittotpāda]/ Wish-fulfilling gem like bodhicitta. The mind of eniightenment associated with the perfection of prayers possessed by a Bodhisattva on the eighth ground of advancement.
ཡིད-འོང-གི-བྱམས-པ	[manojсamaitrī]/ Appealing love; heart-warming love.
ཡིད-ལས-བྱུང-བ	[manobhava]/ Mind-arisen; synonymous with the intermediate state of rebirth (bardo).
ཡུམ	[mātṛ]/ Female aspect; tantric consort; a female counterpart of a male deity or tantric practitioner symbolizing the wisdom aspect of practice.
ཡུམ-གྱི-ཕྱག-རྒྱ-ལྔ་	Five adornments of a female deity.\n1. {དབུ་རྒྱན།} head-dress\n2. {སྙན་རྒྱན།} earrings\n3. {མགུལ་རྒྱན།} necklace\n4. {གདུ་བུ།} bracelets\n5. {སྐུ་རགས།} belt.
ཡུམ-གྱི-འགྲོལ-རྐང-བརྒྱ-དང-བརྒྱད	One hundred and eight topics of the Perfection of Wisdom text.\n1-53. {ཀུན་ནས་ཉོན་མོངས་ཕྱོགས་ཀྱི་འགྲེལ་རྐང་ང་གསུམ།} fifty-three topics of the ever afflicted phenomena (see {ཀུན་ནས་ཉོན་མོངས་ཕྱོགས་ཀྱི་འགྲེལ་རྐང་ང་གསུམ})\n54-108. {རྣམ་བྱང་ཕྱོགས་ཀྱི་འགྲེལ་རྐང་ལྔ་བཅུ་རྩ་ང་།} fifty-five topics of the purified phenomena (see {རྣམ་བྱང་ཕྱོགས་ཀྱི་འགྲེལ་རྐང་ང་ལྔ}).
ཡུམ-རྒྱས-འབྲིང-བསྡུས-གསུམ	The large, medium and short Wisdom Perfection [sūtra]s ([prajсāparamitā sūtra]).\n1. {འབམ}1 The One Hundred Thousand Verse ([ṡatasāhasrikā])\n2. {ཉི་ཁྲི།} The Twenty Thousand Verse ([virṃṡatisāhasrikā])\n3. {བརྒྱད་སྟོང་པ} The Eight Thousand Verse ([aṣṭasāhasarikā]).
ཡུལ-གྱི-འོད-གསལ	Objective clear light; the emptiness.
ཡུལ-ངེས-ལྔ་	Five determining mental factors; five determinants.\n1. {འདུན་པ།} [chanda]/ aspiration\n2. {མོས་པ།} [adhimokṣa]/belief\n3. {དྲན་པ།} [smṛti]/ mindfulness\n4. {ཏིང་འཛིན།} [samādhi]/ concentration\n5. {ཤེས་རབ།} [prajсā]/wisdom.\n{ཡུལ་ཅན་གྱི་འོད་གསལ།}\nSubjective clear light; the wisdom cognizing emptiness in tantra.
ཡུལ-ཅན-གསུམ	Three object-perceivers; three object possessors. A.\n1. {སྒྲ།} [ṡabda]/ sound\n2. {བློ།} [manas]/ awareness\n3. {སྐྱེས་བུ།} [puruṣa]/ person. B.\n1. {གཟུགས} [rūpa]/ form\n2. {ཤེས་པ} [jсana]/ consciousness\n3. {ལྡན་མིན་འདུ་བྱེད།} [viprayukta saṃskara]/ those that are neither.
ཡུལ-དང-ཡུལ-ཅན	[viṣaya viṣāyin]/ Object and object-perceiver; object and subject.
ཡུལ-དྲུག	Six types of objects.\n1. {གཟུགས} [rūpa]/ form\n2. {སྒྲ།} [ṡabda]/ sound\n3. {དྲི།} [gandha]/ odors\n4. {རོ།} [rasa]/ tastes\n5. {རེག་བྱ།} [sparṡa]/ object of touch\n6. {ཆོས།} [dharma]/ phenomena
ཡུལ-དབུས-ཀྱི-གྲོང-ཁྱེར-དྲུག	The six cities of central India; six cities in ancient India connected to Buddhist culture.\n1. {རྒྱལ་པོའི་ཁབ།} [rājagṛha]\n2. {ཡངས་པ་ཅན།} [vaiṡālī]\n3. {མཉན་ཡོད།} [ṡrāvastī]\n4. {ཙམ་པ་ཀ།} [campaka]\n5. {གནས་བཅས།} [sāketā]\n6. {ཝཱ་རཱ་ཎ་སཱི།} [vārāṇasī].
ཡུལ-བཞི	Four types of objects.\n1. {སྣང་ཡུལ།} apparent object\n2. {གཟུང་ཡུལ།} apprehended object\n3. {འཇུག་ཡུལ།} focussed object\n4. {ཞེན་ཡུལ།} implied object.
ཡུལ-ལ-གཉིས-སུ-དབྱེ-བའི-རྣམ-གྲངས	Two-fold division of objects; two-fold divisions of all phenomena. A. {རང་མཚན་དང་སྦྱི་མཚན།} Self characterized and generally characterized phenomena B. {མངོན་གྱུར་དང་ལྐོག་གྱུར།} Manifest and hidden phenomena C. {འདུས་བྱས་འདུས་མ་བྱས།} Compositional and non-compositional phenomena D. {དགག་པ་དང་སྒྲུབ་པ།} Negative and affirmative phenomena E. {འགལ་བ་དང་འབྲེལ་བ།} Contradictory and non-contradictory phenomena F. {སྣང་བ་དངསེལ་བ།} Apparent and excluding phenomena G. {སྤྱི་བྱེ་བྲག} General.and particular phenomena H. {རྫས་ཆོས་དང་ལྡོག་ཆོས།} Substantial and opposite phenomena I. {མཚན་ཉིད་དང་མཚོན་བྱ།} definition and defined phenomena J. {ཀུན་རྫོབ་དང་དོན་དམ།} conventional and ultimate phenomena.
ཡེ-ཤེས-ཀྱི-མཁའ-འགྲོ-མ	[jсāna ḍākinī]/ The wisdom dakini; the primordial wisdom dakini. A. The transworldly female Bodhisattvas. B. Vajra Yogini.
ཡེ-ཤེས-ཀྱི-ཐིག-ལེ	[jсāna bindu]/ The primordial wisdom drop. The indestructible drop within the heart center in the central energy channel.
ཡེ-ཤེས-ཀྱི-རྡོར-དྲིལ	[jсāna vajra]/ The primordial wisdom vajra and bell. The inner method and wisdom, i.e. the great bliss and emptiness, symbolized by the nine-spoked vajra and bell.
ཡེ-ཤེས-ཀྱི-སྣང-བ	The primordial wisdom appearance; the primordial wisdom vision. The vision of everything seen as totally pure.
ཡེ-ཤེས-ཀྱི-སྤྱན	[jсāna cakṣu]/ The primordial wisdom eye; the wisdom eye; the divine look. In its highest sense it is the ability to see everything that exists.
ཡེ-ཤེས-ཀྱི-ཕྱག-རྒྱ	[jсāna mudrā]/ The primordial wisdom mudra. The wisdom of non-dual profundity and clarity.
ཡེ-ཤེས-ཀྱི-ཚོགས	[jсāna saṃbhāra]/ Collection of wisdom; accumulation of\ninsight. The virtuous energy conjoined with the mind of enlightenment and wisdom understanding emptiness that is a cause for producing the resultant wisdom-body of the Buddha.
ཡེ-ཤེས-སྒྱུ-མ	[jсāna māyā]/ The illusory body of wisdom. The inconceivable activities of all [tathāgatas]; the emanation of their wisdom projected in action.
ཡེ-ཤེས-ལྔ་	[paсca jсānāni]/ The five wisdoms of a Buddha.\n1. {མེ་ལོང་ལྟ་བུའི་ཡེ་ཤེས།} [ādarṡā jсānam]/ mirror-like wisdom\n2. {སོར་རྟོགས་ཡེ་ཤེས།} [pratyavekṣaṇā jсānam]/ wisdom of discrimination\n3. {མཉམ་ཉིད་ཡེ་ཤེས།} [samatā jсānam]/ wisdom of equality\n4. {བྱ་སྒྲུབ་ཡེ་ཤེས།} [kṛtyānusthāna jсānam]/ wisdom of accomplishment\n5. [dharmadhātu jсānam]/ wisdom of reality.
ཡེ-ཤེས-ཆོས-སྐུ	[jсānakāya]/ Wisdom truth body; the omniscient mind of a Buddha.
ཡེ-ཤེས-སེམས-དཔའ	[jсānasattva]/ Wisdom being. The actual meditational deity that is meditated upon or visualized; a generation stage practice of meditation in tantra in which a wisdom being is meditated at the heart of one's pledge being ({དམ་ཚིག་པ}) seated on a sun and moon cushion.
ཡོ-བྱད-བཅུ-གཉིས	Twelve ritual articles of a Yogi.\n1. {རྡོར་དྲིལ་གཉིས།} [vajra] and bell. 2 {ཅང་ཏེའུ།} small hand drum\n3. {ཐོད་པ།} skull cup\n4. {ཁ་ཌཾ་ཁ།} staff\n5. {རུས་རྒྱན།} bone ornaments\n6. {རིན་ཆེན་བརྒྱད།} eight jewel ornaments (see {རིན་པོ་ཆེའི་རྒྱན་བརྒྱད})\n7. {གཙུག་ཏོར་སྲོག་གཞུ།} hair knot at crown\n8. {དགང་བླུགས།} ritual ladle\n9. {བུམ་པ།} vase\n10. {ཕྲེང་བ།} rosary\n11. {སྟག་ཝགས་ཤམ་ཐབས།} a tiger-skin garment\n12. {སྟོད་གཡོག་སྨད་གཡོག} upper and lower garment.
ཡོ-བྱད-བཅུ-གསུམ	Thirteen articles of a monk (see {འཚོ་བའི་ཡོ་བྱད་བཅུ་གསུམ}).
ཡོ-བྱད-དྲུག	Six articles of a monk; six basic articles of a monkhood. 1-3. {ཆོས་གོས་རྣམ་གསུམ།} the three Dharma robes—two upper and one lower garment\n4. {ལྷུང་བཟེད།} begging bowl\n5. {ཆུ་ཚགས།} water strainer\n6. {གདིང་བ།} cushion.
ཡོངས-གྲུབ-གཉིས	Two thoroughly established phenomena.\n1. {ཕྱིན་ཅི་མ་ལོག་པའི་ཡོངས་གྲུབ།} correct thoroughly established phenomena\n2. {འགྱུར་མེད་ཡོངས་གྲུབ།} unchangeable thoroughly established phenomena.
ཡོངས-འཛིན-གཉིས	Two types of tutors.\n1. {ཕྱིའི་ཡོངས་འཛིན།} the external tutor\n2. {ནང་གི་ཡོངས་འཛིན།} the internal tutor.
ཡོངས-སུ-དག-པ-བཞི	Four total purities; the four features to be meditated in their pure entities for cultivating higher tantric practices connected to a deity-practice.\n1. {གནས།} [adhiṣṭhāna]/ environment\n2. {ལུས།} [kāya]/body\n3. {ལུངས་སྤྱོད།} [upakaraṇa]/riches\n4. {མཛད་} {པ།} karya/deeds.
ཡོངས-སུ-འཚོལ-བ-དྲུག	Six thorough investigations. That of:\n1. {དོན།} [artha]/ meaning\n2. {དངོས་པོ།} [bhāva]/existence/things\n3. {མཚན་ཉིད།} [lakṣṇa]/ characteristics\n4. {ཕྱོགས།} [pakṣa]/ directions\n5. {དུས།} [kāla]/time\n6. {རིགས་པ} [nyāya]/ logic.
ཡོད-པ	Existence; synonymous with objects of knowledge.\n{ཡོན་ཆབ།}\nWater-bowl offering; offering of waters to the objects of refuge.
ཡོན-ཏན-བརྒྱ-ཕྲག-བཅུ-གཉིས	Twelve sets of a hundred qualities; qualities attained by a Bodhisttva on the first ground, i.e. on the path of seeing.\n1. {དུས་སྐད་ཅིག་མ་གཅིག་ལ་སངས་རྒྱས་བརྒྱའི་ཞལ་མཐོང་བ།} seeing a hundred Buddhas in a single instant\n2. {སངས་རྒྱས་བརྒྱའི་བྱིན་གྱིས་བརླབ་པརཤེས་པ།} knowing that he is being blessed and inspired by a hundred Buddhas\n3. {སྤྲུལ་པ་བརྒྱ་འགྱེད་པ།} sending a hundred emanations\n4. {དུས་སྐད་ཅིག་མ་གཅིག་ལ་བསྐལ་བ་བརྒྱར་སྟོན་པ།} travelling to a hundred Buddha fields in a single instant\n5. {སྔོན་དང་ཕྱི་མའི་མཐའ་བརྒྱ་ལ་ཡེ་ཤེས་ཀྱི་གཟིགས་པ་འཇུག་པ།} seeing the past and future rebirths over a hundred aeons\n6. {ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན་བརྒྱ་ལ་སྙོམས་པར་འཇུག་ཅིང་ལྡང་བ།} remaining absorbed and rising in a hundred concentrations in one instant\n7. {སེམས་ཅན་བརྒྱ་སྨིན་པར་བྱེད་པ།} maturing a hundred disciples\n9. {ཞིང་ཁམས་བརྒྱ་གཡོ་བར་བྱེད་པ།} shaking a hundred Buddha fields\n10. {ཞིང་ཁམས་བརྒྱ་འོད་ཀྱིས་གསལ་བར་བྱེད་པ།} illuminating a hundred Buddha fields\n11. {ཆོས་ཀྱི་} {སྒོ་མོ་བརྒྱ་འགྱེད་པ།} opening a hundred entrances to dharma\n12. {རང་གི་ལུས་བརྒྱར་སྟོན་པ།} {ལུས་རེ་རེ་ཡང་འཁོར་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ་བརྒྱས་བསྐོར་བར་སྟོན་པ།} manifesting a hundred physical forms, each of which are surrounded by a hundred Bodhisattva disciples.
ཡོན-ཏན-ལྔ་	[paсca guṇāḥ]/ Five qualities; A. As asserted by the [vaiṡeṣika]\nschool of philosophy.\n1. {སྒྲ་ནམ་མཁའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} sound as the quality of space\n2. {དྲི་སའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} smell as the quality of earth\n3. {རོ་ཆུའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} taste as the quality of water\n4. {རེག་བྱ་རླུང་གི་ཡོན་ཏན།} sensation as the quality of wind\n5. {ཁ་དོག་མེའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} color as the quality of wind. B. According to\nthe Nyingma tradition—the five qualities of a Buddha are:\n1. {རྣམ་པར་དག་པའི་ཞིང་ཁམས།} a pure Buddha field\n2. {རྒྱ་ཚད་བྲལ་བའི་ཞིལ་ཡས་ཁང་།} an inconceivable celestial mansion\n3. {གསལ་ཞིང་དག་པའི་འོད་ཟེར།} a clear and luminous light\n4. {ཁྱད་པར་དུ་འཕགས་པའི་གདན་ཁྲི།} a sublime tnrone\n5. {དགྱེས་གུར་སྤྱོད་པའི་ལོངས་སྤྱོད།} inexhaustible resources.
ཡོན-ཏན-འོད	[guṇaprabha]/ [ācārya gunaprabha]. A disciple of [ācārya vasubandhu] famous for his scholarship in Vinaya teachings. His works include the Root [sūtra] of Vinaya and Treatise on the Bodhisattva Levels..
གཡང-འགྲུབ-ཆོ-ག	The fortune summoning ritual. The ritual of invoking wealth deities such as [vaiṡravaṇa], [zambala] or [gaṇeṡ] for affluent resources.
གཡའ-བཟང-བཀའ-བརྒྱུད	Yazang Kagyud Order. One of the sub-sects of the Kagyud order of Tibetan Buddhism originally founded by Drogon Phagmo Drupa's disciple Kalden Yeshi Senge; the main monastery of this tradition in Tibet was built in the upper region of Yalung valley by Yazang Chokyi Moniam.
གཡོ-སྒྱུ	[saṭha]/ Deceit; cunning. Ambitious attitude similar to pretention, trying to gain advantage by hiding one's faults from others; a form of dishonesty.
རཀྟ	Rakta/Blood.\n{རགས་པ་ཉེར་ལྔ་།}\nTwenty-five gross objects. 1-5. {ཕུང་པོ་ལྔ་།} five aggregates (see {ཕུང་པོ་ལྔ}) 6-9. {ཁམས་བཞི།} four elements (see {ཁམས་བཞི}) 10-15. {སྐྱེ་མཆེད་དྲུག} six sources of perception (see {དབང་པོ་དྲུག}) 16-20. {ཡུལ་ལྔ་།} five objects (see {ཡུལ་ལྔ}) 21-25. {གཞི་དུས་ཀྱི་ཡེ་ཤེས་ལྔ་།} five basic wisdoms (see {གཞི་དུས་ཀྱི་ཡེ་ཤེས་ལྔ}).
རང-རྐྱ-ཐུཔ-པའི-རྫས-ཡོད-ཀྱི-བདག	Self-sufficiently existent independent self. An independent self as asserted by the lower schools of Buddhist philosophy.
རང-གི-མཚན-ཉི-ཀྱིས-གྲུབ-པ	Svalaksanasiddha/ Existence by its own nature or characteristics. The assertion that phenomena exist not as mere objects of conceptual labelling but in their own right.
རང-གི-མཚན-ཉིད-སྟོང-པ-ཉིད	[svalakṣaṇa ṡūnyatā]/ Emptiness of own characteristics; lack of true independent existence of the characteristics or marks of all conventional things, of all paths to enlightenment and of all qualities of an enlightened being; one of the sixteen emptinesses.
རང-གི-གཞི-ལ-གཞོལ-བ	Concentration on self-basis/ deity. A tantric practice of self-generation through meditation on the emptiness deity, letter deity, form deity, seal deity and sign deity, while simultaneously reciting and counting mantras.
རང-གྲོལ	Self-liberation. A {རྫོགས་ཆེན་} meditation technique of naturally releasing all conceptual experiences into the sphere of self-arisen intuitive awareness without being forced through the application of antidotes, similar to a snake's self-loosening of its coiled body.
རང-རྒྱལ	[pratyekabuddha]/ Solitary Realizer. Hinayana practitioner who works only for his own liberation from cyclic existence, and who does not rely on a teacher during the last phase of his rebirth; some teach Dharma by means of physical gestures and some by means of miracles; a Solitary Realizer's path is very similar to that of a Hearer ({ཉན་ཐོས}).
རང-རྒྱལ-གྱི-ཐེག-པ	[pratyekabuddha yāna]/ The Solitary Realizer vehicle; the path of Pratekyabuddhas. The paths are similar to that of a Hearer (Sravaka); asserts the selflessness of a person and meditates on the twelve links of interdependent origination, and attains the state of aFoe-destroyer (Arhatship).
རང-རྒྱལ-གྱི-ལམ-ལྔ་	[paсca pratyekabuddha mārgaḥ]/ The five paths of the Solitary Realizer's vehicle. The path of accumulation, preparation, seeing, meditation and no-more learning of this vehicle.
རང-རྒྱལ-གསུམ	The three types of Solitary Realizers; the three categories of Pratekya Buddhas who have not transcended the Sravaka's path before.\n1. {བསེ་རུ་ལྟ་བུའི་རང་སངས་རྒྱས།} the Rhinoceros like solitary realizer\n2. {ཚོགས་སྤྱོད་ཀྱི་རང་སངས་རྒྱས།} the sociable solitary realizer\n3. {རྒྱུན་ཞུགས་ཀྱི་རང་སངས་རྒྱས།} the solitary realizer of the stream-winner.
རང-རྒྱུད-པ	[svātantrika] School. A school of [mādhyamika], who assert the lack of true existence of all phenomena and specifically that of functional phenomena, even nominally; but assert inherent existence. The name of the school is derived from their assertion that, in dependence upon a correct reason (established inherently by its inherent characteristics), the view of true existence can be severed in the mind of correct opponent.
རང-རྒྱུད-པའི-མུ-སྟེགས-པ	Non-Buddhist by nature. Those who assert and are naturally attracted to views describing Buddha as wrong. There are two types: 1. non-Buddhist by birth 2. non-Buddhist by learning.
རང-ངོས-ནས-གྲུབ-པ	Objective existence; existence from its own-side. True and independent existence established only in reference to the thing itself.
རང-སྟོ་	[svaṡūnyatā]/ Self-emptiness. The middle view of the emptiness of self; reality that all phenomena are empty of inherent existence.
རང-དོན-རྗེས-དཔག	[svārthānumāna]/ Inference for self, e.g. an inference generated for one's own understanding, e.g. impermanence through logical reasons.
རང-བྱུང-ཡེ-ཤེས	[svāyambhū vijсāna]/ Self-born wisdom; spontaneously arisen wisdom in the mental continuum of all sentient beings.
རང-འབྱོར-ལྔ་	Five personal endowments.\n1. {མིར་སྐྱེས་པ།} born as a human being\n2. {ཡུལ་དབུས་སུ་སྐྱེ་བ།} born in a central land (a Buddhist country)\n3. {དབང་པོ་ཚང་བ།} possessing complete sensory faculties\n4. {སངས་རྒྱས་བསྟན་པ་དད་པ།} having faith in the teachings of Buddha\n5. {ལས་ཀྱི་མཐའ་མ་ལོག་པ།} not being subject to extremely wrong deeds.
རང-མཚན	[svalakṣana]/ Self-characterized phenomena. A phenomenon which is established from its own side without being labelled by thought, e.g. a vase.
རང-བཞིན-བསྐལ-དོན	The naturally obscure phenomena. Those phenomena that cannot be seen directly by sight, e.g. spirits or demons.
རང-བཞིན-གྱི-ཁ-ན-མ-ཐོ-བ	Misdeed by nature; improbity by nature. Such as the transgression of moral values through killing, lying, etc., which are unwholesome by nature and not specifically prohibited by Buddha.
རང-བཞིན-གྱིས-གྲུབ-པ	[svabhāvasiddha]/ Inherent existence. Self existent without being dependent on causes and conditions.
རང-བཞིན-གྱི-རྟགས-ཡང-དག	[svabhāva samyaghetu]/ Correct reason of (the same) nature. A correct reason which has the same nature as the predicate in a logical syllogism. There are two types:\n1. {ཁྱད་པར་ལྟོས་པ་པོའ་རང་བཞིན་གྱི་རྟགས་ཡང་དག} direct correct reason of the same nature\n2. {ཁྱད་པར་དག་པ་པོའི་རང་བཞིན་གྱི་རྟགས་ཡང་དག} indirect correct reason of the same nature.
རང-བཞིན-རྒྱུའི-གཙོ-བོ	Fundamental principal by nature. The threefold principle of motility, darkness and lightness existing in a state of equilibrium; philosophical view of the [sāṃkhya] school of thought.
རང-བཞིན-སྟོང-པ-ཉིད	[prakṛtiṡūnyatā]/ Emptiness of nature; natural emptiness. Lack of inherent existence of the nature of all phenomena; one of the sixteen emptinesses.
རང-བཞིན-གནས-རིགས	Naturally abiding Buddha nature; natural Buddha lineage. The reality of a stained mind that is liable to transform into the nature truth body of a Buddha.
རང-བཞིན-རྣམ-དག-གི-ཆར-གྱུར-བའི-ངོ-བོ-ཉིད-སྐུ	[svabhāvaviṡuddhabhūta svabhāvakāya]/ Intrinsically pure nature body (of Buddha); i.e. the emptiness of the Buddha's mental continuum.
རང-བཞིན-ལྷུན-གྲུབ	[svabhāvasahajasiddha]/ The natural spontaneity. A. The existence of phenomena independent of effort B. According to {རྫོགས་ཆེན་} meditation this refers to the primordial quality of mind inherently possessed within the three kayas of a Buddha
རང-རིག	[svasaṃvedanā]/ Apperception; self-awareness. A non-conceptual awareness which only apprehends internal phenomena je. a consciousness.
རང-རིག-མངོན-སུམ	[svasaṃvedanā pratyakṣa]/ Direct appreception; direct self-awareness. A direct perception that is devoid of conceptualization and oniy takes aspects of awareness as its object.
རང-ལས-ངེས-ཀྱི-ཚད-མ	Self-evident direct perception. A valid cognition that cognizes itself as being a valid perception, e.g. a valid cognition of a person who has the knowledge of valid perceptions.
རང-སངས-རྒྱས	[pratyekabuddha]/ Solitary Realizer (see {རང་རྒྱལ}).\n{རབ་གནས།}\n[pratiṣṭhā]/ Consecration. Blessing representation of Buddha, Dharma and Sarigha through a ceremony and transforming them into sacred religious articles.
རབ-བྱུང་	[pravrajyā]/ A. Monks and nuns; fully ordained monks or nuns; probationary nuns and novice monks and nuns. B. Sexantry; a cycle of sixty years in the Tibetan caiendar commencing from the year 1027, as introduced by Gyijo Dawe Ozer after the translation of the [kālacakra] tantra in Tibet.
རབ-བྱུང-གི-སྡོམ-པ-ལྔ་	Five types of ordination vows; five kinds of vows. 1-2. {དགེ་ཚུལ་ཕ་མའི་སྡོམ་པ།} [ṡrāmaṇera ṡrāmanerikā]/ novice monk and nun's vows\n3. {དགེ་སློབ་མའི་སྡོམ་པ།} s'iks.āmān.a]/ probationary nun's vows 4-5. {དགེ་སློང་ཕ་མའི་སྡོམ་པ།} [bhikṣu bhikṣunī]/ fully ordained monk and nun's vows.
རབ-བྱུང-གི-ཡོ-བྱད-བཞི	Four articles of a monk; belongings of a monk categorized into four sets:\n1. {འཚོ་བའི་ཡོ་བྱད།} [jīvitopakaraṇa]/ articles of livelihood\n2. {མཁོ་བའི་ཡོ་བྱད།} basic necessities\n3. {ལྷག་པའི་ཡོ་བྱད།} supplementary articles\n4. {ཡོ་བྱད་ཕྲན་ཚེགས།} minor articles.
རབ-བྱེད	Chapter, a textual division. Also a treatise written by [ācarya vasubandhu].
རབ-རིབ-ཅན-གྱི-མིག-ཤེས	[taimiracakṣuvijсāna]/ Blurred vision; the visual consciousness of someone with a cataract.
རི-དགུ	Nine mountains; nine mountains according to the Abhidharma tradition.\n1. {རི་རབ་ལྷུན་པོ།} [sumeru]/ Mt. Meru 2-8. {གསེར་གྱི་རི་བདུན།} the seven golden mountains\n9. {ཁོར་ཡུག་གི་རི།} the encircling iron mountains.
རི-ལྟ-བུའི-སེམས-བསྐྱེད	[parvatopamacittotpāda]/ Mountain-like bodhicitta. The mind ofent ightenment associated with the practice of the perfection of concentration possessed by a Bodhisattva on the fifth ground.
རི-བོང-རྭ	[ṡaṡaviṣāṇa]/ Rabbit's horn. A popular example illustrating non-existence.
རི-རབ-ལྷུན-པོ	[meru]/ Mt. Meru; Sumeru; the king of mountains; central axis of Buddhist cosmology. Founded on a base of gold, the east of which is made of shiny white silver, south of blue lapiz lazuli, west of red crystal and north of yellow gold.
རིག-གྲོལ-གྱི-ཡོན-ཏན-བརྒྱད	[aṣṭa saṃgharatna guṇāḥ]/ Eight qualities of the [saṅgha] Jewel; the [saṅgha]'s qualities of wisdom and liberation.\n1. {ཇི་ལྟ་བ་མཁྱེན་པའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of knowing what is reality\n2. {ཇི་སྙེད་པ་མཁྱེན་པའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quaiity of knowing whatever exists (conventionality)\n3. {རང་རིག་པའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of knowing inner features\n4. {རིག་པའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of knowledge itself\n5. {ཆགས་སྒྲིབ་ལས་གྲོལ་བའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of liberation from alluring delusions\n6. {ཐགས་སྒྲབ་ལས་གྲལ་བའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of liberation from obstructive delusions\n7. {དམན་གྲིབ་ལས་གྲོལ་བའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of liberation from lower delusions\n8. {གྲོལ་བའི་ཡོན་ཏན།} quality of liberation itself.
རིག-སྔགས	[vidyā mantra]/ The knowledge mantra. The mantras primarily meant for establishing the wisdom aspect of realizations and divine activities. In a more generalized sense this comprises the female form of deities, her mantras, [mudrās], etc.
རིག-སྟོང-དབྱེར-མེད	Inseparability of awareness and emptiness; the oneness of mind and emptiness.
རིག-གནས-བཅུ	Ten fields of study; ten knowledges; ten sciences (see {རིག་གནས་ཆུང་བ་ལྔ} & {རིག་གནས་ཆེ་བ་ལྔ}).
རིག-གནས-བཅོ-བརྒྱད	Eighteen sciences. A. According to the Abhidharma tradition these are:\n1. {རོལ་མོ།} music\n2. {འཁྲིག་འཐབ།} amorous skills\n3. {འཚོ་ཆས།} {སོ་ཚིས།} house-keeping\n4. {གྲངས་ཅན།} mathematics\n5. {སྒྲ།} grammar\n6. {གསོ་བ།} medicine\n7. {ཆོས་ལུགས།} theology\n8. {བཟོ་བོ།} arts and crafts\n9. {འཕོང་སྤྱོད།} archery\n10. {གཏན་ཚིག} logic\n11. {སྨན་སྦྱོར།} pharmacology\n12. {རང་གི་བཅས་པ།} self-discipline\n13. {ཐོས་པ་དྲན་པ།} contemplation\n14. {སྐར་མའི་དཔྱད།} astronomy\n15. {རྩིས།} astrology\n16. {མིག་འཁྲུལ།} magic\n17. {སྔོན་རབས།} history\n18. {སྔོན་བྱུང་བརྗོད་པ།} legends.\nB. according to the Vinaya tradition these are:\n1. {སངས་སྔགས་ཀྱི་རྒྱུད་།}\n2. {ཆོ་ག་ཞིབ་མོ།}\n3. {གཏན་ཚིགས་རིག་པ།}\n4. {རིག་བྱེད།}\n5. {བརྡ་སྤྲོད།}\n6. {སྒྲ་ངེས་པར་སྦྱོར་བ།}\n7. {ཤེས་གསལ།}\n8. {ངེས་པའི་ཚིག}\n9. {སྡེབ་སྦྱོར་མཁས་པ།}\n10. {སྐར་མའི་རིག་པ།}\n11. {རྟོགས་བྱེད་ཀྱི་རིག་པ།}\n12. {ཆུར་ལྷུང་གི་རིག་པ།}\n13. {ཆེར་སྤྱོད་ཀྱི་རིག་པ།}\n14. {འཇིག་རྟན་རྒྱང་ཕན་པའི་རིག་པ།}\n15. {བྱེ་བྲག་པའི་རིག་པ།}\n16. {རྒྱུད་དྲུག་ཅུ་པ}\n17. {ཁྱུར་མིད་ཀྱི་རིག་པ།}\n18. gnas 'dug pa'i rig pa/
རིག-གནས-ཆུང-བ-ལྔ་	Five minor sciences; five minor fields of study.\n1. {སྙན་ངག} [kāvya]/ poetry\n2. {མངོན་བརྗོད།} [abhidhāna]/ synonyms\n3. {སྡེབ་སྦྱོར།} [chanda]/ lexicography\n4. {སྐར་རྩིས།} [jyotiṣa]/ astro-science\n5. {ཟློས་གར།} [nāṭaka]/ dance and drama.
རིག-གནས-ཆེ-བ-ལྔ་	Five major sciences; five major fields of study.\n1. {བཟོ་རིག་པ།}\n[ṡilpa]/ arts and crafts\n2. {གསོ་བ་རིག་པ།} [cikitsā]/ medicine\n3. {སྒྲ་རིག་པ།} [ṡabdavidyā]/grammar\n4. {གཏན་ཚིགས་རིག་པ།} [hetu]/ logic\n5. {ནང་དོན་རིག་པ།} [adhyātma]/ philosophy.
རིག-པ	[vidyā]/ A. Knowledge. B. Awareness. C. Wisdom. D. Intelligence. E. Science of learning.
རིག-པ-འཛིན-པའི-སྡེ-སྣོད	The set of discourses of a knowledge-bearer; [mantrayāna] vehicle. An antidote against all the three delusions (see {དུ་གསུམ}) in an balanced manner.
