There are two types:\n1. {བློའི་སེལ་འཇུག} mental eliminative engager, e.g. the concept of a vase\n2. {སྒྲའི་སེལ་འཇུག} verbal eliminative engager, e.g. the statement, 'sound is impermanent'.
སེལ-བ	[apoha]/ Elimination; eliminative phenomena; a negative\nphenomena. There are three:\n1. {དོན་གྱི་སེལ་བ།} meaning eliminative phenomena, e.g. a thing that is not not a vase\n2. {བློའི་སེལ་བ།} mental eliminative phenomena, e.g. the appearance of a thing that is not not a vase to a thought cognizing a vase\n3. {མེད་དགག་གི་སེལ་བ།} affirming negative type eliminative phenomena, e.g. the mere absence of something that is not a vase.
སོ-ཐར-གྱི-སྡོམ-པ	[pratimokṣa saṃvara]/ Vows of individual liberation. Precepts of ordination meant for self-liberation from bad rebirth and [saṃsara] There are generally two:\n1. {ཁྱིམ་པའི་སྡོམ་པ།} a householder's vows\n2. {རབ་བྱུང་གི་སྡོམ་པ།} a monk's or nun's vows.
སོ-ཐར-རིགས-བརྒྱད	Eight classes of individual liberation vows (see {སོ་ཐར་རིགས་བདུན} 1-7)\n8. {བསྙེན་གནས་ཀྱི་སྡོམ་པ།} one day ordination vows.
སོ-ཐར-རིགས-རིས-བདུན	Seven classes of individual liberation vows.\n1. {དགེ་སློང་ཕའི་སྡོམ་པ།} [bhikṣu saṃvara]/ fully ordained monk vows\n2. {དགེ་སློང་མའི་སྡོམ་པ།} [bhikṣunī saṃvara]/ fully ordained nun vows\n3. {དགེ་ཚུལ་ཕའི་སྡོམ་པ།} [ṡrāmaṇera saṃvara]/ novice monk vows\n4. {དགེ་ཚུལ་མའི་སྡོམ་པ།} [ṡrāmaṇerikā saṃvara]/ novice nun vows\n5. {དགེ་བསྙེན་ཕའི་སྡོམ་པ།} [upāsaka saṃvara]/ layman vows\n6. {དགེ་བསྙེན་མའི་སྡོམ་པ།} [upāsikā saṃvara]/ lay woman vows\n7. {དགེ་སློབ་མའི་སྡོམ་པ།} [ṡikṣamāna saṃvara]/ probationary nun vows.\n{སོ་ཐར་རིགས་རིས་བཞི།}\nThe four classes of individual liberation vows.\n1. {དགེ་སློང་ཕ་མའི་སྡོམ་པ།} fully ordained monk and nun vows\n2. {དགེ་ཚུལ་ཕ་མའི་སྡོམ་པ།} novice vows\n3. {དགེ་བསྙེན་གྱི་སྡོམ་པ།} layperson's vows\n4. {བསྙེན་གནས་ཀྱི་སྡོམ་པ།} one day ordination vows.
སོ-སོ-སྐྱེ-བོ	[pṛthagjana]/ Ordinary person; beginner. Persons who have no knowledge of the reality of phenomena.
སོ-སོར-བརྟགས-འགོག	[pratisaṃkhyānirodha]/ Analytical cessation. Cessation gained through the wisdom of meditation and anylysis on the four noble truths, e.g. the truth of cessation within the mental continuum of an [ārya] on the path of meditation.
སོ-སོར-བརྟགས-མིན-འགོག-པ	[apratisaṃkhyānirodha]/ Non-analytical cessation. Cessation that is impermanent by nature and is not acquired through the wisdom of meditation and analysis on the four noble truths, e.g. cessation of rebirth into bad migration within me continuum of a Bodhisattva on the path of preparation.
སོ-སོར-ཐར-པ	[pratimokṣa]/ Individual liberation (see {སོ་ཐར་གྱི་སྡོམ་པ}).
སོ-སོ-ཡང-དག-རིག-པ-བཞི	Four specific perfect understandings. The four ways in which a Bodhisattva knows the distinct features, characteristics and states of phenomena\n1. {ཆོས་སོ་སོ་ཡང་དག་རིག་པ།} [dharma pratisaṃvid]/ specific perfect understanding of dharma\n2. {དོན་སོ་སོ་ཡང་དག་རིག་པ།} [artha pratisaṃvid]/ specific perfect understanding of meaning\n3. {ངེས་ཚིག་སོ་སོ་ཡང་དག་རིག་པ།} [nirukti pratisaṃvid]/ specific perfect understanding of definitive words\n4. {སྤོབས་པ་སོ་སོ་ཡང་དག་རིག་པ།} [pratibhāna pratisaṃvid]/ specific perfect understanding of confidence.
སོར-མོ-ལྔ་	[paсcān'guli]/ Five fingers.\n1. {མཐེ་བོང་།} [an'guṣṭha]/ thumb\n2. {མཛུབ་མོ།} [an'guli]/ index finger\n3. {གུང་མོ།} [madhān'guli]/ middle finger\n4. {སྲིན་ལག} [anāmā]/ ring finger\n5. {མཐེའུ་ཆུང་།} [anāmikā]/ little finger.
སྲི	[peṡī]/ A. Evil spirit; a malignant spirit or devil born of a dead person resurrected in their previous locality who create truble in the vicinity. B. Miserliness. C. A disastrous event or period believed to be a common karma, e.g. evil accidents happening one after another in the same locality.
སྲི-གནོན	Exorcism. A type of tantric ritual to capture, bury and burn a malignant spirit (see {སྲི}).
སྲིད-པ	[bhava]/ A. [saṃsāra]; cyclic existence. B. Existence.
སྲིད-པ-ཆགས-པའི-ལྷ-དགུ	Nine Gods of Tibet. O-de Gung-gyal, the ninth King of Tibet, son of Drigum Tzen-po and his eight sons believed to be residing and guarding Tibet throughout its three regions.\n1. {ཡར་ལྷ་ཤམ་པོ།} Yala Shampo\n2. {གཉན་ཆེན་ཐང་ལྷ།} Nyan-chen Thang-ia\n3. {རྨ་ཆེན་སྤོམ་ར།} Ma-chen Pom-ra\n4. {སྒྱོགས་ཆེན་ལྡོང་ར།} Gyog-chen Dong-ra\n5. {སྒོམ་པོ་ལྷ་རྗེ།} Gampo-Lha-Je\n6. {ཞོགས་ལྷ་རྒྱུགས་པོ།} Zhog-ia Gvug-Po\n7. {ཇོ་བོ་གཡུལ་རྒྱལ།} Jobo Yu-Gyal\n8. {ཤེའུ་ཁ་རག} Sheu Kha-Rag\n9. {འོད་དེ་གུང་རྒྱལ།} O-DeGung-Gyal.\n{སྲིད་པ་ཐ་མ་པ།}\n[caramabhavika]/ One on the last existence. One who is free from being reborn again in cyclic existence through the force of his contaminated karma
སྲིད-པ-འཚོལ-བ	Seeker of existence. Epithet for the being in an intermediate state of rebirth ({བར་དོ}).
སྲིད-པ-བཞི	Four states of existence; the four domains of existence.\n1. {སྐྱེ་སྲིད།} [utpatti bhava]/ birth state\n2. {སྔོན་དུ་ཀྱི་སྲིད་པ།} [sākṣin bhava]/ live state\n3. {འཆི་སྲིད།} [maraṇa bhava]/ death state\n4. {བར་སྲིད།} [antara bhava]/ intermediate state.
སྲིད-པ-གསུམ	The three worlds: A.\n1. {ལྷའི་སྲིད་པ།} [devabhava]/ world of gods\n2. {ཀླུའི་སྲིད་པ།} [nāgabhava]/ world of nagas\n3. {མིའི་སྲིད་པ།} [manuṣyabhava]/ world of humans. B.\n1. {ས་འོག} [bhūtala]/ sub-terrestrial world\n2. {ས་སྟེང་།} [mahitala]/ terrestrial\n3. {ས་བླ།} [antarika]/ heaven. C. The three states of existence:\n1. {སྐྱེ་སྲིད།} [utpattibhava]/ birth-state\n2. {འཆི་སྲིད།} [maraṇabhava]/ death-state\n3. {བར་སྲིད།} [antarabhava]/ intermediate-state. D. According to the Nyingma tradition the three states of existence are as follows:\n1. {ལུས་སྣང་བ་འདོད་པའི་སྲིད་པ།} the desire realm in which physical form is seen\n2. {ངག་ཕྱེད་སྣང་གཟུགས་ཀྱི་སྲིད་པ།} the form realm in which half of speech is felt\n3. {ཡིད་མི་སྣང་གཟུགས་མེད་པའི་སྲིད་པ།} the formless realm in which mind cannot be sensed.
སྲིད-པའི-རྩ-བ-ཕྲ-རྒྱས-དྲུག	Six root delusions of cyclic existence (see {རྩ་ཉོན་དྲུག}).
སྲིད-པའི-ཡན-ལག	The limb of existence. The link of grasping, ninth in the twelve links of interdependent origination which has the force of activating strong karmas through negativities accumulated by body, speech and mind.
སྲིད-རྩེ	[bhavāgra]/ Peak of Existence. The highest state of the three realms within cyclic existence.
སྲིད-ཞི-མཉམ-ཉིད-ཀྱི-སྦྱོར-བ	[bhavaṡāntisamata prayoga]/ Traihing in the sameness of cyclic existence and peace; the Bodhisattva's meditative training in the sameness of sanisara and [nirvāṇa] as lacking inherent existence.
སྲུང-འཁོར	Wheel of Protection. Meditation on a vajra fence, fire fence and vajra tent, etc., as a protection for the residence and resident [maṇḍala] of a deity. The meditation of a vajra fence throughout the ten directions before creation of a [maṇḍala] and bestowal of an initiation.
སྲུང-ཐབས-ཡན-ལག-ལྔ་	Five means of guarding a moral discipline; five ways of protecting one's vows from degeneration.\n1. {དགེ་བའི་བཤེས་གཉེན་ལ་བསྟེན་པ།} relying on a spiritual teacher\n2. {བསམ་པ་ཕུན་སུམ་ཚོགས་པ།} relying on an excellent motivation\n3. {འགལ་རྐྱེན་མི་མཐུན་ཕྱོགས་ངོ་ཤེས་པ།} recognizing the opposing factors\n4. {བ་བ་པ་ངས་ས་ང་པ།} perfectly training in the precepts\n5. {པདེ་བར་གནས་པའི་}^{ན་པ}^{ན་པ།} relyiag on conditions for a peaceful life.
སྲུང-མདུད	Protection cord. Strings that are knotted in a special way, blessed and given by Lamas as their symbol of protection and blessings.
སྲེད-པ	[tṛṣṇā]/ A. Craving; the urge to meet with pleasant feelings and to be separated from ill sensations. B. Attachment; clinging.
སྲེད-པ-གསུམ	Three kinds of craving; cravings experienced at death.\n1. {འདོད་སྲེད།} [rāga tṛṣṇā]/ craving for desired objects\n2. {འཇིགས་སྲེད།} [satkāya tṛṣṇa]/ craving for fear of losing this body\n3. {སྲིད་སྲེད།} [bhava tṛṣṇa]/ craving for existence.
སྲེད-པའི-ཡན-ལག	The link of craving. The link of feeling, seventh in the twelve links of interdependent origination which causes the growth of the faculty to taste various objects and develops attachment and clinging to these, thereby enhancing the state of existence.
སྲོག	[prāṇa]/ Life-force. A. According to Vinaya and the Abhi-dharma tradition it is the vital energy that acts as the basis for consciousness and the warmth of a being; whereas in other traditions it is generally the life as opposed to death. B. In astrology, it is the life-pattern of a person.
སྲོག-སྡོམ-གཟེར-བཞི	The four vital points. The four vital points in the practice of the generation stage of mahayoga tantra according to the Nyingma tradition, meant for integrating the life-like essence of all phenomena into the sphere of non-dual primordial wisdom.\n1. {ཏེང་ངེ་འཛིན་ལྷའི་གཟེར།} the vital point of a deity used for developing meditative concentration\n2. {སྙིང་པོ་སྔགས་ཀྱི་གཟེར།} the vital point of the essential mantra\n3. {དགོངས་པ་མི་འགྱུར་བའི་གཟེར།} the unchangeable vital point of the instruction or thought\n4. {འཕྲོ་འདུ་འཕྲིན་ལས་ཀྱི་གཟེར།} the vital point of virtuous activity or energy for dissolving distractions.
སྲོག-འཛིན-གྱི-རླུང་	[prāṇāyāyu]/ Life-supporting wind. One of the five principal energy winds located at the crown within the brain, responsible for wit and intelligence and the power of memory.
སློབ-དཔོན	[ācārya]/ A. [ācārya]; a spiritual master who takes care of his diciples' material needs. B. Teacher; lecturer. C. An instrument of a carpenter.
སློབ-དཔོན-གྱི-དབང-དྲུག	The six initiations of a master.\n1. {ཕྱིར་མི་ལྡོག་པའི་དབང་།} the irreversible initiation\n2. {གསང་བའི་དབང་།} the secret initiation\n3. {རྗེས་གནང་གི་དབང།} permission initiation\n4. {ལུང་བསྟན་གྱི་དབང།} prophesy\n5. {དབུགས་དབྱུང་གི་དབང།} giving relief\n6. {གཟེངས་བསྟོད་ཀྱི་དབང་།} praise and encouragement.
སློབ-དཔོན-ལྔ་	The five masters (see {སློབ་དཔོན་བདུན}, 3-7).
སློབ-དཔོན-དྲུག	Six masters; six types of teachers.\n1. {དམ་ཚིག་དང་སྡོམ་པ་སྦྱིན་} {པའི་སློབ་དཔོན།} a teacher who bestows pledges and vows\n2. {བཟླས་ལུང་སྦྱིན་པའི་སློབ་དཔོན།} a teacher who bestows oral and reading transmissions\n3. {རྒྱུད་བཤད་པའི་སློབ་དཔོན།} a teacher who bestows tantric teachings\n4. {མན་ངག་སྟོན་པའི་སློབ་དཔོན།} a teacher who gives quintessential instructions\n5. {དབང་བསྐུར་བའི་སློབ་དཔོན།} a teacher who bestows initiations\n6. {ལས་བྱེད་པའི་སློབ་དཔོན།} a teacher who gives ritual guidance.
སློབ-དཔོན-བདུན	Seven masters; seven types of teachers according to the Vinaya tradition.\n1. {བསྙེན་གནས་ཀྱི་སློབ་དཔོན།} master who bestows one day vows\n2. {དགེ་བསྙེན་གྱི་སློབ་དཔོན།} master who bestows lay persons' vows\n3. {དགེ་ཚུལ་གྱི་སློབ་དཔོན།} master who bestows novice vows\n4. {གསང་སྟེ་སྟོན་པའི་སློབ་དཔོན།} master who is one's confidant\n5. {ལས་བྱེད་པའི་སློབ་དཔོན།} master who gives ritual guidance\n6. {ཀློག་པའི་སློབ་དཔོན།} master who teaches basics\n7. {གནས་ཀྱི་སློབ་དཔོན།} resident master.
སློབ-དཔོན-དཔའ-བོ	[ācāryavīra]/ [ācārya āryaṡura]. Perhaps the greatest of all scholarly Buddhist poets, a non-Buddhist of great learning who was defeated in debate by [āryadeva], a disciple of [nāgārjuna] and converted to Buddhism; he composed the Fifty Verses of Guru Devotion.
སློབ-དཔོན-ས-ར-ཧ	[ācārya saraha]. Also called Brahma Rahula; the root Guru of [ācarya nāgārjuna] born in a Brahmin family at Odibida, Orissa of modern India, renowned for his tantric practice.
སློབ-མ-ཁྱད-ཆོས-གསུམ-ལྔན	Disciple with qualities; Ihree basic qualities of a Dharma disciple.\n1. {ཤེས་རབ་རྣོ་བ།} he has clear wisdom\n2. {སྨྲ་བ་ཉུང་བ།} he speaks little\n3. {བླ་མ་ལ་གུས་པ།} he is respectful of his masters.
སློབ-མ-སྟ-གོན	The preparatory rites of disciples. The first phase of initiations meant to prepare the disciple for the actual initiation. This involves:\n1. {ཀུན་སློང་བཅོས་ཤིང་ནང་དབང་བསྐུར་བ།} setting motivation and granting inner initiation\n2. {གསོལ་བ་གདབ་ཅིང་འཛིན་དུ་གཞུག་པ།} making requests and upholding the practice\n3. {སྡོམ་པ་གཟུང་ཞིང་བྱིན་གྱིས་བརླབ་པ།} receiving vows and blessings\n4. {དངོས་གྲུབ་བརྟག་ཕྱིར་སོ་ཤིང་དོར་བ།} examining the siddhi and throwing of the tooth stick\n5. {ངག་ཉེས་སྦྱང་ཕྱིར་ཁྱོར་ཆུ་བླུད་པ།} distnbuting blessed water ({ཁྱོར་ཆུ}) for purifying negativities of speech\n6. {རྨི་ལམ་བཟློག་ཕྱིར་ཀུ་ཤ་གཏད་པ།} distributing kusa grass to avoid bad dreams\n7. {བར་ཆད་ཞི་ཕྱིར་} {དཔུང་སྐུད་གདགས་པ།} distributing protection thread to guard the disciples from interferences\n8. {སྤྲོ་བ་བསྐྱེད་ཕྱིར་ཆོས་བཤད་པ།} giving a summary teaching to generate inspiration\n9. {མཚན་ལྟས་བརྟག་ཕྱིར་རྨི་ལམ་བརྟག་པ།} examining dreams through analyzing the omens.
སློབ-མའི-ཆོས-བཞི	The four qualities of a disciple; four basic qualities to judge the acceptance of a disciple.\n1. {མི་ཕྱེད་པའི་དད་པ།} unfluctuating faith\n2. {མི་ལྡོག་པའི་བརྩེན་འགྲུས།} irreversible efforts\n3. {གཞན་དྲིང་མི་འཇོག་པའི་གསུང་རབ།} incomparable teachings/ texts to be taught\n4. {བཤེས་གཉེན་ལ་དད་གུས།} faith and devotion in the spiritual master.
སློབ-མའི-བྱ-བ-ལྔ་	The five duties of a disciple.\n1. {བཤེས་གཉེན་འཚེལ་བ་ལ་སྐྱེ་བ་མེད་པ།} having no regret in searching for spiritual masters\n2. {སྐུ་ལྟ་བས་ཆོག་མི་ཤེས་པར་བྱ་བ།} being insatiable in meeting and seeing one's teachers\n3. {དེས་བསྟན་པ་དང་རྗེས་སུ་མཐུན་པར་འཛིན་པ།} following his or her teacher's teachings and instructions\n4. {དེའི་ཐབས་མཁས་སྤྱོད་པ་ལ་མི་ཁྲོ་བ།} having no hatred against his or her teacher's skillful behaviors\n5. {དེ་ལས་རྟོགས་པ་ཐེབས་པར་བགྱི་བ།} working towards generating realizations.
སློབ-མའི-དབང-ལྔ་	The five initiations of a disciple (see {རིག་པའི་དབང་ལྔ}).
སློབ-མའི-མཚན-ཉིད-ལྔ་	The five qualities of a disciple.\n1. {བློ་གཟུ་བོར་གནས་པ།} having an unbiased way of thinking\n2. {བློ་གྲོས་དང་ལྡན་པ།} having good wisdom\n3. {དོན་གཉེར་ཆེ་བ།} having interest in one's training\n4. {གུས་པ།} being respectful\n5. {ཡིད་གཏོད་པ།} being devoted.
སློབ-མའི-མཚན-ཉིད-གསུམ	The three qualities of a disciple.\n1. {བློ་གསལ་བ།} having clear wisdom\n2. {ཤེས་འདོད་ཡོད་པ།} having interest in gaining knowledge\n3. {བླ་མར་གུས་པ།} being respectful of one's teachers.
སློབ-ལམ-བཞི	The four paths of a trainee.\n1. {ཐར་པ་ཆ་མཐུན།} aid to liberation\n2. {ངེས་འབྱེད་ཆ་མཐུན།} aid to definitive separation\n3. {དོན་མངོན་རྟོགས།} realization of the meaning\n4. {རྗེས་ལ་མངོན་རྟོགས།} the subsequent realization. These .are synonymous with the path of accumulation, preparation, seeing and meditation, respectively.
གསང-སྔགས	Secret mantra; tantric teachings. Those cycles of teachings involving techniques to protect one's mind from misconceptions and illusions by means of cultivating the path of union of the wisdom understanding emptiness and great compassion aimed ultimately at the actualization of the great wisdom; these are to be practised secretly and cannot be declared to those who are not properly ripe to receive these (see {གསང་སྔགས་ཀྱི་ཁྱད་ཆོས་བཞི།}).
གསང-སྔགས-ཀྱི-ཁྱད-ཆོས-བཞི	The four special qualities of secret mantra; the four features that make tantra superior compared to other practices.\n1. {ཐབས་ཀྱི་ཆ་ལ་མ་རྨོངས་པའི་ཁྱད་པར།} rich in the methods of approach\n2. {ཐབས་མང་བའི་ཁྱད་པར།} has many-fold methods or techniques\n3. {དཀའ་བ་མེད་པའི་ཁྱད་པར།} easy to adopt its methods and techniques\n4. {དབང་པོ་རྣོ་བའི་ཁྱད་པར།} suitable for persons of sharp intellect to carry the practice.
གསང-སྔགས-ཀྱི-སྡོམ-པ	Secret mantra vows; tantric vows (see {རྩ་ལྟུང་བཅུ་བཞི་ཨནད་སྦོམ་པོ་བརྒྱད}).
གསང-སྔགས-ཀྱི-སྣོད	The receptacles of secret mantra; the proper disciples qualified to receive secret mantra teachings.\n1. {དབང་པོ་རྣོ་བ།} sharp intelligence\n2. {དབང་གིས་རྒྱུད་སྨིན་པར་བྱས་པ།} having matured or ripened one's mental continuum through initiation\n3. {རྩེ་བ་དང་ཡན་ལག་གི་དམ་ཚིག་བསྲུང་བ།} having observed the root and secondary vows properly.
གསང-སྔགས-རྙིང-མ	Ancient secret mantra tradition; Ancient Tantra. Tantra was initially introduced into Tibet in the seventh century during the reign of King Songtsen Gampo and in the middle of the eighth century. During the reign of King Trisong Deutsan, Guru Padmasambhava visited Tibet and spread the tantric teach-Lngs widely through translating many tantric texts into Tibetan. In the tenth century Pandita Smrti Jnana and others came to Tibet and further carried out translation works of the doctrine and spread it extensively. The spreading of tantric doctrines in the history of Tibet is known as the Ancient Tantra.
གསང-སྔགས-རྡོ-རྗེ-ཐེག-པ	Secret Mantra [vajrayāna]. Simply called the Vajrayana or Diamond Vehicle concerning the tantric doctrine of the [kriyā], [cārya], [yoga] and [anuttarayoga] tantras; also called the resultant vehicle.
གསང-སྔགས-གསར-མ	New secret mantra tradition; New tantra. Following the eclipse of Buddhist teachings during the reign of King Lang Darma, in the middle of the 9th century, the great translator of Ngari, Rinchen Zangpo (958-1055) translated and revised many tantric texts into Tibetan and revitalized the doctrine once again in Tibet; this period, beginning from Rinchen Zangpo is known in the religious history of Tibet as the new system of tantra.
གསང-སྤྱོད-ལྡོག-སྒོམ	Reversed method of meditation on secret practice. One of the eight means of transmitting the [mahāmudrā] doctrine, primarily a method of passing on the bare techniques of psychic heat meditation based on one's own experience.
གསང-བ-འདུས-པ	[guhyasamāja]. A tantric deity belonging to the father tantra of the highest class of tantric practices.
གསང-བ-ཟབ-མོའི-དབང-གསུམ	The three profound secret initiations. The initiations that are gateways to enter into the mahayoga cycle of tantric practice according to the Nyingma tradition.\n1. {སྤྱོད་པའི་བརྟུལ་ཞུགས་ཅན་ལ་གསང་དབང་།} the secret initiation for adopting ascetic behavior\n2. {རིག་པའི་བརྟུལ་ཞུགས་ཅན་ལ་ཤེས་རབ་ཡེ་ཤེས་ཀྱི་དབང་།} the primordial wisdom initiation for adopting ascetic practices of intuitive awareness\n3. {མཉམ་པའི་བརྟུལ་ཞུགས་ཅན་ལ་དབྱེར་མེད་བདེ་བ་ཆེན་པོའི་དབང་།} the inseparable great bliss initiation for those adopting balanced ascetic practices.
གསང-བའི-དཀྱིལ-འཁོར	[guhyamaṇḍala]/ The secret [maṇḍala]. The vagina of a tantric consort.
གསང-བའི-བདག-པོ	[guhyapati]/ A. Master of secret teachings; Buddha [vajradhāra]. B. [vajrapāṇi]. C. [valṡravaṇa]; the god of wealth.
གསང-དབང་	[guhyābhiṣekha]/ Secret initiation; secret empowerment. One of the highest levels of initiation whereby the disciples are initiated into the conventional [maṇḍala] of bodhicitta of the deities in uhion; their stains of speech are purified; they are authorized to carry out meditation on the yogas of the energy channels and winds; and thereby the seed of attaining [sambhogakāya] Buddha is implanted in their mental continuum.
གསང-མཛོད-གསུམ	Three secret treasuries; three secret texts of the Nyingma tradition.\n1. {བླ་མ་གསང་མཇོད།} secret treasury of the Guru\n2. {ཡི་དམ་གསང་མཛོད།} secret treasury of the meditational deity\n3. {མཁའ་འགྲོ་གསང་མཛོད།} secret treasury of the [ḍākas] and [ḍākinis].
གསང-མ	The secret mother. The consort of a master, tantrika or a tulku.\n{གསན་ཡིག}\nList of teachings, initiations, oral transmissions and discourses received by a great Lama during his lifetime; record of teachings received.
གསལ-སྟོང-དབྱེར-མེད	Inseparability of clarity and emptiness; the intutive awareness of reality and primordial wisdom as fused into one another.
གསལ-སྟོང-འཛིན-མེད	The view of non-apprehension regarding clarity and emptiness. A view of reality as explained in the doctrine of the Sakya tradition; the fact that our mind is primordially clear by natuie and this clarity cannot be found upon any object no matter where we may search for it; and hence such an emptiness is the nature of our mind. When its clarity is found to be its emptiness and vice-versa one has found the natural and inexpressible view of the unity of clarity and emptiness of our mind.
གསལ-སྣང་	Prasena/ A. Clarity. B. Luminosity.\n{གསལ་བ།}\nPredicate. The predicate in a logicial syllogism (see {སྒྲུབ་བྱའི་ཆོས}).
གསུང-ཀུན-ཏུ-བརྗོད-པའི-ཆོ-འཕྲུལ	[ādeṡanāprātihārya]/ Miracles through teachings. Buddha's way of teaching his disciples according to their need; one of the three types of miracles of a Buddha (see {ཆོ་འཕྲུལ་རྣམ་གསུམ}).
གསུང-ལྔ་	The five kinds of speeches; Buddha's five ways of teaching disciples as explained in the Nyingma tradition.\n1. {སྐྱེ་མེད་དོན་གྱི་གསུང་།} the ultimate teachings lacking birth\n2. {དགོངས་པ་བརྡའི་གསུང་།} the intended teachings through gestures\n3. {བརྗོད་པ་ཚིག་གི་གསུང་།} the literal teachings through expression\n4. {དབྱེར་མེད་རྡོ་རྗེའི་གསུང་།} the vajra teachings of inseparability\n5. {མངོན་བྱང་གི་གསུང་།} the teachings through enlightened energy or blessings.
གསུང-དབྱངས-ཀྱི-ཕྱག-རྒྱའི-རྣལ-བྱོར	The yoga of dharma mudra of the teachings. One of the four yogas of yoga tantra (see {ཕྱག་རྒྱ་བཞི}) identified with the actualization of the wisdom of discrimination by means of eliminating adventitious defilements upon the mind.
གསུང-དབྱངས-ཡན-ལག-ལྔ་	The features of melodic voice; the five limbs of enlightened\nspeech of a Buddha.\n1. {འབྲུག་སྒྲ་ལྟར་ཟབ་པ།} deep like that of thunder\n2. {སྙན་ཞིང་འཇེབས་ལ་རྣ་བར་སྙན་པ།} soothing and comfortable to the ear\n3. {ཡིད་དུ་འོང་ཞིང་དགའ་བར་བྱེད་པ།} pleasant and delightful\n4. {རྣམ་པར་གསལ་ཞིང་རྣམ་པར་རིག་པར་བྱེད་པ།} lucid and articulate\n5. {མཉན་འོས་ཤིང་མི་མཐུན་པ་མེད་པ།} suitable and consistent throughout.\n{གསུམ་ལྡན།}\nThe three-fold period (see {བསྐལ་པ་གསུམ་ལྡན}).\n{གསུང་རབ་ཡན་ལག་དགུ}\nNine scriptural categories. These are No. 1-6 and 10-12 derived from the twelve sciptural categories (see {གསུང་རབ་ཡན་ལག་བཅུ་གཉིས}).
གསུང-རབ-ཡན-ལག-བཅུ-གཉིས	[dvādaṡa dharmapravacana]/ Twelve scriptural categories.\n1. {མདོའི་སྡེ།} [sūtram]/ sets of discourses\n2. {དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་བསྙད་པའི་སྡེ།} [geyam]/ intermediate verses\n3. {ལུང་དུ་བསྟན་པའི་སྡེ།} [vyākaraṇam]/ prophetic teachings\n4. {ཚིགས་སུ་བཅད་པའི་སྡེ།} [gātha]/ versified teachings\n5. {ཆེད་དུ་བརྗོད་པའི་སྡེ།} [udānam]/\nspecific teachings\n6. {གླེང་གཞིའ་སྡེ།} [nidānam]/ introductory teachings\n7. {རྟོགས་པ་བརྗོད་པའི་སྡེ།} [avadānam]/ parables\n8. {དེ་ལྟ་བུ} {བྱུང་བའི་སྡེ།} [itivṛttakam]/ legends\n9. {སྐྱེས་པའི་རབ་ཀྱི་སྡེ།} [jātakam]/ life stories\n10. {ཤིན་ཏུ་རྒྱས་པའི་སྡེ།} [vaipulyam]/ grand teachings\n11. {རྨད་དུ་བྱུང་བའི་སྡེ།} [adbhūta dharma]/marvellous teachings\n12. {གཏན་ལ་ཕབ་པའི་སྡེ།} [upadeṡa]/ finalized teachings.
གསེར-གྱི-རི-བདུན	Seven golden mountains. The seven mountains surrounding Mt. Meru as explained in the Abhidharma text.\n1. {མུ་ཁྱུད་འཛིན།} [nimindhāra]/rim holder\n2. {རྣམ་པར་འདུད།} [vinataka]/ perfect bow\n3. {རྟ་རྣ།} [aṡvakama]/ horse-ear\n4. {ལྟ་ན་སྡུག} [sudarṡana]/ lovely to behold\n5. {སེང་ལྡེང་ཅན།} [khadiraka]/ Acacia\n6. {གཤོལ་མདའ་འཛིན།} [īsādhāra]/ ploughshaft holder\n7. {གཉའ་ཤིང་འཛིན།} [yugadhāra]/yoke holder.
གསེར-ཆོས-བཅུ-གསུམ	The thirteen golden texts. The thirteen cycles of restrictive esoteric teachings known to the Tsarpa school of the Sakya tradition. These are: 1-3. {མཁའ་སྤྱོད་སྐོར་གསུམ།} the three concerning Vajrayogini (see {མཁའ་སྤྱོད་སྐོར་གསུམ}) 4-6. {དམར་ཆེན་སྐོར་གསུམ།} the three concerning the major red protectors (see {དམར་ཆེན་སྐོར་གསུམ}) 7-9. {དམར་ཆུང་སྐོར་གསུམ།} the three concerning minor red protectors (see {དམར་ཆུང་སྐོར་གསུམ})\n10. {འཆི་མེད་རྡོ་རྗེ་ལྷ་མོ།} the cycle of teachings of [amṛtavajra devi]\n11. {ཛམ་དམར།} the cycle of teachings of Red Dzambala\n12. {སེང་གདོང་།} the cycle of teachings concerning Sirhhanada\n13. {འཇམ་དཔལ་ནག་པོ།} the cycle of teachings concerning Black [maсjuṡrī].
གསེར-ལྟ-བུའི-སེམས-བསྐྱེད	[suvarṇopamacittotpāda]/ Gold-like bodhicitta. The mind of enlightenment associated with the practice of superior intention possessed by a Bodhisattva on the middling path of accumulation.
གསེར-གདུང་	The golden-tomb. Usually stupas of various sizes containing relics and precious articles of a deceased master.
གསོ-དཔྱད-ཡན-ལག-བརྒྱད	Eight branches of healing; eight types of therapy in the Tibetan medical system.\n1. {ལུས་ནད་གསོ་བའི་དཔྱད།} treatment of physical ailments\n2. {བྱིས་པའི་ནད་གསོ་བའི་དཔྱད།} treatment of children's ailment\n3. {མོ་ནད་གསོ་བའི་དཔྱད།} treatment of women's ailments\n4. {གདོན་གྱིས་འཚེ་བའི་དཔྱད།} treatment of disorders caused by spirits\n5. {མཚོན་གྱིས་འཚེ་བའི་དཔྱད།} treatment of wounds caused by weapons\n6. {དུག་གིས་འཚེ་བའི་དཔྱད།} treatment of poisoning\n7. {རྒས་ཁ་གསོ་བའི་དཔྱད།} treatment to combat old age\n8. {རོ་ཙ་གསོ་བའི་དཔྱད།} treatment concerning fertility.
གསོ-སྦྱོང་	[poṣadha]/ The bi-monthly confession and restortion ceremony of monks and nuns as proscribed by Buddha
གསོ-སྦྱོང-བཅུ-བཞི-པ	The bi-monthly confession and restoration ceremony of monks and nuns during the months of waning moon in which the ceremony cannot be held on the fourteenth day of the 12th, 2nd, 4th, 6th, 2nd phase of 8th and the 10th month of Tibetan calendar.
གསོ-སྦྱོང-བཅོ-ལྔ-པ	The bi-monthly confession and restoration ceremony of the monks and nuns held during the months of waxing moon and the waning moons of the 11th, 1st, 3rd, 5th, 7th and during [aṡvini] ({ཐ་སྐར}) constellation.
བསམ-གྱི-མི-ཁྱབ-པ-ལྔ་	Five inconceiveable topics.\n1. {ལས་ཀྱི་རྣམ་པར་སྨིན་པ་བསམ་མི་ཁྱབ།} inconceiveable ripening of karma\n2. {ནོར་བུ་སྔགས་སྨན་སོགས་ཀྱི་ནུས་པ་བསམ་མི་ཁྱབ།} inconceiveable power of jewels, mantras and medicine\n3. {རྣལ་འབྱོར་གྱི་ནུ་མཐུ་བསམ་མི་ཁྱབ།} inconceiveable power of yogis\n4. {བྱང་སེམས་ཀྱི་དབང་བཅུ་བསམ་མི་ཁྱབ།} inconceiveable ten powers of a bodhisattva\n5. {སངས་རྒྱས་ཀྱི་འཕྲིན་ལས་བསམ་མི་ཁྱབ།} inconceiveable virtuous deeds of a Buddha.
བསམ-གཏན	[samadhi]. Concentration; meditative concentration. A state of mind in which one is able to focus one's attention single-\npointedly on any suitable virtuous object without wandering outside of it. Such a state of mind becomes the source of all spiritual qualities.
བསམ-གཏན-གྱི-དཀྱིལ-འཁོར	[samadhi maṇḍala]/ Concentration [maṇḍala]. Creation and visualization of the residence and resident [maṇḍala] of a deity or dieties through the power of meditation.
བསམ-གཏན-གྱི-སྐྱོན-བརྒྱད	Eight faults of concentration. The eight faults of the desire realm and concentrations realms of the lower level. 1-2. {འདོད་པ་ན་ཡོད་པའི་སྡུག་བསྔལ་དང་ཡིད་མི་བདེ་བ།} suffering\nand mental discomfort within the desire realm 3-4. {བསམ་} {གཏན་དང་པོ་ལ་ཡོད་པའི་རྟོག་པ་དང་དཔྱོད་པ།} investigation and analysis within the first concentration level\n5. {བསམ་གཏན་གཉིས་པ་མན་ཆད་དུ་ཡོད་པའི་ཡིད་བདེ་བའམ་དགའ་བ།} mental\necstacy or joy below the level of the second concentration 6-8. {བསམ་གཏན་གསུམ་པ་མན་ཆད་ན་ཡོད་པའི་དབུགས་འབྱུང་བ་དང་།}\n{རྔུབ་པ་དང་།} {གསུམ་པའི་བདེ་བ།} exhalation, inhalation and bliss\nof the third concentration level and the levels below it.
བསམ-གཏན-གྱི-དངོས-གཞིའི-སྙོམས-འཇུག	Actual meditative absorption. A virtuous state of concentration free of desire-attachment to the lower level of concentration. There are four types belonging to the four concentration levels (see {བསམ་གཏན་བཞི}, A).
བསམ-གཏན-གྱི-ཆོས-བཞི	The four qualities of concentration.\n1. {རྣམ་གཡོང་སོགས་མི་} {མཐུན་ཕྱོགས་ཉམས་པ།} quells distractions and other unfavorable factors\n2. {ཆོས་ཀྱི་བདག་མེད་རྟོགས་པའི་རྣམ་པར་མི་རྟོགས་པ།} generates non-conceptual cognition of the selflessness of phenomena\n3. {འདོད་པ་ཛོགས་པར་བྱེད་པ།} fulfills one's wishes\n4. {རིགས་ཅན་གསུམ་སྨིན་པར་བྱེད་པ།} ripens the three classes of disciples of the three vehicles.
བསམ-གཏན-གྱི-གནས	States of concentration (see {གཟུགས་ཁམས་གནས་རིས་བཅུ་བདུན}).
བསམ-གཏན-གཉིས	Two types of concentration.\n1. {རྒྱུ་སྙོམས་འཇུག་གི་བསམ་ག་ཏན།} [karaṇasamāpattidhyāna]/ concentration in causal absorption\n2. {འབྲས་བུ་སྐྱེ་བའི་བསམ་གཏན།} [kāryasamāpattidhyāna]/ concentration giving rise to result concentration.
བསམ-གཏན-གཉིས-པའི-ཡན-ལག-བཞི	Four branches of the second level concentration.\n1. {ནང་རབ་ཏུ་དང་བ།} [adhyātmasamprasāda]/ internal clarity\n2. {དགའ་བ།} [mudita]/ joy\n3. {བདེ་བ།} [sukha]/ bliss\n4. {སེམས་རྩེ་གཅིག་པ།} [ekāgracitta]/ single-pointed mind.
བསམ-གཏན-དང-པོའི-དངོས-གཞི-གསུམ	Three actual absorptions of the first level concentration.\n1. {ཉོན་མོངས་ཅན་གྱི་དངོས་གཞི།} deluded concentration\n2. {དག་པའི་དངོས་གཞི།} purified concentration\n3. {ཟག་མེད་ཀྱི་དངོས་གཞི།} uncontaminated concentration.
བསམ-གཏན-དང-པོའི-ཡན-ལག-ལྔ་	Five branches of the first level concentration.\n1. {རྟོག་པ།} [vitarka]/ investigation\n2. {དཔྱོད་པ།} [vicāra]/ analysis\n3. {དགའ་བ།} [mudita]/ joy\n4. {བདེ་བ།} [sukha]/ bliss\n5. {སེམས་རྩེ་གཅིག་པ།} [ekāgracitta]/ single-pointed mind.
བསམ-གཏན-དག-པ-བ-བཞི	Four pure concentrations.\n1. {ཉམས་པ་ཆ་མཐུན།} aid to degeneration\n2. {གནས་པ་ཆ་མཐུན།} aid to endurance\n3. {ཁྱད་པར་ཆ་མཐུན།} aid to promotion\n4. {ངེས་འབྱེད་ཆ་མཐུན།} aid to definite separation.
བསམ-གཏན-བཞི	Four types of concentration. A. {གཟུགས་ཁམས་ཀྱི་བསམ་གཏན་བཞི།}\nFour levels of concentration within the form realm.\n1. {བསམ་གཏན་དང་པོ།} [prathamaṃdhyāna]/ first level concentration\n2. {བསམ་གཏན་གཉིས་པ།} [dvitīyadhyāna]/ second level concentration\n3. {བསམ་གཏན་གསུམ་པ།} [tritīyadhyāna]/ third level concentration\n4. {བསམ་གཏན་བཞི་པ།} [cathurthadhyāna]/ fourth level concentration.\nB. {རྒྱུད་སྡེ་འོག་མ་ནས་ཤད་པའི་བསམ་གཏན་བཞི།} Four concentralions according to the lower tantras.\n1. {བཟླས་བརྗོད་ཡན་ལག་བཞིའི་བསམ་གཏན།} concentration of the four limbs of recitation/ incantation (see {བཟླས་བརྗོད་ཡན་ལག་བཞི})\n2. {མེ་གནས་ཀྱི་བསམ་གཏན།} concentration on abiding in fire\n3. {སྒྲ་གནས་ཀྱི་བསམ་གཏན།} concentration on abiding in sound\n4. {སྒྲ་མཐར་} {ཐར་པ་སྟེར་བའི་བསམ་གན།} concentration resulting in liberation at the conclusion of sound.
བསམ-གཏན-བཞི-པའི-ཡན-ལག-བཞི	Four branches of the fourth level concentration.\n1. {དྲན་པ།} mindfulness\n2. {བ་ཏང་}?{མས་ཡངས་དག} pure equanimity\n3. {ཆོར་བ་བ}^{ང་}-f {མས།} neutral feeling\n4. {སེམས་}£{ག}5{ག་པ།} single-pointed mind.
བསམ-གཏན-ས-དགུ	Nine states of concentration.\n1. {བསམ་གཏན་དང་པོའི་ཉེར་} {བསྡོགས་མི་ལྕོགས་མེད།} preparatory stage of the first level concentration\n2. {བསམ་གཏན་དང་པོའི་དངོས་གཞི་ཙམ་པོ་བ།} ordinary stage of the first level concentration\n3. {བསམ་གཏན་} {དང་པོའི་དངོས་གཞི་ཁྱད་པར་ཅན།} exalted stage of the first level concentration\n4. {བསམ་གཏན་གཉིས་པའི་དངོས་གཞི་ཙམ་པོ་བ།} ordinary stage of the second level concentration\n5. {བསམ་གཏན་གཉིས་པའི་དངོས་གཞི་ཁྱད་པར་ཅན།} exalted stage of the second level concentration\n6. {བསམ་གཏན་གསུམ་པའི་} {དངོས་གཞི་ཙམ་པོ་བ།} ordinary stage of the third level concentration\n7. {བསམ་གཏན་གསུམ་པའི་དངོས་གཞི་ཁྱད་པར་ཅན།} exalted stage of the third level concentration\n8. {བསམ་} {གཏན་བཞི་པའི་དངོས་གཞི་ཙམ་པོ་བ།} ordinary stage of the fourth level concentration\n8. {བསམ་གཏན་བཞི་པའི་དངོས་གཞི་ཁྱད་པར་ཅན།} exalted stage of the fourth level concentration.
བསམ-གཏན-ས-དྲུག	Six states of concentration.\n1. {བསམ་གཏན་དང་པོའི་ཉེར་བསྡོགས་མི་ལྕོགས་མེད།} preparatory stage of the first level concentration\n2. {བསམ་གཏན་དང་པོའི་དངོས་གཞི་ཙམ་པོ་བ།} ordinary stage of the first level concentration\n3. {བསམ་གཏན་} {དང་པོའི་དངོས་གཞི་ཁྱད་པར་ཅན།} exalted stage of the first level concentration\n4. {བསམ་གཏན་གཉིས་པའི་དངོས་གཞི།} actual stage of the second level concentration\n5. {བསམ་གཏན་གསུམ་པའི་དངོས་གཞི།} actual stage of the third level concentration\n6. {བསམ་གཏན་བཞི་པའི་དངོས་གཞི།} actual stage of the fourth level concentration.
བསམ-གཏན-གསུམ-པའི-ཡན-ལག-ལྔ་	Five branches of the third level concentration.\n1. {དྲན་པ།} [smṛti]/ mindfulness\n2. {ཤེས་བཞིན།} [saṃprajanya]/ introspection\n3. {བཏང་སྙོམས།} [upekṣa]/equinimity\n4. {བདེ་བ།} [sukha]/ bliss\n5. {སེམས་རྩེ་གཅིག་པ།} [ekāgracitta]/single-pointed mind.
བསམ-པའི-ལས	Intended activity. Karma or activities of body and speech as motivated by the mind.
བསམ-ཡས	Samye Monastery, the first monastery in Tibet built in 763 A.D. by King Trisong Deutsan under the guidance of the Great Abbot Santaraksita and Acarya Padmasambhava on the bank of the fsang-po, south-east of Lhasa.
བསོད-ནམས	[puṇya]/ Merits. Synonymous with virtuous activity ({དགེ་བའི་ལས}); positive energy.
བསོད-ནམས-ཀྱི-ཕུང-པོ-ལྔ་	Five aggregates of merit; five virtuous aggregates. Collection of merits of:\n1. {ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་ཀྱི་ཕུང་པོ།} [ṡīlaskandha]/ morality\n2. {ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན་གྱི་ཕུང་པོ།} [samādhiskandha]/ concentration\n3. {ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱི་ཕུང་པོ།} prajсaskandha]/ wisdom\n4. {རྣམ་པར་གྲོལ་བའི་ཕུང་པོ།} [vimuktaskandha]/ thorough liberation\n5. {རྣམ་པར་གྲོལ་བའི་ཡེ་ཤེས་མཐོངབའི་ཕུང་པོ།} [vimuktajсānadṛṣṭiskandha]/ understanding the wisdom of thorough liberation.
བསོད-ནམས-ཀྱི-ཚོགས	[puṇyasaṃbhāra]/ Collection of merits; accumulation of merits that is the primary cause of producing the resultant form body of a Buddha
བསོད-ནམས-ཀྱི-ལས	[punyakarma]/ Meritorious karma. Karma that results in rebirth as a human being, demi-god or a god of the desire realm.
བསོད-ནམས-མ-ཡིན-པའི-ལས	[apuṇyakarma]/ Non-meritorious karma. Karma that results in rebirth as an animal, a hungry ghost or a hell being.
བསོད-ནམས-རྟེན-གྱི-ས	The ground of basis for merits. According to the Nyingma tradition this refers to the fifth ground attained during the second stage of yoga which leads to actualizing the uncontaminated primordial wisdom.
བསོད-ནམས-སུ-བྱ-བའི-དངོས-པོ-བཞི	Three kinds of meritorious deeds; three ways of collecting merits.\n1. {སྦྱིན་པ་ལས་བྱུང་བའི་དངོས་པོ།} merits collected through the practice of giving\n2. {ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་ལས་བྱུང་བའི་དངོས་པོ།} merits collected through the practice of morality\n3. {བསྒོམ་པ་ལས་བྱུང་བའི་དངོས་པོ།} merits collected through the practice of concentration.\n4. {ཛས་ལས་བྱུང་བའི་དངོས་པོ།} merits collected through the power of substances.
བསྲུང-བ-མེད-པ-གསུམ	Three unguarded actions; the three bases of self-confidence of a Buddha\n1. {སྐུ་བག་མེད་པ་ལས་བསྲུངབ་མེད་པ།} he need not protect himself from physical faults\n2. {གསུང་བག་མེད་པ་ལས་བསྲུང་བ་མེད་པ།} he need not protect himself from vocal faults\n3. {ཐུགས་བག་མེད་པ་ལས་བསྲུང་བ་མེད་པ།} he need not protect himself from mental faults.
བསྲི-འཕོ-དགུ-སྐོར	The yoga of ninefold mixing; the nine rounds of mixing. According to the glorious Rechungpa's version these are:\n1. {འདོད་ཆགས་བདེ་ཆེན་དང་བསྲི་བ་གཏུམ་མོ།} the psychic heat mixing lust with great bliss\n2. {ཞི་སྡང་བདེན་མེད་དང་བསྲི་བ་སྒྱུ་ལུས།} the illusory body through mixing hatred with lack of true existence\n3. {གཏི་མུག་མི་རྟོག་པ་དང་བསྲེ་བ་འོད་གསལ།} the clear light mind mixing ignorance with non-conceptuality\n4. {གཏུམ་མོ་དང་སྒྱུ་ལུས་བསྲེས་ལ་ཉིན་མོ་བསྒོམ།} the broad day light meditation mixing psychic heat with the illusory body\n5. {རྨི་ལམ་དང་འོད་གསལ་བསྲེས་ལ་མཚན་མོ་བསྒོམ།} the midnight meditation mixing dreams with the illusory body\n6. {བར་དོ་དང་འཕོ་བ་བསྲེས་ལ་འཆི་ཁར་བསྒོམ།} the meditation at death mixing the intermediate state of rebirth and consciousness transference\n7. {གང་ཟག་བརྩོན་འགྲུས་ཅན་ལ་གཏུམ་མོ།} psychic heat for persons of great diligence\n8. {ལེ་ལོ་ཅན་ལ་རྨི་ལམ།} dreams for lazy persons\n9. {ཚེ་ཐུང་འཕོ་བ་དང་བསྲེ་བ།} the consciousness transference for persons of short life-span.
བསླབ-ཁྲིམས	{བསླབ་སྡོམ།}\n[ṡikṣā ṡīla]/ The precepts and trainings; the vows of individual liberation, Bodhisattva and tantra.
བསླབ-པ-ཀུན-ལས-བཏུས-པ	[ṡikṣāsammuccaya]/ Compendium of Precepts. An important work by Acarya Santideva compiled from [mahāyāna] teachings dealing with moralities, vows and precepts. This complements his A Guide to the Bodhisattva's Way of Life ({སྤྱོད་འཇུག}).
བསླབ-པ-རྒྱུན-གྱི-ས	The ground of continual training. According to the Nyingma tradition this refers to the fourth ground attained at the second level of yoga where a yogi enhances his training on the continual experience of the state of union of seeing all exist-ents as being empty like illusions and clear light appearance.
བསླབ-པ-གསུམ	Three trainings.\n1. {ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་ཀྱི་བསླབ་པ།} [ṡīlaṡikṣā]/ training in moral discipline\n2. {ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན་གྱི་བསླབ་པ།} [samādhi ṡikṣās]/ training in concentration\n3. {ཤེས་ར་ཀྱི་བསླབ་པ།} [prajсaṡikṣā]/ training in wisdom.
བསླབ-པའི-གཞི-བརྒྱད	Eight fundamental precepts of a one day vow holder (see {བསྙེན་གནས་ཡན་ལག་བརྒྱད}).
བསླབ-པི-གཞི-ལྔ་	The five fundamentai precepts of a layperson (see {བསྙེན་གནས་ཡན་ལག་བརྒྱད}, 1-5).
བསླབ-པའི-གཞི-ཉིས-བརྒྱ-ལྔ-བཅུ-རྩ-གསུམ	The two hundred and fifty three vows of a fully ordained\nmonk ([bikṣu]). 1-4. {ཕམ་པ་བཞི།} The four downfalls 5-17. {ལྷག་མ་བཅུ་གསུམ།} the thirteen remainders 18-47. {སྤང་ལྟུང་}\n{སུམ་ཅུ།} the thirty abandoning downfalls 48-137. {ལྟུང་བྱེད་འབའ་} {ཞིག་པ་དགུ་བཅུ།} ninety solid propelling downfalls 138-141. {སོར་བཤགས་བཞི།} the four individual confessions 142-253. {ཉེས་བྱས་བརྒྱ་དང་བཅུ་གཉིས།} the one hundred and twelve faults.
བསླབ-བྱ-གསུམ	The three types of precepts.\n1. {དགག་པའི་བསླབ་བྱ།} precepts of negation\n2. {སྒྲུབ་པའི་བསླབ་བྱ།} precepts of cultivation\n3. {ཆ་} {མཐུན་གྱི་བསླབ་བྱ།} auxiliary precepts.
བསླུ-བའི-ཆོས-ཅན	[moṣadharmiṇa]/ Deceptive nature; deceptive phenomena.
ཧམ-པ	[mānya]/ Avarice; conceit. An attitude of expecting and demanding; an expectation or possession of more than one's share.
ཧེ-རུ-ཀ	Heruka. A tantric deity belonging to the mother tantra of the highest class of tantra; also identified as Cakrasambhara.
ཧྭ-ཤང་	Hashang. Equivelant to Upadhya—abbot; the master learned in Buddhist trainings. It came to be identified with the Chinese master, Hashang who spread the view of simultaneous enlightenment ({ཅིག་ཅིར་བའི་ལུགས}) and asserted that both virtuous and non-virtuous ideas and thoughts are equally negative because both bind one within [saṁsāra], hence, meditation on nothingness could only lead one to liberation. He contested a debate with Acarya Kamalasila during the\nreign of the Tibetan King Trisong Deutsan and being defeated is said to have returned to China.
ཧྲིལ-པོ	A. Entire; whole; all. B. Spherical shaped.
ལྷ	[deva]/ A. A meditational deity in tantric practice. B. Gods; one of the six living beings of [saṃsāra].
ལྷ-ཆེན-བརྒྱད	Eight great gods; eight lords.\n1. {དབང་ཕྱུག} [īṡvara]\n2. {བརྒྱ་བྱིན།} [indra]\n3. {ཚངས་པ།} [brahma]\n4. {ཁྱབ་འཇུག} [viṣṇu]\n5. {འདོད་པའི་དབང་ཕྱུག} Kāmadeva\n6. {ཚོགས་བདག} [gaṇeSa]\n7. {བྷི་གི་རི་རྡི།} [bhṛṃgiriṭi]\n8. {གཞོན་ནུ་གདོང་དྲུག} [ṡaḍmukhakumāra].
ལྷ-ཆོས-དགེ-བ-བཅུ	The ten divine principles; the ten moral principles. The moral code of law proscribed by King Songtsen Gampo (see {དགེ་བ་བཅུ}) along with the sixteen moral conducts (see {མི་ཆོས་གཏཟང་མ་བཅུ་དྲུག}).
ལྷ-ཆོས-བདུན-ལྔན	The seven-fold deity and texts (see {བཀའ་གདམས་ལྷ་ཆོས་བདུན}\n{ལྷ་རྗེས་སུ་དྲན་པ།}\nRecollection of the deity. One of the six recollections (see {རྗེས་སུ་དྲན་པ་དྲུག}); reflecting upon the qualities of gods within the desire realm, form realm and the noble one's
ལྷ-མཐོ	Votive cairn or heaps of stones in honor of a local deity, or in memory of a holy person, erected at the top of a pass or mountain.
ལྷ-དྲུག-རྣལ-འབྱོར	The yoga of six deities. The deity yoga of kriya tantra can be classified into the practice of six deities (see {བྱ་རྒྱུད་ཀྱི་ལྷ་དྲུག}).
ལྷ-བབས-དུས-ཆེན	The day of Buddha [ṡākyamuni]'s descent from heaven. The 15th of the ninth Tibetan month when Buddha [ṡākyamuni] descended from the heaven of the Thirty-Three' god realm to this world.
ལྷ-བླ-མ-ཡེ-ཤེས-འོད	Lha Lama Yeshe Od. A tenth century Tibetan King of Ngari region, western Tibet, who was the younger son of the King of Guge; in the latter part of his life he offered the kingdom to his brother in order to become a monk, and was later instrumental in inviting [atiṡa] to Tibet.
ལྷ-མ-ཡིན	[asura]/ Demi-gods. One of the six types of beings believed to be anti-gods by birth and are in constant conflict with gods due to jealousy.
ལྷ-མ-ཡིན-གྱི-གྲོང-ཁྱེར-བཞི	Four cities of the demi-gods.\n1. {འོད་ལྡན།} With Light\n2. {སྐར་} {ཕྲེང་།} Star-garland\n3. {ཟབ་པ།} Profound\n4. {གསེར་ལྡན།} Golden.
ལྷ-མོ-ཚེ-རིང-མཆེད-ལྔ	The five female guardians of Tibet (see {ཙེ་རིང་མཆེད་ལྔ}).\n{ལྷ་མོ་དབྱངས་ཅན་མ།}\n[sarasvatīdevī]. The feminine aspect of wisdom found both in Hindu and Buddhist pantheons; also called the goddess of\nmelody.
ལྷ-མོའི-པཞོན-པའི-ཁྱད-ཆོས-གསུམ	Three features of Palden Lhamo's (highest goddess in Tibetan Buddhism) mount.\n1. {རྫུ་འཕྲུལ་གྱི་རྐང་པ།} miraculous legs\n2. {རླུང་གི་གཤོག་པ།} wings of wind\n3. {མྱུར་མགྱོགས་ཀྱི་རྩལ།} swift.
ལྷ-བཙུན-བྱང-ཆུབ-འོད	Jangchub Od. Song of King Lhade of Ngari region of Tibet. After much hardship he invited AtiSa to Tibet on the instruction of his Uncle Lha Lama Yeshe Od. At his request [atiṡa] wrote the famous text--A Lamp on the Path to Enlightenment (bodhipathapradipa).
ལྷ-སྲིན-སྡེ-བརྒྱད	Eight gods and spirits.\n1. {གཤིན་རྗེ།} [yama]/ Lord of Death\n2. {མ་མོ།} [mātṛka]/ Female-protector (see {མ་མོ})\n3. {བདུད།} [māra]/ Devil; demons\n4. {བཙན།} [haṭa]/ Mountain-dwelling spirits\n5. {རྒྱལ་པོ།} [rāja]/ Principal local gods\n6. {ཀླུ།} [nāga]/ Serpent's\n7. {གནོད་སྦྱིན།} [yakṣa]/ Harmful spirits\n8. {གཟའ།} [graha]/ Malignant stars or planets.
ལྷ-གསོལ	The incense burning ceremony. The ceremony of tying prayer\nflags and offering incense as a feast to appease gods, nagas and protectors.
ལྷ-བསང	The incense burning ceremony. The ceremony of tying prayer\nflags and offering incense as a feast to appease gods, nagas and protectors.
ལྷག-པཅས-མྱང-འདས	[nirvāṇa] with remainder, residual state of liberation. A state of liberation within the mental continuum of an Arhat who continues to live in the body derived from his previous contaminated mental and physical actions even after attaining [nirvāṇa].
ལྷབ-མཐོང་	[vipaSyanā]/ Penetrative Insight. Penetrative insight meditation. A single pointed concentration able to apply analysis of its object; an apex form of all concentrations able to see the indepth reality of phenomena.
ལྷག-པའི-ང-རྒྱལ	[adhimāna]/ Exalted pride. A feeling that you are better than everyone else.
ལྷག-པའི-ཡོ-བྱད	Additional articles of a monk. The articles that a monk is allowed to possess not out of necessity but to use these in times of need for oneself or for others, e.g. an extra robe.
ལྷག-པའི-བསླབ-པ-གསུམ	Three hjgher trainings. The trainings that are superior to a training undertaken by a common or a non-Buddhist practitioner.\n1. {ལྷག་པ་ཚུལ་ཁྲིམས་ཀྱི་བསླབ་པ།} [adhiSīlaSikṣā]/ higher training in moral discipline\n2. {ལྷག་པ་ཏིང་ངེ་འཛིན་གྱི་བསླབ་པ།} [adhisamādhiSikṣā]/ higher training in concentration\n3. {ལྷག་པ་ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱི་བསླབ་པ།} [adhiprajсaSikṣa]/ higher training in wisdom.
ལྷག-མེད-མྱང-འདས	[nirvāṇa] without remainder; non-residual state of liberation. A state of libertion within the mental continuum of an Arhat who is freed from the physical aggregates derived from contaminated action as soon as he attains [nirvāṇa].
ལྷག-བསམ	[adhyāSaya]/ Resolute intention. A pure wish to accept responsibilities upon oneself to liberate all sentient beings from the bonds of cyclic existence; one of the fundamental causes to produce the mind of enlightenment (bodhicitta) within oneself.
ལྷག-བསམ-དག-པའི-སེམས-བསྐྱེད-བདུན	The seven minds of enlightenment with pure resolute intention; the mind of enlightenment possessed by Bodhisattvas on the seven impure grounds-first to seven of the ten grounds.\n1. {གཏེར་ལྟ་བུའི་སེམས་བསྐྱེད།} the treasurelike bodhicitta\n2. {རིན་ཆེན་འབྱུང་གནས་ལྟ་བུའི་སེམས་བསྐྱེད།} the jewel-source-like bodhicitta\n3. {རྒྱ་མཚོ་ལྟ་བུའི་སེམས་བསྐྱེད།} the ocean-like bodhicitta\n4. {རྡོ་རྗེ་ལྟ་བུའི་སེམས་བསྐྱེད།} the vajra-like bodhicitta\n5. {རི་རྒྱལ་ལྟ་བུའི་སེམས་བསྐྱེད།} the Mem-like bodhicitta\n6. {སྨན་ལྟ་བུའི་སེམས་བསྐྱེད།} the medicine-like bodhicitta\n7. {བཤེས་གཉེན་ལྟ་བུའི་སེམས་བསྐྱེད།} the spiritual teacher-like bodhicitta
ལྷང-ངེ-བ	Clear and lucid understanding; articulated meaning or sound; solid and vivid appearance of the object of meditation.
ལྷན-སྐྱེས	[sahaja]/ Innately born; innately produced; aquired by birth or from beginningless time, e.g. the view of holding one's transitory aggregates as oneself or as I or self ({ལྷན་སྐྱེས་ཀྱི་འཇིག་ལྟ}).
ལྷན-སྐྱེས-ཀྱི-ཉོན-མོངས-པ	[sahajakleSa]/ Innately produced delusions. The negative emotions in those whose minds or perspective of looking at things are not stained by philosophical views but are natural tendencies, e.g. the innately born ignorance ({ལྷན་སྐྱེས་ཀྱི་མ་རིག་པ}).
ལྷན-སྐྱེས-ཀྱི-ལྷ-ལྔ་	The five natural gods of human beings. The gods or spirits supposed to be born along with oneself from birth.\n1. {འཚོ་བའི་ལྷ།} god of livelihood\n2. {སྲུང་བའི་ལྷ།} god that protects oneself from enemies\n3. {སྐྱོབས་པའི་ལྷ།} god that guards oneself from fears\n4. {འགྲོགས་པའི་ལྷ།} god that associates with oneself\n5. {འགོ་བའི་ལྷ།} personal god.
ལྷན-སྐྱེས-ཀྱི-ལྷ-འདྲེ	Natural devils or spirits. The spirits or gods and their influence that are incorporated into one's own life from birth, perhaps caused by one's previous karma, and are separated from oneself when one is dead.
ལྷན-ཅིག-སྐྱེས-སྦྱོར	[sahajayoga]/ Simultaneous production and union; innate union. A [mahāmudrā] meditation tradition of the Dvagpo Kagyud Order of Tibetan Buddhism.
ལྷན-ཅིག-སྐྱེས-པའི-ཡེ-ཤེས	[sahajajсāna]/ Wisdom of innate production; innately born wisdom. The immense joy and bliss experienced by a Yogi through the practice of making the energy wind enter, abide and dissolve within the central energy channel at the initial level of the completion stage practice of tantra
ལྷན-ཅིག-འབྱུང-བའི-རྒྱུ	[sahabhūhetu]/ Simultaneously arisen cause. Anything that exists simultaneously not only with it cause but also integerates it as an inseparable part of the result and does not impede its production, such as the four elements co-existing and supporting each other.
ལྷན-ཅིག-བྱེད-རྐྱེན	[sahakārikāraṇa]/ Auxiliary condition; co-operative condition or factor. For instance the hammer used by a carpenter in making a table.
ལྷན-ཅིག-མི-གནས-འགལ	Non-simultaneously abiding mutual exclusion. Things that nullify each other for co-existence, e.g. the antidotes and their direct elimination.
ལྷམ-མེ-ལྷན-ནེ-ལྷན-ནེ	[bhāsate tapati virocate]/ Outshining, majestic and illustrious. An imposing outlook.
ལྷའི-རྟེན-ཅན-གྱི-རྒྱུན-ཞུགས-སྲིད-པ-ལན-བདུན-པ-བ	Stream-winner who attains liberation after seven successive rebirths as a god.
ལྷའི-དེ-ཁོ-ན-ཉིད	The suchness of a deity. One of the four yogas of suchness according to action tantra (kriya). This concerns generating oneself in the form of a deity by means of the six deity yogas within action tantra practice and inviting wisdom-beings in front, and focussing one's attention on them just as a servant would attend to his master, and requesting their virtuous energy or siddhi.
ལྷའི-རྣལ-འབྱོར	[devayoga]/ Deity yoga. Meditation on a deity or dieties; visualizing deities infront or generating onself as the deity.
ལྷའི-རྣ-བའི-མངོན-ཤེས	[divyaṃSrotamābhijna~_na]/ Clairvoyance of the divine ear; extra-sensory aural perception. The divine power to hear and listen to sounds or voice of a distance covering hundreds of yojanas (see {དཔག་ཚད}).
ལྷའི-མིག-གི-མངོན-ཤེས	[dirvyacakṣurvijсāna]/ Claivoyance of the divine eyes; extrasensory visual perception. One of six types of extra-sensory perception (see {མངོན་པར་ཤེས་པ་དྲུག}) enabling one to see where and when a person would die or be born without being impeded by any factors of time, location and nature.
ལྷའི-གཙོ-བོ-གསུམ	Three principal gods.\n1. {ཚངས་པ།} Brahma\n2. {དབང་ཕྱུག} [īSvara]\n3. {ཁྱབ་འཇུག} [viṣṇu].
ལྷའི-ཡང-ལྷ	[devātideva]/ God of gods; divine among divinities. An epithet for Buddha
ལྷའི-ང-རྒྱལ	The divine pride. Imagination of oneself as being the deity in the generation stage meditation of tantric practices in order to remove a sense of ordinariness of oneself.
ལྷའི-གསལ-སྣང་	The divine vision; the clear perception of a deity. The imagination and appearance of seeing each and every feature of the deity lucidly without oblivion during the course of the generation stage meditation of tantra aimed at removing attachment to the oridinariness of oneself.
ལྷས-བྱིན	Devadatta. Cousin of Buddha [ṡākyamuni] who was his persistent antagonist, not only after Buddha's enlightenment but even when he engaged in the Bodhisattva trainings.
ལྷས-བྱིན-གྱི-བརྟུལ-ཞུགས-བསླབ-ཚིག-ལྔ་	1 Five ascetic practices of Devadatta; five precepts of Devadatta\n1. {ཤ་མི་ཟ་བ།} not eating meat\n2. {འོ་མ་མི་འཐུང་བ།} not drinking milk\n3. {ལན་ཚྭ་མི་ཟ་བ།} not taking salt\n4. {གོས་དྲས་དྲུབ་ཅན་མི་གྱོན་པ།} not wearing ragged cloths\n5. {དགོན་པར་མི་གནས་པ།} not living in a hermitage.
ལྷུང-བཟེད	[piṇḍapātra]/ Monk's or nun's begging bowl. Traditionally it is required to be made of stones or metal.
ལྷུན-གྲུབ-ཐོད-རྒལ	The spontaneous leap-over path. A {རྫོགས་ཆེན་} meditation technique especially for highly advanced followers; a speedy method of realizing {རྫོགས་ཆེན་}.
ལྷུན-གྲུབ-རིག-འཛིན	The state of spontaneous [vajradhāra]. The Nyingmapas name for the state of Buddha [vajradhāra].
ལྷུན-གྱིས-གྲུབ-པ	Spontaneous existence; natural; existence by nature; unintended incident.
ཨ	A. The last of the thirty letters of the Tibetan alphabet; a universal vowel present in all letters. B. The shortest form of the Perfection of Wisdom. It is explained to contain the meaning of the entire teachings of Buddha; heavily blessed syllable.\n{ཨ་ཏི་ཡོ་ག}\nThe atiyoga tantra. The peak of the nine vehicles according to -the Nyingma tradition called the Great Completion stage, {ཛོག་པ་ཆེན་པོ}.\n{ཨ་ནུ་ཡོ་ག}\nThe anuyoga tantra. The eighth of the nine vehicles according to the Nyingma tradition dealing primarily with the completion stage practices of tantra.\n{ཨ་ཏི་ཤ།}\n[atiṡa] (982-1054). A renowed Indian master and scholar w visited Tibet in the early 11th century and taught extensive thereby restoring the purity of Buddhist practice in Tibet. I wrote the famous text "A Lamp on the Path to Enlightenme" ([bodhipathapradhīpa]), and founded the Kadampa tradition.
ཨ-ལི	Vowel letters of the Sanskrit alphabet.
ཨ-ལི-བཅུ-དྲུག	The sixteen vowel letters. {ཨ།} [a], {ཨཱ།} [a], {ཨེ།} [i], {ཨཱེ།} [ī], {ཨུུ།} u {ཨཨཱུ།} [ū], {རྀ།} [ṛ], {རཱྀ།} [ṛī], {ལྀ།} [l.], {ལཱྀ།} [l.ī], {ཨེ།} [e], {ཨཻ།} [ae], {ཨོ།} [o], {ཨཽ།} [au], {ཨཾ།} [aṃ], {ཨཿ} [aḥ]. These represents the sixteen emptinesse: (see {སྟོང་ཉིས་བཅུ་དྲུག}) and are the sources of the thirty-two {མཚན་བཟང་པོ་སུམ་བཅུ་རྩ་གཉིས}).
ཨིཎ-དྲ-ཎཱི-ལ	[indraṇīla]/ sapphire.
ཨུུ-རྒྱན	[oḍḍiyāna]. The birth-place of Guru Padmasambhava, the kingdom of King Indrabodhi. Some identity this place with Swat in Pakistan. This is also regarded as a sacred place of [ḍākini]s.
ཨེ-ཝམ	E-Wam syllable. E represents emptiness as the wisdom side and Wam great bliss, the method side.
ཨེ-ཝམ-ཟུང-འཇུག	The union of E and Wam. Represents the ever supreme reality emptiness and the supreme unchangeable great bliss.
ཨེར-ཀ-འུན-གྱི-ཆོས-ལུགས	Shammism of Mongolia. A pre-Buddhist religious tradition in Mongolia similar to the Bon religion of pre-Buddhist Tibet, in which practice of animal sacrifice and offering of their blood to the gods and spirits was common. The Third Dalai Lama, Sonam Gyatso, (1543-1588) banned this practice and taught the virtues of Buddhism.
ཨོ-ལོ	The monks on duty serving tea or gruel during the Great Prayer festival in Tibet.
ཨོཾ	The head of mantras. Has many meanings such as symbolizing the Vajra body of a Buddha.
ཨོཾ-སྭསྟི	[om svāsti]/ May all be auspicious. May all enjoy peace and prosperity.
